High Infidelity

by hurricxneamelia, thetbone

Summary

"If Agatha can’t have joy, she’ll take power. If she can’t have friends, she’ll take victims. If she can’t have love, she’ll take this — fucking someone’s wife at a luxury resort."

Rio Vidal is a lawyer stuck in a toxic marriage. Agatha Harkness is a con artist on the heels of a nasty divorce. The two cross paths at a Sicilian hotel and start an affair that will change their lives forever.

Or: the White Lotus AU.

Chapter 1: Day 1, Part 1

Disneyland. Chuck E. Cheese. Sky Zone. All cesspools crawling with pee and screaming children but all places Agatha was prepared to brave for Nicky when she’d asked him where he wanted to go during their (too-short, unfair, single) week of summer vacation together. 

She should’ve known he wasn’t going to pick a normal place. Nicky wasn’t a normal six-year-old. Nicky was peculiar. Nicky was exceptional. And Nicky was… 

Well, Nicky was sick. Cystic fibrosis. 

Nicky’s being sick certainly wasn’t the reason for her divorce. They were mismatched from the beginning — Agatha was a “cold, selfish bitch” (Wanda’s words), and Wanda was an “insufferable, sanctimonious cunt” (Agatha’s) — but it had likely sped up the inevitable. 

Nicky was also a trooper, weathering a nasty disease and an equally nasty custody battle without ever losing the smile that made Agatha’s entire world turn. That made her life worth living.  

And so because he had spent the vast majority of his life in waiting rooms and courtrooms, doctor’s offices and lawyer’s offices, Agatha had told him he could go anywhere he wanted. 

Sicily. He’d picked Sicily. Apparently, he’d learned about it in some book Wanda had read him during one of their many weeks together. (Agatha only got Wednesdays and every other weekend — and she was apparently lucky for that considering her “checkered past,” as her lawyer had said. She didn’t feel very lucky. She felt like she wanted to stab someone in the throat. It only seemed fair. She felt like she was being stabbed in the heart every time she had to say goodbye to her son for any length of time.) 

Agatha wasn’t wealthy — especially not after the outrageous pile of medical bills and mountain of lawyers’ fees — but she was resourceful. And smart. And she would do absolutely anything for her little boy.  

And so some light credit card fraud later, she found herself on a boat to a luxury resort surrounded by people who were decidedly not resourceful or smart — people who got everything handed to them on a silver fucking platter. Self-righteous people. The privileged elite who thought they were better than her. People like her ex-wife and her ex-wife's lawyer and her own lawyer and the judge and Nicky's pediatrician and the first specialist and the second specialist and— well, she could go on.

Agatha scans them, ever watchful and aware of her surroundings. It was a habit at this point, to assess risks and threats and marks and opportunities. It was always good to figure out the dynamics from the get-go — figure out who everyone was so she could strategize how she could play them. If this boat crashed on a deserted island, for example, who would be useful to align herself with, and who should she convince everyone to eat first? 

Agatha wasn’t good with people, but she was good at people. She had to be to survive.

There’s a stylish bald woman dripping with wealth and her alternative…assistant? Girlfriend? Whatever. Agatha writes them both off almost immediately as irrelevant. They were too self-involved to be dangerous to Agatha but too skeptical to be advantageous — not to mention too irritating to tolerate. They wouldn’t try to take anything from Agatha, but Agatha wouldn’t be able to get anything from being in proximity to them either.

The pair is sitting next to a kooky woman adorned with ridiculous handmade jewelry she almost certainly paid way too much for and hair so big it made her look like Albert Einstein's much more gullible sister. Agatha files her away as a potential target. As easy money. She could get a couple thousand bucks at least by selling her bullshit shell necklaces or artisanal sea glass she claimed was a rare treasure of the ocean.

Then there’s a beefy, clean-shaven white man who looks remarkably like a thumb resting his hand on the thigh of a younger Latina woman. Trophy wife. She’s admittedly sexy — far out of his league, that’s for damn sure — but undoubtedly stupid as hell, a fact that’s further confirmed as she has the gall to give Agatha a pitiful smile. Because Nicky is using his PEP mask, most likely. Agatha scowls and pulls him closer to her side.

The woman blinks, face immediately falling. Serves her fucking right. Agatha hated these two on sight. If the quirky old woman was going to be easy to manipulate and the girlboss and her sidekick were neutral territory, these two were born at the top of the food chain and, in Agatha’s not-so-humble opinion, had no business being there.

Thankfully, the woman doesn’t have the nerve or audacity to look at her the rest of the ride, but Agatha watches her and her hideous, always-failing-up husband as Nicky loudly rattles off facts about Italy. It’s a little annoying, frankly, but it’s better than listening to the rich Black woman talking the Asian woman’s ear off about recycled lotion or organic beauty blenders or something equally, mind-numbingly stupid. 

The Latina doesn’t say much — just turns down the champagne one of the employees offers her. 

What a fucking square.

Rio isn’t sure what she did wrong. Rio’s never sure what she does wrong, but she seems to be doing it all the time. She’s not talking enough — she’s talking too much. She’s not drinking enough — she’s drinking too much. She’s not being friendly enough — she’s being too friendly. There are so many rules, and she can’t seem to follow them. Not to Thanos’ liking, at least, and apparently, not to this brunette woman’s either.

Somehow, Rio is always doing wrong. Somehow, Rio is always feeling wrong. And she has been since…since when? Since she said, ‘I do’? Since she said, ‘Yes,’ when he got down on one knee? Since she said, ‘Okay,’ when he asked her on a date? 

She married him anyway (though he hurts her and always will no matter how many times he promises he won’t anymore). She fucks him anyway (though she’s not attracted to him and never has been). She came on this vacation anyway (though their getaways are always far from relaxing; though Rio has not relaxed since she met him). Maybe it’s not what love is supposed to be, but it’s what it is now.

Rio will grin and bear it, even as everyone whispers she’s with him for his money despite the fact she’s a lawyer. Despite the fact she used to make more than him until one of his investments paid out better than anyone could have ever anticipated. They were always well off — had first-class-ticket, chartering-a-yacht, luxury-hotel money — but now they had private-jet, buying-their-own-boat, owning-a-private-island money.

Rio doesn’t give a shit about any of that, but she will pretend to. She will make do. She has to if she wants to survive.

But she will also relish any second she can get away from him. She feels her shoulders relax the smallest bit as Thanos tells her to hang back as he gets their room key — feels herself breathe a little easier despite the fact she finds herself standing next to the hostile brunette woman.

Rio hates tension. Being with Thanos, Rio has had to get good at defusing it.

“I’m sorry if I offended you on the boat or something,” Rio tells her. “I’ve been told sometimes my facial expressions don’t come off right. I was just trying to say hi.”

“And you couldn’t manage it?” the woman dryly quips back, glancing at her with a raised brow. “You tried to say hi and found you were unable to do so?”

Rio grimaces. She’s demeaned in public all the time, but the embarrassment never fades. She’s not sure if it’s worse coming from her husband or a stranger. “Small talk isn’t usually my thing, but you seemed the least insufferable out of everyone on the boat. I was trying to non-verbally greet you.”

“Top 10%,” she coolly replies.

Rio furrows her brows. “What?”

“Of the most insufferable people on the boat. I found you to be in the top 10%.”

“Oh.” She sucks in a breath. “Any reason? I was minding my own business.”

“Is that what you call staring at my son like he’s some Make-a-Wish kid?”

“I wasn’t…staring. Or assuming anything about him,” she stutters. It’s not a lie, but her face flushes anyway.

“Bullshit. Everyone makes assumptions about everyone all the time. I, for instance, assume that oversized frat boy getting your room key is your husband?” The woman nods toward Thanos. “I assume he’s in tech or finance — the same industry his daddy works in. The same company, too. I assume he probably gave you the wedding of your dreams but never, ever an orgasm. Please, dear — do stop me if I have it wrong.”

Her cheeks grow hotter, some rage now mixed in with the humiliation. “Actually, his father fired him because he was so bad at his job — he’s only recently started making any real money. I paid for the wedding. I’m a lawyer — civil and human rights. And people do make assumptions. The assumption I made about you is that you weren’t a snobby rich person. I now realize I was wrong.” 

Fuck, she’s said too much. She’s said far, far too much. Screw this woman for baiting her like that. For making her crack so easily. She has to get away. She has to get away now.

“I’ll see you around,” she says, ducking her head as she reluctantly goes to join Thanos at the concierge. He didn’t like it when she talked to people he didn’t know. He certainly didn’t like it when she aired their business. Made him out to be anything less than the perfect husband.

The woman steps in front of her, blocking her path. “So you assumed I was poor? That I don’t have enough money to be here? Is that it?”

“No, I just assumed you weren’t wealthy enough to be completely out of touch.”

She puts a hand to her heart and adopts a thick Southern accent. “Well, ain’t that just the sweetest backhanded compliment I ever heard.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “No one is calling you poor. I am calling you a presumptuous asshole, though.” She once again steps around her to join Thanos. He didn’t like it when she cursed either — felt it unladylike — but this woman was making her break all the rules. Become someone she wasn’t. Or at least, had never allowed herself to be.

The woman obnoxiously mirrors the movement, landing in front of her once again. “How do you figure? Sounds like everything I said was pretty spot-on. Unless he has made you cum..." She glances over her shoulder at him. "Though I sincerely doubt that."

Rio grits her teeth, lowering her voice now — anxious that Thanos might retaliate if he heard her talking to this infuriating woman. “You assumed I thought badly about your kid, which I didn’t," she hisses. "You assumed I was a gold digger, which I’m not. What’s your problem?”

“People like you,” she answers simply. 

They’re interrupted by the sound of tiny footsteps running toward them from the bathroom. “Mama!” the little boy from the boat says. “Can we go to the pool now?” 

The woman turns to him, leaning down to tenderly ruffle his hair as if she hadn’t just committed verbal warfare against Rio. “Of course, sweetheart. Let’s go.”

Chapter 2: Day 1, Part 2

Chapter Summary

After a routine argument with Thanos, Rio runs into Agatha again, leading her to make a dangerous, spontaneous, and irresistible decision.

Chapter Notes

Although we've tagged for domestic violence, a reminder that this story does depict an emotionally and physically abusive relationship. Please take care of yourselves if that's something that could be potentially triggering for you. Here is a link to some resources worldwide if you need additional support: https://safeandtogetherinstitute.com/international-domestic-violence-resources/.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio feels like she might cry. She’s not the problem here, and what’s worse is that she has no one to tell about the interaction, much less complain about it to. Her husband would be upset — at both the woman and herself, no doubt — and she wasn’t about to put herself through that. She wouldn’t even want to put the woman through that, as obnoxious as she was. She wouldn’t wish Thanos’ rage on her worst enemy, which is exactly what that woman might very well become if she ever saw her again.

Contrary to what that woman seemed to think, Rio wasn’t born with a silver spoon in her mouth. She was raised by a single father in a small town in Puerto Rico — a loving father, yes, but one who couldn’t help her pay for college. One who certainly couldn't help her pay for law school. Rio busted her ass in high school to get a small scholarship and then busted her ass working multiple minimum wage jobs — retail, waitressing, nannying, you name it — to cover the rest. And that’s not even mentioning the ungodly amount of student loans she took out. 

God, that woman was a bitch. An effortlessly beautiful bitch.

With the indulgence of one final sigh, Rio attempts to put her out of her mind as she straightens her shoulders and finally walks over to Thanos. “What do you want to do first?”

He flexes a bicep, room key now in hand. “I was thinking we could hit up the gym. I have to get my reps in — the grind never stops. Plus, I don’t want my lady getting chunky.” He slaps her ass before giving it a squeeze. “All those Italiano carbs.”

Rio grimaces, flinching away ever so slightly. She’s small — she’s always been small — but that doesn’t make her feel any less insecure when her husband constantly comments on her body. “Sounds good. Let’s head up to the room and change then?”

“Sure thing, babe.” He nods, shaggy blonde hair bouncing as they walk. He looks over at her with a conspiratorial grin. “I booked us the honeymoon suite.”

She wrinkles her brows. “But we aren’t on our honeymoon. And isn’t that more expensive?”

“I wanted to do something romantic for you. No need to thank me. Or, well, I can think of a different way you can thank me later.” He winks, poking the inside of his cheek with his tongue in a very unsubtle gesture. “And we’re loaded now, thanks to Stark Pharmaceuticals," he says with a laugh.

Rio hums as he opens the door. It’s…nice, admittedly. Rose petals on the bed. Giant balcony overlooking the ocean. Heart-shaped tub in the corner of the enormous space with towels folded into swans — something that’s overkill but somehow not as tacky as one might think. She’d rather be sharing it with just about anyone else, though.

“Loaded with what?” she asks, setting her purse down on the couch. The staff had already brought their suitcases up, assembled them neatly in the corner.

Thanos laughs. “Anything we want, babe. We’re richer than god now.”

“I think I’ll stick to my edibles,” she casually declares. She wouldn’t necessarily be opposed to trying something else — something a little harder — but she’s not going to do it with him. It’s awful, but she has this fear he might take advantage of her. It’s awful, but she knows it’s not an altogether irrational one. 

“You’re so cute and clueless.” He shakes his head with a chuckle as he pulls off his shirt. “Stark Pharmaceuticals is the company I invested in. The reason we now have half a billion dollars to our name.”

Oh. Right. Rio knew that. She wishes she hadn’t known that — had tried to block it from her mind and apparently managed to succeed until this very moment — but she did know that. As much as she attempted to ignore his work, some information inevitably slipped through. As does her next comment of distaste, “They’re corrupt as hell.” 

Thanos scoffs. “Tony’s not corrupt.”

“It’s no biggie — everyone does drugs on vacation. And fucking while high is the best.”

“For you. Last time you kept going when I said I was done.”

“Because I wasn’t.” He slips on a pair of shorts, casual as can be as if that’s not a huge fucking problem. Rio’s not about to make it one. Things never end well when there’s a huge fucking problem.

She rolls her eyes. “I don’t want to talk about this anymore.”

“That’s new. All you women ever seem to want to do is talk.”

She doesn’t dignify that with a response, venturing to the gym without glancing back.

Unfortunately, he’s got about a foot on her, easily catching up to her even after taking the time to slip on his tennis shoes. He possessively takes her arm in his. To the naked eye, it’d look merely protective — romantic even. He was good at appearances. They both were. “You’re acting like an ungrateful little bitch," he whisper-hisses.

“I’m not ungrateful,” she replies, stiffening the slightest bit in his hold.

“Then why do you keep complaining about every little thing?”

“I’m not complaining.” She looks at him, some odd combination of challenge and repentance in her eyes. “What do you want me to do to make you see that I’m not complaining?”

He doesn’t, of course. He never does.

This treatment was relatively tame, all things considered. The infuriating, attractive woman had completely thrown her off her game.

“Your salary’s a drop in the bucket now, and your personality fucking sucks at the moment.”

Rio sighs. She could not pick this battle. “Let’s just work out, okay?”

“I’m gonna hit the tread before I lift,” he says, letting go of her arm like nothing ever happened. And it didn't. Nothing ever happened to him.

Rio spends the next hour lifting weights. Thanos always told her to go easy on them — didn’t like his woman looking too muscular either — but she loved them. They made her feel strong. Powerful. More in control.  

By the time she leaves the gym, she’s sweating. She’s also alone once again, with Thanos announcing he wants to get extra reps in. His technique is god awful, and Rio finds herself hoping that bites him in the ass. Makes him sprain something. Break something. Even kill him, maybe.

She’s looking down at her phone, skipping a song on her playlist, when she nearly bumps into someone. She resists the urge to curse when she sees it’s the woman from earlier. Because of course it fucking is.

“I’m sorry,” she says, taking her earbud out. Apologizing had become second nature. Habitual.

The woman lets out a deep sigh. “Do watch where you’re going, won’t you?”

“Yeah,” she mutters. “My bad.” 

The combination of her tiff with Thanos and the workout has made her too tired to snark back, leaving her with no energy to match the woman’s. She’s also suddenly, annoyingly self-conscious of the way she looks. Thanos judges her, so surely this woman would, too. Any appetite she might have had from exercising disappears. She crosses her arms protectively across her chest.

The woman cocks a brow, raising her chin. “Where are you off to in such a rush anyway?”

“Just my room. I need to get away from him.” Fuck. She’s said too much again. Why did this woman have that effect on her?

The woman blinks, mask faltering for the briefest second before reappearing as if it’d never fallen at all. “The room you’re presumably sharing with him? That he has a key to? Seems an odd hiding place, hon.”

Rio’s already dug her hole, made her bed, done all of the cliche things that mean she’s screwed — she may as well dig it deeper, lie in it, etc. “He’ll be upset if I go anywhere else. Right now, he’s too busy staring at himself in the mirror while he lifts weights with poor form.”

“Hm.” The woman grunts in disapproval. “Think I’d do my best to avoid any and all reflective surfaces if I were him.”

Rio laughs — an awkward, unexpected sound but a genuine one nonetheless. She hasn’t laughed much lately. “I wish I could tell him that to his face.”

“I don’t see any reason why you couldn’t. You have a mouth; he has a face, ugly as it may be.”

Her laughter stops at that. This woman doesn’t understand. Nobody understood. “I— He wouldn’t like that. It wouldn’t be good.”

“Well, no — that’s precisely the fun of it. Believe me, pissing men off is much more fun than stroking their undersized penises and oversized egos.”

“He wouldn't react well. I'm not trying to make my life miserable."

“What’s miserable is feeling like you have to bite your tongue all the time.” A beat. “I can imagine. I’ve never actually experienced that instinct before.” The woman shrugs.

It is miserable, Rio thinks. But it’s her normal. Maybe it’s even her fault. She doesn’t know anymore. “Lucky you.”

The woman squares her shoulders. “I make my own luck.”

What must that be like, she wonders. “I’m Rio, by the way. I don’t think I ever said my name.”

The woman sticks out her hand. “Agatha. Agatha Harkness.”

Rio hums and shakes it. For some reason, this woman — in all of her insufferable haughtiness — is magnetic. “That’s a pretty name. Powerful.”

“Mm, yes — the one and only thing my mother did right was choosing it.”

“I can understand that maybe.” Rio thinks of her own mother, gone shortly after her first birthday, never to return.

“Well, the harpy’s dust now.” Agatha waves her free hand. “Past is the past. I have more relevant feuds to foster."

“With whom?”

“Roughly 30% of New Jersey. Percentage doubles if we zero in on the town of Westview.”

Rio furrows her brow. “Why?”

“Precisely 0% your business.”

She holds her hands up in surrender. “Sorry.”

“My god, you apologize a lot. It’s excruciatingly boring.”

“Well, it tends to happen when your husband gaslights you until you don’t know left from right.” Again, there was the whole business with the already dug hole and the already made bed. And maybe crude honesty would shock Agatha into not being a raging asshole.

No dice, apparently. Agatha is unfazed. “Sounds like it’s time for a divorce. I would not recommend my attorney. Overpriced cunt.”

“Being an apathetic cunt isn’t cute either,” she hears herself retorting. “And if you remember — which you probably don't because you probably weren't actually listening — I’m a lawyer myself.”

“Ohh, aren’t we a feisty little thing?” Agatha asks, amused. “Believe it or not, dear, I was just trying to help, but I’ll nip that right in the bud — I’m not in the habit of helping people who are unwilling to help themselves. Be your own attorney then. Or don’t.” She shrugs. “It really has no bearing on my life.”

Rio sighs, running a hand down her face. This is really not her day. “Look, it’s more complicated than that. Today, he’s a dick, and I’m pissed at him. Tomorrow, he’ll be sweet, and I’ll feel bad for ever thinking that way. I know, objectively, it’s…not great, but I’m trying to get there.” She’s being honest with Agatha, and in the process, she’s being honest with herself — maybe for the first time in her life. She’s never said the quiet part out loud before.

“It doesn’t sound complicated. It sounds simple and incredibly fucking bleak to me.”

“That’s what everyone says. At least people who don’t understand what it’s like.” Which did, in fact, seem to be ‘everyone.’ Rio shakes her head. This was so stupid. She was so stupid. “I’ll see you,” she says, making a move to go around her.

Agatha easily steps in front of her once more — it was quickly becoming their little dance. Rio wants to shove her hard out of the way, forget about her. Rio wants her to do it again and again and again, see her every day for the rest of her life. 

“You do that a lot, don’t you?” Agatha asks. “Start a conversation and then abruptly end it when you don’t like what you hear?”

“I end a conversation when I’m being disrespected,” she says firmly, her court voice coming out. “If you’re interested in actually learning about me and my situation, we can talk at a bar or something — not a hallway.”

“You’ll end a conversation but not a marriage. How peculiar.” Agatha tilts her head, squinting at her. “Okay, you can buy me a drink."

She thinks, 'Fuck no, you crazy bitch — I was obviously just calling your bluff.'

She says, “Tomorrow? After dinner?”

“Why not tonight?" Agatha replies. "After dinner?”

“I don’t want to deal with the drama of telling him I’ve made last-minute plans.” She’s never this blunt — not outside her job — but bluntness seems to work for Agatha.

“Oh.” She blinks. “I suppose it didn’t cross my mind that you were actually planning on telling him the truth. I forget people do that — the whole honesty thing.”

“Tomorrow,” Rio simply replies. “Hotel bar. 8pm.”

“8:30,” Agatha coolly corrects. “I put Nicky to bed at 8, and he makes me sing at least two songs before he’ll even shut his eyes.”

“Fine,” Rio agrees, sidestepping her once again — successfully this time. “See you then.”

She doesn’t know what the fuck just came over her, what the fuck just possessed her to do that, who the fuck that person impersonating Rio was back there just now.

And she doesn’t know what the fuck this feeling in her stomach is either — some awful cocktail of anxiety and fear and regret. So much regret.

And she doesn’t know why the fuck she’s smiling. Why the fuck she feels giddy and alive and so much like herself for the first time in a long, long while.

Chapter 3: Day 2, Part 1

Chapter Summary

A frightening incident has Rio and Agatha reuniting sooner than either of them anticipated.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Dinner with Thanos…well, it happens. Rio mostly dissociates through it — pretends she’s somewhere else. (Lying by the ocean, floating in the pool, already having drinks with Agatha.) The trend continues as he fucks her — pretends he’s someone else. (Penélope Cruz, that paralegal who works at her friend’s office, Agatha.)

He’s rough. Too rough. Rough in a way that’s not at all enjoyable for her, though she can’t imagine it’d be all that enjoyable for her if he was gentle either. It’s not the roughness that’s the problem. Still, she lets him do it without complaint, needing him in a good mood for when she turns out the light a little after midnight and says, “I’m meeting a friend for drinks tomorrow.”

“Friend?” he asks, voice laced with suspicion. “What friend?”

“I met her here.” Then, “She’s a mom. She and I talked about kids. Thought she could give me some advice.” She’s trying to play into the housewife of it all — his perfect, submissive fantasy.

It works like a charm. God, Thanos was so predictable — except when he wasn’t. “That’s great, babe. You know I want at least three, and you’re not getting any younger.” He puts a hand on her stomach. She resists the urge to squirm or slap it away.

“What do you mean ‘at least’? What’s your ideal number?”

“I dunno. Four? Five?” he says flippantly. “Does this mean you’re finally thinking about quitting that silly little job of yours?”

Rio frowns. “No. I like work.”

“Well, soon, you’ll be doing more important work — cooking our basketball team of kids…” He rubs her belly. “And then cooking for our basketball team of kids.” He laughs at his own joke.

“My job is important, too,” she mumbles, closing her eyes. “I wouldn’t be picking between them.”

He gives the skin of her stomach a squeeze. “Motherhood is the most important job a woman can have. It’s a biological fact.”

She clenches her jaw. “You’re conflating a biological purpose with a societally defined role.”

“You getting all academic is such a boner-killer,” he whines.

“Good,” she mutters, rolling onto her side. “I need to sleep,” 

He removes his hand from her stomach. “God, what happened to you? You used to be fun — not this…this uptight feminazi.”

She doesn’t respond, curling into herself and willing sleep. She’s always been miserable, but talking to Agatha so candidly…it’s like it finally made her realize just how miserable.

Thanos huffs, put out, before shoving himself out of bed. “I’m going for a nightcap.”

Luckily for Rio, that nightcap must have turned into two or three or four, as Thanos is still dead asleep by the time she wakes up the next morning, meaning she can start her day with some too-rare, much coveted alone time. She skips breakfast and heads straight to the beach, sending him a text to let him know what cabana she’ll be in. 

Reading and swimming take up most of the morning. At one point, the exhaustion of it — the inherent toll that living with him takes on her — hits, and she lies sprawled out on her chair, people-watching. A couple walking hand-in-hand. A child picking up shells. A group of teen girls giggling, huddling around a phone. They seem happy. She wonders if they really are. Rio probably seemed happy, too. Seemed like she lived a fairytale life.

A while into observing this carousel of people, she sees a little boy frantically looking around, no adult in sight. She sits up straighter and squints, recognizing him as Agatha’s son upon closer examination.

She gets up from the chair, walking toward him slower than usual so as not to frighten him. “Hey,” she says gently. “What’s wrong?”

He looks up at her, eyes wide and watery. “Can’t…” He sucks in a shaky breath, thumb going to his mouth — a nervous habit that, if Rio had to guess, he hadn’t indulged in for years now. “Find my Mama.”

“Do you want help?”

“Mm,” he lets out a little whine around his thumb, cowering away. “Not supposed to talk to strangers.”

She puts a hand to her chest. “I’m Rio. I met your mom the other night, and I promise I just want to help you. Can you tell me where you last saw her?”

“There.” He points up the beach closer to the resort. There’s a large group gathered taking painting lessons, another doing a cocktail-making class. “I saw a seagull — he was my friend — so I ran after him.”

Rio nods as if this is perfectly understandable. “Let’s walk up together and try to find your mom. Is that okay?”

He looks at her, brows furrowing. “Are you going to kidnap me?” 

“Nope. You can even lead the way."

He continues staring at her suspiciously. “You pinky swear you won’t kidnap me?”

Rio crouches down to his level, holding her finger out. “Pinky swear. I know things like this can be scary.”

He nods again, a fresh round of tears bubbling up in his eyes as he locks his finger around hers. “Want my mama,” he admits, the confession causing them to spill over onto his cheeks.

“Yeah,” he agrees, wiping his tears with his free fist as they begin to walk. “Do you have another name, too? That your mama uses? A longer one?”

“Oh.” Nicky nods. “I don’t have a dad. I have two moms, but they don’t like each other anymore.”

“No,” he agrees. “You can share my mom with me if you want.”

Rio stifles a laugh. She certainly wouldn’t mind having Agatha as...something. A very different kind of mommy maybe. She chastises herself for entertaining the thought as soon as it pops into her head. “That’s very sweet of you.”

Because he’s opened the door like this, it’s harmless — she tells herself — to do the smallest bit of prying. Try as she might, she can’t resist asking about Agatha. Nicky is presumably one of the people who knows her best, after all, even if he was a child. “What’s your mom like?”

“She’s silly,” he says, which surprises her more than it maybe should. She did have a wicked wit to her, but she sort of assumed she might be the stricter type when it came to her kid. “She makes up funny songs and takes me to the playground when I’m not feeling yucky.”

Her heart melts a little at that. “She sounds like a very good mom. What about pets? Do you have any of those?”

“Yeah.” He perks up a bit at that, some anxiety temporarily fading away. “A bunny rabbit named Señor Scratchy.”

“Señor Scratchy, huh? Do you happen to know Spanish, or was that just the perfect name no matter what?”

“Un poco,” he says proudly. “I watch Dora even though the kids at school say it’s just for girls.”

“It’s not just for girls,” Rio assures him. “And do you want to know something about me?”

He nods, peering up at her curiously.

“Hablo español,” she says, speaking clearly and a bit slower than normal so Nicky can process it.

His eyes widen in wonder. “No waaay. That’s so cooool.”

She chuckles. “Do you have any words you really want to know?”

“Bunny! And pool. And ice cream.” He frowns a little. “I guess that last one is two words.”

“Well, bunny is conejito, pool is piscina, and ice cream is helado.”

“Conejito, piscina, helado. Conejito, piscina, helado. Conejito, piscina, helado,” he repeats in a sing-song voice. “I know all my colors already. I’ll prove it. What’s your favorite?”

Rio hums with a playful smile, thinking. “Green,” she decides. “Forest green.”

He gasps. “That’s my favorite! Verde! Mama’s favorite is purple morado, and Mom’s is red rojo.”

“Great job,” she praises. “Those are all very good colors. Do you know how to say that your favorite color is green in Spanish?”

“Mm…” He narrows his eyes in focus. “Mi color…favorito…es…verde?” he tries.

“Yeah, that’s right,” she encourages, her smile growing. “Good job.” She wonders briefly if her own kids would be like this. If they could. If something that was half of Thanos could possibly be so sweet. If her love for and from them — her hypothetical children — could make up for the lack of it for and from him. 

Nicky mirrors her expression, clearly proud of himself. She sees his tiny shoulders drop, some tension leaving them. “Rio?”

“Hm?”

“What’s your favorite food? And your favorite animal?”

She taps her chin. “Well, I really like sweet potatoes, and my favorite animal…would probably have to be a cloud leopard. What about you?”

“Ice cream,” he replies easily. “And bunnies. Helado y conejuto,” he says, pride growing that he’d remembered.

“Nice job.” She smiles again. “What grade are you in?”

He holds up a single finger. “First. I have to miss it sometimes to go see the doctors, but Mommy and Mama say that I’m so smart it makes up for it.”

“Well, you seem very smart.” She nods. “Do you like school?”

“Sometimes.” He shrugs, his smile faltering a little as he looks down at the ground.

She cranes down to look at him. “Sometimes?” she gently presses.

He shrugs again, face flushing with embarrassment.

“It’s okay,” she soothes, deciding not to push further. She understood better than anyone not wanting people to pry about certain things — press delicate subjects. “Sometimes, school isn’t great, for whatever reason. Rio hesitates for a split second before pursing her lips and nodding. “Yeah. Sometimes, kids can be cruel. It sucks.”

“A few of them did. They made fun of how I looked and how my dad talked.”

Nicky looks genuinely confused. “But you’re so pretty.”

Rio breathes out a little laugh. “Thank you — that’s very kind. She could count the number of non-white students at her small Catholic school on one hand. “There weren’t a lot of other parents who talked like my dad either. He had an accent and didn’t speak a lot of English, so they couldn’t always figure out what he was saying.”

“Oh.” Nicky frowns.

“Yeah. But I think I turned out pretty okay, even if it hurt.”

Nicky bites the inside of his cheek. “They make fun of me because I have two moms,” he quietly admits. “And because I have to use an inhaler and wear a vest that shakes my chest sometimes.”

“Well, neither of those things are bad. Families come in all shapes and sizes.” She lowers her voice a little. “Do you wanna know a secret?”

He nods seriously. “I won’t tell anyone,” he promises with a whisper.

“I have something called POTS. It’s an acronym for a long word, but basically, my nervous system is deregulated, so sometimes I’d black out at school or have really intense reactions to things. People could be mean about it, which made me feel sad for a long time, but finally, I learned that my illness doesn’t make me bad.”

He nods again — slowly this time, trying to process it. Rio hopes it helps. Her dad would tell her every day that her health didn’t define her, but it took a cashier at the grocery store of all people — one who happened to have POTS as well — for it to finally click. A stranger who actually knew what it was like.

“Did you fight back and not let them push you around?” Nicky asks. “Or were you the bigger person?”

“Sometimes, I’d push back. Eventually, I learned to let it go most of the time. It was hard to do that, but I learned that no matter what you do, some people just don’t understand and are never going to try to.”

“I think it’s just two different people having two different responses,” she tenderly reasons. “Both can be valid and useful.”

“I’m sorry. I can imagine that’s really rough.”

“Yeah.” His shoulders hunch a bit. “I don’t like it when they yell.”

“It can be really overwhelming,” she agrees, mind flickering to Thanos.

She snaps out of it when she finally spots who they're looking for talking to a resort employee. “Agatha!” she calls.

Agatha briefly glances over. It's clear she could not give less of a fuck about Rio at the moment. “Not now,” she snaps, turning back to the poor, terrified employee. Rio doesn't read lips or anything, but Agatha's not exactly being quiet. She's pretty sure she can make out the words 'woefully incompetent' and 'fucking moron.'

Rio sighs. “Agatha!” she repeats. “I found Nicky!”

Her head whips back over to Rio at that — and then down a little.

“Oh my god,” Agatha says, over at them in an instant. She kneels down and wraps Nick in a crushing hug. “My baby. My baby.” She rocks him back and forth, back and forth. “I was so worried.” 

Nick lets her do it — for a few moments at least. “Mama…” he eventually whines. “You’re squeezing me.” 

“I don’t care,” she says, voice devoid of any sympathy. She sniffles as she pulls back just enough to look at him, hands on his arms. “Don’t ever scare Mama like that again.” His head dips in shame, and she puts a hand under his chin, tilting it back up. “Do you understand me?” 

“Yes,” he says, voice small. “I’m sorry, Mama.” Agatha takes a deep, shaky breath before pulling him close once more.

Rio stands there, awkwardly watching. The selfless part of her wants to reassure Agatha he was really all right. The selfish part of her just doesn’t want to go back to where she’s sure Thanos is sitting by now. Doesn’t want to leave Agatha. 

She lets them have their moment before she clears her throat. “If it helps any, he was safe on the beach. Nothing bad happened. I saw him, and we started looking for you — that’s all.”

Agatha, ever suspicious, pulls back to look at Nick — scans his body for injuries before meeting his eyes again to confirm whether this is true. 

“Rio took care of me, Mama,” Nick promises. “And she taught me Spanish.” 

Agatha quirks a brow at him. “Did she now?” 

“El helado, el conejuto, la piscina,” he recites. 

The corner of Agatha’s mouth curves into the smallest of smiles. She plants a kiss on his temple. “That’s very good, darling.”

She looks at Rio and clears her throat, preparing to say two words that didn’t come easy for her. “Thank you.”

“Of course.” Rio shrugs. “Maybe you can repay me by buying me a drink,” she ventures.

Her nonchalant demeanor falls back into place. “We’ll see.”

Sure enough, Thanos is sitting on Rio’s chair once she wanders back. “Where the hell have you been?” he asks by way of greeting. “The strawberry daiquiri I got you is almost completely melted.”

“I was helping a little boy find his mom.” Surely, he couldn’t be pissed at that, right?

Wrong. “Of course.” He rolls his eyes. “You and your bleeding heart.”

Rio resists the urge to roll her own. “Weren’t you just talking about being parental last night?”

“With our kids — our own flesh and blood — not some snot-nosed little brat we don’t even know.”

“I didn’t want anything bad happening to him.”

“Something bad could happen to you. God, Rio — are you that stupid? Do you not see the Facebook posts my mom shares? Human traffickers use kids to lure women into sex slavery all the time. Are you dumb enough to become a sex slave?”

She’s used to his bullshit, but fuck, this was a new level she hadn’t previously known existed. You already treat me like one, she narrowly resists the urge to say. Instead, she simply shakes her head. “I’m going for a walk.”

“You just went for a fucking walk.”

“Well, I’m going for another.” She turns back toward the resort.

He grabs her wrist — firm but not enough to bruise or draw attention from the other people on the beach. “Sit down, Rio,” he quietly growls. “Drink your drink and stop embarrassing me.”

Rio stiffens, a chill running through her. “No one is paying attention to us.” It’s true. The couples are still on their romantic walks. The kids are still building their castles out of sand. The teenage girls are still laughing at their phones. The world keeps spinning and spinning and spinning. Her vision is beginning to do the same.

“Sit. The fuck. Down,” he repeats.

Rio is frozen. She’s frozen except for her head, which she manages to shake — a weak, ‘No.’

“Rio,” he warns. “You’re going to make a scene.”

“I won’t if you just let go,” she promises, voice squeaking ever so slightly with panic. She fucking hates it. She fucking hates it so much. And she hates the next word more, “Please.”

“Are you going to walk away from me?”

“I just want to have a minute,” she desperately explains.

“You can have a minute with me — you can have all the minutes you fucking want with me — but you’re not going anywhere.”

“Please, let me go.” She attempts to pull her arm away. His grip only tightens — hand twisting her wrist the slightest bit. Rio winces, pulling harder out of instinct. “Thanos. Please.”

His hold gets tighter, too. “Then sit. Down.”

Rio whimpers under her breath, her increasingly blurry vision leaving her with no choice but to comply. She lowers herself into the chair, unable to meet his gaze.

He holds on for another moment before finally releasing her, handing her the daiquiri like nothing ever happened. “That wasn’t so hard now, was it?”

Rio grits her teeth but takes a sip of the drink anyway. Alcohol probably wasn’t the best idea at the moment, but she needed something cold — something to shock her system out of the nightmarish daze he’d put her in.

“I asked you a question.”

“What the hell do you want me to say?” His treatment of her wasn’t new, but her reaction was. She was never this bold — put up this much of a fight. 

“It’s a simple yes or no — isn’t it easier when you remember your place instead of forcing me to put you in it?”

Rio glares at him over her glass. “I’m supposed to be your equal.”

He laughs, dark and hollow. “Whatever gave you that ridiculous notion?”

“I don’t know — maybe the fact we live in the 21st century?”

“The fact that society has gone woke doesn’t change that men are the stronger, dominant sex — the head of the households.”

“That’s not true,” she argues. “That’s a pigheaded belief from colonialism.”

“I told you last night, it’s so not sexy when you talk like that.”

“Well, I don’t care. I’m not just here to be sexy for you.”

“That’s exactly what you’re here for — exactly what you signed up to do when you said ‘I do.’ You’re my trophy wife. Your entire purpose is to look pretty on my arm. It’s the easiest job in the fucking world, and you still can’t manage to do it.” He shakes his head, downing his gin and tonic. “Fucking pathetic.”

She half flinches, the fight quickly draining from her. The fire evaporating into smoke — dissipating in defeat. “But you know I have a job I love,” she says softly. “You said that was okay, and now suddenly, it isn’t.”

“Hobbies. You were allowed to have hobbies as long as you put me first and understood how this worked. But you haven’t been, and it seems you’ve forgotten the terms.”

“You didn’t say that.”

“I shouldn’t have to say it!” he snaps. A few people look over at them. He lowers his voice back to a harsh whisper. “I shouldn’t have to fucking spell it out for you.”

She ducks her head. “You said you didn’t mind me working,” she quietly reminds him. “That’s verbatim.”

“Until we had kids," he clarifies. "Which I’ve been wanting to start trying to have for years now, but you’ve been dragging your feet.”

“You fuck me all the time,” she can’t resist pointing out — the last spark of snark. “It’s not my fault it’s not taking.”

“I wouldn’t be surprised if you’re still secretly on the pill,” he retorts. “Lying, sneaky bitch you are.”

Fuck, she’s exhausted. This was exhausting. “Why do you feel the need to call me that?”

“Because you feel the need to act like that. Everything I do is the result of your own actions, Rio.”

Rio hates the power those words have. Hates the way they sting. Hates the way she believes them, deep down. She wants to crawl out of her skin, but she settles for picking up her phone and mindlessly scrolling for a few minutes.

Thanos flags one of the cabana boys to bring him another gin and tonic. “Who are you talking to on that thing?”

“Nobody. I’m on Instagram.”

He grabs the phone from her hand, looking through himself. “Who the fuck is this?” he asks, turning the screen so she can see what he’s referencing — a man she seems to be following.

“That’s a film director.” She holds her hand out. “Who’s married,” she adds. “We’ve seen his stuff, at least some of it. He did Hush.”

“Oh, right. I hated that piece of trash,” he says, clicking the unfollow button and scrolling further. “And him?” He turns the screen again.

“I don’t follow him,” she points to the top of the screen. “It’s just the algorithm. Give me my phone, please,” she says as calmly as possible — as if reasoning with a child.

He snatches his arm back, holding it out of her reach. “Why would your algorithm be showing you other dudes? It's based on your searches and interests."

“Probably because I follow actors who have been in movies with him. I’m not attracted to him.” Or most men, she resists the urge to say.

“I don’t care if he’s an actor or a milkman or the fucking president — I don’t want you looking at pictures of other guys.”

She sighs, doing the only thing she can — relent. “Fine. I’ll scroll past those posts. Can I have my phone now?”

He considers. “If I find out you’re lying, I’ll break your phone and then your hand,” he warns before reluctantly handing it back.

Rio nods, a shiver traveling down her spine. She knows he means it.

Chapter 4: Day 2, Part 2

Chapter Summary

Rio and Agatha finally get that drink.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha ultimately decides on a purple sundress for drinks, the thin straps showing off her slightly burned shoulders. The sun exposure has brought out a few freckles as well, lightly dotting her cheeks and the bridge of her nose. She’s not usually big on hair or makeup — not since Nicky, anyway; no time — but she swipes some mascara onto her lashes and actually runs a brush through her hair before she leaves the hotel room.

After she sings Nicky his promised two songs, that is. And makes sure the iPad is set up in the corner of his room. She finally figured out how to get it to livestream onto an app installed on her phone so she could check in on him periodically. It took a lot of YouTube tutorials and cursing at an IT guy over the phone to figure it out. She’s pretty sure she made him cry. She doesn’t want to talk about it. Her struggle with technology, that is. Making him cry had been therapeutic and fun.

Agatha never feels underdressed — never feels inadequate period — but she feels a little twinge of something close to insecurity in her gut as Rio struts over in a green velvet slip dress. That — and a big stir of desire at her core. Fuck, she was hot. Has she always been this hot? 

“Got all dressed up just for me, did you, hot stuff?”

That’s all it takes to make Rio’s newly tanned cheeks flush. “You don’t look too bad yourself,” she says, sliding into the barstool next to her.

“Oh, this? It’s just something I threw on,” she lies with a dismissive wave of her hand. She’d spent far too long picking it out. Which is to say, window shopping and then stealing it from one of the local ritzy boutiques.

“Mhm.” Rio nods, eyes raking over Agatha. She knows then that going through the trouble of shoplifting had been worth it. “I usually drink a negroni.”

She scoffs. “Are you under the impression that I’m your bartender?”

“No, but I’m under the impression you’ll buy the lady a drink.”

“Actually, the original deal was that you buy me one. If you’ll recall.”

Rio’s lips jut into an adorable little pout. “But I was your knight in shining armor today.”

Agatha lifts her chin a little. It was hard to argue with that. “Then I suppose we’re even. Which means we can each pay for our own — or we can stay for at least two rounds, both get one.”

“I’ll cover the first,” Rio replies, glancing down at the menu despite already knowing what she’s going to order. People seemed to struggle with that — looking Agatha in the eyes for too long. “What do you drink?”

“Wine. And not the cheap shit.”

“I would never,” Rio promises. “Not for a woman like you.”

“What do you mean by that?” she baits. “A woman like me?”

“Beautiful,” she answers easily. “Self-assured.”

Agatha raises her brows a bit, amused and marginally surprised at the forwardness. “True.”

Rio gives her a little smirk before ordering their drinks, choosing a very respectable red for Agatha. “How’s Nicky doing after that scare today?”

“Better than ever,” she deadpans. “It was ‘Ms. Rio this’ and ‘Ms. Rio that’ all afternoon.” Her worst nightmare had seemed to be a highlight of the trip for him so far. Little shit. He was lucky she loved him so much.

“Oh?” Rio laughs. “What did he say?”

“What didn’t he? He was very talkative. And more bilingual than usual.”

“He seemed excited that I was fluent in Spanish.”

“Yes, he’s…a curious one.” Agatha takes her wine from the bartender. “A nerd, really.”

“It’s sweet, though. It’s nice to see a kid who wants to learn. You’ve done a good job parenting — it’s clear he loves you.”

“He’s easy.” She throws back a long sip of her wine. Nobody had ever said that to her before — that she was doing a good job parenting. The last few years seemed to be all about pointing out how fucking terrible she was at it. At everything.

“Still,” Rio presses. “He’s a good kid. You must be doing something right.”

“He’s the best,” Agatha agrees. “Very intelligent. Very chatty. I just hope it doesn’t evolve into mouthy during his teenage years.”

“Who knows.” Rio shrugs, taking a sip of her negroni. “I don’t have kids, and I don’t want to with him, so I can’t really speak on that.”

Agatha cocks a brow. “‘With him’ — you don’t want to ‘with him.’”

“Yeah.” Rio glances down, swirling the cocktail around in her glass. “He wants them with me. He wants…well, think classic conservative nuclear family.”

“I’d rather blow my brains out.”

Rio nods, pursing her lips. “So would I,” she softly admits before falling quiet. “You know…” she says after a long moment. “You know, I lied to myself for years that I liked him.” She shakes her head a little, breathing out a humorless laugh. “That I like men. Talking so frankly to you yesterday made something click about how fucked up it all is. How fucked up he is.”

“You’re welcome?” Agatha says slowly. “Or…congratulations on finally seeing the very obvious blinding light? I clocked him the minute I laid eyes on him.” She takes another sip.

“You may have,” Rio relents, still staring at her drink. “But he was kind when I first met him, and he got along with my dad. He was the easy answer — what I thought I was supposed to want. Marrying him was what I thought I was supposed to do, you know?”

Agatha did not know. Agatha never thought about what she was supposed to do — what other people thought she should — much less cared. Still, she senses that this is a rhetorical question and makes the rare decision to stay quiet.

“And it was…okay, for a while,” Rio continues. “Not exciting or fulfilling but okay.” She takes a breath. “But then he started telling me I couldn’t do certain things or associate with certain people. I’d try to talk to him — try to reason with him — but he’d either wear me down or make me feel guilty. Gaslight me into thinking I was doing something wrong — that the way he was treating me was my fault.” Clearly uncomfortable at the admission, she downs half her drink in one go.

“I…suppose I can understand that,” Agatha says, running her finger around the rim of her wine glass. “To a degree.” Things were good when she first met Wanda, too. It had never gotten to that point, but it had certainly gotten ugly.

“It sucks because I’m a lawyer. Like, I’m not stupid, you know? I never thought this would happen to me…” Rio chews on the inside of her cheek. “But it’s not really about how smart you are. And he’s not stupid either. Not about this. He knows how to get in my head. He knows how to twist my words. He never leaves bruises anywhere people would see unless you can easily make an excuse about it. He acts like he loves me, but really, he just loves fucking me no matter how much I say no.”

Jesus, Agatha was in over her head. Luckily, she was very good at pretending she wasn’t. 

“You know that’s against the law, right?” Agatha asks. “Being a lawyer and all? My feeling on most laws is that they’re meant to be broken, but ones concerning…” She makes a few circles with her hand. “…that? Well, let’s just say that if I were you, I’d break a few laws of my own.” Which wasn’t saying much, of course — she’d broken a lot more laws for a whole lot less.

Rio squirms in her seat. “I just don’t know how to get…untrapped from him.”

“Sometimes, escaping a trap requires gnawing your own leg off,” Agatha says, finishing her wine in one last gulp. Another thing she’s learned about survival was that it was often an ugly, painful thing — sometimes uglier and more painful than death might be. Still, it was worth it. To Agatha, it was always worth it.

“I have to do it right,” Rio whispers. “If I don’t, I’m afraid he might kill me.”

“Not if you kill him first,” Agatha says, tone making it unclear how much she’s joking — if at all.

“Mm…” Rio hums, no more clarity in her own voice. “That could be self-defense, I suppose. Maybe righteous justice.”

Agatha flags the bartender down, motioning him to get them another round. “And presumably very satisfying."

“I’m not sure I’d feel satisfied. I’d probably just be…relieved.”

“Relief is still a hell of a lot better than misery, no?”

Rio tilts her head in tentative agreement, thinking. “The way he fucked me up, I’m not sure I'd have many prospects after.”

Agatha snorts, indulging in another scan of her body. “Oh pul-lease. Look at you.”

Rio looks up at her then. “What does that mean?” she coyly inquires.

She doesn’t take the bait — won’t make it that easy for her. “You know damn well what it means.”

“You could still humor me. Or…show me what you mean?” she ventures, taking a sip of her second negroni.

“Show you?” Agatha lifts her brows, pretends to ponder. “Well, that’s an interesting idea. Though I’m not sure you’re prepared for all that.”

“Don’t underestimate me. I can handle myself.”

“You sure about that?” she asks, testing the waters by gently running the top of her sandaled foot up Rio’s bare leg, watching her for any microreaction.

Rio bites her bottom lip, glancing around a little before taking Agatha’s hand and setting it on her thigh. “I’m sure. Are you sure you can handle me?”

“Easy, tiger,” Agatha says, moving her hand back down to settle on Rio’s knee — though she notably slides it under the hem of her dress. She leans forward, whispering in her ear. “But I’m absolutely positive I can handle you in ways you’ve never been handled before.”

Agatha sees the little hairs stand up on her neck. “I hope you can live up to all of these promises. I’m getting excited.”

“Mm, I’m sure you are.”

“Oh, yeah?” Rio asks, leaning back enough to look at her. “What exactly do you think is happening here?”

For once, she lets his words wash over her — nothing but a fleeting, inconsequential wave in the ocean. She rolls her eyes. “My whole life doesn’t revolve around sex or men.” 

“Don’t worry — you’ve made that obnoxiously clear with your incessant bitching and moaning and holding out on me.”

“Do you realize how insolent you sound?”

“Oh, that’s rich coming from you.”

Rio sighs. He was relentless. That’s what it always came down to. He was terrifying, but more than that, he was exhausting. “Can you just calm down?”

“Also rich. You hate it when I tell you to calm down. You’re such a fucking hypocrite it makes me sick.”

“If you don’t calm down, they’ll see the bruises and question you,” she says, attempting to appeal to his nonexistent reasoning skills.

“Not when you tell them you’re clumsy — a real stupid klutz who’s always hurting herself by accident. And who’s ‘they,’ huh? Nobody here gives a shit about you. Nobody anywhere gives a shit about you — except me. I’m all you have, Rio. I’m all you’ll ever have. The only one who will ever love you.”

That’s enough to make her stop. Enough to make her blood freeze in her veins. She thinks of Agatha’s words: ‘I’d want Nicky to tell me.’ “I’m going to tell my dad about what you do,” she threatens, voice more serious than it’s ever been.

Thanos is unfazed. “You’re threatening me with crying to daddy? Your dirt poor daddy who couldn’t even afford to pay your college tuition?”

Her blood turns to a boil. Because it was one thing to insult her, but bringing her father into things? “Shut up,” she hisses. Don’t talk about him like that.”

“What are you gonna do, hm?” Thanos asks. It’s weird having the roles reversed like this. While Rio was getting riled, Thanos’ voice was even — dangerously so. “What is he gonna do? Money is power, and I have a whole lot more of it than either of you. I can make people believe your bruises are from an accident. I can make people believe a lot of things are just an accident.”

Rio feels nauseous again. “Did you just threaten to kill me?”

Thanos looks at her — gaze ominous in how calm it is. How cold it is, too. “Now you’re just talking crazy. You should be thrown into the looney bin. Locked up. I’m sure that could be arranged, too — for your own safety, of course.”

“The world doesn’t work like that anymore,” she spits.

“My world does.” 

And the scary thing is, he’s right. With the money he has now, the network of people he can access…

“That’s so fucked up,” is all Rio can manage, trying to keep the shakiness from her voice.

“Well, it’s the truth. If you don’t believe me, feel free to keep testing me and see what becomes of you.”

“I’m going to have dinner,” she announces before turning on her heel and beelining to Agatha’s table. She can feel Thanos trailing close behind.

“I respect the commitment to being fashionably late, dear,” Agatha starts, scanning her menu as Rio slides into her seat. “But I don’t like to be kept waiti—”

She glances up, removing her reading glasses. Her eyes travel from Rio to Thanos and back to Rio again. “Oh. You have company.”

Chapter End Notes
