Chapter 8: Day 3, Part 2

Chapter Summary

Agatha meets Thanos and bullies a waiter.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Thanos helps himself to a nearby chair, pulling it to the side of the table between Agatha and Rio. He plops down into it like he owns the place — because, in his mind, he probably does — ignoring the odd looks from the occupied table he took it from. 

“Don’t be rude, honey,” Thanos chastises Rio, reaching his hand under the table and placing it — rough and territorial — on her thigh. He sticks the other out to Agatha. “I’m Thanos. Rio’s husband.” 

“Agatha,” she replies simply, taking his sweaty and fishlike palm. She shoots Rio a glance like, ‘How do you want me to play this?’ Deferring. Not something she does often. Not something she does ever. But this is a delicate situation, and she doesn’t want to make things worse for Rio. She…cares…about her.

“We’re having dinner, Thanos,” Rio says curtly. “I promise our conversation isn’t going to be very interesting to you. Why don’t you go on that boating trip you mentioned?”

“They only do boat rides during the day, and I want to get to know your friend.” He turns to Agatha. “She’s hardly told me anything about you,” he says like it's some biting dig. Agatha resists the urge to laugh in his hideous face. He picks up the menu and begins to peruse. “I’ll at least stay for a drink. What’s good?”

“Maybe all three of us can have dinner tomorrow,” Rio suggests, desperately attempting to divert his attention elsewhere — at least for the time being. “Besides, didn’t you promise the guy we met at wine tasting you’d grab a beer with him tonight?”

His fingers dig into her thigh under the table. Above it, however, he seems calm — to the untrained eye, at least. The untrained ear that couldn’t pick up the danger underlying it when he says, “What’s the rush, babe?” with a seemingly harmless laugh. “Trying to get rid of me?”

“That’s all right, Rio — you can tell him the truth,” Agatha steps in, turning to Thanos as if letting him in on a secret. “She’s trying to keep me from making a terrible first impression,” she says bashfully, adopting a persona akin to a mother in a 1950s sitcom.  

“I told this one that I’m positively desperate for some more girl time,” she continues, nodding over at Rio. “We had a hoot last night, and between my son and husband, it’s all testosterone in my house all the time. Even our rabbit is a boy — Señor Scratchy!” She throws her head back and laughs.  

She then grows more serious, leaning in closer and lowering her voice — even managing to conjure a slight blush into her cheeks. She really was an excellent performer — a talented liar. “And I’m a little embarrassed to admit it, but my marriage with my dear Ralph could use some…spicing up if you know what I mean. Rio went on and on last night about how wonderful her relationship with you is, and I was hoping she could give me some advice, lady to lady.”

Thanos narrows his eyes, a little skeptical — but only a little. Agatha was very convincing, and he was very stupid. “You didn’t have time to cover that last night? She was out until morning.” 

“Oh.” Agatha covers her face, faking embarrassment. “I am so sorry about that. I was having so much fun that I just didn’t want the night to end. I kept ordering more and more drinks, and Rio was too polite to decline. Naughty of me, I know! But I assure you it will not happen again.”

“See?” Rio says with a grateful smile. “It’ll be fine. You should go enjoy yourself.”

Thanos looks between them. “You’ll make sure she’s back at a reasonable hour this time?” 

“Of course,” Agatha promises, putting a hand on her chest. Cross her heart and hope he fucking dies. “Yes, sir.” 

There’s another beat before he somewhat reluctantly stands up. “All right. I’ll see you later.” He gives Rio a look, a subtle warning, before turning to Agatha. “Nice to meet you.” 

“The pleasure is all mine,” Agatha assures him, plastering on a huge grin as he walks away.

After he’s out of eye- and earshot, it immediately falls. She rolls her eyes, putting her reading glasses on again — seamlessly snapping back into herself. “Dumb fuck,” she mutters, picking up her menu. “What are you getting to drink?” she casually asks.

“God, anything that’ll help me forget that I live with that. Double vodka on the rocks, maybe.”

“Easy, tiger — I met you two days ago and already know you’re a lightweight.”

Rio scoffs. “I’m not that much of a lightweight. Plus, after my day, I need it.”

“Texting me was so terrible it’s driven you to the bottle?”

“No, that was the highlight of the day. Him forcing me to suck him off is what’s driving that.”

Agatha’s hand balls into a subtle fist under the table. She would love nothing more than to slam Thanos’ head into the stupid fucking chair he swiped, but she could not get too involved. Not in this. Not with Rio. “Has that moved the needle at all on what we discussed last night?”

“A bit, yes. Though I’m a little afraid he might beat me to the punch.”

“That’s why you’d hypothetically want to act fast.”

“Hypothetically, I’m seriously considering it.”

“Well, we probably shouldn’t talk business around all these witnesses, darling,” Agatha cautions. She was a criminal but not a careless one. “Best to stick to pleasure right now.”

Rio raises a brow. “Is that so.”

“Unless you’d like to talk about the weather or, god forbid, a sports team,” Agatha says dryly as a lanky waiter with curly brown hair finally approaches their table.

“Good evening. My name’s Bil—”

“Took you long enough,” Agatha cuts him off before he can get through his spiel. Why everyone thought she gave a shit about their name was a mystery to her. “Two vodkas — doubles — on the rocks.”

Rio gives the waiter a small look of thanks before turning back to Agatha. “Pleasure is perfectly fine with me.”

“All right.” Agatha nods. Then, without missing a beat, “What color underwear do you plan on leaving in my room tonight?”

Rio adorably chokes on her water, though she recovers impressively quickly. “Well, I’m not currently wearing any, so…”

“Pity.” Agatha sips her own water. “The pair I have might get lonely.”

“We have a few nights left — a few more chances for you to amass a collection.”

“Not nearly enough.” Ew. What the fuck. She sounds desperate. And Agatha Harkness is not desperate.

“Who says this has to be the end of it?” Rio asks with a mischievous little smile.

Agatha gives her one in return, though hers is bittersweet and uncharacteristically gentle. “This isn’t real life. We both know that.”

“We could make it real life,” she suggests before raising her palms. “Just seeing each other casually. Nothing fancy.”

Agatha likes the thought of it, but Agatha likes the thought of a lot of things. Thoughts were just that — ideas, dreams, fantasies. Thoughts weren’t practical or tangible, and even when you managed to make them a reality, they rarely lived up to what you’d hoped. Were rarely worth plucking from your head at all. 

“It’s already complicated enough here, Rio. In paradise. Without the stress of jobs or doctors’ appointments or traveling. I mean, where do you even live?”

“I’ll be moving after I’m done with him, so I don’t know.” She shrugs. Agatha can sense the smallest bit of stubbornness in the motion.

Agatha immediately grabs the vodka as soon as the server sets it on the table and downs half of it in one large gulp. She gives him a dirty look as he keeps standing there, his pen poised above his pad to take their orders. “A minute, please?” Agatha snaps at him. He blushes and scurries away. 

She finishes the rest of her drink, sighing as she looks at Rio. “Are you sure you’re really done with him?” she asks, lowering her voice. “Because women say that to me all the time — that they’re going to leave their husbands. They rarely do. The only one who did was…” She trails off, pursing her lips. Was Wanda.

Rio stares at her own vodka for a moment before she downs it just as quickly as Agatha had. “He raped me this morning. Gave me new bruises. Threatened to kill me or have me committed. That’s too far, even for the part of me that still thinks it’s all my fault.”

Her hand balls up again, her jaw clenching. She wants him to rot in a place worse than hell, and she wants to protect Rio, but she wants to protect herself more. And she needs to protect Nicky most of all. 

“But there is still a part of you,” Agatha counters. “And that part of you has won out for…how many years have you been with him?”

“That part hasn’t necessarily won out,” Rio argues. “Compulsive heterosexuality plus my frequent dissociation has. But when I met you, despite how rude you were, you were so blunt that it just sort of…hit me. What the reality of it all was.”

Agatha shifts uncomfortably in her seat. Agatha loves to be adored. She loves to be the mastermind. She loves to be in control. But she does not love to be in charge. It’s a frequently confused and blurred distinction, but it’s different — it couldn’t be more different. Save for Nicky, Agatha is committed to no one but herself. Depended on no one but herself and had no one depend on her. 

“This isn’t a fairytale, Rio. I’m not a knight in shining armor riding in on a horse coming to rescue you from the beast or ogre or however the fuck the analogy would go.”

“I know,” Rio says. “I don’t want that. I know well and good I have shit to sort out, but it just so happens the way you phrased something resonated with me, regardless of…” She gestures between the two of them. “…this. Us.” She tucks a piece of hair behind her ear. “When I suggested seeing you, it was under no pretense of rescue. I know, in the end, no one is coming to save me.”

“Good,” Agatha replies simply — maybe a little shortly. “Because they’re not.” She looks down at the menu again. “I’m getting a steak,” she announces.

“I’m getting the parmesan chicken. He loves to control what I eat — always tells me to watch my figure — and maybe it sounds stupid, but this feels like the first step of breaking away from that, you know? Going against his wishes and indulging in something I want just for me. In feeling free.” She pauses, embarrassed. “Sorry. I’m rambling. It’s just been a while since anyone’s wanted to listen.”

“Who said I wanted to listen?” It's instinct. A defense mechanism. The more terrified Agatha is, the bitchier she becomes. But she doesn’t know how to change it. Doesn’t know how to stop.

Rio flinches, eyes dropping down to the menu. “Sorry,” she says softly.

She gives her a look. The constant apologies were enough to drive her crazy. “Let’s not start all that back up again.”

Rio gives her a little nod, face flushing red. Maybe it’s just the reflection of the candle, but Agatha thinks she can see her eyes get glassy with unshed tears.

Fuck. Fuck. She’s traumatized the woman. Usually, Agatha loves doing that — takes pride in that — but Rio…well, it sort of felt like kicking a dog who was down. She doesn’t open her mouth. She’s not sure what would come out of it. That happens a lot, her saying shit without thinking. Where’s the fucking waiter when you needed him? 

“Did you know that one blue whale can weigh as much as 24 elephants?” Agatha finds herself blurting to fill the silence — a stupid ocean fact she learned during that dreadful lecture with Nicky.

Rio purses her lips, gives her another tiny nod. 

Agatha clears her throat a little, continuing to look at the menu despite knowing — and announcing — what she was going to get. “You probably knew that already. Nicky did.”

Rio hesitantly peers up. “I don’t know a lot about whales, actually,” Rio says, voice quiet and careful as if she’s afraid that one wrong word would make Agatha bite her head off. Agatha can’t exactly blame her. “I’m better versed in sharks.”

Considering her husband, Agatha’s sure she is. She somehow smartly avoids commenting on this — the shark-infested waters. “They don’t have bones. And their skin feels like sandpaper,” she continues, going to take a swig of her vodka and realizing she’s out. Goddamn it. “Or so I’ve heard.”

“Sharks? Yeah. They also have electroreceptors on their foreheads, which—” Rio abruptly stops herself, looking down again and sipping her water. 

She raises a brow. “Which what?” she prompts. “Don’t keep me hanging, hot stuff.”

“Which allows them to sense the electromagnetic fields of other creatures,” Rio finishes, chewing on the inside of her cheek for a moment. “Are you playing mental games with me?”

”Pardon?”

“You acted like you didn’t want to listen, and now you’re having me ramble about sharks. I’m…confused.”

Agatha sure as fuck is, too. About Rio. About herself. About everything. “Not intentionally.” For once.

Rio furrows her brows. “So?”

“So...what?”

“You want to listen to me?”

A beat. “I just don’t like people assuming what I want.” Agatha looks down at her lap, smoothing the napkin on it.

“And that’s…fair, but you didn’t answer my question.”

Another beat. “Yes. I want to listen.”

“Okayyy,” she says slowly before letting yet another excruciating few seconds of silence overtake them. “I just don’t want to bother you.”

“I’d get up and leave if you were bothering me. I’d have no problem doing that.”

Rio nods a little, movement just as slow as her previous words.

The waiter comes back then, which Agatha is supremely grateful for despite the fact the boy seems supremely stupid. “Another round for both of us. A filet mignon for me, medium rare. And upgrade those mashed potatoes to truffle fries,” she says, handing him the menu without looking at him. Sharon Davis, her latest credit card fraud victim, was buying, after all.

“Um…” Rio clears her throat nervously. “House salad. Dressing on the side. Thanks,” she says, giving him her menu as well.

“What happened to the chicken parm?” Agatha asks as the waiter begins to walk away.

“I got too…anxious to order it,” Rio says, shaking her head in embarrassment. “It’s stupid, I know.”

“Why does chicken make you anxious?”

“It’s not the chicken — it’s everything else on it. The, um…calories. The fat. You know.”

Agatha gives her a look. “Fuck that.” She turns around and snaps her fingers. “Benny!” she calls. 

Their waiter turns around, eyes wide and terrified as he slowly approaches their table again. “Billy?” he corrects — it sounding more like a question. 

“Whatever. Add a chicken parm.” 

“Do you…want that…instead of the steak or—”

“In addition. In addition to the steak. How fucking hard is that?” 

Billy nods frantically. “I’ll put it in right away.”

Rio shakes her head as he walks away, pursing her lips to hide a smile. “You’re crazy."

“So I've been told."

“Well, I hope you know I mean it as a compliment. I can be loud and commanding when I need to, but that’s usually at work. Otherwise, it’s been beaten out of me.” 

Agatha knows how literally Rio probably means that. She knows because she’s experienced it herself. Not that she's about to air out her mommy issues at the dinner table. She'd rather gouge her eye out with the steak knife.

“People have certainly tried,” Agatha says with a flippant wave of her hand. “Turns out I’m unbeatable.”

“Which is admirable. Like I said, I’m one hell of a lawyer, but it’s been a while since I’ve felt powerful outside of the courtroom.”

There’s a long, long moment of silence as Agatha contemplates. She was a fucking control freak, which is why she doesn’t usually do this. She was a fucking control freak, which is why it felt exhilarating to occasionally do this. 

And then there was that split-second moment of authority — of command — in Rio’s voice last night that sent a pleasant heat through her core. 

“How would you feel about experimenting with having power in the bedroom then?” she asks.

Rio chews on the inside of her cheek, taken aback by the suggestion. “I— I don’t know. Maybe?” She thinks for a moment longer before deciding, “I think I’d be open to trying it once I know you a bit better.”

She shrugs. “It might be good for you is all — help you find your voice, your confidence.”

“I’d be willing to give it a shot. I just want to know you better before I let myself possibly look incredibly stupid.” She breathes out a laugh.

“What is it, exactly, that you’re dying to know?”

“I don’t know. Anything, really. I just want to learn more about the enigmatic Agatha Harkness.”

“Well, that spoils the mystery, doesn’t it?” Agatha challenges. “I tell you all my secrets, then I'll no longer be an enigma."

“I have a feeling I’ll like the woman underneath the enigma, too.”

Agatha snorts. That certainly hadn’t been her experience. She was an acquired flavor, and most people had terrible taste. “First time for everything, I suppose.”

“Well, go ahead,” Rio urges. “Tell me something about yourself. Whatever you want to say.”

She doesn’t know. For the first time in Agatha Harkness’ life, she’s speechless. Lying to Rio felt oddly cruel, but the truth was simply too awful. Too depressing.

Rio tilts her head at the uncharacteristic silence. “It doesn’t have to be anything special,” she assures her. “I just want to know you.”

She stirs her water around in her glass. “Nicky has a wonderful voice. He learned to sing before he learned to speak.” It’s cheating, really — giving her information about her son instead of her. Agatha did that a lot.

Thankfully, Rio doesn’t seem to notice. Or at least doesn’t seem to mind. Her mouth curves into a soft smile. “That’s sweet. What kind of music does he like best?”

“None of that inane kiddy crap, that’s for damn sure.” Agatha scoffs. That shit drove her nuts. “I make sure he’s exposed to real music."

Rio breathes out a laugh. “Fair enough. What kind of music do you like then?”

Oh, she was good — redirecting the conversation back to her. Asking a leading question. She really was a lawyer.

“I grew up in the ‘80s, so a lot of Joan Jett, Stevie Nicks, Pat Benatar,” Agatha replies. “Anything my mother hated, really.” She started listening to them because it pissed Evanora off, made her clutch her pearls. She kept listening to them because it resonated with her — sounds of anger. And of longing, too, for something else.

“Stevie Nicks is great.” Rio nods. “I also really love Gloria Estefan.”

Good taste. “Did your father introduce you to her?”

“Yeah, but I also listened to her on the radio. I’m an early '90s kid — she was still popular then.”

“Right. She would’ve been,” she agrees.  

The waiter is taking approximately eight thousand fucking years to bring them another round of drinks — so much for five-star service — so she fishes around in her purse for a cigarette.

Rio watches her all the while, taking a sip of her drink. She still had some. Lucky bitch. “You really are beautiful, you know,” she observes.

“Well aware.” Agatha flicks a lighter on, holding the cigarette to it. “But that’s kind of you, nonetheless.”

“I was just noticing,” Rio muses, her gaze somehow intense and vaguely dreamlike. “Your jawline is so nice, and your hair is so perfect.”

“I’m not actually sure I own a brush for myself. I used Nicky's to do mine yesterday. And yours last night,” Agatha admits, taking a long drag. The nicotine makes her brain feel pleasantly fuzzy. After she blows it out, she reaches across the table, offering it to Rio.

Rio plucks it from her fingers, inhaling as well. “Well, your hair is perfect. And the way you did mine was, too.”

Agatha shrugs. “Like I said, I’ve had practice.”  

Their waiter — Billy, was it? — picks now to approach the table. “Excuse me, but you can’t be smoking here.”

Agatha opens her mouth to tell him off, but Rio surprisingly beats her to the punch. “Other guests are.” She nods to a few businessmen a couple of tables away. “Why are we the only ones you’re policing?”

“They’re not in my section,” he says apologetically. 

“For fuck’s sake — we’re outdoors,” Agatha points out. “In Sicily.”

“And I’ve read your policies,” Rio adds. “None of them say you can’t smoke outside.”

The waiter anxiously bites his lip. “It’s only my first week—“

“That much was evident,” Agatha cuts in. 

“—and my boss was really, really strict about it during training.”

“Is your boss out here?” Agatha interrogates. “Or are you planning on being a little narc?”

“She’s in the back. Watching me like a hawk,” Billy says, growing more panicked. He’s still focused on Rio, no doubt because she seemed the nicer, more understanding of the two.

“If she comes out here, I’ll tell her what I told you,” Rio assures him, voice kind but firm.

The stupid kid bites his lip. “Please. I really need this job,” he begs, on the verge of bursting into tears.

“Can you get your manager?” Rio asks, tone softening. “I’d like to have a word with her.”

“If I cause problems already and show her I can’t enforce the rules, she’s going to fire me.”

“Sounds like a you problem,” Agatha replies, unsympathetic.

Billy looks like he's on the urge of combusting, desperately racking his brain for a solution. It makes him look sort of constipated. Not exactly the view you want at the dinner table. “If you put it out, I’ll give you free dessert!” he desperately blurts. 

Agatha narrows her eyes, considering. “I’m listening.”

“I’ll tell them it’s your birthday or…or anniversary or something!” 

Anniversary. The thought of an anniversary with Rio was…well, it was something. Gives her a feeling she’s not sure how to name. So she doesn’t try. 

“Two free desserts,” Agatha expertly negotiates. “I’d like to take one back to my kid. And a bottle of champagne — not the cheap shit. If it’s our anniversary and all.” 

The waiter purses his lips. That was a tall order. 

Agatha raises a brow. “Or you can get the manager, and I’ll tell her I saw you spit in our drinks. Unemployed with legal fees?” She clicks her tongue. “Not a great combo.” 

“Okay!” he quickly agrees. “Okay, okay — two desserts and champagne. Just, please — the…” He looks over at the cigarette. 

Agatha snatches it from Rio’s hand and stomps it out on the ground. She and the waiter have a short staring contest before it becomes clear she would not be picking it up. 

“Thank you,” Billy mumbles, crouching down to grab it before scurrying away. Another piece of evidence gone, just like that.

Chapter End Notes

Billy being tortured in every universe? So true.

Not to get all cheesy, but the love and support for this story has been particularly overwhelming lately! 🥹 We're beyond thrilled so many of you have decided to go on this journey with us — and that you seem to be digging it! There's plenty more to come, so buckle up. 🫡

Coming up next time: Dinner, disagreements, Dostoevsky.

Chapter 9: Day 3, Part 3

Chapter Summary

Dinner, disagreements, Dostoevsky.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio chuckles despite herself. “You terrified the poor kid.”

“So did you, Ms. ‘I’ve Read Your Policies,’” Agatha replies with an amused sip of water. Because she still didn’t have any more fucking vodka. Shitty ass waiter. “And threatening to pull a Karen with the manager?”

“Actually, I was planning to tell the manager off for being an asshole.”

“Noble.”

“That boy was probably 18. The manager likely got off on scaring him. It irked me.”

“I sort of got off on scaring him,” Agatha admits with another unashamed gulp of her drink. “Does that irk you, too?”

Rio considers for a moment. “I don’t approve,” she slowly notes. “But I would approve of you scaring me.”

Agatha narrows her eyes. “You’re very forward about what you want but very bad at actually taking it. It’s peculiar.” Agatha was the opposite. Secretive but unafraid to grab whatever she liked. 

The waiter finally — finally — returns with their second round of drinks as well as the promised bottle of champagne. “You’re much too polite,” Agatha informs her as he pops the cork and pours their glasses. “Just like nobody is going to save you, nobody is going to give you any power. You have to steal it for yourself.”

“I don’t think I have to steal it. I think I have to earn it or…bargain for it."

“It is steal,” Agatha disagrees as Billy disappears, clearly wanting to spend as little time at this table as possible. “Power, whether you want to admit it or not, is a finite resource — one most people don’t easily part with. And it should always be your first priority. It’s survival. It’s everything.”

“You can maintain power more easily when it’s not stolen,” Rio argues.

Agatha feels her jaw clench. What a privileged, righteous view of things. “Well, not all of us have that luxury.”

“Maybe we try and see if we can find that luxury together sometime,” Rio proposes, so innocent and optimistic it makes Agatha feel simultaneously tender and sick.

She lifts her palms. “I was trying to offer you some friendly advice, but if you’d rather continue being delusional and naive, that’s just fine.”

“I didn’t ask for advice, Agatha. Why is it so hard for you to imagine a world where you don’t always feel like you have to fight everyone for everything?”

Agatha ignores her question in order to pose a few of her own. “Is that a prerequisite? You’ll only want to be in my life if I ask very nicely for what I’m fucking owed? If I stand by like a church mouse while the most undeserving people continue to stay at the top? Because, if so, you should probably just save yourself the time and leave now. That is not who the woman under the enigma is.”

“I don’t mind you being brash at all,” Rio replies, annoyingly calm. “In fact, I quite like it. What I’m saying is there are smarter, more efficient ways to use that brashness. And that I can help.”

Agatha bristles at that. “Sweetheart, I’m plenty smart. I’ve got things handled just fine all on my own,” she curtly declares.

“I know you do,” Rio says, annoyingly patient, too. “You’re very capable. But that doesn’t mean I can’t add anything valuable to the equation.”

“I work alone.”

“Well, I’d like to change that,” she challenges, meeting her eyes with an intense gaze.

Agatha is unfazed. “Not interested. Thanks, though,” she says, tone not particularly sincere.

“Well, I am,” Rio pushes, adding annoyingly persistent to the list. “And I think you’re only uninterested because you’re terrified of what that would mean for you.”

Agatha lets out a laugh that’s devoid of humor and full of surprise. The fucking audacity. “Oh, is that so? And what exactly do you think it would mean for me, hm? Let’s hear it.”

“You would have to admit you’ve become attached again,” Rio accuses, bold and unflinching. “And that terrifies you because of what happened.”

“And what exactly do you think happened?”

“You hinted at a bad divorce.”

A week ago she’d be calling herself crazy. A week ago, she’d convince herself it was all in her head. But this trip had snapped her out of that delusion — Agatha had snapped her out of that delusion — which means she’s more terrified than ever as she falls asleep.

Chapter 13: Day 4, Part 1

Chapter Summary

A breakfast that changes everything.

Chapter Notes

Once again, warning for sexual assault in this chapter. It's not graphic, but it can still be triggering. Please use your best discretion and take care of yourself. If you’d rather skip past that part, scroll down until you see a line, and you can just read from there.

Here are some international sexual assault resources if you have been personally affected and need help: https://rainn.org/international-sexual-assault-resources.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

He laughs lightly. “I just said good morning. It’s after nine. You never sleep after nine.”

“Guess vacation is draining me,” she says with a small yawn, forcing a smile. It seems he’s still in his strangely good mood, and as ominous as it is, she wants to keep it that way as long as possible. It’s better than the alternative, after all.

“I made you some tea,” he says, handing her a mug.

“Oh.” She blinks in surprise. He’s never made her tea. He’s never made her anything. “Thanks.”

“You’re welcome. You deserve it.”

She leans down to blow on and discreetly sniff it. It’s mint, which is not her favorite — she preferred something floral like lavender or jasmine — but she drinks it anyway to appease him. Plus, she was thirsty. She had consumed a lot of alcohol yesterday.

Maybe that’s why she feels like absolute shit — a feeling that seems to get worse by the second. Her head is pounding as she answers a few work emails, her stomach churning as she slowly gets dressed, the room spinning as she brushes her hair. 

Rio can usually suck it up. Rio always sucked it up — showed up to work on time dressed in a suit and a smile no matter what horrors Thanos had inflicted on her the night prior — but this is next-level bad.

“I’m not feeling so great,” she admits. She hates to do it — hates to feel any weaker than she already does around him — but she doesn’t feel like she has much of a choice. Another form of panic sets in as she looks over to see Nicky loading up his own waffle with whipped cream, chocolate chips, and sprinkles. She has to try to act normal in front of this kid. This sweet, innocent kid. She forces her mouth into another smile. “Hey, Nicky. Did you sleep well?”

His mouth drops into a small frown at the question. “A little bit. But then I woke up and coughed a lot, so Mama had to come pat my back and give me my inhaler.”

“Well, I’m very glad she was there to take care of you. Are you feeling better this morning? It looks like you’re hungry.” She nods to the waffle. The small movement is enough to make her head spin.

His mouth quirks back up, his smile more bashful this time. “Mama said I could put all the toppings I wanted since I was a brave boy as long as I didn’t tell Mom she let me eat it all. Mama told me that you were brave last night, so you can probably have sprinkles if you want, too.”

“What’s for his safety?” Thanos asks, stepping behind Rio — no doubt already up to get seconds. He places his free hand on her back, giving Nicky a forced smile.

Nicky frowns. “Yes, I can. Mama said so.” 

“It sounds like your mama is too soft on you. Wants to keep you from living in the real world.”

“Wow, great example you’re setting for him, cursing at me like that.” He turns to Rio. “And you took parenting advice from her?”

“You were a jerk to her kid, Thanos,” she says. It’s a bold move — one that will surely get her ass kicked, make this morning look like a picnic — but she has to. He’s not going after her now — he’s going after Nicky and Agatha.

“He was getting snot all over the place,” Thanos defends. “Is that what you want at breakfast? Do you want mucus on your waffle, Rio? It's not sanitary." 

“He’s six, and he has cystic fibrosis, you ignorant prick. I wish he’d coughed directly into your mouth,” Agatha retorts, voice as sharp as her touch is gentle as she continues patting Nicky’s back. 

“So I could get sick?” 

“It’s not contagious,” Agatha replies. “Jesus Christ — didn’t you just invest in a pharmaceutical company? No wonder the American healthcare system's in the toilet.” 

“What happened to the nice lady I met at dinner?” Thanos asks. 

“I killed her,” Agatha growls.

“Cystic fibrosis is an autosomal recessive Mendelian trait,” Rio points out. “You quite literally cannot catch it.”

Thanos rolls his eyes. “God, you’re such a know-it-all. It’s so unattractive.” 

“Better than being a know-a-nothing,” Agatha quips. 

“Why are you still standing here by the waffle bar?” Thanos questions.

“Why are you still standing here on this planet?” she snaps back. 

“Mama,” Nicky softly whines. “I hurt.” 

Agatha purses her lips. She clearly does not want to back down from this fight. But she was fighting for Nicky, and he needed her to be a nurturing mama bear right now instead of a feral one. 

“I hurt, Mama,” Nicky repeats, soft cries beginning to rack his body — something he really did not need along with the coughs. 

“Shh,” Agatha soothes, gently bouncing him as if he’s a baby again. “It’s okay, honey. I have your PEP mask in my purse,” she says, giving Thanos one last glare before going back to her table. 

Thanos turns to Rio. “Don’t ever fucking embarrass me like that again. Taking that whore’s side over mine? Have you lost your fucking mind?”

“No, I haven’t,” Rio replies. But the truth is, maybe she has. And maybe that’s not the worst thing. The drugs and adrenaline are making her bolder and less anxious and completely unlike herself, and maybe that’s not so bad. “You embarrassed yourself. It’s also not very smart to call women you don’t like ‘whores.’ It makes it seem like you don’t know the definition of the word.”

“Oh, I know the definition. And that she talked very openly about her sex life within five seconds of meeting me last night. I thought maybe she was just a little weird, but now I see she's truly fucking crazy. You’re not allowed to talk to her anymore.”

Rio realizes that she would rather fucking die than never talk to Agatha again.

Rio might end up doing just that. Dying.

“No.” She shakes her head. “No, you don’t get to do that anymore. You don’t get to do that anymore because…” Fuck it. Fuck it all. “Because I’m leaving you, Thanos.”

“Leaving me?” he asks, voice serious and mouth a thin line before he bursts into mocking laughter. “Leaving me? You leave me — oh, you’re funny, Rio.”

“No, I am,” she says, tone as serious and decisive as it’s ever been. It’s not what she envisioned for this moment, but things were rarely what Rio envisioned. Maybe it was always going to be like this — not some big, planned-out speech but a spontaneous blurt by a waffle bar. Maybe that’s the only way she’d ever get the courage. “I’m fucking leaving you. You hit me, and you rape me, and you fucking drugged me.” There’s a strange power in laying it all out like this — accusing him in public, even if there weren’t any immediate witnesses listening in.

Thanos rolls his eyes. “Oh, for fuck’s sake — it was some Xanax and molly. I didn’t inject you with fucking heroine. And for the millionth time — I fuck you exactly how I know you like it. Which I’m allowed to do because you’re my wife. That’s all.”

“No, I don’t like it,” Rio says, gaze fiery and voice firm. “Listen to me: I hate it. I hate it, and I hate you. This is over.”

“Fine.” Thanos scoffs. “Go. You’ll come crawling back by sundown — I know you will.”

Rio won’t. Rio can’t.

So instead, she’ll crawl to Agatha and hope to god she hasn’t just made the biggest mistake of her life.

Chapter 14: Day 4, Part 2

Chapter Summary

Agatha reacts to Rio's big decision.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Can we talk?” Rio asks, approaching Agatha’s table. She’s still feeling shaky, though whether it’s from the drugs or the adrenaline of what she’s just done, she’s not entirely sure. Maybe some combination of both.

“I’m a little preoccupied,” Agatha replies without looking at her, rubbing Nicky’s back. 

Nicky moves his PEP mask away from his face. “I’m okay now, Mama,” he insists. 

Agatha immediately places it back over his nose and mouth. “You keep that on, young man.”

Rio doesn’t want to intrude — she really doesn’t — but it’s not like she has much of a choice right now. She’s high as fuck, and she’s just blown up her entire life. “It’s— It’s urgent. I’m sorry.”

Agatha opens her mouth, no doubt to snap at her, but she stops short when she sees her face. And Nicky’s face. And she must decide she can’t. Not now.

So instead, she sighs and purses her lips before opening her mouth again. “You mean in private, I presume?”

That would be ideal, but Rio knows there’s no way in hell Agatha is walking even the shortest distance away from Nicky for even the shortest amount of time right now — nor would Rio ever ask her to. So instead, she pulls out her phone and opens her notes app, attempting to type in spite of her blurry vision. She manages a mostly cohesive message: Drugged me. Scaared. Told him Iwas leavng.

Agatha blinks, head dipping back the smallest bit in surprise. She looks into Rio’s glassy eyes for a few seconds before decisively standing from the table. “Nicky, sweetheart, let’s go back to our room.” 

“But I didn’t get to eat my waf—"

“We’ll order you an ice cream sundae through room service. All the same stuff on top.” 

He perks up at that. “For breakfast?” 

“For breakfast,” Agatha confirms, already nudging him up. “Come on.”

Rio stays put, unsure of what to do. She doesn’t want to be presumptuous, after all. She wraps her arms around herself, suddenly feeling so…small. She certainly doesn’t want to be a burden. Doesn’t want to be an imposition or—

Agatha waves a beckoning, almost impatient hand at her. “You too. Let’s go.”

Rio nods, squaring her shoulders as best she can before walking to the building with them.

“Want me to hold your hand?” Nicky asks, peering up at her.

It’s weak and stupid, but she doesn’t really want to be touched — doesn’t really feel safe to be touched by anyone but Agatha. It was insane, too. Nicky was sweet — the sweetest — and he was a child. He was a literal child who wouldn’t, who couldn’t, hurt her. So she pushes down her irrational feelings and hopes he doesn’t notice the hesitation before she offers it to him.

Agatha must sense it somehow — this ridiculous conflict she’s having — and intercepts the hand Rio holds out before Nicky can. She shuffles Nicky to the other side of her, taking his hand as well. “I’m going to hold both of your hands,” she asserts.

Rio could cry at the kindness of the gesture, but she settles for giving Agatha’s hand a light, grateful squeeze instead.

“When we get back, you both are going to be very good patients for me, yes?” Agatha asks. 

“Ms. Rio’s sick?” Nicky inquires, brows pinched in concern. 

“Yes, she…ate something bad,” Agatha explains — not technically a lie. “So the two of you need to rest for a while.” 

“And eat ice cream?” 

“And eat ice cream,” Agatha confirms.

“Thank you,” Rio whispers to her.

Agatha simply nods, keeping her gaze forward. Rio can practically feel the adrenaline simmering in Agatha's palm — the rage flowing through her veins — from how Thanos spoke to Nicky and perhaps what he’d done to her. Rio can practically see the wheels turning in her head — telling herself to channel this in a way that doesn’t come as naturally for her. Not violence towards him but softness towards her son. And perhaps toward her, too.

“Please don’t pass out in front of my kid,” she tells Rio, voice low.

“Won’t,” Rio promises. It’s a struggle to utter every word. Every syllable.

“Do you want to watch Dora with me, Ms. Rio?” Nicky asks. “And hug Señor Scratchy? My stuffed one — not my real one. My real one’s at home with Mom because Mama said he couldn’t come on the plane.”

Rio takes a deep breath, preparing to rip more words from herself. “You’re really sweet to offer all of that, Nicky. I think right now I just need some quiet time, though. Like your mom said, I ate something that made me feel really bad.”

“Oh.” He frowns, disappointment written all over his face. “Okay.”

It breaks her heart to break his heart. “Maybe we could do a hug if you wanted?” she suggests — an awkward compromise, maybe, but she can’t think of anything better right now.

He tilts his head. “My bunny? Or me?”

“Whichever you’d like.”

“Hm.” He ponders this very seriously as they reach their hall. “Well, maybe I could hold bunny, and then you could hug us at the same time. Or is that cheating?"

“I can do that.” Rio nods. "Promise me you’ll get some rest, too?”

“Grown-ups are always making me rest,” Nicky complains with a stomp of his tiny foot. 

“Stop the whining, or you can have cabbage and raisins for breakfast,” Agatha cuts in. “And instead of Dora, I’ll put on the news.” Rio knows it’s more than likely an empty threat, but it shuts him up fast.

“I have to rest, too, if it makes you feel any better,” Rio offers with a small smile. “Sometimes, grown-ups have to, too.”

“Okaaay,” he reluctantly agrees. “Maybe after you’re done with your quiet time, we can do something fun while we still rest,” he proposes as Agatha unlocks their door.

“We’ll see — okay, bud?” Rio asks, sliding her sandals off in the entryway so as not to track sand in.

“Nicky, why don’t you call your mom? I bet she’s missing you,” Agatha suggests — something Rio knows she absolutely does not do. She’s said more than once how much she hates that woman. But she’s also said more than once that Wanda and Nicky could yap for hours, and they do need him distracted from the shit show that was Rio’s current state and predicament. Rio tries not to think about what that means — Agatha taking one for the team like this. Taking one for her.

“Okay,” Nicky says, seeming to brighten a bit at that. “Can I tell her that I held my breath underwater for three whole seconds? And that I made a seagull friend? And that I built a sandcastle almost as tall as me?” 

“You can,” Agatha permits. Rio sees her quickly change the name in her phone from GINGER BITCH to simply WANDA before going to hand it to him. Before she does, she holds up a finger. “Just no mention of—”

“Ice cream for breakfast or Ms. Rio,” Nicky recites. “I know, Mama.” 

Agatha nods. “Ms. Rio and I are going to rest in my room. I’ll order your ice cream, but no opening the door when they knock — I’ll come out here and get it. And no running around. Plant your butt on the couch and keep it there. If you’re feeling better later, maybe — maybe — we can go to the pool, all right?” 

“Okay, Mama.” 

“Good boy.” She ruffles his hair and gives him a kiss on the top of the head before handing him the phone.

“Do you still want to hug bunny and me first, Ms. Rio?” Nicky asks, grabbing his stuffed rabbit.

“I would be happy to.” She gives him a smile — small but sincere — as she crouches down to wrap her arms around him. She tries to keep herself from wincing at the change in position. Tries to keep the nausea rising up in her chest at bay.

“You’re a good hugger,” Nicky notes.

“Thanks, bud,” she whispers before standing back up. “You go rest now, okay?”

“Ms. Rio?”

“Nicky…” Agatha warns, albeit gently. 

“I just have one more question. I pinky promise.” 

Rio imagines he was always saying that. One more question, one more song, one more glass of water or trip to the bathroom. Still, Agatha indulges him. “Okay. Ask it.” 

“Ms. Rio, are you going to be my mom, too?” 

Oh. Oh, Rio really wishes Agatha had not indulged him. 

“I— Well— That’s…that’s a complicated question,” Rio stammers out. She feels her face grow hot and knows it must be some combination of the inquiry and the drugs in her system. A recipe for disaster.

He frowns. “You say a lot of things are complicated.”

“I know,” she sympathizes. “Because they are. I wish they weren’t.”

“Mm.” His frown deepens. “Well, I would be happy,” he says. “If you were.”

Rio is speechless. Rio is on the verge of bursting into tears. Rio is…

Rio is feeling like her world is spinning out of control. Rio is attempting to keep the bile from spilling out of her mouth. Rio is running to Agatha’s bathroom to vomit up the few contents left in her stomach.

“Ms. Rio!” Nicky calls, attempting to dart after her. 

Agatha catches him by his shirt. “Give her a minute, Nicky.” 

“But— But—" Tears well up in his eyes. 

“Shh,” Agatha soothes as she crouches in front of him, putting a hand on both his shoulders. “It’s okay, Nicky. She’s okay.” 

“She’s not,” he insists, lip wobbling. 

“She will be,” Agatha promises. “You know how I take care of you when you’re feeling bad?” 

He nods, sniffling. 

“Mama is going to do the same thing for her, okay?” she says, thumbing away his tears. “Can you try to be brave and take some deep breaths for me?” 

He nods again, inhaling a few shaky times, followed by a few coughs — not great but not necessarily cause for concern on their own. 

“Good,” Agatha praises. “Good boy. Do you think you can relax out here for a little bit while I make sure she’s all right?” 

Another nod. 

She gives his shoulders a squeeze. “Okay,” she says softly. “I love you, baby.” 

“I— love you, too, Mama.” 

Agatha places another kiss to his temple before heading into her bathroom. 

Once inside, she immediately crouches down next to Rio. “I’m going to tell you what I just told my six-year-old: breathe.”

Rio gives her a small nod despite the fact that more bile rises up in her throat — another retch wracks her body. “I’m— I’m sorry,” she heaves.

“Less talk, more breathe.”

Rio attempts to suck in another breath — this time through her teeth — which seems to do the trick. She manages to take a small gulp of air. Then another. And another. Finally, she feels her body go limp, the top half of her slumping down onto the toilet bowl. It was unsanitary. Disgusting, really. And yet, Rio can’t bring herself to care.

“Do you feel like you're going to hurl again?” Agatha checks.

Rio shakes her head. “I’m just tired,” she says, the admission followed by a sob she hadn’t felt coming. It’s vaguely mortifying — not only the action itself but being so caught off guard by it. She wants to crawl into a hole, but she settles for curling up on the floor instead.

“No, Rio,” Agatha says, gentle yet firm. “We’re not doing that yet, all right? First order of business is getting you to a bed.”

She’s right. Rio knows she’s right. As much as she doesn’t want to move, she forces herself to unfurl herself from her little ball and grab onto the sink in an attempt to pull herself up. She feels like a baby giraffe, clumsy and unbalanced. 

Agatha grimaces, sucking some air through her own teeth now before putting her arms out in Rio’s direction. “Jesus, Rio — take it easy, would you? I don’t want to touch you without your permission, but I also don’t want you cracking your head open on the side of my tub.”

Rio drops back down to the floor and looks at her, considering. She can practically feel how red her eyes are — from the drugs and the tears. Can practically feel the dark, exhausted circles forming beneath them. “Go ahead,” she tells her, throat raw and voice ragged.

Agatha seems a little relieved by this. “It’s like 10 steps,” she assures her, taking her arm and helping her up. “15 tops if only because this bathroom is fucking enormous.”

She can’t help but let out another small whimper as Agatha leads her to the bed. It feels like fucking miles instead of mere feet, and by the time she collapses onto the mattress, she’s winded. She’s about to go back to the relative safety of her curled-up position, but it’s like Agatha’s a mind reader or a fortune teller, butting in before she can.

“No, Rio. Still not yet.” She disappears into the bathroom briefly before turning with a glass of water and a damp washcloth. “Sit up and drink this. Come on.”

The thought of anything going into her stomach sort of made Rio want to kill herself — drinking water sounded about as appealing as eating glass at the moment — but she sits up just enough to let Agatha hold the cup to her lips. After she’s sipped about three-quarters of it down, she pulls back and looks at Agatha for approval.

She shakes her head, tapping the bottom of the glass with her nail. “Whole thing.”

Rio whines, a half-hearted and petulant sound that Agatha seemed to enjoy hearing in a much different, more fun context.

“Stop whining, or I’ll feed you cabbage and raisins, too.” 

Any other time, Rio would tell her to get some new material — that what worked on her six-year-old son was not going to work on her. 

But this isn’t any other time. 

Instead, she wordlessly finishes the rest. 

“You can lie down now,” Agatha permits, putting the empty glass on the nightstand.

Thank fucking god, Rio thinks. She lies back, immediately squeezing her eyes shut. But instead of blocking out the memories, calming the feelings of forced intoxication, lessening the horror of feeling so…violated, her eyelids are like a dark, blank canvas for it all to be displayed. Heightened. Made worse.

The feeling of Agatha gently placing the wet washcloth on her forehead helps a little, serving to ground and soothe her. Rio knows she should probably be lying on her side instead — less risk of choking on your own vomit that way — but it was fine. Well, as fine as it could be, which is to say, not very fine at all.

She tries to focus on her breathing again — sucking in little puffs through her teeth. She thinks she has it under control, but when she opens her mouth to say something — "sorry," probably — only a strained, incoherent sound comes out. And maybe that’s for the best.

“If you apologize for being drugged, I will intentionally go slam my head against the bathtub,” Agatha threatens. “And then make you pay for any and all medical attention it requires.”

Rio knows that, just like the cabbages and raisins, it’s not really a threat, but she can’t help but flinch at the violent image anyway.

She hears Agatha walk over to the hotel phone. “I’m ordering you food — avocado toast and a green smoothie,” she announces. “Obnoxious, I know, but you need magnesium when you come down from this shit.”

Rio nods, heaving in another breath. “Want to shower,” she manages to force out.

“Later. After you’ve eaten. You can barely stand up right now.”

A strange panic blooms in her chest at that. Suddenly, this request feels urgent. Now that she’d noticed it, she couldn’t unnotice it. She opens her eyes, then, looking at the other woman intensely. “Agatha, I— I feel him. On me. All over.”

Agatha sighs, pausing mid-dial to consider. “I can let you sit in the bath,” she compromises. “Or get you another cloth to wash off with.”

“Bath.” Rio nods.

“I’ll run it after I order breakfast,” she says, punching the rest of the numbers for room service. “You’d think a luxury resort wouldn’t still have a goddamn corded phone, but alas.”

The smallest ghost of a smile flicks on Rio’s face at that. It feels foreign and wrong. Like a shape her mouth shouldn’t be able to make.

After Agatha has ordered — from the same waiter from the previous night, Rio’s pretty sure, from the voice she can make out on the other end of the line and Agatha’s generally shitty attitude toward them — she disappears into the bathroom to fill the tub.

“Try and drink another cup,” she orders as she returns with another glass of water. “Hydration is important right now. Believe me, I’ve done a lot of drugs in my day.”

Rio doesn’t even bother arguing this time. She doesn’t have the energy. Plus, it’s…sort of nice — feeling cared for like this. Strange and uncomfortable but nice, too. 

Agatha stands near the bed, arms crossed over her chest, finger tapping the one on top. “Do you have any idea what the son of a bitch gave you?”

Rio nods. “Molly,” she says, voice even hoarser than before. “A benzo.”

“Psychopath,” Agatha mumbles, blowing out a breath. “Though I’ve ingested plenty of both, and I’m all right. I’m sure you will be, too.”

Rio looks down at the glass in her hand. “I’m scared,” she finds herself confessing in a whisper. Maybe she’s baiting her. Maybe she wanted Agatha to cradle her. To tell her everything was going to be all right. To feed her comforting lies. 

“I’m telling you that you don’t need to be. I’ve taken a lot harder, and the best thing you can do is wait it out, get some food and water in you, and try to relax. Panicking about it is only going to make you feel worse. Just try and...ride the high as much as you can.” 

Rio gives her a look, and Agatha holds up her palms. “Maybe that sounds fucked up, all things considered,” she admits. “But...in my experience, that's what works."

Rio nods. She continues to look at her, but her gaze turns pleading now. Agatha had given her verbal reassurance, but she was still craving the physical. Everything was starting to feel so…far away. Almost like it wasn’t real. She finds herself floating to that space she so often does with him — the one slightly above reality. The one where she’s detached from her body, looking down at it.

Usually, with him, it’s something of a comfort. But without an immediate threat, the beginning stages of the dissociation freaks her out. She doesn’t want to drift. She wants to stay here with Agatha where it’s safe, and she can't hang on unless she has something to grip. Unless she has Agatha within reach.

Agatha sighs softly, doing her weird mind-reading trick again. “I can’t now, Rio. We can’t. Nicky’s wide awake and right outside — plus, the bath’s almost ready.”

“The bath isn’t running yet,” Rio stutters out, her anxiety rapidly increasing along with the cadence of her breaths and her frustration at Agatha’s stupid fucking made-up rules for herself. Rio needed her. Can’t Agatha see that she needed her? She didn’t want to have sex right now, for fuck’s sake. She just wanted Agatha to put her arms around her — hold her together so she wouldn’t fall apart. Why couldn’t she see that? Why could no one ever see that?

Agatha’s brows furrow, a small frown appearing on her face. “The bath is running, sweetheart,” she slowly reminds her. “I turned it on after I called for the food.”

Rio blinks, trying to focus. Everything suddenly feels too bright, and the sounds. Oh god — the sounds. There are so many of them, and they’re all happening at once. So jumbled and noisy she can’t separate one from the other. Can’t tell them apart let alone process what the hell they are.

Rio covers her ears, hoping that’ll get the strange static to stop at least. Hoping that’ll help this all feel not so fucking unbearable. She’s not sure if it’s a panic attack or a sensory meltdown or some combination of the two — all she knows is it’s hell. All she knows is that she’s in hell, and she’s all alone there.

All she knows is she’s always in hell. 

And she’ll always be alone there.

Being threatened with having to watch the news so true.

Chapter 15: Day 4, Part 3

Chapter Summary

Agatha tries her best.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha doesn’t know what the hell is going on. Rio seems to be having some sort of…seizure. Or psychotic break maybe. She doesn’t fucking know — all she knows is she’s clearly not well. Agatha was usually the ‘jump into action’ type, but she finds herself oddly frozen, helplessly watching. God, she hated feeling helpless. “Rio…?” she asks. “What’s happening?”

“I’m overstimulated,” Rio snaps through gritted teeth, body beginning to shake as she continues to cover her ears. “I need you to hold me. Please.”

The seriousness of her tone is weirdly disarming. “Okay,” Agatha says, quickly climbing onto the mattress beside her. Maybe the tub would overflow, flood the bathroom. And so what if it did? Let it. Let it trickle into this room and drown them. 

“All right,” Agatha says, wrapping her arms around her. Something — though she’s not sure what — tells her that, despite her sensitive state, she will want her grip to be tight. “Okay,” she repeats. “All right.”

Agatha feels Rio trembling against her and once again thinks of her rabbit — the way he used to quiver until she tucked him into her arms, stroked his silky ears.

“Again, breathe,” Agatha orders, though her tone is gentle.

Rio takes one hand off her ear, dutifully hitting her sternum with her fist as if the action will help.

“Not—" She grabs her hand before it can come down again. “—like that. Look at me.” This was mercifully in Agatha’s wheelhouse, with Nicky having a respiratory condition and all. 

Rio does as she’s told once more, craning her head back to look at Agatha.

She places Rio’s hand on her chest. “Feel what I’m doing and follow it.” She takes a deep inhale through her nose, an equally deep exhale through her mouth.

It takes Rio several long tries before she can even manage to suck in half a breath. Agatha can tell by the way the space between her brows pinches that she’s frustrated. Can tell by the clench of her jaw that she’s getting discouraged.

“It’s fine, Rio,” she assures her. “You’re fine. Just keep going. Focus on me — nothing else.”

After another small eternity, Rio takes a deep breath in, a few more tears coming out with the exhale. She’s still not well by any means, but she seems sufficiently calm at least. That was something, Agatha supposed.

“The bath should be ready now,” she tells her.

Rio nods. She seems to be cognizant of the water now, which was another something. Still, even the tiny movement of her head is sluggish — exhausted and not quite right.

Agatha purses her lips. “Not to sound totally infantilizing, but would it be okay if I carried you?”

Rio nods again, a silent plea in her eyes.

“All right,” she says softly, shifting so she can pick her up. Agatha was much more comfortable with this part of caretaking — when she had a clear task and purpose and it was primarily physical instead of emotional. 

When they get back into the bathroom, she gingerly sets Rio on the edge of the dangerously full tub. “Would it be okay if I helped you take your clothes off?”

Another nod.

“All right,” she repeats once more. She takes the hem of Rio’s shirt and lifts it over her head before going to unhook her bra. “It’s okay if you don’t want to talk,” she assures her, another mysterious voice or feeling or whatever telling her that maybe it’s what Rio needs to hear. “Or if you…can’t…talk. I understood you just fine with a gag in your mouth,” she reminds her, moving down to slip her pants down her legs.

Rio takes a deep, forced breath — something Agatha appreciates.

“You’re doing so well,” she praises, which was pretty true, all things considered. And also something Rio seemed to like to hear, albeit in a much different and more fun context than this.

Agatha hooks her fingers into the waistband of her underwear, though she stops and looks at her face before she moves them. “Still okay?”

One, two, three more forced breaths before another tiny nod.

“We can keep them on if you’d prefer,” Agatha adds at the hesitation. “It’s really not a big deal either way. Do you want to leave them?”

Rio shakes her head. “I want my whole body clean from him,” she manages to say.

“Okay,” she agrees. “That’s okay, too.” She shifts them down past her knees and over her ankles before placing her hands on her waist and slowly helping her into the tub. “There you go.”

Rio grabs a washcloth, immediately squeezing on some body wash and scrubbing away at her skin. Agatha stands there for a moment, feeling uncharacteristically awkward and weirdly out of place despite the fact she was paying for this bathroom, for fuck’s sake.

After a beat, she lowers herself to sit on the edge of the tub. “Would it be okay if I washed your hair again?” It really was mostly for her own benefit. She needs another physical task, and she still probably had a few minutes before the food would be there and she could go get it.

Rio nods without ceasing, shoulders seeming to relax the smallest bit at the inquiry. It had calmed her the other night, after all. 

Agatha knows she should probably chide her for scrubbing so damn hard, but it’s not like she doesn’t understand the instinct — to crawl out of your skin or do the next best thing and peel it off layer by layer — and nothing is bleeding, at least. Instead, she makes sure her own touch is exceptionally gentle as she cups some water to pour onto her head and begins to massage in some shampoo.

“I didn’t…put the pieces together,” Agatha says a few moments into lathering her hair.

Rio’s brow wrinkles the smallest bit as she looks back at her. She manages a strained, “Hm?” 

“The reactions you had. The…autism you mentioned,” she says, voice matter-of-fact. “I didn’t grow up with any of that stuff. My mother was an adamant denier that it even existed.”

Rio gives a half nod, clearly trying not to disturb Agatha’s hands — thinking of everyone else, even in this movement. She finally puts the washcloth down, busying herself with picking at a hangnail instead. “It’s okay,” she says after a long moment. “I’m weird.”

“You are,” Agatha confirms. “But not because of that. The doctors said Nicky might be, too.”

“Makes sense.” Another long pause. “You probably are, too, then. Genetics.”

“Mm. Autism is usually inherited from the father,” Agatha points out.

“Not always.”

“Believe it or not, that’s why I said ‘usually.’ Why are you so certain I’m the culprit, hm?”

“Ask me later.”

Agatha should respect her wishes in her condition, but two of her most dominant characteristics are curiosity and impatience. “Oh, come on,” she baits. “You can’t leave me hanging like that. Give me the short of it, at least. The bullet points.”

Rio gathers a deep breath. “Rigidity,” she finally says. “Black-and-white thinking. Low emotional intelligence. Bluntness.”

She had a point with the emotions. And the bluntness. The other two, however… “I think I’m extremely flexible,” Agatha counters. “And that everything about me is grey.”

Rio shakes her head, though it’s clear she doesn’t have the energy to elaborate. Agatha puts a pin in it for later and simply gives a little hum in response.

Just then, there’s a knock on the door. 

“The food,” Agatha muses. “I have to go get that — I don’t want Nicky answering it.”

“Okay,” Rio whispers with a little nod.

“I’ll be back,” she promises. “Don’t drown.”

“Mama,” Nicky says the moment Agatha opens the door from her bedroom. He wisely stays on the couch just as she’d instructed. 

“Hi, sweetheart. Did you talk to your mom?” 

“Yeah. She says she misses me.” 

Agatha is glad he doesn’t elaborate about the bitch on the other end of the line. She also feels a little smug about the fact Wanda had to settle for the occasional phone call right now. That was usually what she had to do. “I’ll bet.” 

She opens the door to get their cart of food, making sure not to tip once she sees it’s the waiter from the previous night delivering it.  

“How are you feeling?” Agatha asks once the door is relocked. She’s confident she could take Thanos if he were to get in, but still. She’d prefer to do the ambushing, not be the one ambushed. Plus, Nicky was in the room, and she'd be damned if he got near him again. 

“Good,” Nicky says. “Better.” 

“I’m glad to hear that.” Agatha goes to hand him the ice cream, keeping her fingers around the bowl as he reaches for it. “Are you just saying that because you want to go to the pool later?” She looks him in the eyes. 

“No.” A small cough. 

She raises a brow. “No?” 

“That wasn’t a real cough!” he insists. “I promise!” 

“Mhm.” She lets go of the bowl. “Will you be all right if I go check on Ms. Rio again?” 

“Is she okay?” Nicky asks, concern pooling in his pupils. Her sweet, sweet boy.

“She’s fine. Just taking a bath. I was helping her wash her hair.” 

“You’re good at that,” Nicky muses with a serious nod. Agatha breathes out a small, almost touched laugh. “I’ll be fine, Mama. I’m six now,” he insists.

“All right, all right — I forgot you were all grown up.” She lifts her palms and goes to retrieve Rio’s toast and smoothie.

“You’re eating at least half of this,” she announces without room for argument as she strides back into the bathroom. “And drinking the entire thing.”

“Drink first,” Rio replies in a reluctant mumble.

Agatha places the cup on the side of the tub, positioning the straw to her lips before cutting the avocado toast into smaller pieces. It was maybe vaguely disgusting to be eating in a bathroom, but housekeeping came every day, and they did a damn good job.

“Be careful,” she orders as she brings the plate over. “The thought of you bathing in soggy breadcrumbs makes me want to puke. Although knowing this ritzy ass place, that’s probably one of the bizarre fucking spa treatments they offer."

The corner of Rio’s mouth quirks into a tiny smile as she picks up a piece of the toast. 

“The dumb fucking waiter dropped it off,” Agatha continues. “You should’ve seen his face — I think he almost pissed himself when he realized it was me.”

She’s upgraded from a small smile to a brief, hollow huff of laughter.

“Tough crowd,” Agatha muses.

“I’m tired,” Rio defends.

“And I’m funny.”

“Mhm,” Rio replies, noncommittal.

“I’m very funny,” she reiterates.

“Okay.”

Agatha sighs. She's trying to stall the inevitable, but Rio’s clearly not in the mood. She imagines she’ll be even less in the mood for what she asks next, but she has to rip the bandaid sometime. 

“What’s the plan here, Rio? I don’t mean to overwhelm you even more than you are, but it is…more urgent than it was, all things considered.”

Rio swallows the bite of toast she’s chewing and takes a sip of smoothie before she responds. “I’m gonna go get my stuff today, then…I’ll figure it out from there.”

“You’re going to get your stuff and you’re going to put it…where exactly?”

Rio looks at her. “Here?” she asks, voice so quiet it’s barely audible. “Please?”

Agatha takes a breath, considering. “Does he know where my room is?”

Rio gives her head a vehement shake. “No.”

“You’re absolutely positive? I can’t have Nicky in danger, Rio. I won’t.”

“I never told him,” Rio promises. “I never would.”

Another deep breath. “All right. Here, then. For tonight, at least. Just in case — with the drugs and all.” Is it an excuse to keep Rio close? Maybe, partially, it is. Does Agatha care? Maybe, partially, she doesn’t.

“Okay,” Rio replies, shoulders relaxing down another inch. She finishes her smoothie, holding the empty cup up as if presenting evidence. “Can I rest now?”

Agatha raises a brow, looking at the still nearly full plate. “That’s not half the toast. I definitely said half the toast.”

“It's a third.”

“Which is very much not what I said.”

Rio sticks her bottom lip out, pouting, but Agatha holds firm. “I told you that look doesn’t work on me. Come on.” She gestures toward the plate.

Rio grumbles a few choice words under her breath before reluctantly complying.

“Good girl.” Agatha pats her head, her tone some mix of playful condescension and affection.

It’s slightly less than half if they’re getting all technical, but Agatha lets it slide once she takes a few more bites. “Give me the rest,” she orders, opening her own mouth. In all the chaos, she hadn’t thought to order anything for herself (which was a first), and it was approximately $30, which was fucking outrageous. Thanks again, Sharon Davis, for footing the bill.

Rio obliges, holding up a piece. Agatha leans forward, taking a large bite.

“Mm,” she says as she chews. “I feel like Cleopatra.”

“You’re pretty like her,” Rio muses.

“That’s why you said I was like Gaea, too.”

“Mhm.”

“I feel objectified."

Rio pouts once more.

“Don’t you know the definition of insanity?” Agatha asks.

Rio continues to pout, though she raises her hand out of the water in order to flash her a middle finger. 

“Aww, there you go — that’s something new. Something that might actually get you a different result.”

Rio raises an expectant eyebrow, causing Agatha to blink in surprise. Did she really want to…do something? Right now? Would it even be responsible for Agatha to indulge it with Rio in her state and Nicky awake and right outside the door?

“What kind of reaction did you want that to get you?” Agatha asks. It’s…a strategic question at the moment.

Rio thinks for a long, long beat. “I just want to rest,” she finally admits.

Agatha softens. “Okay, sweetheart — you can rest now. Do you want to borrow some more comfortable clothes?”

Rio rapidly nods as if the thought of putting on anything he’d touched — anything he’d even seen her in — was too much to bear. “Please.”

“Give me a minute,” Agatha says before disappearing to her closet. She returns a few moments later with some fleece shorts, a t-shirt with a design Rio can’t yet see, and a faintly mischievous smirk on her face.

“What’s that look for?” Rio asks as she towels off.

“I’ve brought you the best of the best,” she says, turning the shirt to reveal a truly ridiculous design: BOHNER FAMILY REUNION — it reads in red-and-green letters around a campsite design — PITCH A TENT!

“Oh my god,” Rio says, managing a full laugh this time. “What’s the story?”

“Stupid-ass ex’s stupid-ass brother made us all go camping. Do I look like a person who enjoys fucking camping?” she asks, tossing her the clothes.

Rio shakes her head, a small smile still on her face as she pulls it over her head.

Agatha leads her back to the bed more slowly than what’s probably strictly necessary — she really does not want her slipping and cracking her head on that damn tub — and slides in beside her so they’re lying face-to-face.

Rio scoots close the second she does, immediately burying her face in Agatha’s chest.

They’re interrupted by a shy little knock on the door. “Shit,” Agatha mutters under her breath. Then, louder, “What is it, bud?” 

“Can I open the door?” Nicky asks meekly. 

Agatha sighs. “Are you okay if he comes in?” she whispers.

Rio nods against her chest before pulling her head back slightly to look at the doorway.

“You can open it,” Agatha announces. Nicky turns the handle slowly and creaks it even slower. “What’s wrong, my love?”

“Tummy hurts.”  

“Did you eat the ice cream too fast?” He looks down at his feet. “Nicky..." she warns. "We talked about this.”

“I’m sorryyy.” He gives her a pathetic little look. “Can I have a sandwich?” 

“You just said your stomach hurts.” 

“Not the eat kind. The lie-down kind.” And by that, he means he wants to lie all cozy between them. Wanda had coined the term. Dumb bitch. “I’ll be quiet and not bother you even at all,” he promises.

Agatha looks at Rio. “Are you okay if he rests with us if he’s very calm and quiet?” she interprets, emphasizing the last words.

“Yeah.” Rio nods again. “Of course.”

“Come on, then,” Agatha tells Nicky, pulling the blankets back in invitation. 

The little boy quickly pads over to the bed, climbing in from the end and squeezing himself in the middle of them.

Rio manages a smile — weak but sincere — before she closes her eyes again. Nicky follows suit shortly after, naturally snuggling into Rio in his slumber. 

Agatha feels her heart ache as she looks at them both, picturing a future that almost certainly could never come to fruition.

Chapter End Notes
