Coming up next time: A confrontation.

Chapter 16: Day 4, Part 4

Chapter Summary

A confrontation.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio drifts off immediately and sleeps hard — the kind of slumber that only comes from pure, bone-deep exhaustion.

Agatha, on the other hand, doesn’t sleep at all, staying awake for the next...hour? Two? Three? She’s not entirely sure, the whole situation blurring into a haze. All she knows is it’s well into the afternoon when Rio finally opens her eyes again and groggily mumbles, “Agatha?”

“That’s my name — don’t wear it out.” A beat. “Scratch that. I like the way it sounds when you say it. How are you feeling?"

Rio presses the heels of her hands into her eyes. “Good. I’m still tired, but I feel…better.”

“I’m glad. The little human heating pad probably helped a bit.” She lightly scratches her nails on a still-sleeping Nicky’s scalp.

“Probably. How is he?”

“Oh, he’s fine. He’ll be fine.” Agatha nods, now running a hand through his locks.

“That’s good. I’m glad."

She takes a deep breath. “Okay, I think we’ve pretty much exhausted our small talk, sweetheart."

Rio looks down at the blankets, picking at a loose thread dangling off the sheets. “What do you want to talk about?”

Agatha’s eyes briefly flicker down at Nicky — a silent warning to be careful what she said just in case he awoke. “When do you want to get your things?”

She shrugs a shoulder. “I can go now if you want.”

“I don’t want you to do it at all, but you seem to think a passport is important.”

“Well, I do need to reenter the United States, Agatha.”

“Shithole country,” Agatha mutters. “And there are very much ways to do that without a passport — they just require some creativity.”

Rio gives her a look. “I don’t think I have the energy for creativity right now.”

Agatha purses her lips. “Do you have a tracking app on his phone?”

“No.” She glances down again, wrapping the thread around her finger so tight the tip goes pale. “He was too stupid to figure out how that worked. Double-edged sword, obviously.” 

“So you don’t know if he’ll be there,” Agatha muses, chewing on the inside of her cheek. “I don’t want you confronting him alone, Rio. That’s a supremely stupid idea.”

“I know it is.” She glances at the clock on the nightstand. “Though, I think he was supposed to be on some dumb yacht right now.”

“I don’t care. I don’t want you to risk it.”

Rio sighs. “I have to go get my stuff.”

“I’ll go with you,” Agatha offers. Any other time, she’d be positively humiliated at how desperate she sounds. At how…frightened she is, deep down. “I just don’t want to wake Nicky or have him wake up and freak out because I’m not here.”

“It’s okay, Agatha,” Rio assures her. “You stay. It’ll only take a minute, and I’ll have you on speed dial in case anything happens.”

There’s a long, long beat. It’s not right. Agatha can’t explain it, but something about this is not right. It made all the logical sense in the world, and yet. And yet. And yet.

“I don’t feel good about this, Rio,” Agatha admits, voice uncharacteristically soft.

“It’ll be all right.” She untangles herself from Nicky, swinging her legs over the side of the bed. “I’ll be back before you know it.”

“Rio—” Agatha sighs, running a hand over her face. Part of her is willing Nicky to wake up if only so there would be an interruption to distract Rio from this suicide mission she seemed hellbent on going on, but he doesn’t stir. He doesn't make a peep. He gets the sleep he needs. “Just…just wait for me, for fuck’s sake. Please. For my own sanity.”

Rio looks at her, eyes pleading. “I just want to get this over with,” she whispers. “I just want to be done with him.”

“You can be done with him when I can go with you.” Agatha does not beg. Agatha does not pray. In this moment, Agatha does both.

“He’ll be back by four,” Rio says, glancing at the clock again. “It’s 3:30 now. Trust me, Agatha — please, I need you to trust me now.”

She purses her lips, considering. Rio was playing dirty, and they were running out of time. She considers waking Nicky herself, but he’d almost certainly have questions and need reassurance — eat up more precious seconds from this rare window. 

“If you’re not back here by 3:55, I’m going to your room and busting the goddamn door down,” Agatha warns. “Be fast and be careful.”

“I will.” Rio nods, slipping on her sandals. “I promise.”

Agatha is not going to say ‘I love you,’ even if they’re the first words that pop into her brain for some fucking reason. She’s not going to say ‘I love you,’ even if she’s starting to think it may be true. Because that was crazy. She’d known her for less than a week.  

She’s not going to say ‘I love you.’ She’s just fucking not. 

“Hurry,” she reiterates instead.

“Okay,” Rio whispers. “Okay.”

Rio does three things on the walk back to her room. She clutches her phone tight in her hand, Agatha’s contact pulled up — her own better version of her keys slotted between her knuckles. She walks with her shoulders squared and her head held high — the posture she always adopts to enter a courtroom. And she tells herself that he will not be there — that he will be on the boat like he’s supposed to be.

But despite this — and despite her reassurances to Agatha — the short journey feels like a death march.

She is surprised but also not when she opens the door to see him sitting on the bed, an X-rated movie playing on the TV, a laptop perched in his lap, and at least a dozen alcohol bottles littering the side table, residual white powder amongst it. “I told you you’d be back,” he says with a dark chuckle. “You barely even lasted five hours. Fucking pathetic.”

“I’m just getting my stuff,” she says, forcing herself to not even spare him a glance — a power move but also an efficient one. She grabs her passport from the pocket of his suitcase before sliding it into her own, along with some clothes she manages to haphazardly stuff into it. She’s not even sure why she’s packing them — they didn’t fucking matter, in the grand scheme of things — but she’s already here, and it’s sort of the principal of it. He didn’t get to enjoy any trace of her. “I told you: I don’t want you,” she says, shutting the bag with a definitive zip.

She goes through a mental checklist in her head: passport, clothes, computer…computer…where had she put her computer? It wasn’t on the desk where she thought she left it, but it wasn’t in her laptop bag either…

"Because you're a filthy fucking dyke?” he asks. “That's the only explanation. Oh, and I have evidence. You love evidence, don't you, counselor?" 

She doesn’t find her computer because it’s on his lap, her iMessages pulled up. “‘Hey, hot stuff,’” he reads. “‘You left something in my room.’ ‘I know. He couldn’t see the evidence. Plus, I thought you would enjoy it.’”

Rio’s blood runs cold — an old instinct, an old reaction. She freezes. She had been caught. She had been caught, and that was fucking terrifying. This was the worst thing that could happen.

Rio’s blood runs cold, and then it runs very, very hot — a newer instinct but an even older one, too. One she had before Thanos had happened to her. One that had reappeared after Agatha did.

She fumes. She had been caught. And so what? And so fucking what? Agatha was the best thing to ever come into her life.

She glares at him with the intensity of a thousand burning suns. “Give me my shit.”

“Actually, it’s my shit — I fucking paid for it,” he argues before going back to reading. “‘Both are hot. At least with you in mind.’ ‘Makes sense.’ ‘You’re hot. What can I say?’”

He’s trying to embarrass her. She will not let it embarrass her. She will not let him take this from her, too. He could have her and her dignity and her body, but he could not have Agatha.

“No, actually, you didn’t — I paid for that laptop before we were married, you stupid fucking asshole.”

“Well, I paid for the fucking room it’s currently in. And considering you’re standing in it, I guess that means I own you, too.”  

“You’re renting the room. Your analogy is as dumb as you are.”

Thanos ignores her. He takes a swig of gin and tonic, looking at the screen once more. “‘What else do you want to hear?’ ‘Your moaning was rather nice last night.’ ‘We can arrange that again.’” He tilts his head thoughtfully, wagging a finger at the laptop. “See, I always knew you were a cheating little bitch, but the carpet muncher thing...”

Rio doesn’t justify that with a verbal response. Instead, she swiftly grabs the computer off his lap and snaps it shut.

With her still feeling some effects of being drugged against her will and him drunk and drugged very much by choice, they’re on a slightly more level playing field than usual, though he is still much bigger and stronger. His reflexes are sloppy, but he does manage to snatch the laptop back and throw it across the room, it smashing into the sliding door to the balcony, before doing the same with her phone.

She flinches at the noise, but unlike the glass, she doesn’t break. “You’re such an asshole,” she mumbles. It was annoying, to be sure — she had a lot of shit on that computer and phone — but she could buy new ones. She turns on her heel, freedom so close she can taste it. It tasted like ocean air and all the chicken parmesan she could eat and Agatha.

He manages to get to her suitcase before she does, immediately fishing out the passport in a rare display of intelligence and holding it above his head. With his other, he reaches for her neck, though instead of grabbing her throat, he rips the necklace she’s wearing — a relatively inexpensive but sentimental piece her father had gotten her for her quinceañera — easily breaking the chain and holding it in his fist. “Cheap piece of shit. You and the fucking necklace.”

“What the fuck?!” Rio snarls, hand instinctively going to her now bare neck. She won’t cry. She can’t cry. After a moment of shock, she snaps back into action, grabbing at the arm holding her passport and twisting it with all her might. She’d never really understood that phrase before — seeing red — but her vision is all crimson now.

He throws her off of him easily, sending her flying backward against the tub in the corner of the room, before grabbing a lighter next to the heart-shaped candle on the ledge and holding the corner of her passport to it.

Adrenaline pumps hard and loud through her veins, masking some of the pain she’s sure she’d feel otherwise. It’s enough to help push herself back up and bring her knee as hard as she can into his groin.

“Ow! Jesus fuck,” he hisses, dropping the lighter and passport to the ground. 

Thankfully, the lighter flips off, not setting the room ablaze. Even more thankfully, she manages to snatch the passport up and shove it deep into the pocket of her shorts.

“Help!” she yells as she begins to run to the door. “Fire!” 

“Always so dramatic,” Thanos grumbles as he stands, grabbing the collar of her Bohner Family Reunion shirt and yanking her back hard. “Where the fuck do you think you’re going?”

Rio answers by screaming at the top of her lungs and hoping to god the walls are thinner than she thinks. She kicks back frantically, eventually finding a kneecap, though it only makes him tighten his grip on the fabric. It starts to rip in the struggle, but he manages to make her lose her balance in the process, sending her to the ground once more. He drops to his knees, pinning her to the floor.

“Not so tough now, are you?” he asks, breathing out another menacing laugh.

Rio absolutely refuses to go out like this — by his hand and in a shirt that says Bohner on it. She desperately reaches out to her side, managing to grab the lighter before flicking it on and holding it to his neck.

“Ow!” He cries out again, holding a palm to the burn. She uses his recoil as a chance to scramble up and away once again. “You stupid fucking cunt.” He pushes himself up, grabbing at the closest thing — the lamp from the side table — and chucking it as hard as he can at her retreating figure.

It hits her calf — enough to make her stumble, enough for her to feel a rush of sticky blood burst from it — though thankfully, her brain is working overtime, allowing her to then reach down and grab it as an impromptu weapon.

He throws the alarm clock as well. A vase with a bouquet of roses. Another candle. Anything he can get his hands on, charging toward her all the while.

The clock and vase she can avoid, but she makes the mistake of briefly turning to see what she’s up against, causing the candle to hit her square in the gut. She winces, folding over a little and faltering just enough to let him reach her.

He drags her back into the room by her hair before shoving her against the wall. He sneers as his hand does wrap around her throat now, squeezing hard. “If I can’t have you, nobody can.”

This is it. This can’t be it. This has to be it.

Rio thrashes, hitting and kicking and fighting like she never has before — giving it all she has. Finally, she thinks to herself, all of those stupid hours in the gym are paying off.

God, her head hurts. Her throat hurts. Everything hurts. 

Maybe it’s two seconds after he begins choking her, or maybe it’s two minutes or two hours or two days. Maybe she’s blinded by rage and the drugs that he fed her, or maybe this is as clear as she’s ever been. Maybe it was never supposed to end like this, or maybe it always was. She doesn’t know.

All she knows is she swings up with the bottom of the lamp as hard as she can. All she knows is she hears a dull thud and then a sharp crack as it makes contact with the back of his skull. All she knows is she will never forget that sound as long as she lives.

His grip suddenly gets loose, his eyes growing wide and panicked for a moment as he looks at her with…fear. That’s what this feeling is. He inflicted it often, experienced it never, but something is wrong. Something is very wrong. “What did you do?” he whispers before sinking to the ground. “Rio, what did you do?”

It’s almost cartoonish, the way he drops to the floor — propped against the ridiculous heart-shaped tub.

Rio collapses a moment later, beginning to cry like she never has before. She goes to clutch the necklace her dad gave her, crying harder when she realizes it’s not there.

She can barely crawl over to her now-cracked phone and dial the emergency number, the way her hands are shaking. The people on the other end of the line can barely understand her, the way she’s sobbing. She did this so she could live, but right now, she wants to die.

She sends Agatha a text — three words. Not the three words she wanted to say to Agatha but three words nonetheless: You were right. 

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: Agatha reacts to the news.

Chapter 17: Day 4, Part 5

Chapter Summary

Agatha reacts to the news.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

AGATHA HARKNESS [3:46pm] What do you mean I was right? 

AGATHA HARKNESS [3:46pm] Hello? 

AGATHA HARKNESS [3:47pm] Rio? 

AGATHA HARKNESS [3:47pm] Rio, answer me. Now. 

AGATHA HARKNESS [3:48pm] What happened?

At 3:49, Agatha calls her. So what if it’s only been three minutes since the first text? So what if it’s still six minutes from when she threatened to let herself in? A lot could happen in three minutes. A lot more could happen in six. 

“Pick up,” Agatha mutters as she holds the phone to her ear. She’s pacing around the living room now, leaving Nicky to slumber away in blissful ignorance — the way it should be. The only thing going right at the moment. “Pick up, goddamn it. Pick up.”

Rio answers on the third ring. “Agatha?”

Thank fucking god. She’d breathe a sigh of relief if Rio sounded even marginally coherent at the moment. But she doesn’t. She sounds like she’s just been hit by a bus and then run over by a train and then lit on fire.

“Rio,” Agatha responds as calmly and evenly as possible — trying to balance out her decidedly uncalm energy. “I need you to tell me what the hell is going on.”

There are a few desperate, shaky breaths. “Dead,” she finally manages.

Agatha sucks in a sharp inhale — some may even call it a gasp — but recovers quickly. “Did you—?” ‘Kill him’ goes unspoken.

“I had to!” Rio defends. “He— he— he attacked me! That’s what— that’s what I told them!”

“Okay, okay — calm down.” Rio seems to forget that Agatha didn’t actually give a fuck about this man. In fact, she hopes it was a slow and painful process. “Who do you mean by ‘them’? You called the cops?” That’s the thing she was really judging her for.

“I’m not—” she hiccups “—getting arrested for murder, Agatha,” she winces.

Yeah, she sure the fuck hoped not, but she didn’t trust the police. She rubs a hand over her face. “What exactly did you tell them?”

“That he attacked me. That it was self-defense. There are witnesses to corroborate my story. You and— and the people at breakfast. They must have seen something,” she desperately lists. “And physical evidence. If they examine me. The drugs and— and— and the…the way he....even though I took a bath, I think…” She can’t finish her sentence, but Agatha doesn’t need her to. Some things are just too awful to speak aloud.

Agatha really wishes Rio was thinking like a lawyer right now. Thanos’ lawyer, to be more exact. That man was rich and powerful, and he would remain rich and powerful even in death. They would bring up the fact that she was Latina, that she was queer, that she was cheating — cheating with a criminal like Agatha — and they would twist it. That’s how they operated. 

Agatha really wishes Rio would have just called her first. They could’ve thought of a lie together. A story to better protect her. He made a bad investment and jumped off the balcony. He caught wind that was being investigated for fraud and fled Sicily to god knows where. He went for a swim and got lost at sea. 

But that’s not where they were. Rio’s fatal flaw — her inclination to be honest — had reared its ugly head. 

“I’ll be right there,” Agatha quietly assures her.

After waking Nicky and doing a lot of soothing and apologizing — she promises that Ms. Rio is going to be just fine and that the two of them will go to the pool later and get even more ice cream for dessert — she makes her way to Rio’s room, her heart pounding to the rhythm of her quick footsteps. 

She stops short of Rio’s door, the kooky, curly-haired woman she recognizes from their boat ride to the resort in front of it. 

“Can I help you?” Agatha snaps at her.

“I heard her screaming. Do you know what happened?”

“I don’t see how that’s any of your business.”

The old woman scoffs, crossing her arms. “She was yelling for help! I’m worried for her.”

“Well, go be worried from a distance, you nosy bitch.”

“Jesus Christ.” The woman rolls her eyes. “Do at least keep me updated,” she requests, going back into her room.

“You can watch the news like everybody else.”

The door is locked, of course — automatic for the resort — meaning Agatha has to knock. “Rio,” she says, knuckles tapping the wood. “It’s me. Let me in.”

It takes Rio a few moments, considering she literally crawls to the entrance — evident by the fact she’s on her knees as she slowly turns the handle and pushes it open.

It feels like some kind of twisted game show. Right behind door #1 is…the woman you might love battered within an inch of her life — a dark bruise around her neck, a bloody gash on her calf. 

Agatha doesn’t feel guilt, but she’s flooded with it right now. Agatha doesn’t take responsibility, but it’s all her fault. It’s all her fucking fault. She wasn’t there. She should’ve been there. She had a bad feeling. Agatha doesn’t apologize, but— 

“I’m sorry,” she whispers, unable to stop her voice from shaking with sadness and shame alike. “I’m so sorry, Rio.”

Rio whimpers as she glances up, a fresh round of tears welling in her eyes. She raises a weak arm, beckoning Agatha to hold her.

For once, Agatha doesn’t argue. Doesn’t let herself think about what this kind of innocent intimacy might mean. She just steps inside and lets the door close behind her before dropping down to the floor and pulling her close.

Rio buries her face against her, still shaking as shock courses through her body.

“It’s okay,” Agatha soothes. “It’s okay,” she lies. It wasn’t okay. Not one tiny fucking part of this was okay. 

Her eyes drift over to Thanos. To his lifeless body. 

Agatha had been in the room with a corpse before — her mother’s corpse. It made her feel so light and so heavy all at once. So relieved and haunted at the same time. There are some things you just don’t forget. The sound of someone hitting the ground, taking their last breaths. The smell of blood in the air. The look of vacant eyes. No matter how much they deserved it, it stayed with you. 

“It’s okay,” she repeats for her own sake as much as Rio’s.

“Scared,” Rio mutters.

“You don’t have to be scared anymore,” she comforts, running a hand through her hair. “He’s gone, okay? It’s over. It’s over.”

“I don’t…I don’t know what to do.”

Agatha’s not sure if she means that in a literal short-term sense or a longer existential one. Considering she can only answer the former, that’s exactly what she does. “They’ll probably come take your statement. Get you some medical treatment.”

“I know the drill.” Rio nods against her. “Statement. Rape kit. Tox screen. Preventative antibiotics. Fluids. I’ve seen it before.”

“Me too. I loved watching SVU marathons when I was pregnant with Nicky,” Agatha says, attempting a little dark humor, though it is the truth.

Rio either doesn’t find it funny or doesn’t have the energy to laugh. Maybe both. “Before I did human rights specifically, I did stuff like this. It got to be too much, so I switched. It’s—” Rio takes a deep breath. Speaking was a currently large mountain she was valiantly attempting to climb. “I told you — I have witnesses to the drugging, to the way he pulled me around. Defensive wounds that multiple professionals can attest to. I screamed for help, so someone could have heard me—”

“Your temporary neighbor,” Agatha confirms. “She was listening outside the door like a fucking freak.”

Rio raises her head to give her a chastising look. “Don’t be so harsh on her. I doubt she literally had her ear up to the door. I spoke to her a few times, and she seemed sweet — a little strange, maybe, but nice. Plus, it’s good for me — for someone to attest to the fact that I was screaming bloody—” She stops herself from saying it. ‘Bloody murder.’ A bit too on the nose. “—that I was screaming as loudly as I could,” she amends.

“Whatever,” Agatha says, easily dismissing all of this logic. “I thought she was a crackpot even before she played bouncer outside your room. She looks like the type to own a different crystal ball for each day of the week and howl at the moon.”

“Maybe not howl at the moon because she’s…you know…a human being? Not a wild animal?”

“Yeah, but woo woo people like that are so in touch with nature or whatever the fuck that the lines get blurred.”

Rio’s frowns. “Now you’re just being mean.”

“I’m always just being mean.”

“Not to me,” Rio argues. “I want soft Agatha right now.”

“You’re getting her. Your batty neighbor’s the one getting bitch Agatha. I can multitask.”

Rio grumbles, shifting in her arms. “Then hold me tighter.”

“Forgive me for trying to be gentle at your husband’s crime scene.”

A beat as Rio’s mouth becomes a thin line. “He’s not that anymore. He’s dead.”

“That’s…true,” Agatha relents.

Another beat. “And it was horrifying.”

“I am sorry about that,” Agatha says, voice growing softer and more sincere again. “It should’ve happened on your timeline. On your terms.”

Rio nods a little. “I wish it had.” She takes a deep breath — something Agatha is eternally grateful for. Her track record with that — with oxygen — wasn’t exactly stellar. “I’m tired. It’s all so much. Too much.”

It’s about to be more, but Agatha doesn’t have the heart to tell her that. Death was devastating when you loved someone, but it was complicated when you didn’t. Especially when everyone expected you to be devastated. Expected you to love them. Blamed you for protecting yourself. 

But she was still your mother, Agatha — she gave birth to you, raised you. You knew she was fragile; why did you have to argue with her? But he was still your husband, Rio — he married you, provided for you. You knew he was jealous; why did you have to push his buttons?

She snapped out of her thoughts by a wince. “My body hurts,” Rio admits. “I didn’t really feel it until now. Did he…”

“Did he what?”

Rio purses her lips. “I don’t want to look,” she whispers.

“I will look. What are you asking?”

“How…how badly did he hurt me?”

Agatha sighs. “Your calf is cut — I’m not sure if it’ll need stitches. Your neck is bruised, though I’m not sure there’s a whole lot they can do about that besides some painkillers. That’s all I could see with your clothes on. If you want me to look under them, I’m happy to.” For once, there’s no suggestion or innuendo in the comment.

“No.” Rio shakes her head. “That’s okay. The doctors will have to. Will you stay with me while they do that?”

“All right,” she finds herself agreeing. “I’m not sure if they’ll want to do that or take your statement first. And I’m not sure they’ll let me be there for that part.”

“It’s okay. I’m just anxious." Rio chews on the inside of her cheek. “I hate that I'm so anxious,” she quietly admits.

“I mean…this is presumably your first homicide, no?” she rationalizes.

“Yeah, and technically legally speaking it wasn’t a homicide because it was self-defense,” Rio clarifies. As if Agatha gives a shit. As if Agatha wasn’t the one who suggested she kill him in cold blood multiple times. She should save it for the cops.

“I just meant that…the first time for anything can be scary — killing someone included. Maybe even especially.”

“It’s just so…” Rio pauses, searching for the words. “I heard his body hit the ground, and I can’t…stop…hearing it. I keep hearing it, and I keep feeling his hands on me — feeling what he did — but it’s all so past tense and removed that it doesn’t feel like me.”

“I think that’s probably your brain’s sort of fucked-up way of protecting you,” Agatha reasons. She sounds like her dumbass court-ordered therapist, and she hates it. But Rio doesn’t seem to, and she supposes that’s all that matters.

“I guess,” Rio concedes. “I just…I hate it all.”

“You’re free from the immediate physical threat of them. That’s one thing to not hate, hopefully.”

“No,” she agrees. “I’m just…I don’t know…nervous,” she repeats.

Agatha sighs. She had very little patience for circles. They were inefficient and ineffective. She wanted to cut right through the middle of them — get to the core. “What, exactly, are you afraid of?”

“Everything.”

“Nuh-uh.” Agatha shakes her head. “Specifics.”

Rio thinks for a moment. “The nightmares,” she finally says. “The flashbacks. Him haunting me.”

“Well…” Agatha struggles for an answer. “You believe in therapy, so…you could try that. And I bet your weird-ass neighbor has some sage to help keep the evil spirits away.”

Rio nods. “But I’m also afraid of the uncertainty — of not knowing where I’m supposed to go from here.” She looks down. “I’m scared…I’m scared that you might decide I’m not worth it.”

Agatha purses her lips, quiet for a few long moments. She can’t imagine a future where she’ll ever decide that — Rio not being worth it. But she can’t imagine a future where she doesn’t fuck it up either — do something to make Rio realize it’s Agatha who's never been worth it at all.

“I’m still here, aren’t I?” she finally says.

Rio glances up at her. “Yeah,” she replies. “Yeah, you’re still here.” She looks back down, takes another breath. “I never asked, where do you live?”

“Jersey. Westview. I mentioned it during our…second conversation.” Agatha was incredibly good at that — filing the little details away. She’s had to be. “You never did tell me where you do, though. Just that you’re originally from Puerto Rico.”

“Brooklyn,” Rio answers. “So not that far, but…I don't know. I might move after this. I sure as hell don’t want to live in that apartment anymore.”

Agatha slowly nods. “Brooklyn’s overpriced as fuck, too.”

Rio meets her gaze again. “Do you think maybe I could…stay with you?”

Agatha opens her mouth to respond despite not knowing what the fuck is going to come out of it. But before she can find out, the universe (merciful, for once) intervenes. 

A team of cops and medical personnel burst into the room, erupting it into chaos — mirroring exactly how Agatha feels on the inside.

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: Agatha struggles to keep her emotions at bay and finds herself (very reluctantly) confiding in a most unexpected source.

Chapter 18: Day 4, Part 6

Chapter Summary

Agatha struggles to keep her emotions at bay and finds herself (very reluctantly) confiding in a most unexpected source.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha should go back to Nicky, even though — according to the live stream she has set up on her phone — he’s perfectly fine, obliviously watching Dora the Explorer with his stuffed rabbit perched beside him.  

Agatha wants to go back to Nicky. Her perfect Nicky. She wants to see his sweet little face, hug his tiny little body, hear his beautiful little voice. No matter what Agatha was going through, Nicky always made it…maybe not okay but worth it. He made life worth living. 

Agatha can’t go back to Nicky. Not like this. Not in the state she's currently in. She doesn’t want him to see her like this — all…all…triggered, some dumbass therapist Agatha very much did not believe in would say. Traumatized. They loved those stupid fucking buzzwords that meant jack shit. 

So instead, she smokes in the hallway. Paces Rio’s floor. The environment is almost ominously normal despite the fact it's a crime scene. Despite the fact there’d been a death in it not an hour prior. The resort was obviously trying to keep it hush-hush. Death was bad for business, after all.  

She smokes and she paces and then, when the weirdo fucking neighbor’s door opens, she curses into the air. “Didn’t I tell you to just watch the news?”

“Oh, you can fuck right off,” the woman retorts. “How’s the young woman doing? Not well, from the looks of it. You’re out here stress smoking — looking brittle as a twig.”

“You’re one to talk, you frail-ass, old-ass bag of bones.”

The old, curly-haired woman shakes her head. “I see right through the act, you know. You’re pretending to be tough, but you’re a feral animal — lashing out because you’re afraid. Now answer my goddamn question.”

Agatha is most certainly not about to give her that satisfaction — especially after the feral animal callout that felt a little too accurate. “What kind of animal?” she inquires, blowing out a stream of smoke. Her hand was shaking a bit, which was annoying as fuck. “Like what species?”

“Answer my question, or I will find the girl myself.” The woman crosses her arms, face contorting in a smug expression. “Very well could distress her, and we wouldn’t want that, hm?”

“She’s in an ambulance,” Agatha snaps. “You know, being checked out by medical professionals?” She scoffs, taking another puff as she scans her patterned muumuu, her chunky handmade jewelry. “You probably don’t. You look like the kind of person who doesn’t believe in vaccines.”

“Oh, shut your big, overcompensating mouth — you know what they say about assumptions. Medical science and spirituality can and do coexist, not that it’s any of your business.”

“Okay, so wait — let me just get this straight: your view on vaccines is none of my business, but what happened to the woman next door is yours?” Agatha narrows her eyes, pointing her cigarette at the woman. “Hmm...I’m not quite sure I’m following that particular line of logic.”

The woman promptly ignores her. “I see the crime scene tape. I can draw certain conclusions—”

“I thought you didn’t like those. I thought drawing conclusions made you an ass.”

She’s stalling, of course. She doesn’t want to tell her about Rio. Doesn’t want to tell her about any of the emotions that Rio — that Rio’s situation — stirred up in her. The memories and feelings she’d long buried that it unearthed. 

“What’s an old woman like you doing here anyway?” Agatha asks. “Nursing home excursion?”

“I’m connecting to my heritage.”

Agatha quirks a brow. “You’re Sicilian?”

“Yes, and you’re deflecting.”

She huffs, eyes scanning the hall — kids in water wings and influencers in sunglasses leisurely strolling down it. She’s not airing Rio’s business out here. 

Agatha pushes past the woman, inviting herself into her hotel room and walking straight to her mini bar.

“It’s mostly empty,” the woman warns, shockingly unfazed. “All that’s left is cheap wine.”

Agatha opens the tiny fridge door, nose wrinkling as she confirms the woman’s words. “Gross.”  She promptly shuts it once more and puts her cigarette out in the ashtray before taking another from her purse. Not the first time this trip she was left wanting for alcohol and resorting to nicotine instead.

“Those are horseshit,” the woman says, digging around her tote before tossing her a different pack. “I’m Lilia. Now tell me what the fuck is going on.”

She blinks but manages to catch the box of Platinum Kols. Agatha much preferred Marlboro Reds, but after a beat of consideration, she drops her own pack back into her purse and fishes one out from the container the woman — Lilia, apparently — had tossed to her. Agatha wasn’t in the habit of turning down free stuff. 

“Her husband was an abusive piece of shit,” Agatha says, flicking her lighter on and holding the cigarette to it. “He is no longer a piece of shit because he is also no longer breathing.”

“Huh.” Lilia softens a bit. “Well, I’m glad to hear that — men like him deserve worse than what he probably got. How do you know her?”

She shrugs. “Met her here a few days ago.”

“And?”

Agatha gives her a look. “What do you mean ‘and’? That’s the full answer to the question.”

“I’m not stupid. You’re attached, or you wouldn’t be so mean and defensive.”

“Patently false. I’m always mean and defensive. It’s, like, my whole thing.”

“Not with her.” Lilia shakes her head. “I saw you two at dinner the other night.”

Agatha crosses her arms, feeling uncharacteristically vulnerable. “What are you, a spy? Are you his fucking spy?”

Lilia scoffs. “Paranoid much?”

“Well, can you blame me for being a little paranoid right now?” she snaps.

Lilia throws up her hands. “About what? From the sounds of it, he was your run-of-the-mill man. Barbaric? Yes. Smart enough for espionage? No.”

“You don’t have to be smart to be dangerous. And you don’t have to be a man either,” Agatha spits. She immediately wishes she hadn’t. That was a whole can of worms she’d just cracked open — given the chance to crawl out.

Lilia softens once more. “I know.” There’s a beat as she scans Agatha up and down. “Shit mom?”

Agatha considers for a moment before plopping down onto Lilia’s couch, her legs beginning to feel as shaky as her hands. “No,” she says. At least her voice was staying even — for now, at least. “No mom. She’s also no longer breathing.”

“But she was awful,” she notes. A statement — not a question.

“So fucking what?” she replies. She hates this. Hates the way the mommy issues radiate off her. Hates that the bitch is still haunting her in death. “That has nothing to do with anything.”

“It has everything to do with your reaction.” Lilia sighs, sitting on the chair across from her. “I’m curious about you and that woman because it was clear — even before I got confirmation — that he wasn’t good to her. I could see it in her body language. Now, I don’t know her well, but she seemed sweet, and the idea of her being with someone who doesn’t care for her doesn’t sit well with me.”

Agatha looks down at her lap — cracks her knuckles between her knees. “She’s not with me — we’re not together — but obviously, I…care about her. Or I wouldn’t be here.”

“Do you want to be with her?”

“It’s really not that simple.”

“That question is. Do you want to be with her?”

Agatha glances up at her then. “It is really. Not. That simple,” she repeats through gritted teeth.

It usually was that simple. Usually, Agatha went after whatever the hell she wanted. Usually, she acted on whatever the hell she felt. Usually, she was selfish and impulsive. 

But usually, Agatha didn’t hold her hookups while they cried. Usually, she didn’t let them sleep over. Usually, she didn’t let them meet her child. Nothing about this — about Rio — was usual.

“Why is it not?” Lilia presses.

“Oh, I don’t know — maybe because she just killed her husband? And I killed my mother? And frequently want to kill my ex-wife and a large percentage of the population?”

“Okay. But do you want to be with her?” she repeats.

God, she was relentless. She was effortlessly typing in the nuclear codes to make Agatha explode. “It doesn’t fucking matter — I’m not the kind of person she needs.”

Lilia tilts her head, calm as can be. Infuriating bitch. “And what do you mean by that?

“Fucking hell, lady — how dense can you be? I’m not a good person!” she blurts. “I’m not good enough for her!”

“Good and bad aren’t black and white,” Lilia counters. “Nor are they set in stone. Be better with her. Be better for her. And regardless of your opinion, she may want you.”

“Wow.” Agatha breathes out a humorless laugh. “You know, you’re even more delusional than I initially thought, and that’s really saying something.”

“Have you even asked her what she wants? Have you even tried not being someone you so clearly despise deep down under this phony exterior?”

“Of course, I’ve tried,” she hisses. “I’m not capable. I’ve never been capable.”

“You are,” Lilia argues, voice even but firm. “And I don’t say this to give you false hope — because I don’t do that shit. People who can’t change don’t even think about it. They don’t hate that they can’t. They don’t loathe themselves underneath their bravado. They don’t have a bravado — that’s just who they are. Yours? Yours is bravado.”

Agatha shoots daggers at her. She hates this woman. She hates how persistent and obnoxious and presumptuous and optimistic and…right…she is. About the bravado, at least. About the loathing. Agatha hates that this woman can see her. Agatha did not give this woman permission to see her. 

“You don’t know me,” she accuses anyway. Because that much was true. Agatha was still a fundamentally bad person, and there was no fixing that. Nobody had ever been able to pray or beat or starve the badness out of her, no matter how hard they tried. “And I don’t know who the hell you think you are.”

Lilia scoffs, lifting her chin. “I’m pretty damn smart is what I am. Like I said, you’re a wounded animal lashing out. But that cage you’re trapped in? You put it there yourself. You need to woman up, find the key, and break out so you can be the person that girl deserves.”

“I can’t be the fucking person she deserves! Just like I couldn’t be the fucking daughter my mother hoped for! Or the fucking wife my ex wanted! Or the fucking mom my son needs!” 

Agatha’s pretty sure she can physically feel fire coming out of her eyes in the intense glare she gives Lilia, but then she realizes that — fuck — those are tears. Those are tears because she’s about to cry. 

She’s sure as shit not about to cry in here, though.

She pushes herself up and charges toward the sliding glass door, ripping it open and stepping onto the balcony. She grasps at the ledge overlooking the beach, gasping in the fresh sea air.

Lilia follows behind a few seconds later. “You tell yourself all of that now, but the fact that you’re so worried about it tells me everything I need to know about who you are deep down — about who you have the potential to be.”

“Jesus, take a hint,” Agatha growls. “I clearly want to be alone, and it’s not like I’m about to fucking jump.”

“You’re ashamed that you’re crying.”

“I’m not crying. Get your eyes checked, old lady.”

“I’m very right, and you’re very upset. Touch your own face, you dumb bitch — you’ll find tears.”

Agatha does touch her face, harshly swiping it in an attempt to clear it of any tears. She is a dumb bitch. And she is very upset because of it. “I let her go there alone,” she whimpers, voice finally cracking.

“But she survived,” Lilia says more gently than before. “She’s still here, and she needs you now.”

“It’s all my fault,” Agatha whispers, taking a shuddering breath. “It’s all my fucking fault.”

“How could that be true, hm?”

“I should have come with her. I should have protected her.”

A tiny wince escapes Agatha’s throat as she squeezes her eyes shut, thinking of Nicky — how tiny he was when he was born. How wrong it looked, seeing him hooked up to all those machines. Wailing all alone in that hospital room as the doctors ran tests, Agatha helpless on the other side of the window. She couldn’t even hold him. Agatha could never protect anyone.

“You have a chance to do that now,” Lilia reasons. “The active threat, so to speak, may be neutralized, but she’s still got a long road ahead of her.”

Agatha shakes her head. “I’ll only make it worse.”

“You don’t know that. And only she can decide that. Would you rather not try and hurt her more by running off?”

“Yes,” Agatha hisses, looking over at her again. “Yes, because it will hurt her less in the long run.”

“You don’t know that. Again, you need to stop with these asinine assumptions.”

“There’s fucking heaps of evidence to suggest this.”

“Evidence isn’t always damning,” Lilia counters.

“No, but you’d be an idiot not to see the pattern and draw the conclusions I have.”

“Either way, she deserves support,” Lilia rationalizes. “And she clearly wants it from you if she called you right after it happened.”

“That phone call is not the piece of damning evidence you think it is — she doesn’t know anyone else on this fucking island.”

“She could have called reception.”

Agatha narrows her eyes at her. Is silent for a beat. “It’s weird that you never asked how.”

“How what?”

“How I killed my mother. People usually ask for the gory details, but you didn’t flinch. You didn’t even bat an eye.”

Lilia shrugs. “It’s in the past. It clearly haunts you. No need for me to press for details.”

“You’re not curious? You don’t want to know if it was on purpose? If it was justified?”

Another shrug. “Honestly, I’m more concerned with making sure you get your head out of your ass.”

She crosses her arms, chews on the inside of her cheek, uncomfortable with this…lack of prying. Of judgment. Of…fear. “It was a heart attack.”

Lilia blinks. “Okay. Now can we talk about how you’re going to stop being a coward?”

“I was 17,” Agatha continues. She wants to make her stop. She wants to scare her away. She wants to make her understand that she is not meant to have someone like Rio. “Just days away from being able to leave her fucking house and never go back. I tried to run away at least once a month from the time I could walk. In all honesty, I probably tried before that — attempted to crawl away. She caught me sleeping with another girl — she was one of those religious types, you know — and raged so hard she dropped dead right there. Right on my bedroom floor.”

Lilia blinks again, maybe slightly more distributed this time. “Well, that’s horrible. But it’s still not relevant to this situation.”

“I pissed her off on purpose,” she keeps going. She’s not sure she’s ever said this aloud. She’s not entirely sure why she’s saying it now. “Constantly. Raged at her right back. Screamed at her until she fell and kept screaming as she convulsed there. I’m not even the one who called the ambulance — the girl I was fucking did. The whole world told me I should feel sorry. I didn’t feel sorry. I don’t feel sorry. I’m not a good person, Lilia.”

She has the fleeting thought that Lilia might try to hug her. She’s not sure what she would do. If she’d push her off the balcony or if she’d let it happen. If she’d like it a little more than she’d hate it.

Lilia doesn’t hug her, but she does place a gentle hand on her forearm. “You couldn’t control the fact that her body gave out. Couldn’t control the way she treated you.”

Agatha doesn’t lean into the touch, but she doesn’t shrug her hand off either. Instead, she simply looks down at it as if it’s foreign. Because it is. It’s quite foreign to Agatha.  

“I couldn’t control it,” she softly agrees. She feels herself take a shaky breath, feels the snot blocking her nose. “I couldn’t control it,” she repeats. Nobody ever trusted that. That it wasn’t on purpose. That it was a weight off her shoulders, but it wasn’t on purpose.

“I know. I believe you.”

More tears. Fuck. Fuck, fuck, fuck. “Okay.”

Lilia’s thumb rubs gentle circles on her skin. “What you can control is what happens now. You can choose how you behave going forward.”

Another sniffle. “Talking about my behavior. What are you, my mother?” she halfheartedly snarks. But she’s not. She’s shown more compassion for Agatha in 18 minutes than Evanora did in 18 years.

Lilia snorts. “I’m just trying to drive some sense into your thick skull.”

“My skull is perfect just like the rest of me,” Agatha replies, finally looking up at her. “I don’t know how long all this will take. I can’t just leave my son alone.”

“I’ll check on him,” Lilia offers. “Or he can stay with one of the paramedics — I’m sure they’d watch him.”

“No.” Agatha shakes her head. “No, he doesn’t like doctors, and I want to keep him as far away from all this as possible.” 

Agatha purses her lips, looking at Lilia closely. She was a stranger — and a weird one at that — but Agatha…trusts…her for some reason. Innately trusts her like Rio seems to trust Agatha. 

“Would you just…would you sit with him in the room?” Agatha asks. “Maybe take him to the pool. I…promised him he could go. If he starts coughing, you just need to pat his back, put on his PEP mask. It’s not complicated, and he knows how to use it. Just don’t let him take it off too early. Or overexert himself. Or—“

“I will,” Lilia cuts her off. “But do tell me your name first. And his.”

She takes a deep inhale, lets out something like a sigh. “I’m Agatha."

Lilia nods. "Agatha."

"His name is Nicky — he’s six. If he gets so much as a scratch in your care, I’ll make you wish you were Rio’s husband.”

“I take care of my great-niece often. He’ll be okay.”

Agatha takes her bottom lip between her teeth, considering for another moment. “My room is just downstairs — I’ll introduce you.”

“All right.” Lilia nods. “Lead the way.”

Chapter End Notes

We deserved more Lilia and Agatha interaction in canon! They had so much dysfunctional but deep-down caring mother-daughter dynamic potential!

Coming up next time: The ambulance ride.

Chapter 19: Day 4, Part 7

Chapter Summary

The ambulance ride.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Nicky practically leaps up from the couch when Agatha opens the door. “Mama,” he says, his little legs running to greet her. He stops short when he sees the strange woman with her. “You’re not Ms. Rio.”

“Nicky, don’t be rude,” Agatha chastises. She doesn’t know why she does. For show, maybe. She doesn’t actually give a shit, and she was about a million times ruder herself. “This is Ms. Lilia.” 

“I don’t care.” The space between his brows wrinkles, and his eyes grow watery — some combination of pissed off and panicked. “Where’s Ms. Rio? I want Ms. Rio.”

Lilia crouches down so she’s at his eye level, and Nicky responds by shyly stepping to hide behind Agatha. If Lilia wasn’t doing her an enormous favor right now, Agatha would make some dig about how she better have life alert handy if she’s going to drop down to the floor like that at her ancient age. Help — I’ve fallen and I can’t get up.

“It’s good to meet you, son,” Lilia tells him. “Ms. Rio will be back soon. She’s a little hurt right now, and your mom is going to go make sure she’s okay.”

Nicky grips onto Agatha’s pant leg and looks up at her. “I want to make sure she’s okay, too.” 

Agatha sighs. “Not right now, buddy. I need you to be brave for just a little longer and stay here with Ms. Lilia, okay?” 

“No,” he stubbornly insists. “I don’t want to.” 

“Well, I’m very sorry to hear that, but that’s what’s happening.” 

Nicky peers at Lilia. “But I don’t know her. Who even is she?” 

Agatha does not appreciate this attitude when it’s directed at her, but it is sort of a valid question. “She’s…” Agatha runs a hand over her face. “She’s my friend,” she forces out, resisting the urge to throw up as she does. 

Nicky gives her an odd look. “You don’t have any friends at home,” he points out.

“I know.”

“Here, you have two.” 

“I know.” 

“That’s weird.”  

“I know.”

Lilia steps in, effectively ending the childish exchange. “I’m sure you can see her when she’s feeling a little better,” she reassures him. “You know how sometimes you get a paper cut on your finger or fall and skin your knee so you need a bandaid?”

Nicky nods a bit. 

“Ms. Rio needs a little more than that, but it’s the same idea. The grown-ups just need some space in order to take care of her.”

“But why?” he asks earnestly. “I can help. I’m a good helper.”

“I’m sure you are,” Lilia agrees. “But she needs help from people who went to school for a long, long time.”

“I’m in first grade,” he mumbles — because that seemed like a pretty long time to him. “I did preschool and kindergarten and got all A’s.”

“And that’s wonderful, but these people have gone to medical school.”

“What grade is that?”

Lilia tilts her head a bit, considering. “Well, it’s complicated, but I suppose you could call it around 20th grade, if not higher.”

“Oh,” he says, not quite convinced but beginning to warm up to the idea. 20 was a pretty big number. “Do you speak Spanish, Ms. Lilia?”

“I’m sorry, I don’t — but I do know Sicilian and a lot of other things. What are you interested in?”

“Mm…” he ponders. “Animals — especially bunnies and the ones in the sea. And music. And books.”

“Well, you’re in luck because I also happen to love animals. Do you want to go sit on the couch and tell me about your favorites?”

Nicky’s grip on Agatha’s pant leg loosens the slightest bit as she looks up at her. 

“Go on,” Agatha says, giving his back a gentle nudge of permission. 

His lips purse in contemplation. “Wait here. Don’t leave yet,” he orders. 

Agatha lifts her palms. “All right.” 

Nicky runs the few steps over to the couch, returning momentarily with his raggedy stuffed rabbit.

“Scratchy?” Agatha questions. 

“For Ms. Rio,” he explains. “In case she gets scared with the doctors, too.” 

Agatha softens, her heart aching in a way that’s not altogether bad. “Are you sure, buddy?” 

He gives her a confident nod. “I’m sure.” 

Agatha feels her eyes burn again. That just won’t do. She clears her throat, leaning down to ruffle his hair and place a lingering kiss on his forehead. “I’ll be back soon, okay? I love you,” she murmurs. 

“I love you, too, Mama.”

Agatha stands, and with one last look at Lilia — some combination of gratitude and warning — she goes out to the front of the resort where the ambulance is parked.

A paramedic breathes a sigh of relief when they see Agatha approach. “Ms. Harkness? Hi. Ms. Vidal requested you ride with her to the hospital. It’s a short trip, and we said you could meet us there, but she insisted. Wouldn’t get in the ambulance without you.”

“All right.” Agatha gives them a look, her defensive mask snapped firmly back on. “Don’t get your panties in a fucking wad.”

“Um, okay…” they mumble, turning on their heel and leading Agatha to where Rio’s sitting. She’s curled up on a bench, eyes vacant and far away.

Agatha reaches down, lightly touching the top of her head. “Hi, sweetheart.”

Rio blinks at the contact — nearly flinching — but once she looks up and sees who the hand belongs to, she relaxes once more, sinking into it. “Agatha,” she manages to mumble after a second. “Missed you.”

She’s not going to say she missed her, too, even if it's the truth. “I was gone for less than an hour,” she says instead. That was a truth, too.

“Missed you,” Rio repeats anyway as the bureaucracy around her begins wrapping things up. Quite literally, in fact, as they wheel out a black body bag. With a whimper, she turns her face.

Agatha sighs and strokes Rio’s hair before shooting the people wheeling Thanos out the dirtiest look she can conjure. “You couldn’t fucking wait until she was gone to do that? Bunch of fucking morons. Sei un idiota,” she translates in Italian — one of five phrases she learned before coming here.

Agatha looks back down at Rio, fingertips softly brushing over her bruised neck — noticeably bare. “Did the paramedics take your necklace?"

She doesn’t know the story behind it. All she knows is that it’s significantly cheaper than all of Rio’s other jewelry and that she fidgeted with it in a way she never did with her wedding ring or tennis bracelet. That it must be valuable for a non-financial reason.

This is further confirmed when Rio shakes her head, a few tears starting to fall. 

“You lost it?” Agatha asks. “When did you last see it? Maybe it’s in my room.”

“He— he broke it,” she manages through heaving breaths.

“Rio, look at me.” Agatha takes her chin. “I can be pretty handy. I’m a lesbian, for fuck’s sake. Do you have it?”

Rio nods, reaching a shaky hand down to her pocket and producing the pieces.

“Oh, that’s not so bad,” she soothes as she examines it. “It’s really just the clasp. Is the chain important, too? Or just the pendant?”

“I don’t— I don’t want it to change. I’ve had it for over 20 years.”

“All right.” Agatha nods. “That’s fine. I’ll figure it out, okay?” It would take much more time and effort than simply replacing the chain, but she would figure it out. For Rio, she would. “But right now, we need to get to the hospital.”

“I know.” With no small amount of effort, she manages to push herself up and begin to walk the few steps to the ambulance. “Agatha?” She looks over her shoulder. “Come with me.”

“I’m right behind you,” she assures her. “I’m right here.”

“Promise?” 

Agatha sighs. “I’m not leaving you again,” she says softly. Not now. She won’t make that mistake again.

“Please don’t.”

“Rio. I’m not,” she slowly but firmly repeats. “You trust me, remember?” And she probably shouldn’t. She definitely shouldn’t. But Rio had said that she did, and she needs to use that to her advantage right now — to calm her down.

Rio gives her a slow nod before stepping into the ambulance, forgoing the bed in the middle of it to sit on the small bench to the side instead. She scoots over, leaving space for Agatha — a spot she occupies without hesitation.

Agatha pats her leg. “Lie down on my lap. Come on.” 

“That’s not really what we'd recom—" a paramedic starts.  

“It’s better than fucking nothing, isn’t it?” she snaps.

The paramedics look at each other as if to say, ‘This bitch is crazy,’ but don’t argue.

Rio adjusts herself so her head is resting on Agatha’s legs. She absentmindedly reaches up to play with one of Agatha’s hands — an action that seems to relax her. “Sorry if I’m gross. I know I need a shower."

“You’re fine, Rio,” Agatha replies, resisting the urge to scold her for the completely insane and unnecessary apology. “I should have brought you one of those little things Nicky likes to fidget with,” she muses, stroking her hair with her free hand.

“Is he okay?” Rio asks, a little guilt laced through her tone as she traces the ridge of Agatha’s knuckle.

“He’s fine. He’s…with a babysitter.”

Agatha sure as fuck doesn’t want to get into all of that right now, and luckily, Rio doesn’t press for details. After a second, she speaks again, voice even softer than before. “I'm so fucking scared, Agatha."

Agatha takes a deep breath. "Well, actually, you're in luck. Nicky was worried you might be, so…” Agatha reaches into her purse and pulls out the stuffed rabbit. “He wanted you to borrow this to help you feel less afraid. And believe me, Rio, that’s a big fucking deal — he doesn’t go anywhere without him.”

Rio removes her hand from Agatha’s, going to fiddle with the rabbit instead. “That was sweet of him.”

“He’s basically Nicky’s version of your necklace.”

“I used to have a weighted stuffed animal,” Rio muses as she runs the rabbit’s ear through her fingers.

“Oh yeah?”

“Mhm. A shark. He thought it was stupid, so it’s been in a box in my closet for a couple of years.”

“Well, you can free him now.”

Rio looks up at her. “You don’t think it’s dumb?”

Agatha shrugs. “Not particularly. People do all kinds of weird shit to comfort themselves.” Agatha preferred sex, alcohol, and the occasional hard drug as a treat, but different strokes for different folks.

“Okay,” Rio replies after a moment, curling in closer. “You’re comfy.”

“So you’ve said.”

“Because it’s true.”

“You repeat yourself a lot,” she notes. “I hate repeating myself. Everyone should listen to me the first time.”

“Sometimes people are hard of hearing,” Rio counters. "Or have auditory processing issues.”

“I don’t mean them.”

“Oh.” Rio blinks. “Sorry.”

Agatha shrugs again, unfazed. “It’s fine. I am a bitch in most situations, so.”

“I like you, though.”

Agatha breathes out a laugh. “That doesn’t mean I'm not a bitch.”

Rio bites her bottom lip. Agatha can practically see the wheels turning in her head, debating whether to open her mouth before she finally comes out with an, “Agatha?”

“Hm?”

“Can you hold me tighter?” she requests, tone bordering on embarrassment. “I realized we’ll probably be there soon, and…yeah…” she trails off. She doesn’t need to say any more than that.

Agatha obliges. “You’ll be okay. You said you’re no stranger to doctors, right? And I’m not either. I won’t let you take any shit from them.”

“Doctors aren’t usually performing a rape kit on me,” Rio quietly admits. “That’s what I’m nervous about.”

“I can take you for ice cream after,” Agatha offers. “Would that help? That’s how I bribe Nicky.”

Rio gives her a tiny smile. “I think I just need someone to be there for me so my mind doesn’t go…places I don’t want it to.”

“Do you think I’m coming with you for the delicious hospital food, Rio?”

Her small smile grows the tiniest bit before disappearing completely, some color draining from her face. “I’m fine with cardiologists, endocrinologists, you name it, but I really, really hate OBGYNs.”

“Why is that?” Agatha asks, voice uncharacteristically soft. “I mean, besides the obvious.”

Rio takes a deep breath, looking down at the rabbit. “It was fine until we were married. Then he insisted he had to come with me. He’d make inappropriate remarks, and…touch me. When the doctor wasn’t there.”

The confession is so vile, Agatha actually feels like she might throw up. “Jesus fucking Christ, Rio.”

She blinks up at her, innocent. “What?”

“That’s supervillain shit.”

Her eyes drop back down to her hands. “Yeah.”

Agatha purses her lips. “Well, I’m obviously not going to do that.”

Rio nods. “I know. Still. Scary.”

“I know,” Agatha replies, softly repeating her words.

Rio chews on the inside of her cheek. “Will they think it’s stupid? If I cry?”

Agatha scoffs. “First of all, who gives a fuck? Second of all, I think crying during a literal rape kit is probably pretty standard.”

“I guess so.” Rio pauses for a second. “What if—” She shakes her head. “No. Never mind.”

Agatha sighs. “Rio, don’t do that. Come on. What were you going to say?”

After a moment of deliberation, she finishes in a small voice. “What if my birth control didn’t work?”

Fuck. Fuck, fuck, fuck. If Agatha thought she was out of her depth before, she was really out of it now. She was in a leaky submarine in the deepest part of the fucking ocean out of her depth with this. “Well…you’d have options,” she says, attempting to stay as calm and logical as she can.

“I know. I wouldn’t want it. It’s just…it’s my worst nightmare.”

“Having an abortion?”

“No, being pregnant with his…thing.”

Agatha stupidly thinks back to those Law & Order: SVU marathons. “They’ll check during the kit. And give you a morning after pill if you want it.”

“I do,” Rio says quickly. Another beat. “I hope it works.”

“It should. We’ll keep an eye on it,” Agatha slips. Because that would mean implying there would be a future off this island for them.

Rio nods and forces herself to take a deep breath. “All of the worst possibilities are flashing through my mind right now.”

“You lived through the worst for a long time, Rio,” Agatha reasons. “You can do it again.”

There’s a long, long stretch of silence before Rio replies, voice so quiet it’s barely audible, “I’m already so tired, Agatha.”

“So you rest. So you recover. So you keep going because you have to,” she says, voice firm and adamant. “He doesn’t get the satisfaction of making you give up.”

“I know,” she confirms, voice just as soft as before.

Agatha is almost grateful when they pull up to the hospital. There’s not a whole lot of time to talk there — not about anything other than her physical health, that is. Agatha knew how to handle that. A lot better than emotions, at least.

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: Rio gets a phone call.

Chapter 20: Day 4, Part 8

Chapter Summary

Rio gets a phone call.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Between getting her blood drawn, fluids pumped into her, and her leg stitched up, Agatha is fairly certain Rio has bruised her hand from squeezing it so hard. Not that she particularly cares. She’s ready to bruise anybody a hell of a lot harder in a place a hell of a lot more painful than their hand if they so much as look at her wrong.

After all of that, as well as countless swabs — of the side of her cheek and under her nails and between her legs — and just as many silent tears from Rio, they’re finally cleared to leave the hospital. 

“Is the fact that it happened here going to make things more complicated?” Agatha asks in the taxi on the way back to the resort. The driver seems to speak only Italian, which was probably a good thing — he’d make a shitty witness to their conversation. Paranoid, she can hear Lilia’s voice in her head. How fucking obnoxious. “International law and whatnot?”

“Possibly,” Rio admits. “But the fact we were both American citizens should make things a little simpler.”

“That’s good.” Agatha purses her lips, racking her paranoid brain. If only Rio hadn’t called the fucking cops. “Did he have family?”

Rio nods. “A mom. She’s divorced from his dad. His father wouldn’t talk to him anymore.”

“Well, his mom also won’t talk to him anymore unless she holds a seance,” Agatha mumbles. “Is she one of those godawful boy moms?” Agatha, too, could be potentially characterized as such, though she would shank anyone who dared to suggest as much. Her boy was different. Nicky could actually do no wrong. “You think she’ll try and fight you in court? Or…smear you in the press?”

“Press? No.” Rio shakes her head. “Court…maybe? She’s not…particularly invested in public appearances because of said messy divorce, nor does she have the money to pay for a halfway decent lawyer. She might show up and harass me, though.”

“No. She won't,” Agatha replies, voice cool and confident. She’ll make sure of that. “And she might not have the money for a half-decent lawyer now, but he was loaded. Will his money still go to you, or...?"

“I’m next of kin, so despite everything, it probably will. Plus, chances are Stark won’t want his reputation tarnished with this scandal, so he won’t dig his nose into it. He hated Thanos anyway. Only let him invest out of pity.”

“Hm.” Agatha considers. “Tony Stark having a brain cell. How unexpected.”

“Not a brain cell. An ego,” Rio corrects. 

“Ah.” Agatha nods. “Yeah. Makes more sense. Arrogant bastard.”

Rio shrugs a bit. “Works in my favor now.” She’s being…oddly nonchalant about this whole thing. Agatha wonders if that’s a defense mechanism — her way of coping. Agatha doesn’t not relate.

“We’ll take it.” A beat. “Is there anyone else that’s likely to cause you trouble — legally, publicly, or otherwise?”

“Mm…” Rio hums, considering. “Maybe his brother?” She shakes her head. “I’m not sure. I could never figure out how Eros actually felt about anything. But he seemed…nice the few times I met him.”

“Nice like how?” she asks, suspicious. “That’s his only sibling?”

“Yeah, just the two of them. I don’t know — once, he told Thanos he shouldn’t yell at me. They almost got into a fist fight because of it.”

“You think it’s a brain cell thing or ego thing?”

“Brain cell, most likely. He’s sort of a loser but not in an incel way. He seemed…vaguely self-aware.”

“Okay, well that’s…potentially promising.” Agatha still doesn’t completely trust him or his intentions, but she hardly ever did. “Have you thought about calling your dad?” she asks more gently.

Rio purses her lips, an odd, conflicted expression crossing her face — as if she wants nothing more than to talk to him right now. As if she wants nothing less. “Maybe tomorrow.”

“Why not tonight?” Agatha presses.

“Talking’s hard. I can’t wait to stop.”

“That’s…” Concerning. A relatively unreasonable request, all things considered. “…fair enough.” 

The car pulls up in front of the building, and Agatha hurries out, wordlessly going to the other side of the car to open Rio’s door and help her out. She gives her an arm for her to balance with as they walk into the building, her calf rendering mobility attainable but more difficult than normal.

“Thank you,” Rio says softly, voice so touched and eyes so wide and earnest that Agatha can’t bear it.

So she doesn’t, quickly moving onto a less-than-savory but probably necessary topic.

“Oh, um — I should probably tell you. Nicky’s babysitter is…” Agatha clears her throat. “It’s your weird next-door neighbor.”

“Okaaay…” Rio flashes her an odd look but thankfully doesn’t make her relay the whole humiliating series of events that led up to it happening. “So you changed your mind about her?”

“No, but I vetted her, and she seemed a passable babysitter in a pinch,” Agatha clarifies. “She is also extremely annoying, though. And nosy. She knows your name now.”

“That’s okay. She’s nice.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “She’s fine.”

Rio shoots her another look — more scolding this time. “She’s nice. You’re not going to explode if you admit that someone’s nice.”

“I might,” Agatha argues. “You really want to take that risk?”

“Yeah, because I’m that confident you won’t.”

“You’re gonna feel really bad if I spontaneously combust. Leave a poor, sweet child without a mother.” It wasn’t even true — Nicky would still have Wanda if Agatha died. But ginger bitch didn’t count.

“Just fucking admit it,” Rio goads. “Your ego will be fine.”

“She was…she was…she was ni—" Agatha makes dramatic explosion noises and gestures with her free hand, causing a few people to give them odd looks as they make their way through the halls.

“Agatha,” Rio says, unamused.

She promptly ignores her, continuing the explosion theatrics.

Rio sighs now, running a hand across her face. “Agatha.”

“Oh, come on.” She gives her a light nudge. “You know you want to laugh. Or at the very least crack a smile.”

“And yet here I am, not laughing or smiling.”

Agatha’s bottom lip juts into a pout. “You’re gonna hurt my feelings.”

Rio stops walking and turns to Agatha, wrapping her arms around her. “Compromise.”

Agatha immediately hugs her back. She has the sneaking suspicion this was far more about Rio’s needs than her own, but at the moment, she’s happy to oblige under whatever guise Rio wanted. “Not as good for my ego, but I’ll take it.”

Rio leans against her for a long moment, melting into her touch.

“Cozying up to me after all that talk about desperately needing a shower,” Agatha notes. “Charming.”

“Just to get rid of him,” Rio clarifies, voice muffled as she buries her face into Agatha.

“I know. I know,” she assures her, running a hand through her hair. “I was just teasing.”

“Oh.” Agatha feels her tense up a bit — her skin flush out of embarrassment. “Sorry.”

“It’s all right,” she assures her. “Jokes are my default in this situation.” A beat. “Most situations. Not all of them are good. I mean, most of them are, but occasionally, I miss.” Another beat. “That was another joke, in case that wasn’t clear.”

“Good joke or not, I’m probably gonna miss it,” Rio notes — her own attempt at humor.

Agatha pulls back to give her a small smile. “Good thing you’re pretty,” she quips.

“Am I?”

“Rio, I got two strangers on the beach to tell you that you were last night.” Last night. Jesus, had that all only been yesterday? It seems like a lifetime ago.

“But it’s your opinion I care about,” Rio insists.

“You think I’d fuck someone ugly?” Agatha scoffs. “I’m a little insulted.”

“Agatha,” Rio groans. “Please?”

“Please what?”

“Just be forthright for once in your life.”

“I think you’re beautiful, Rio,” Agatha says. “I think you’re on another plane of existence from most of the world.”

The corner of Rio’s mouth curves into a small smile. “It’s nice when a pretty woman thinks I’m pretty.”

“It is, isn’t it?” Agatha says, giving her a light kiss on the nose — an oddly tender action. “Are you ready to face the shitstorm that is my six-year-old and his six-hundred-year-old babysitter?” She nods toward her door.

Rio stares at it for a long moment, seemingly overwhelmed at the mere sight. “I guess so.”

“He should be in bed by now, but Lilia seems like a fucking pushover, and he’s been worrying about you nonstop.”

Rio shifts her gaze from the door to look at Agatha. “He was worried?”

Agatha scoffs at the understatement of the century. “He was practically inconsolable.”

“Oh.” Rio blinks as if the thought of someone worrying about her — besides her father, maybe — somehow never occurred to her. “That’s sweet of him.”

“That kid adores you, Rio. I don’t think you realize how much.”

“I…appreciate it. But I don’t get why.”

Agatha shrugs. “You know Spanish and like his rabbit. He’s not a particularly harsh critic, really.”

“I suppose so.” Her brows furrow once more. “I just never figured kids would really like me.”

Agatha really has to stop doing that — making jokes Rio doesn’t pick up on. Especially right now. But it’s just how Agatha is wired.  

She decides not to draw attention to the missed quip. “Why? You’re great with them, and you have vaguely kindergarten teacher energy — at least in the streets.” A beat. “A very sexy kindergarten teacher, but still."

“Thank…you?” Rio says slowly. “I don’t know how to interpret that. Kids didn’t really like me when I was a kid, so I figured that probably wouldn’t change as an adult.”

“Yeah, well, don’t take it personally — most kids are freaks,” she replies, unlocking her hotel room. She hears Rio take a deep breath beside her — sees her attempt to plaster on a more convincing smile.

“Mama! Ms. Rio!” Nicky exclaims immediately — just as Agatha knew he would. 

Agatha steps in front of Rio to intercept him if necessary. “Calm, Nicky. Be calm.”

Lilia raises an eyebrow from her place on the couch. “Nicky, I told you to what?” 

He freezes before slowly — almost comically — walking backwards. “To rest quietly. Sorry, Ms. Lilia.” 

Agatha blinks in surprise. How the hell had she gotten him to listen like that? Was she…was she actually a good babysitter?

She scoops him up, walking him back to the couch. “What did my favorite boy do today?” 

“Ms. Lilia took me to the pool,” Nicky tells her. “I held my breath a long, long, long, long, long time.” 

“Wow, that sounds fun — you’ll have to show me next time. What else?” Agatha glances over at Lilia.

“I also made sure he got some dinner in him, and we watched Animal Planet,” Lilia offers. “He told me many fish facts.”

“Daddy seahorses are the ones that have the babies,” Nicky shares. “You can tell how old a goldfish is by looking at the rings on its scales — like a tree. Dolphins sleep with one eye open.”

“So smart,” Agatha absentmindedly praises despite giving approximately zero fucks about marine life. She lowers herself onto the couch and sets him on her lap, brushing his hair away from his face. “What did you eat?” 

“Spaghetti. She only let me have ice cream after I finished 10 whole bites.”

“Because it’s important to get nutrients,” Lilia explains.

“That’s true. I want you to grow big and strong. But not too big or too strong, young man.” Agatha pokes his stomach. “You take your time growing up, understand?” 

“Yeah.” Nicky gives her a tiny smile, turning his head to look at Rio still standing silently in the doorway. The beautiful elephant in the room. He turns his head again — this time to whisper in Agatha’s ear. “Can she sit by me?” 

Agatha cups her hand around her mouth, whispering back. “You can ask her. But be gentle, okay? She’s still feeling a little yucky.” 

Nicky dutifully nods. “Ms. Rio? Do you want to come sit by me?”

“Sure,” Rio says with another smile — only half-forced. Nobody could resist Nicky. “For a little bit. But then I need to rest.”

“That’s okay. Me too,” he assures her. He frowns as she walks toward him, noticing her condition. “What happened to your leg? And your neck?” 

“Nicky.” Agatha runs a hand over her face. She really should’ve specified no prying questions either. Rookie mistake. 

“I thought it was her tummy that hurt.” Fuck, he was smart. Too smart. How impressive and infuriating.

“Well…” Rio gives Agatha a glance before attempting to answer the question. “I got hurt. And it was scary, but I’m safe now.”

“How?” 

“Nicky,” Agatha warns.

“Did you fall down?” he presses.

Rio purses her lips — as if even the vague discussion of it is physically painful. “Someone hurt me. Please, leave it at that,” she gently but firmly pleads.

“Oh.” Nicky’s eyes grow wide and concerned. “Are they in time-out?” he whispers. 

“In a way,” Agatha answers for her. “They won’t be hurting her again.” 

He nods, marginally reassured by this answer. "Did…did my bunny help? At the doctor’s?”

Rio nods. “He was very soft.”

“He’s a good bunny,” Nicky agrees, his fingers fidgeting in his lap. Agatha can tell he’s anxious — that he wants him back now. 

“Lilia, would you mind grabbing him out of my purse?” she requests.

Lilia wordlessly nods and goes over to the table, reaching into Agatha’s purse and retrieving the bunny — along with a crumpled-up $20 bill, which she deftly slips underneath her bangles. Frankly, Agatha would respect the hustle if she went for something bigger — a few 100s at least.

“I’ll leave you all be,” Lilia says as she walks back to the couch to hand it off. “It was nice to meet you, son.”

“You, too, Ms. Lilia,” Nicky politely replies, though Agatha can tell he means it.

Agatha takes the stuffed animal, simultaneously reaching under Lilia’s bracelets to snatch her money back, too. "Goodbye, Lilia."

Lilia scowls, “accidentally” hitting Agatha in the face with her own purse as she turns toward the door. “See you around.”

Agatha itches the side of her head with her middle finger, casually flipping her off. “Bitch,” she mutters under breath.  

“What, Mama?” 

“Nothing, baby.”

The ambient sound of Animal Planet playing in the background is interrupted by the buzz of Rio’s phone — the notification she receives nothing good from the way the color drains from her face, the way tears begin to bubble in her eyes again as she types back a shaky response.

Nicky clocks it immediately. “What’s wrong, Ms. Rio?” 

“Hey.” Agatha reaches out to lightly touch her leg. “You okay?”

Rio wordlessly turns the screen just enough for Agatha to see a short text exchange. The contact at the top says Papá, and it reads: Mija, saw the news about a violent death in Sicily. Have you heard anything about that? Are you all right? Love and miss you. Xx

Yes, actually, Rio has typed back. I was involved. She really wasn't one to beat around the bush.

“Shit,” Agatha mutters. “Do you need to call him?” 

As if on cue, her phone rings, her father no doubt beating her to the punch. Rio lets out a nearly imperceptible whimper, unable to bring herself to answer it.

Agatha sighs, taking the phone from her hand and declining the call. She sends a text to her father: I’m okay. Call you in a few. 

“Bedtime, Nicky,” she announces. 

“But Mama—"

“No whining. You’re already way past.” 

Nicky looks at Rio, eyes wide and scared. “Are you really okay?” he whispers.

Rio purses her lips, considering. She clearly doesn’t want to lie, but the truth was too awful for anyone to bear, much less a six-year-old. “I will be,” she responds after a second, voice just as quiet.

“Can I give you a hug?”

Rio nods a little. “Yes.”

“Gentle, Nicky,” Agatha cautions.

Nicky shifts, wrapping his arms around her as lightly as he can, Señor Scratchy clutched in his hand. “Te amo,” he tells her.

One of the tears in Rio’s eyes falls onto her cheek. She squeezes her eyes shut, presumably in the hopes of stopping any more. “Y tu.” 

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: An endless day finally comes to a close.

Chapter 21: Day 4, Part 9

Chapter Summary

An endless day finally comes to a close.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha returns to the living room approximately three and a half lullabies later. She’s being more indulgent with Nicky than usual, feeling the slightest bit of guilt about leaving him all evening with a stranger. He’d been a trooper. He always was.

“He’s asleep,” Agatha announces. “Lilia wore him out, I think.”

It takes Rio a moment to answer. To speak. That was hard for her sometimes, Agatha had learned. “That’s good,” she finally manages.

She could try to force some more small talk, but what would be the point? Band-aids were meant for ripping. “Let’s go into my bedroom — call your dad.”

Rio looks at her, eyes wide and shining with panic. “He’ll be worried. And I don’t want him to— but I can’t— or else he—”

Agatha raises her palms. “I can do most of the talking,” she promises. “But I’m sure he’s going to want to hear your voice as proof of life.”

She sighs, looking down and squeezing her eyes shut. “Okay,” she agrees after a moment, voice barely audible.

“Okay,” Agatha repeats, holding out her hand. “Come on.”

It's another beat before Rio opens her eyes, but once she does, she takes it and allows herself to be pulled up and led into the room. 

“Hardest parts are over,” Agatha reassures her once they settle on the bed. “From what you told me, he’s just going to want to make sure you’re okay.”

Rio nods, which Agatha takes as permission to press the contact for her father. It doesn’t even get through an entire ring before he answers, frantic. “Hija, ¿qué pasa? ¿Qué pasó? ¿Estás bien?” 

“Mr. Vidal,” Agatha says. It feels strange to call him that — vaguely childlike — but she realizes she doesn’t know his first name. “It’s Agatha.” 

“Agatha? Who the hell is Agatha? Where’s my daughter? I need to speak to Rio. Quiero hablar con mi hija.”

“Estoy aquí,” Rio speaks up, voice small. “Agatha es…una persona que yo conocí en Sicily. Ella cudia a mí mas mejor que Thanos. El es muerto. Y...por muchos años el abusó de mí. No dije nada porque estaba avergonzada. Lo siento. Thanos trató de matarme. No tengo la energía hablar ahora mucho. Lo siento. Lo siento, Papa.” She manages almost in one quick breath before the tears start to fall.

Agatha can’t make all or even most of it out, but there are certain words she picks up on — a combination of the rare high school Spanish class she didn’t skip and being in the room when Nicky watched his cartoons. She knows “person” and “dead” and “I’m sorry” — she can infer “abusó” and “energía.”
