Her father is quiet for a long, long moment — Agatha can’t say she blames him. “¿Mi niña?” he responds, so quiet and broken that Agatha feels it deep in her chest. “He was hurting you? And you didn’t feel you could—” A soft sob.

“I wanted to,” Rio chokes out, pinching her arm until blood begins to bead — no doubt in an attempt to hold back more shuddering sobs.

Agatha opens the bedside drawer, grabbing a balled-up pair of socks from it. She wordlessly removes Rio’s hand from her forearm and puts it in her palm instead. “Mr. Vidal—”

“Santos,” he says. “You can call me Santos.” 

“Santos.” Agatha nods. “It’s been a long, long…long day. Perhaps Rio could rest for a bit, call you again tomorrow once she has a clearer head so you can discuss…logistics.”

“I can be on a plane in an hour,” he responds. “I can be there in…how far is it? 12 hours?”

“It’s okay, Papa,” Rio whispers. “I’m okay.”

“I don’t want you alone, mija. In a strange country after all that has happened…”

“I have Agatha.”

“Who is this Agatha person?” Santos asks, a bit of suspicion creeping into his voice. “Does she work at the resort?”

“No, she’s…she’s someone I met.”

“Mija…” he says, voice almost scolding at the vagueness.

Rio gives Agatha a look that says she’s not picking a label. Agatha stares right back. She’s not going to either, and she can play this game all day. 

“Rio?” Santos speaks up. “Are you still there?” 

Rio hits mute on the phone. “Agatha.”

“No.” Agatha shakes her head. “No fucking way. He’s your dad — you decide what to tell him.” She unmutes the phone.

Rio mutes it again. “Just tell me what to say.”

“No. You’re not living like that anymore — with someone putting words in your mouth.” Unmute.

Rio glares at her, gritting her teeth. “She’s— she’s my…something. She’s taking care of me.”

“She is your nurse, then? Your doctor?”

“My—? No.” Rio massages her temples. “Please, can we talk later? I promise I’m safe for tonight.”

Another long, long beat of silence. “You will call me when you wake up tomorrow? Or if you need me before then for any reason? I meant what I said — I will get on a plane, no questions asked.”

“Yes,” Rio weakly manages, nodding for…well, Agatha’s not sure whose benefit.

“Take care of my girl, Agatha,” Santos says firmly. “Whoever you are. If you hurt her more…”  

“You’ll get on a plane to chop my limbs off one by one and leave them scattered around Sicily like a bloody scavenger hunt.” 

“That is…not exactly what I was going to say,” Santos says slowly, a bit taken aback. “But the sentiment, yes.” 

“I figured.” Agatha would do the same for Nicky. And she’s no stranger to violent threats — unfazed at this point. 

“Te quiero, mija,” Santos softly tells Rio.

“Te quiero.”

Agatha hangs up and looks at her. “See? That wasn’t so bad.” Rio shakes her head in disagreement, a fresh round of tears starting to fall. It breaks Agatha’s fucking heart every time. “What was so bad about it, hm?” she asks, cupping her face.

Rio doesn’t verbally respond, only shaking her head harder — the tears speeding up.

“Rio.” She sighs. “I get that this is hard, but I need you to at least try and communicate with me, or else I’m just going to be talking to myself. And as much as I find conversations with me highly stimulating, it’s not going to help much in this case. I know you don’t always like the verbal thing. Write it down if you’d prefer.” Agatha grabs the pad of paper and hotel pen from the side table, dropping them in front of her. Rio’s phone number is still on the top page from when she’d jotted it down next to the underwear she'd left a few nights ago.

Cares too much, Rio writes.

“Take it from me — he can’t help how much he cares. And in my never-humble opinion, he cares exactly how much a parent should.”

Rio’s brow furrows for a second before she clarifies. Worries too much.

“Worrying is synonymous with parenting — that’s the job,” Agatha flippantly retorts. She’d learned that hard and fast with Nicky and his plethora of health problems since the moment he was born. Before it, even.

The space between Rio’s brow creases further. Not about me. I’m glad he’s dead. That’s bad. I’m bad. I shouldn’t be glad someone’s dead. Even him.

“You’re not bad for that, do you understand me? Not in the slightest,” Agatha says firmly. She’s a hypocrite, maybe — considering everything she told Lilia about her feelings surrounding her mother’s death. But it was different. Rio was different. “You survived. You’re alive. You deserve to throw a fucking party right now.”

Rio shakes her head once more. Everything hurts.

“I didn’t mean a literal party,” Agatha clarifies. A beat. “Unless you want, I suppose. I’m sure I could bully the stupid waiter kid into more free desserts — maybe some confetti and a few balloons.”  

She’s joking again despite the fact none of her humor had seemed to land all day. She’s joking again because that’s all she knows. She’s joking again because, if she doesn’t, she might break down once more, and she wouldn’t do that in front of Rio. She couldn’t.

Rio gives her a timid shrug, setting the notepad aside before curling up and lying her head on Agatha’s lap.

She reaches down to stroke her hair. “What do you want, Rio?” she whispers. “What do you need?”

Rio closes her eyes, silent for a moment. “Just hold me,” she finally mumbles.

“Okay.” A beat. “Do you want to…do...anything else?”

Another head shake.

“You don’t want me to—” Agatha shakes her own head. Like a hypocrite. “No. Never mind. Of course, you wouldn’t right now.”

Rio turns her head to look up at her, confusion etched into her features.

“Forget it. I’m…” Ashamed and humiliated for even thinking it. “Please, let’s just pretend I didn’t say anything, okay?”

Rio shrinks into herself. “I'm sorry,” she mutters.

“No, don’t. Don’t be sorry. I’m…” She sighs. She’s embarrassed — this is embarrassing — but she has to explain at least a little, or Rio would continue to spiral. To blame herself. “I…tend to solve a lot of problems with sex is all. Try to, anyway.” She clears her throat. 'Hypersexuality,' one of her stupid court-ordered therapists had said, 'from childhood trauma.' Fucking idiot. She liked to fuck because it felt good — not because her mommy didn’t love her.

Rio pushes herself up a bit, reaching for the notepad again. You don’t understand intimacy when it’s not rough and sexual because you didn’t experience any from a caregiver when your brain was still developing.

Agatha scowls — something Rio is already addressing with her next sentence. 

Sorry to be clinical or whatever, but when I shut down, logic works, and that’s about it. I don’t want to have sex, but I’m not mad at you for your instinct to suggest it. 

She bristles at the words Rio writes — at the psychoanalyzing. It was vulnerable and deeply uncomfortable and she absolutely did not want to talk about it further. So she doesn’t. “We don’t have to fuck. Obviously. I would never force you. It was just…it was a dumb idea. Which is rare for me.”

Not dumb. A reaction that makes a lot of sense. Even if I don’t want to do that, I still want to be around you.

“Well, you don’t really have a choice. Your room is a crime scene at the moment.” Rio gives her a look. “What?” she questions with an innocent shrug, though she knows damn well it wasn’t the right thing to say before she even said it. The problem was, Agatha didn’t know the right thing to say.

Deflecting makes it obvious you’re nervous. 

“I’m not nervous. I’m not nervous — I’m just…well, maybe I’m not always great at staying still,” she admits. It feels like glass in her throat, admitting to not being excellent at something.

You’re nervous, she writes again, punctuating it with an underline and a knowing look. And you can play with my hair or do whatever you need to do to stay grounded.

Agatha glares at her, though her fingers do begin mindlessly braiding a small section of her dark locks. Rio lets out a contented sigh, leaning back against her. That’s a good sign, Agatha thinks — her muscles relaxing.

“Did you grow up playing with dolls?” Agatha asks.

Rio makes a so-so motion with her hand. 

“Hm,” she hums. “Nicky does, too. I didn’t. I ran around and made potions with shit in the backyard, much to my mother’s dismay. She used to call me a witch, and she wasn’t joking. Ironic considering I grew up in Salem of all places — somewhere those kinds of accusations got famously dicey.”

Rio nods a little, having a silent debate with herself — did movement or speech feel like the lesser of two evils right now? The latter seems to win out. “Did the potion thing, too. And everything else.”

“Meaning what? Dinosaurs? Sharks? Trains? Well, I already know it’s a yes on the sharks.”

“Yeah,” she confirms. “Dinosaurs, too.”

“But no trains,” Agatha muses. “Not big into transport, huh?”

Rio cracks a small smile — the first in a long while — and shakes her head no.

Encouraged by the grin, however minuscule, she continues on that line of questioning. “No? Not planes or boats or, I don’t know, skateboards either?”

Another head shake — and an eye-roll at the ridiculousness.

“You ever been on a motorcycle?”

“Mhm,” Rio hums, reaching for her phone. She was clearly over talking and writing by hand, so she opens her notes app and types, My dad has one.

“Oh,” Agatha says, a little surprised and a lot impressed. She smirks, wiggling her brows. “You know, if I swung that way, I’d probably find that sexy.”

Her smile grows a bit, though she finds the energy to slap Agatha on the arm. I can ride one — just never got my actual license.

“I can, too. And licenses are for suckers.”

And people who don’t want to get arrested. 

Agatha scoffs. “I’m not scared of the pigs.”

Felon disenfranchisement is a real thing, Rio types, expression serious.

“I can’t believe you’re the one who killed someone today, and yet I’m the one getting lectured about the law.”

In self-defense.

“I know, angel,” Agatha relents, carding her hair through Rio’s hair. “I’m sorry. Dark humor is my default, remember?”

I know. I’m just tired.

“So sleep.”

Need to shower.

“You took a bath right before it all happened,” Agatha points out. “And you have a big ‘ole bandage on your leg that’s going to be a pain in the ass to work around. Maybe we just wait until tomorrow.”

I’ll change it, Rio pushes back. And be careful.

Agatha sighs. Rio was her match, stubbornness-wise. So fucking annoying. “Well, at least let me help. I actually need a shower, too, you know. And that lecture Nicky dragged me to? They went on and on about water waste. Maybe we could…conserve?” She looks at her out of the corner of her eye, gauging her comfortability with the idea.

Rio doesn’t seem bothered, simply typing, Will you wash my hair? 

“Have I ever not washed your hair when you’ve bathed in this hotel room?”

Rio purses her lips, a silent, ‘No.’

“That’s what I thought.” She shifts Rio off of her in order to stand from the bed. “Come on, then.”

Once they’ve effectively waterproofed the wound, Agatha strips down immediately and without shame. She’s never been one to be shy about her body.

Rio follows suit, though her movements are slower. Much slower. More tired and self-conscious and obviously sore. There was no way she couldn’t be, after everything she’d been through.

Agatha flips the water on as Rio carefully sheds her clothes, turning the handle until steam begins to rise. She steps in first, taking Rio’s hand to help her in right after. 

Their first few seconds under the water, Agatha can’t help but stare at her, watching her hair go from dark brown to fully black as the hot water drips down onto it, begins to roll down her face.

Rio tilts her head. “What?”

“Nothing." She shakes her own a little. "You’re just really beautiful,” she says softly.

“Oh.” Rio’s cheeks tinge pink, and Agatha knows it’s not from the water temperature. “Thank you,” she mutters. 

“I know you don’t want to have sex, but would you be opposed to me kissing you?”

“No.” Rio shakes her head a little, managing a small but sincere smile of encouragement. “I wouldn’t.”

She lifts Rio’s chin, careful not to touch her bruised neck, and leans forward to plant a rather chaste kiss on her lips. Rio happily holds it for a long moment before burying her face in Agatha’s collarbone.

It’s a little awkward, trying to wash Rio’s hair with her resting in the crook of her neck, but not — as it turns out — actually the worst angle to work from.

“I’m definitely going to be stealing this shampoo,” Agatha says as she lathers it into Rio’s hair. “And the seasell shoaps.” She blinks. “The sheshell— Fuck. The sea-shell soaps,” she says slowly, pronouncing each syllable. “Jesus Christ — I feel like I just had a stroke. Try and say that five times fast.”

She purses her lips as Rio does not, in fact, try to say it five times fast. Agatha didn’t like silence, nor did she like heaviness, which is why she constantly tried to fill and lighten it. Rio made it challenging to do either. She couldn’t blame her, of course — especially right now — but it was…uncomfortable. It was all deeply uncomfortable.

So she just…stands there. She doesn’t like just standing there — it makes her feel…anxious and…vaguely useless — but that’s all there is to do. That’s all she can do.

After a beat, Rio pulls away and reaches up to absentmindedly play with a few strands of Agatha’s hair.

She quirks a brow. “Switching it up, hm?”

“It’s soft,” Rio notes.

“Because I don’t use any products or tools on it, including a hairbrush.”

“Let me brush it,” she requests. “I’ll be gentle.”

Agatha snorts a little. “You’re going to have your work cut out for you.”

“I know. That’s okay.”

“I’m still giving you a chance to back out.” Rio shakes her head, and Agatha shrugs. “All right — suit yourself. There may be a few rats living in there, though. Maybe even a bat or two.”

“I like rats,” Rio says, voice endearingly earnest.

She breathes out a laugh. “Of course you do. You like the things nobody else does.”

“They’re smart, clean, and sweet. No reason not to.”

Agatha was alluding to herself — to Rio liking her when few others did — but that sounded like a pathetic thing to admit. To explain aloud. “Didn’t they spread the bubonic plague?”

“Not really. They carried it, but that’s because infected fleas would bite them. They were victims, too.”

“I see.” Agatha nods. “So we should blame the fleas instead.”

“Mhm.” 

“Fuck the fleas.”

“Fuck the fleas,” Rio agrees.

“What’s your position on flea circuses?”

Rio crinkles her brows. “On what?”

“You’ve never heard of flea circuses?” Agatha scoffs. “And here I thought you were an endless well of useless knowledge…”

“What the hell are they?”

She shrugs. “Exactly what they sound like. Sideshow attraction where fleas perform tricks.”

The crease between Rio’s brow deepens, unable to wrap her head around this. “Fleas are tiny, though.”

“That’s the point,” Agatha explains. “They’re attached to mini carts and canons and stuff in a confined space.”

Rio considers this for another moment. “Huh.”

“I can’t believe you didn’t know about this. I’ll show you a video of it when we get out."

Rio nods a little before leaning against Agatha one more, face pressed against her skin.

“Why do you do that?” Agatha inquires, voice free of judgment. “Act like you want to crawl inside me?”

The inside of her, Agatha knows, is rotten. Is an ugly place. She’s glad that Rio can’t actually see it, or she’d be running. If she knew what was good for her, she’d be gone.

“I just want to be close to you,” Rio whispers. 

Agatha swallows back everything she’s tempted to say. “We should get out — get you some sleep.”

Rio tilts her chin just enough to peer up at her. “You’ll still be here when I wake up?”

“It is my room, Rio,” she says dryly.

“You know what I mean,” she grumbles.

“Yes,” Agatha confirms after a beat. “I’ll still be here.” It’s a rare promise she intends to keep.

Chapter End Notes

Thank you for taking the time out of this most sacred holiday season (Agatha All Along week, of course) to read this fic when I know there are so many being posted! Shamelessly plugging the fact that the two of us write another story together (a canon universe post-finale fix-it called Beats for Me where Agatha is a psychic vampire...and Billy's teacher...and there's breeding...coincidentally fitting many of the prompts, now that I think about it!) and that I (thetbone) have been posting one focusing on Rio as Death encountering Natasha Romanoff over the years (and getting angsty about Agatha and Nicky in the process, of course). Chapter 22: Day 5, Part 1

Chapter Summary

Nightmares. So many nightmares.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio sleeps until she doesn’t. Sleeps until she screams. And gasps for air. And desperately scrapes her throat. 

Rio screams, and then Nicky screams, and, god, does it make Agatha want to scream as she’s pulled from the restless rest she’s fallen into. 

She’s still groggy, but she manages to reflexively take a firm hold of Rio’s hands. Clawing at your neck was already not great, but the fact Rio’s was already bruised to shit by the attempted choking out? It was fucking dangerous. “Stop,” she says sternly. “Stop that.”

Rio tries to shrink away from Agatha’s touch, but it’s clear that — even as she manages to quit yelling her lungs out — she’s not completely lucid, attempting to rip her arms from Agatha’s grasp in a panicked daze.

“Rio, look at me,” she says, her hands still holding her wrists. “I need you to look at me.”

It takes a long, long moment for Rio to finally meet Agatha’s eyes, though once she does, something seems to click. She stops struggling, falling into her instead as she collapses into sobs. “I’m sorry,” she mutters. “It was a nightmare. I— he—”

“It’s okay,” Agatha reassures her. “It’s okay. I have to calm Nicky down. I’ll be right back, but I need you to not hurt yourself while I’m gone, do you understand?”

Rio looks up at her, eyes frantic but serious. “I don’t want him to see me like this, Agatha. Even if he wants to talk to me—”

“That’s all right.” She understands, of course. She understands better than anyone. Avoiding Nicky for his own protection was how she got roped into a heart-to-fucking-heart with Lilia. “I’ll keep him away.” Rio nods, pulling her knees to her chest in an attempt to stop shaking. “Deep breaths, okay?” Agatha reminds her.

“Okay,” Rio whispers, forcing some oxygen into her lungs.

“Okay.” She pats her wrist, the action strangely tender. “I’ll just be a minute.”

Nicky is in much the same position when she comes into his room — curled up and struggling to breathe. He flinches when the door opens, burrowing further under his blankets. “It’s just me, baby,” she soothes, going to sit on the edge of his bed. “It’s just Mama.” 

“Heard a— a scream. Like a scary monster attack,” he whimpers. 

“I know.” She rubs his leg over the covers. “It was just Ms. Rio. She thought there was a monster, but it was all in her head.” This time, at least. The monster had been real mere hours ago — still a living, breathing thing. 

Nicky peeks his head out of the blankets. “Her head?” 

“Yeah. She had a nightmare. You know how sometimes you get those bad dreams? And even though they’re pretend, they feel really, really real?” 

“Mhm.” He nods. “Like when I thought bunny got sucked down the bathtub drain.” 

“Exactly,” Agatha confirms. “And you woke up, and bunny was perfectly fine. But it still had you a little shaken up, remember? So you came and slept in bed with me to feel better.” 

“Yeah.” Nicky nods again. 

“Would it be okay if I go and sleep with Ms. Rio to make her feel better?” 

“Can I come?” 

“I think for tonight she just needs another grown-up.” She strokes his hair. 

Nicky frowns, considering, but miraculously ends up not fighting her. “Okay,” he finally agrees. 

“Are you sure?” Agatha checks. “I know you’re a little scared, too. And I won’t leave you if you want me to stay.” That much was true. As much as she cared about Rio, Nicky would always, always come first. 

“No.” He shakes his head. “No, it’s okay. I’m a big boy. And Ms. Rio is scareder.” 

She leans down to kiss his forehead. “I’m very proud of you for being so brave. Try and get some sleep, okay?” 

“Okay.” He hugs his stuffed animal close to his chest, nestling his head into the pillow once more.

Rio has mostly managed to stop shaking by the time Agatha returns after briefly disappearing into the master bathroom and coming out with a glass of water and Nicky’s hairbrush. She knows Rio’s not going to be able to go back to sleep right after that — not going to want to even try, as much as Agatha might encourage it — so she doesn’t bother. 

“Here,” Agatha says, handing her both before going to sit cross-legged in front of her. “You never did brush my hair. And believe me, you want to do it while it’s still damp.”

Rio nods, clearly grateful for the distraction as she slowly pushes herself to sit up on her knees and begin combing through her tangled locks. It’s strangely nice — and strangely intimate. Agatha finds her head lolling back, her eyelids falling shut. The repetition, the promised gentleness — it’s soothing in some strange way. “Did your father used to do your hair?”

“Mhm. He learned how to for me.”

“That’s sweet." Agatha absentmindedly fiddles with the comforter. "The dads at Nicky’s school…let’s just say I’m unimpressed by their handiwork.”

“It was a little rough to start, but he got better over the years.”

“My mother had no patience for mine,” Agatha informs her. “She’d just yank the brush through as fast as she could. Hurt like shit. ‘How can someone be so hardheaded and tenderheaded at the same time? You defy everything — including logic,’” she quotes.

“What a bitch.”

“A bitch with some of the flattest, dullest hair anyone's ever seen, mind you. Thank god Nicky didn't inherit it."

The space between Rio’s brows creases. “Her hair?”

“Yeah. Sometimes those things skip a generation, and I’d kill myself if he looked anything like my mother.”

“That’s…fair.”

Agatha turns her head as if she wants to look back at her. “You think so? I sort of thought you’d say suicide wasn’t the answer to giving birth to your mother’s clone.”

“Well, it’s not, but I understand the feeling,” Rio says, sucking on the inside of her cheek.

A heavy silence hangs in the air. “The doctors didn’t see anything on the scan, Rio,” she gently assures her. “And they gave you the morning-after pill. You should be fine.”

“Doctors can be wrong,” she replies, tone stiff.

“Oh, I’m well aware of that. But they can, on occasion, be right.”

“I hope this is one of those times.”

“Yes, me too,” Agatha says, tensing the smallest bit as Rio brushes over a particularly tricky tangle. “You find any mice or fleas yet?”

“No.”

“Pity. I’m sure Nicky would like another pet. He’s so bonded with Scratchy.”

“What’s he like?” Rio asks. “Your rabbit?”

“You’ve already met the stuffed version. Not so different, really.”

“Yeah?”

“He’s soft,” Agatha explains. “Cuddly. I found him when he was smaller than my palm.”

“Well, I can’t wait to meet him.”

When does Rio expect that to be, she wonders. They still hadn’t really talked about it — where Rio would go after this. What would happen with the two of them. Rio’s question of whether she could live with Agatha in Westview had gone unanswered when the authorities and medics had busted in, and it’s hung in the air ever since.

As if on cue, she follows up. “You never answered me when I asked if I could stay with you,” Rio reminds her. As if she'd forgotten. As if she ever could.

“You are staying with me,” Agatha points out. “Right now.”

Agatha can hear the eye-roll in her voice. “You know what I mean. After this.” She shifts uncomfortably, cursing the fact that she was currently in Rio’s grasp — her hair in her hands. “Agatha,” Rio presses.

“What?”

“Answer me. We need to have this conversation.”

“At—" She glances at the clock. “—3:48 in the morning?”

“Yes, because you’re procrastinating.”

“Procrastinating?” Agatha scoffs. “It’s not a fucking English essay.”

“Fine, you don’t like that word? I’ll use another. You’re delaying. You’re stalling. You’re putting it off.”

“‘Putting it off’ is three words.”

Rio ignores the childish snark. “Let’s talk.”

Agatha presses the heel of her hands into her eyes. “Pass.”

Rio sighs. “Agatha, we have to.”

“Hear me out — what if we don’t?”

“But we do.”

“Well, I don’t want it to,” she rather petulantly insists. “So…that’s that.”

“It’s not about want.” Rio puts the brush down, scooting so she’s sitting in front of Agatha — looking her in the eyes. “I’m serious."

Agatha raises a brow. “I’m serious, too.”

“This isn’t an optional thing. I have to know what to tell my dad.”

“And I have to know what to tell my ex,” she counters. “Got any bright fucking ideas for that one?”

Rio shrugs a shoulder. “Tell her the truth — that you met someone you’re interested in. You can mention my complicated past if necessary, but keeping it simple is probably better.”

“It’s obviously going to be necessary, Rio. And she’s obviously going to run off and tell the state of New Jersey the second she hears — do everything she can to make my home seem like an unsafe place for a child. For my fucking child.”

“With what evidence? That I was abused? That I was a victim?”

“Yes, Rio. With that evidence,” Agatha finds herself snapping. Her optimism could be sweet, but it could be irritating, too. “Do you think the justice system gave a fuck when I told them I was abused by my mother, hm? That I was a victim? Spoiler alert: They didn’t. They blamed me. They blamed me for fighting back — labeled me a difficult, problematic child — and they sent me back to live with her in that hellhole over. And over. And over.”

She feels her face grow hot, her eyes grow hot, her blood grow hot. She fucking hated talking about this. She fucking hated everything about this. “No, I’m not a fancy human rights lawyer like you, and yes, I have a criminal record and a shit ton of enemies, but we are not different in their minds. You need to wake up and realize they are going to paint you as a villain anyway. A crazy, lying, cheating bitch. That’s what they always paint us as.” She gets up from the bed to pace and rub at her chest, trying to make the air enter her fucking lungs, goddamn it.

“I know how to win cases like this, Agatha,” Rio evenly assures her. “With the mountain of evidence that’s stacked in my favor? I’m confident I can win it. Besides, they would have to talk to Nicky before doing any of that, and he adores you and seems to at least like me. That’s not nothing.”

“Are you listening? I just told you they don’t listen to kids and what they want,” Agatha retorts. “And let’s just say you’re right and they investigate first. You know what they do in the meantime? While they’re doing that? They rip him the fuck away from me.” She presses her palm harder to her sternum, unable to catch her breath. “Fuck.”

“They don’t take him away unless there are any red flags in your initial evaluation,” Rio calmly explains. “I know those signs. I can teach you how to play the role of a model reformed parent. Plus, I know a judge in Jersey who usually sides with kids — an old classmate of mine. I can pull some strings to get him to preside over your case, but Agatha, you have to breathe.”

She crouches over and puts her hands on her knees. That’s what the girls on the softball team used to do when they were winded. And the track team. And the soccer team. Agatha didn’t play, of course, but she liked to watch them while smoking weed under the bleachers. “I can’t…just fucking breathe…when it comes to my kid.”

“Yes, you can,” Rio encourages. “You have to.”

“I can’t,” she says through gritted teeth, glaring over at her. “The thought of losing him…makes me feel…like my lungs are going to fucking explode.”

“Then you won’t lose him.”

“You don’t…fucking…know that.” She wants to continue glaring, but the pain of not being able to get proper oxygen makes her look away, squeeze her eyes shut. God, this was humiliating.

“I may be a lawyer, but I can play fucking dirty,” Rio insists.

“I wish…you’d played dirtier yesterday,” Agatha admits. “We wouldn’t…be in this situation.” With a wince and a huff, she stands up straight and goes to the bathroom to splash some water on her face.

Rio follows close behind. “We would,” she argues. “The injuries he gave me, no matter what I did, would arouse suspicion. Believe me — it’s legally safer for both of us this way.” Rio leans on the counter. “They also don’t know we’re romantically involved. You can tell your ex and the court that the relationship didn’t start until after he died.”

She glances up in order to shoot her a look in the mirror. “I’m all for some light perjury, but there are witnesses. Jen and her assistant?”

“Neither of them wants to touch this. She kept going on and on about the NDA, remember?”

“Okay, but our texts, Rio? That would never hold up.”

“The texts happened over international lines,” Rio reasons. “If both of us close them on our phones, they can’t be easily traced.”

“You don’t think that’d look extremely fucking suspicious?”

“Not if I explain I had one to communicate with my dad and you say you had one for Nicky to stay in contact with your ex. Once we’re back in the States, there would be no reason to keep them open.”

Agatha splashes another handful of water onto her face — manages to take something resembling a deep breath. She turns to face her. “You’re sure?” she pushes. “You’re absolutely fucking positive?”

“Yes. I know how these things work.” Rio stares back at her, gaze just as serious. “But to pull this off, you have to play by the rules I give you.”

Agatha bristles, the idea of going by the book downright repulsive. “I don’t play by anyone’s rules, sweetheart.”

“Well, that’s going to have to change. Do you want to win this? Or do you want to lose your son?”

Agatha clenches her jaw, eyes darkening. “Don’t fucking do that, Rio,” she practically growls. “Threaten me with him.”

Rio remains impressively calm. “It’s not a threat — it’s a legitimate question, to which I know the answer is no. So swallow your fucking pride and let me tell you what to do.”

She squares her shoulders, lifts her chin to conjure some sense of strength, of bravado, of the upper hand. As much as people loved to wax poetic about collaborating and being a team, someone always had the upper hand. Agatha always made sure it was her.

Rio raises a prompting brow. “Do we have a deal? I need a promise you won’t go rogue.”

“Then I need a promise from you that you will play as dirty as it takes,” Agatha counters. “I’m not fucking kidding, Rio. If you need to kill again for my son — hell, if you need to die for him — I expect you to do it. He is the most important person to me, and he always will be.”

The smallest flicker of hurt flashes in Rio’s eyes, though she recovers quickly. “That won’t be necessary, but sure. It’s not like I have much to live for at the moment.”

Agatha runs a hand over her face. “Well, don’t say that — Jesus, Rio.”

“Well, it’s true. Now, listen up—”

“It’s not true." Agatha crosses her arms. "And I’m not listening to shit until you take it back.”

“That is not how this works.”

“It is, actually, how it’s going to work right now,” she insists. “Try me.”

Rio massages her temples. “Agatha, do you care more about being stubborn or making a plan to save everyone in this hotel room’s ass?”

She moves her hand in a so-so motion. “It’s pretty even, honestly.”

“Stop being a petulant brat for once in your life. You can worry about my self-esteem later.”

“No, I can’t. It’s important to me now.”

Rio huffs. “I’ll let you pester me after this conversation, okay?” she tries.

“I’d like to pester you before it.”

“Too bad.”

Agatha shrugs. “Then I guess I’m not going to listen to you.”

Rio’s nostrils flare. “Fine. I love myself, and I’m so happy to be alive,” she deadpans. “There. Now moving on—”

Agatha snorts. “You’re not winning any Oscars for that, sweetheart. Say it like you mean it.” 

“Agatha—”

She puts her hands over her ears. “Say it like you mean it, or I’m going to start humming really loudly to tune you out.”

“Agatha.” Rio sighs, her patience wearing thin. “I mean it. If you don’t stop acting like a chi—”

Agatha follows through on her promise, beginning to hum a song she and Nicky had made up on a walk one day. Rio throws her hands up in response, turning on her heel and walking out of the bathroom.

Agatha finds herself oddly stunned and…strangely hurt by the sudden abandonment. Many people had left Agatha over the years, but the fact it's Rio? It feels…different somehow. Cuts deeper.

Even more so because of the reason she’d gone. She had left not because Agatha hated her — because she had intentionally driven her away — but rather because Agatha cared about her. Cared that she felt like she was worth something in this world. Sure, she was being a petulant brat about it, but that was the reason she refused to move on from the conversation. It stings. And it pisses her off. So, like always, she leans into the latter.

Well, fine, she tells herself. If Rio wants to play that game, she has no problem playing it. She wins it every time, after all.

Agatha grabs two towels — the first to ball up and use as a pillow, the second to act as a blanket — before curling up on the bathroom floor.

God, this was bullshit.

Usually, people in the doghouse at least got to sleep on the couch.

Chapter End Notes

Bitches will literally sleep on the bathroom floor instead of talking about their feelings. (It's Agatha. She's bitches.)

Chapter 23: Day 5, Part 2

Chapter Summary

Somebody has to cave.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

It’s probably fucked up for Agatha to feel like she’s won when she hears Rio’s footsteps come back into the bathroom, but there is a jolt of smug victory that runs through her. After a few beats of heavy silence, Rio finally speaks — just one word. One syllable. “Why?” 

Still, the smugness doesn’t erase the bitterness. Agatha is exceptional at grudges. “Why what?” she asks. She’s on her side facing away from the door, and she makes no move to turn to face her.

“Why do you act like a child when I’m trying to help you? Why do you make it a point to remind me, in the cruelest way possible, that the most important person to you is your son? Why do you hum and lie on the bathroom floor instead of just talking to me? It’s confusing. I’m confused.”

“That makes two of us,” Agatha mumbles. 

Rio sighs. “You hurt my feelings, Agatha. You have to start communicating — actually communicating — because it makes no sense why you would dismiss my situation, my fears, and then turn around and insist that I’m worth something.”

Agatha picks at a loose string on the towel-blanket, considering. “How did I dismiss your situation and fears?”

“Hours ago, I was almost murdered. Hours ago, I endured one of the most exhausting, terrifying things in my life. I asked if I could stay with you, and you immediately made it all about you. Did it ever occur to you that I don’t want to go back to the apartment I lived in with him? That I can’t move back in with my dad because of the location of my job? That I only asked because I thought you cared? I like to think I’m a pretty logical person. It's not like I was expecting you to move mountains for me, but you left no room for me and my feelings whatsoever.”

Another jolt runs through her — one of guilt this time. The bitterness melts into something more shameful. “I didn’t…I didn’t mean to do that,” she says softly. “I—" She rolls to look at her now. “I would help you find a new apartment. Go into your old place and pack up all your shit. Obviously, I would help you figure something out. You were never going to have to do any of it alone.”

Rio shrugs a little before crossing her arms over her chest. “Well, you didn’t make that clear. All you did was turn on me about, ‘Well, what do I say to my ex?’ Then, when I tried to reassure you, you lashed out. It was uncalled for.”

Her tongue pokes the inside of her cheek, contemplating once more. That was rare for her — thinking before she spoke. “It might be hard to believe, but I’m not exactly great at accepting help. I don’t trust my ex. I don’t trust anyone, including…” Her eyes drop back down to the floor. “…including you,” she admits.

Agatha can sense the slightest bit of hurt simmering under Rio's surface, though her tone is impressively neutral when she asks, “Why not?” 

Agatha sighs. “This is going to sound like a break-up scene from an inane rom-com from 2003, but it’s not you — it’s me. I can count on half a hand the number of people I’ve truly trusted in my life. Each time, it’s backfired spectacularly."

Rio purses her lips. “I’m not going to stand here and promise I’ll never make a mistake. But what I will promise is that I would never do anything to intentionally harm you or your son.”

“Say that’s true. My life is…” Agatha shakes her head, picking at the pristine tile on the ground. “It’s extremely fucking complicated, Rio. It’s eggshells, or a house of cards, or whatever fragile analogy you want to use. I know you’re smart, and I know you’re capable, but trusting you to be able to handle all that? For you to…” She takes a deep breath. “…take the lead?”

“My life is eggshells, too,” Rio points out, going to carefully lower herself to the ground so she’s sitting across from Agatha. She manages it with only a small wince due to her slashed calf. “You don’t have to do it all at once,” she continues. “But I know how to work the system, and I know how to get things to pull in your favor.”

“The system has never once worked in my favor. No matter what way I pulled it.”

“Because you come at things with a brash, rough-and-tumble approach,” Rio notes. “Of course, it didn’t work. That never works in these situations.”

Agatha clenches her jaw. “I don’t want to be a doormat — all meek and polite.”

“Well, you have to,” Rio bluntly counters. “I need you to tone it down. No yelling, no accusations, no threats of violence. They have to see that you’re the ideal mother — that Wanda was wrong to ever question you in the first place. And if she sees you on your best behavior, surely, it’ll rile her up, which will, in turn, make her look like a bitter ex who’s upset that you moved on.”

Agatha squints. She’d never said her name. She never spoke that bitch’s name aloud. “You stalked me online.”

Rio rolls her eyes, immediately clocking the accusation. “No, I didn’t. I saw you change the contact from ‘Ginger Bitch’ so Nicky could call. The rest of it is inferences.”

“Oh.” Agatha’s mouth curves into a small, disappointed frown. “I was actually sort of flattered thinking about you sleuthing like some 15-year-old with a crush.”

“I did briefly look at your Facebook,” Rio admits. “But we can talk about that later.”

Agatha cocks a brow. “You sure you don’t want to talk about it now? Because I gotta say, I think I’d really love to talk about it now.”

“I’m serious,” Rio reiterates, unamused. “You have to play the ideal mother for the courts. Calm. Polite. Reformed.”

She rubs her hands over her face, already feeling a headache coming on. “Those are not words anybody has ever used to describe me.”

“Then pretend. I know what they’re going to ask. I can coach you on your answers, but you absolutely cannot tell anyone I’m doing that. You also can’t mention that I’m the one who helped find a judge who’d take the case. If they find the texts, we tell them it was flirting, fantasy — nothing real until he was gone. We end the international lines and won’t mention them unless they're brought up. They’re most likely going to ask Nicky if he feels safe with me and interrogate me if that conversation raises any red flags. We can paint your ex as vengeful — vindictive, even — to get sympathy.” Rio closes her eyes, massaging her temples. “I also need the names of both your lawyers. You should call around — chat with others in the area about the case so if she tries to switch counsel, they’ll have a conflict of interest.”

Agatha takes a deep breath and lets it out slow. “Hers is Matt Murdock; mine’s Jen Walters.”

Rio nods. “Matt is good. Jen is better, though. Call her first thing when we get back to tell her about this development.”

Agatha bites the inside of her cheek so hard she tastes blood. She usually loved danger, but when it came to Nicky? All she wanted to do was keep him safe and protected and with her.

Rio opens her eyes, lifting a brow. “Agatha,” she prompts. “Are you with me?”

“It doesn’t sound like I have much of a choice.”

“Not really,” she admits. “We can do it your way, and it can all fall apart, or we can do it my way and more than likely avoid any major disasters.”

“‘More than likely’ isn’t good enough — I need certainty.”

“Agatha,” Rio sighs. “There are no one hundred percent guarantees, but the way I see it, these are the odds: We do it your way, and there’s about a 70% chance you lose your son and I lose my job. We do it my way, and there’s about a 90% chance everything will go off without a hitch. But in order for that 90% to really be 90%, you have to listen to me. Play the game.”

Agatha tilts her head. “How did you come to those numbers?” she asks, genuinely curious.

Rio shrugs. “It’s not an exact math, but I know the statistics and the complications that come up in cases like these. I also know you.”

Agatha shifts a little at that declaration — at Rio's insistence that she knew her. Squirms a little at the fact that it might just be the truth. "Fascinating, the way your brain works.”

“Is it?” Rio shakes her head a little before Agatha can elaborate. “We can ponder that later.”

“You love to delay my gratification, don’t you, baby?” she purrs.

“It’s healthy for the brain.” Despite the seriousness of it all, the corner of Rio’s mouth quirks into a tiny smile. “You on board?”

“If you agree that, at the very least, this gives you something to live for.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “Yes. Fine.”

“That’s a Daytime Emmy performance at best.”

“Which is better than before."

“True,” Agatha relents. “You only got a nomination, though — you didn’t win.”

“And that’s a-okay.”

“Hope you don’t take that attitude into the courtroom.”

“Oh, trust me — I don’t.”

“Bedroom either.” Agatha wiggles her brows. “When you’re ready,” she clarifies.

“Mhm.” Rio rolls her eyes once more before getting off the floor. “Speaking of the bedroom, let's get back to it. Come on — up.”

“This floor’s not so bad, actually,” Agatha says, nestling into the towel under her head. “It’s heated and everything.”

“Please? I’m injured.”

“What does that have to do with me sleeping in the bathroom?”

Rio’s bottom lip juts into a tiny pout. “The bed is comfy, and I want you to cuddle me.”

Agatha narrows her eyes. “Name three things you have to live for first.”

She lets out an exasperated huff, running a hand over her face. “Agatha, I’m not doing this with you again.”

“Three things.”

She glares at her from between her fingers. “Adopting a hypothetical cat, keeping Nicky happy, and um…weed.”

Agatha thinks. “Marginally offended I didn’t make the list, but good enough.” She pushes herself up to stand.

“You were on there,” Rio confesses, suddenly self-conscious. “But I didn’t know if you’d want to be included.”

Agatha momentarily freezes, though she recovers quickly. That was…fair enough, all things considered. She clears her throat. “I want to be included,” she admits, oddly vulnerable.

“Really?”

A small, nearly imperceptible nod. “Yes,” she says quietly.

“Well, rest assured, you are,” Rio says, sticking out her hand. 

Agatha raises a brow. “You want to hold hands as we walk the eight steps back to bed?”

“Stop being a bitch,” she orders, grabbing her hand and yanking her back toward the bedroom.

“Bossy girl," Agatha accuses without any irritation behind her words, allowing herself to be led back. “Though I guess it makes sense considering you are the boss now, hm?” She sighs. “How the fuck did that happen?”

“I’m a lawyer,” Rio reasons.

“So? No lawyer has ever been the boss of me. Just ask Jen Walters.”

Rio pouts at her again. “Well, there’s a first time for everything.”

“Maybe so, but that little puppy dog face? Not really living up to the title.”

Rio shrugs. “I’m multi-faceted.”

“Ain’t that the truth,” Agatha agrees as she crawls back into bed.

“You mean that in a good way?” Rio checks as she slides under the covers, face inches from Agatha's.

She reaches out to absentmindedly tuck a stray hair, still the slightest bit damp, behind her ear. “Do I seem like someone who likes simple people, Rio?” she deadpans.

“I suppose not.”

“Exactly. You answered your own question.”

Rio nestles closer to her. “Cuddle me.”

“Ah, okay — so bossiness is back out now."

“Agatha,” she whines.

“Pouty again. You oscillate fast. It’s really quite impressive.”

“Agatha, I’m serious,” Rio says, voice growing more earnest — pleading almost — as she looks up at her. “Can you just hold me?”

“Yes," Agatha agrees as she pulls her close, relenting more easily than usual. "Yes, I’ll hold you."

She tries not to think about what that might mean.

Chapter End Notes
