Chapter 24: Day 5, Part 3

Chapter Summary

Dawn finally breaks. (Agatha tries to keep Rio from breaking with it.)

Chapter Notes

If you want a face claim for Rio's father, I personally picture Javier Bardem! In my mind, Rio's parents had her rather young. (If you've been imagining someone else, please drop who in the comments, because now I'm curious lol.)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Thankfully, the next time Rio stirs, the sun has finally peeked over the horizon. She briefly opens her eyes before squeezing them closed again, letting out a soft wince of pain.

“You awake?” Agatha asks.

“Do I have to be?” Rio groans, eyes still shut.

A beat. “Before you ask, it wasn’t a dream,” she says quietly. “I don’t know if that’s cause for anxiety or relief.”

Rio takes a deep breath. “Both,” she decides. “I just…don’t think I know how to keep going.”

“You just do, Rio. You take it hour by hour, minute by minute, second by second.”

“I know. Logically, I know.” She sighs. “I’m just still so exhausted,” she quietly confesses.

Agatha purses her lips. She’d been saying that a lot. Too much. “What’s it going to take to get you unexhausted, hm?”

“Downtime, comfort food…” Rio lists, hesitating before adding, “You.”

There’s time to go down on me — let me be your comfort food, Agatha is tempted to say, though that’d probably be entirely inappropriate at the moment. For some reason, she cares about that right now with Rio.

Instead, she clears her throat. “Well, I’m sure we can accomplish that. We’re still at a luxury resort, after all.” She reaches over her to grab the room service menu from the bedside table. “Peruse,” she orders.

Rio finally reopens her eyes, albeit with some reluctance, before scanning the menu with an equal amount of resistance. Agatha knows she didn’t necessarily mean she wanted comfort food right at this moment — knows she probably doesn’t want to eat at all — though thankfully, it’s a battle she doesn’t pick. “Waffle,” she chooses. “With fresh strawberries.”

“Good girl.” Agatha takes the menu from her, handing her the remote now. “Peruse,” she orders again. “While I call this in.”

Rio does as she’s told once more, scanning through a few channels as Agatha dials the number. “One strawberry waffle,” she tells them, the menu fanned out in front of her. “One blueberry waffle. One with chocolate chips. And put a rush on it — there’s a very special guest who requires food with her medication. I will not hesitate to sue the fuck out of you if she’s not able to do so in a timely manner because of your incompetence — something you’re lucky I’m not doing already considering everything that happened on your property yesterday,” she threatens, hanging up before they have a chance to respond.

Agatha raises a brow when she looks up at the TV screen, seeing that Rio has settled on some movie channel playing a horror film. “Fascinating choice of comfort content, doll.”

Rio shrugs. “I hate rom-coms, and reality TV grates on my nerves. Usually, the characters in these have even more fucked-up lives than I do.”

“That tracks.”

Rio looks over at her. “It does?”

“Mm,” she hums in the affirmative. “You told me that you like fucked-up shit because you’d been through fucked-up shit.”

“Right.” Rio nods, shifting to curl up once more.

“Nuh-uh,” Agatha chastises. “None of that. Food’ll be here soon.”

“I can lie down until they get here,” she insists.

But Agatha doesn’t want her to fall back asleep. It’s selfish considering she could surely use some more rest. It’s even easier, frankly, not having her awake to talk about things.

Still, she doesn’t want her to fall back asleep because…well, maybe because she doesn’t want to be awake on her own. The fiercely independent Agatha afraid of being alone. Hell must be frozen the fuck over. 

“Why do you hate rom-coms?” Agatha asks, attempting to subtly bait her into a conversation to keep her from drifting off.

“I usually find them unrealistic. Cheesy. Too straight 90% of the time and too horny in the most boring ways.”

“As opposed to horny in an interesting way — like me.”

“I suppose so.”

Agatha scoffs. “Well, that’s not particularly reassuring. A little more enthusiasm for my sex drive would be appreciated.”

The corner of Rio’s mouth curves into a grin as she peers over at her. “It’s a very nice sex drive,” she admits.

Agatha smirks, relieved that she’d gotten Rio to crack a smile. “Well, it’s ready and waiting for you whenever you’d like to take it out of the garage again."

“Soon,” Rio promises. “When my neck isn’t bruised to hell and breathing is easier.”

“I can be gentle with you, too, you know,” she says — informative but not pressuring. “I know you like me rough, but I don’t always have to be that way.”

“I know, and I’ll probably need that for a while.” Rio’s face flushes with embarrassment. “It’s so stupid that I need that.”

“Not wanting to die while I’m fucking you isn’t stupid.” A beat. “I mean, it admittedly would be a pretty fucking baller way to go out, but still — nothing dumb about self-preservation.”

“Logically, I know that, too. But it still feels…weak.”

Agatha nods, chewing on the inside of her cheek. She could understand that. “What makes you feel strong?”

“My job,” she replies immediately.

Predictable but not super helpful at the moment. “What else?”

Rio considers for a few seconds. “I don’t know,” she finally admits.

“Come on — that enormous brain is stuffed full of legal jargon and shark facts. Surely, it has more than one answer to that, too.”

“Sometimes…weightlifting, I guess?” Rio says. “But that’s a no-go right now in my condition.”

“What about when you were a child, then? Before gyms and cross-examinations?”

Another beat of silence. “I’m not really sure.”

Agatha sighs and purses her lips. “I’m trying to help you here, Rio.”

“I know. I know.” Rio puts a hand on her forehead, massaging her temples. “I’ve just spent the majority of my life feeling sort of…aimless. Hollow.”

If they couldn’t look to the past, perhaps the answer lay in the future. “Well…is there anything you’ve always wanted to do that might help?”

Rio bites her lip, worried, maybe, that Agatha might think it’s stupid. “I’ve always wanted to swim with sharks,” she confesses.

Also predictable. But also more helpful. Agatha tilts her head. “We could do that.”

“We could?”

She shrugs. “Why not? Nicky would lose his shit, combining two of his favorite things — sharks and swimming.”

Rio bites her lip as if she doesn’t know how to react — how to act — when she gets something she wants. “I probably can’t do it today with the injuries. Maybe tomorrow, if the doctors think it would be okay.” 

“Tomorrow, then.” Agatha nods. “Pending doctoral approval.” 

“Maybe we could go to the aquarium today,” Rio suggests. “Get Nicky extra excited about some of the creatures he’s going to see while he’s in the water tomorrow.”

“All right,” Agatha agrees. “But before you do anything, you need to call your father back.”

Rio groans, covering her face with her hands. “Do I have to?” she whines.

“Yes, Rio — you do. That poor man is in hell. If it were Nicky in your position, I’d have paddled a canoe across the fucking Atlantic last night.”

“What do I tell him you are? Friend? Girlfriend?”

“Just…” She shakes her head, uncharacteristically flustered. “Tell him that I’m Agatha and that I bullied you in the lobby.”

Rio uncovers her eyes to give her a look. “That’s not going to fly. He’s an inquisitive man. Would you prefer I tell him the details?”

“'The details' meaning that I’m drop-dead gorgeous and great in bed?”

“You’re deflecting.”

Agatha sighs. “Well, what details are you referring to?”

“That what we have is deep and real and…complicated…and messy. That I have feelings for you, and you have them for me, but that I’m scared, and you’re scared. That I trust you but can’t name exactly who you are to me.”

She lifts her chin, squares her shoulders. “Well, don’t tell him I’m scared. I wouldn’t want you to lie to the guy.”

“You are,” Rio insists. “Despite your posturing, despite your denial, you’re fucking terrified. Do you want me to tell him that, or do you want me to say something else?”

She huffs, contemplating. “Friends,” she decides. “Just say we’re friends. We’re going with the slow-burn story, aren’t we? Pretending we didn’t fuck on night two?”

“Okay, yeah.” Rio nods, running a hand over her face. “That’s a good idea.”

“You know me — I’m full of them.”

“Mhm.”

Agatha raises a brow. “That little ‘mhm’ makes me think you believe I’m full of something else.”

“Shit.”

She rolls her eyes. “Yes, that was what I was implying.” 

“I know.”

“So you just wanted to say it then,” she deadpans. “That I’m full of shit.

“Mhm,” Rio hums again. Infuriating little brat.

Agatha narrows her eyes. “Someone woke up on the wrong side of the California King.”

“No, I didn’t.”

“No?” Her brow lifts again. “Because I’m sensing a bit of a ‘tude.”

“Well, I’m really struggling with the whole ‘wanting to be alive’ thing, so can you blame me?” Rio mumbles, deciding this is the moment she wants to busy herself with grabbing her phone and scrolling to her father’s contact.

Agatha blinks as her head jerks back a little, surprised at the bluntness — her teasing tone promptly dropped. “Don’t even think about it, Rio,” she says firmly.

Rio must sense this — that it was too far, too dark, too honest. She peers up from her phone, nervously attempting to backtrack. “I don’t actually want to. Or…you know, however they phrase it — I have no plans, no method. I just…I wish it a little bit is all.”

“I don’t care,” she says — voice serious as it’s ever been. “You’re not allowed. I’m not fucking kidding. I don’t want you even entertaining the smallest thought, do you understand?” Rio swallows hard, giving her a little nod. It’s not good enough. It’s not good enough at all. “Tell me that you understand,” Agatha demands. “Out loud.”

“I understand,” she mumbles, dropping her gaze back to the phone in her hand.

“No.” Agatha puts a hand under her chin, her touch gentle but insistent, and immediately tilts it back up so she’s forced to look her in the eyes. “Try again. Not even Daytime Emmy nomination worthy.”

“I get it.”

“Again. You know I can sit here all day.”

“Agatha,” she pleads.

“Rio,” she says sternly. “I’m not playing around this time. This isn’t a game. I will not lose you.”

“I’m not going to do anything,” she insists, her voice quiet but seemingly sincere. “I can’t exactly control the thought aspect of it all — they’re called ‘intrusive’ for a reason — but I don’t plan to act on them.”

Agatha stares at her for a long moment before sucking her teeth and dropping Rio’s chin. “Fine,” she relents. “You better not. Nicky would never recover.” Neither would she, for that matter, but it was easier to use her son as a shield. And more effective to weaponize a child’s feelings. She nods down at the phone in Rio’s hand. “Call your father.”

“Will you stay here?”

“I have to check on Nicky and get our food. Plus, I’m sure he wants to chat with you alone.” Rio gives her a look that makes it clear she’s not too keen on this idea, and Agatha sighs. “Sweetheart, trust me — I get this is a lot, but he’s going to want to talk to you by yourself. You don’t want him to resent me for playing guard dog before we even tell him our…situation, do you?”

Rio says nothing, but she does press the contact and hold the phone to her ear, which Agatha takes as reluctant permission to leave the room.

He answers on the first ring, as if he’d been waiting for her to call back since the second they’d hung up. Maybe he had. “Mija?”

Rio takes a deep breath. “Hey.”

“What— Did— How are you doing?” he settles on.

“I’m tired,” she admits, unsure how much to elaborate. Unsure how honest to really be. It hadn’t worked so great with Agatha. Had clearly concerned her quite a lot. “Really tired. But I did manage some sleep.”

“That’s good. You need it.”

“Did you rest?” she counters.

A beat. “Yes. Yes, I managed to get a bit.”

Rio sighs. Her father is not a particularly good liar. “No, you didn’t. I promise I’m okay, but you have to sleep after we get off the phone.”

His turn to sigh. “I will try my best. I promise you that.”

“Good. Like you said, rest is important.”

“But my last few days haven’t been as eventful as yours, mija,” he gently points out.

“I know,” she says, some almost teenagery irritation creeping into her tone as if he’s nagging her to clean her room or do her homework. “And I’m taking it easy — I promise.”

“Where? Not at that resort still I hope?”

“Yes, at the resort,” she slowly admits. “I still have time off from work, and it’s not like everyone here is plotting my demise.”

Santos clicks his tongue in disapproval. “You should be home, mija. So I can look after you. Take care of you.”

“I’m okay. I promise,” she insists again. “I’m trying to salvage the trip as much as I can so all my PTO days aren’t wasted.”

“Rio.” He breathes out a humorless laugh. “This is not healthy. Continuing to go on vacation after something like this? You need to come back. You need to heal.”

“Which I’m working on doing here. I deserve at least part of this trip not to be marred with trauma.”

“I’m not saying you don’t, but don’t you think this particular trip has been marred with enough trauma already?”

“I have two more days to make it a little better,” she stubbornly reasons. “Which I will be doing.”

“Why don’t you want to come home?” he asks, clearly trying hard to keep the hurt from his voice. “You didn’t tell me, and now you don’t want to see me — I…did I do something wrong? Am I doing something wrong? Please, just tell me if I am so I can fix it. I only want to be there for you. I only want you to be okay.”

Rio’s heart can’t help but ache at that. “You didn’t do anything,” she gently reassures him. “I promise. I didn’t tell you because I didn’t want to seem weak. I didn’t want to admit that something was wrong. I didn’t want to admit that…that something was wrong with me.”

“Mi niña, you don’t have a weak bone in your body,” Santos whispers, though his voice is emphatic. “You’re perfect. You’ve always been just perfect.”

Rio rolls her eyes. They burn with a few tears. “You’re biased because you’re my dad.”

“No, I’m sure because I’m your dad. Because I know you better than anyone in this world. You are much too hard on yourself. You always have been. You…you are more than I ever could have hoped for, Rio. More than I ever dreamed. And the fact he couldn’t see that — how special you were, how you deserved to be treated…” His voice cracks a bit, and he stops before it can do so again.

Rio sucks in a sharp breath. “I hate him. I really do. He tried to get me to quit my job. He controlled who I saw and who I was friends with, what I wore, what I talked about. I married him because it felt like I had to.”

“But why did you feel you had to? You could have lived with me as long as you wanted. You could have married the garbage man. Neither would have made me think less of you.”

Rio bites the inside of her cheek. This is so strange, telling him all these things she’s kept bottled up for so long. All these parts of herself she’d kept secret and hidden. “I’m gay,” she admits, ripping another band-aid before she can lose her nerve. “Like…like a lesbian. I…couldn’t accept that, and I thought, if I married a man, I could pretend.”

It takes her father a moment to process — to wrap his head around it. “That’s okay, mija,” he says after a beat. “That’s perfectly all right. I love you no matter what. Did you think that I wouldn’t?”

“No,” she says quickly. Was that entirely true? “Yes?” she tries, though that doesn’t feel completely right either. “I don’t know,” she admits. “I was just scared.”

“I understand,” he slowly admits. “The world can be unkind.”

“Mm,” Rio hums in agreement. “Very.”

There’s a small beat before Santos takes a deep breath. “So this Agatha woman…”

Rio picks at the comforter, some anxiety creeping up at the prospect of this interrogation. “What about her?” she asks as casually as possible.

“She is kind? She treats you well?"

“She is,” Rio confirms. It was true — she was…in her own strange way. “And she does.”

“You met her there?"

“I did.”

“Where is she from? What does she do for a living?”

“She’s from New Jersey. Mostly stays at home with her six-year-old son.” Rio is not keen on telling him that her main source of income seemed to be fraud and theft, so she grasps at the offhand comment she made about a brief stint at a hair salon. “Occasionally temps, mostly as a receptionist.”

Santos seems to buy it, ignoring the career portion of the answer entirely to muse, “I remember you at six.”

“Yeah, Nicky’s a sweet kid,” Rio replies. She hopes maybe that will be the end of this particular discussion, but alas.

“This is all very fast, Rio. You only met her days ago…”

“So? We became fast friends. We have a lot in common.”

“Rio,” Santos flatly responds, almost insulted. “Come on. I’m your father — and I was not born yesterday.”

“What are you talking about?” Rio blushes, wrapping a loose string from the bedsheets around her finger. “I’m telling the truth.”

“Half-truth,” Santos corrects. “You are not just friends. You don’t talk about her like a friend.” A beat. “You didn’t even use to talk about him like that,” he says softly. Rio can practically read his thoughts: I should’ve known. How could I not have known?

“I can’t…talk about the details of it all right now,” Rio replies, getting flustered for a multitude of reasons. “It’s not you. It has to do with something on her end — something with her ex and the custody battle of it all.”

“I understand,” he says. Rio’s sure he does. Her mother…well, she was a piece of work. “You’re positive she has good intentions?” he checks. “You have money, Rio, and you’re in a vulnerable position. This isn’t about me not trusting you — I want to be clear — it’s about me not trusting everyone else.”

“I’m positive,” she asserts. “Truthfully, she can be kind of…” Rio searches for the nicest, cleanest word. “...brash,” she settles on. “But the way she’s helped me? I know she wouldn’t just pretend to care.”

This is apparently a decent justification for Santos. “All right,” he agrees — albeit a little reluctantly. “If that changes, you know you are not stuck with her, yes? That you can always leave any situation at any time and come to me. Papa will take care of you.”

Rio softens once more. “I know. She’s…she’s not like him, though.”

“She better not be,” he mumbles, protectiveness flaring up once more. “When are you coming home?"

“First, I’m going back to Brooklyn to get some more of my stuff — figure out my situation,” she says, dread spreading through every vein like spilled ink — a dark, consuming thing.

“On the same flight you had booked? Two days from now?”

“Yes,” she says slowly. “Why?”

“I’ll pick you up at the airport.”

“You don’t have to do th—”

“I want to. I’m going to,” he asserts.

Rio sighs. She loves him so much. He loves her so much. And that’s why facing him was going to be…a lot. “What about work?”

“You’re not the only one with vacation days.”

Not very many. And requesting it with this short of notice? Well, his bosses weren’t going to be happy. “Dad, are you sure?”

“I’m positive.”

He’s already made up his mind, Rio knows. There was no use arguing with him, so she doesn’t. “I’ll be okay,” she reassures him once again instead.

“But it’s okay if you’re not right now, mjia. You know that, yes?”

She picks at the thread once more. “I…I guess so.” She doesn’t even believe herself as the words leave her mouth.

“I wish you’d believe me.” His voice is so…sad. She hates to disappoint him, even when it comes to something like this. Hates to worry him.

“You know I’m bad at this sort of thing.”

“But I also know you can do whatever you set your mind to.”

“My mind is the enemy here.”

“Then let your heart be the hero.”

Rio can’t help but scoff. “That’s super cheesy.”

Santos remains completely unfazed. “I’m your father — that’s my prerogative.”

“Is it?”

“Oh, yes,” he replies, voice solemn. “It’s in the handbook and everything. Ask your Agatha if you don’t believe me — I'm sure it’s in the mother one, too.”

A ghost of a laugh passes her lips despite herself. “You’re so sure about that.”

“I am. I am very sure.”

There’s a beat of silence, which gives the seed of guilt in Rio’s chest time to blossom into a prickly, nagging thing. “How have you been, Dad?” she asks, voice soft. “Really? Are you okay? I know this is…a lot for you, too.”

“Don’t worry about your old man, Rio.”

“I always will,” she insists. It’s the truth — they had always only had each other.

“Worry about taking care of yourself right now. That’s the best thing you can do for me.”

“But you didn’t answer,” Rio presses. “Are you doing all right?”

“I’m fine. It’s the same old, same old here.”

It’s not the full truth, but what could Rio do even if he was honest? There was no taking back what had happened — what she had divulged. “I love you,” she tells him.

“I love you, Rio. You be safe, and you call me if you need anything. Call me even if you don’t need anything.”

“I do call you, Dad.”

“But can always call me more,” he says — his primary paternal grumble. “But I know you are very busy working that important job of yours.”

Rio fiddles with the thread again, her mind drifting to Agatha’s comment in the ambulance. Maybe a little item for her to fidget with wouldn’t be the worst investment in the world. There were a lot of things Thanos didn’t allow that might not be the worst idea. “I was thinking I might get a cat,” she says. “Might help with that work-life balance thing.”

“That could be good for you,” he agrees.

“There are plenty in shelters that need loving homes,” she reasons, as if trying to justify it to herself.

“Well, I’d be happy to go with you while I’m visiting. If you’re ready.”

“Maybe. If not, you’ll at least get pictures,” she vows.

“Send me pictures of your vacation, too, yes?” he requests. “And this Agatha woman.”

“Vacation, yes. Agatha, no — unless she agrees.”

“She’s basically a stranger in a strange country. Please, Rio. For my sanity.”

“Not without her consent.”

He sighs. She hears a light sweeping sound as if he’s rubbing his temples. “Then at least give me her last name.”

Rio contemplates. She wants to ease his nerves, and revealing her last name doesn’t feel like a total violation of her trust. “Harkness.”

“And she’s from where?”

“I told you, New Jersey.”

“More specifically. I’m sure she’s not the only Agatha Harkness in the state.”

Rio groans, decidedly not comforted by where this line of questioning is going. She’d given him an inch hoping that would be enough, but he’s clearly interested in taking a whole mile. “Don’t stalk her.”

“I’m not going to stalk her, Rio,” he defends. “I just want basic information in case something — in case something else — happens. It’s just a safety precaution. If you want your old man to rest…”

He’s playing dirty, employing that light, paternal emotional manipulation, but Rio holds firm. “She hasn’t agreed to any of this. Pictures or information...”

“And if she doesn’t, that seems rather suspicious to me.”

“Let me remind you, she has a complicated thing going on with her ex. She’s trying to figure out what to say and what all of this means for her. She deserves that privacy.”

“Privacy? Sure. Anonymity? Concerning. A city and a photo are both extremely reasonable asks, Rio.”

“They’re going to freak her out,” Rio argues. “Listen, I know you mean well, and I love you so much, but you have to back off this and trust me on her.” She feels her throat get unexpectedly thick, eyes burning with the first sign of tears. She just needs him to believe her. She just needs to be believed. “Please, Dad,” she whispers out a plead.

There’s a long, long beat of silence. “Okay,” he finally finds himself saying — obviously against his better judgment. “Okay. Just be careful. I’ll see you in a couple of days.”

Rio lets out a breath of relief. “I’ll see you then.”

“I love you, Rio. Te veo.”

“Te veo, Papa.”

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: Breakfast. The most important (and triggering) meal of the day.

Chapter 25: Day 5, Part 4

Chapter Summary

Breakfast. The most important (and triggering) meal of the day.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha and Nicky are at the suite’s small breakfast nook cutting into their waffles — blueberry for the former, chocolate chip for the latter — when Rio limps in, wincing every few seconds. The two look up, almost creepily synchronized, when they register her presence.

“Good morning, Ms. Rio,” Nicky politely greets. Agatha is grateful that he seems to have heeded her warning to be calm and quiet around her.

“Morning,” she whispers, her forced smile not particularly convincing.

Nicky frowns, looking at Agatha in concern. Maybe it’s a little fucked up and gaslighty, but she decides the best course of action is to pretend everything is normal despite the fact that approximately zero percent of it is. “How’d it go?” she asks.

“Mm.” Rio shrugs a little as she grabs some orange juice. “Fine.”

“How did what go?” Nicky asks.

“She talked to her dad on the phone,” Agatha says. 

“Oh.” He pauses for a second, racking his brain. “He's nice, isn't he?"

“He is.” Rio nods. “He’s a very good dad.”

“Was he sad that you got an ouchie?”

“Yes, very worried.”

His frown deepens, looking up at her neck before craning his head down to peer at her leg. He doesn’t notice the way Rio shuffles, no doubt feeling exposed. An injured bug under a microscope. “I’m worried, too.” 

“I’ll be okay.” Rio reaches down to give his hair a reassuring ruffle before taking a seat in the chair next to him. “I’ve survived this long.”

“You’re not old, though,” Nicky argues. “Not as old as Mama, at least.” 

“Hey.” Agatha thumps his shoulder. “Watch it, kid.”

“I’m only a little younger than your mom,” Rio explains. “Couple years.”

That’s generous, Agatha thinks. She had roughly a decade on her.

Nicky, on the other hand, is about as ungenerous as they come. “One of them,” he corrects. “My other mom is younger than you, I think.” 

Agatha runs a hand over her face, desperate to change the subject from her age and bitch ass ex. “Rio, why don’t you tell Nicky what we were planning to do today, hm?” she encourages.

“There’s an aquarium nearby. You want to go?” 

Nicky gasps, bouncing in his chair. “Yes! Can Ms. Lilia come?” 

“Can—” Agatha scowls. “What? Why do you want her there?” 

“Because.” He shrugs. “She’s nice, and she liked it when I told her about the fish on TV.”

Agatha’s hoping Rio might intervene, say she doesn’t want extra company, but she doesn’t. She just sits there. Picking at her food. Like a traitor.

“Plus, you’re lonely—“ Nicky accuses. 

“I am not,” Agatha defends. 

“—and she’s lonely, and it’s nice to invite people to play or eat lunch when they’re all by themselves.”

Rio gives Nicky a little thumbs up at the kindness. Yup. Fucking traitor.

She gets out her phone, changing the contact from HIPPIE BITCH to LILIA before handing it to Nicky. “Call and invite her if that’s important to you.”

“Who is this person again?” Rio asks. 

“Your nosy neighbor,” Agatha deadpans with a grumble. 

“Oh? How did she get involved?”

Agatha gives her a funny look, opening her mouth to respond before closing it again and pursing her lips. She glances over at Nicky, who seems to be oblivious to the exchange — too busy navigating the screen. “Nicky, go call her in your bedroom, okay?” 

For once, he mercifully doesn’t argue or interrogate, hopping down from his chair and putting the phone to his ear as he patters into his room. “Hi, Ms. Lilia. Yes, I slept — just like you said I should because rest is important.”

“She babysat him yesterday when I was with you at the hospital,” Agatha tells Rio, tone hushed even with Nicky in another room. “She was here when we got back. Do you…not remember?”

Rio blinks before tapping her hand to her head. “Wait, yes. Of course. Sorry. All of yesterday is just a huge blur.”

Agatha looks at her intently, eyes narrowing. “Yeah? You’re sure? It’s not — I don’t know — amnesia or something?”

“I mean, if it is, it’s the dissociative type. Neurologically, I checked out.”

She crosses her arms. “Is that supposed to make me feel better?”

Rio shrugs. “Dissociative amnesia is a lot less problematic than other types.”

She chews on the inside of her cheek. “Maybe we should have them do more scans. Those doctors yesterday were fucking idiots — they hardly did any scans.”

“I’m okay,” Rio promises, laying a hand on her arm. “Aside from my neck being bruised and the giant gash on my leg, I’m physically fine. I’ve dissociated most of my marriage — this is normal for me.”

“But it’s not normal in general. It shouldn’t be fucking normal.”

“Well…” Rio replies. “I don’t know what to tell you.”

Agatha tastes a little blood in her mouth, so she reluctantly removes her teeth from her cheek. “How are we going to change that, hm?”

“For starters, I’ll probably find a new therapist. One he didn’t pick.”

“He picked your—” Agatha stops herself. “Never mind. Never mind. Of course he did. More supervillain shit.”

“Yeah,” Rio says, much too casual for Agatha’s likening. “I mean, that’s his gig. Or was.”

“Well aware.” She peers into Nicky’s bedroom. He still seems to be talking Lilia’s ear off, which means now’s as good a time as any to broach another subject they didn’t want discussed around prying ears. “So, how’d the convo with dad actually go, hm?”

“It went okay. It was…a lot. He was obsessive about figuring out who you are.”

“And you told him what exactly?”

“Your name. State. He begged for a picture and city, and I said I wouldn’t without your consent.”

Agatha nods slowly. “How annoying. And flattering. I can’t really say I blame him.” She considers for a moment before tossing her hair over her shoulder. “Send him a picture of me if you’d like. Just make sure I look good in it.”

“You always look good.”

“True,” she agrees. “Every side is my good side.”

“I think so.”

“Just think?” Agatha scoffs. “Wow. Okay.”

“Oh, shut up, Agatha. I’m agreeing with you.”

She raises her chin. “Agree with me with more confidence.”

“That was my version of confidence.”

“Well, I’m gonna need you to work on that because it’s a little pathetic.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “Okay, sure. Whatever.”

“No need for the ‘tude.”

Rio gives her a tight smile. “It’s funny how you shorten words like that. Very suburban mom of you.”

Agatha puts a hand to her chest. “That’s quite literally the meanest thing you’ve ever said to me.”

“Is it?”

“Jesus, yes. Suburban mom? Just fucking kill me.” It’s probably not the right thing to say in the moment, all things considered, but Agatha isn’t used to filtering herself for sensitivity’s sake.

“Mm, well, it’s true. And lucky for you, it’s hot.”

Agatha raises a brow. “It is? Do say more. I want the deets, baby.” She internally curses at herself. 

Rio gives her a look. “You just proved my p—”

“Yeah, yeah — I realized I fucked up as soon as it left my mouth.” Agatha waves her off. “Doesn’t mean I don’t still want deets.”

“Well, that’s too bad. You can wait.”

“Until when?”

“Wait and see.”

Agatha scoffs. “You’re such a tease.”

“So are you,” Rio counters.

“Yes, but unlike me, you’re not going to do anything about it.” Agatha drags her pointer down Rio’s chest — gentle and testing. They hadn’t been…intimate like that since the whole shitshow went down.

“Maybe I will,” Rio replies. “Who knows?” 

It’s noncommittal, but it’s not a total shutdown of the idea, which is deeply intriguing to Agatha. “Oh?” Her brow arches higher. “Well, I’d love to see you try.”

“Later,” she says. “Maybe.” Her gaze lands back down at the table, and she lets out a groan.

“What’s the moaning for?” Agatha asks. “The unsexy kind.” It wasn’t unsexy, really — nothing Rio does ever is — but still.

Rio gestures to the nearly untouched waffle on her plate.

“Oh. Yeah. You are going to have to take care of that. I’m not going to have you swept away by the wind.”

“Missing one meal would not turn me into a plastic bag,” Rio argues. 

Agatha blinks. “Did you…did you just reference Katy fucking Perry at me?”

Rio promptly ignores her, staring back at the daunting plate once more. “I think I’m just going to eat a big lunch,” she decides.

“Okay,” Agatha agrees. Rio seems to relax before she says, “After you eat breakfast.”

“Agatha, why are you so hellbent on me eating this one meal?” she whines.

“Because it’s not one meal — it’s a pattern. And because you clearly have food issues that stem from his psychotic vendetta against women enjoying chicken and cheese.”

Rio sucks on her cheek before stuffing a rather large bite of waffle into her mouth — maybe so she doesn’t have to admit Agatha is right.

“Well, you don’t have to scarf it,” Agatha says. “I don’t want you to choke.” A beat. She peers into Nicky’s bedroom — sees him still obliviously chattering away on the phone. “I want to be the only one to make you do that,” she declares, voice low. 

Rio grimaces a little. “Maybe not now.”

“Well, no. Definitely not now,” she agrees. Rio’s neck was still bruised to shit, a dark ring around her throat.

“I’m not sure if…ever?” Rio admits after a second, voice so nervous it comes out like a question. “I liked it before, but I really thought I was going to die yesterday,” she whispers.

“That’s all right,” she easily assures her. “Plenty of other places I can squeeze — plenty of other things we can do instead. I don’t mind getting creative.”

Shock flickers across her face for a moment before she’s aware enough to try and hide it, looking back down at her plate. “Thanks.”

“It’s quite literally the barest minimum.”

“I suppose.”

“It is, Rio,” she insists. “You’re allowed to not want your airways blocked, for fuck’s sake."

She doesn’t look up. “He didn’t…care about that. What I wanted. It still takes me by surprise that you do.”

“Well…get used to it,” she says awkwardly.

“It’s just new. I’m sorry.”

“Rio, please.” Agatha runs a hand over her face. “You know how I feel about the unnecessary apologies.”

Rio hunches a little, sinking down into her seat as if to make herself smaller. “It felt necessary.”

“Well, it wasn’t. Okay? It isn’t.”

Rio continues to stare down at the table, which makes Agatha feel like shit. And confused as to how they’d gotten here. Again. How did she always manage to fuck things up to such an extreme degree?

“I don’t— I’m just— I’m not trying to scold you,” Agatha clarifies. “I’m trying to be…reassuring.”

“Which is appreciated, but your tone was…a little harsh.”

“It wasn’t harsh — it was…serious. Certain. Sure. Whatever else you’d find in the fucking thesaurus.”

Rio finally looks up at her. “Well, it came off harsh. I’m not mad at you, but I need you to understand that your tone is not coming off the way you think it is right now.”

She bristles, clenching her jaw. Rio might not be mad at Agatha, but suddenly, Agatha found herself a little angry with her. “Don’t police my tone,” she snaps. “My whole life, people have been policing my tone. God forbid anyone give me the benefit of the fucking doubt for once.”

“Well, god forbid I want some gentleness the day after someone tried to take my life,” Rio counters with a mumble. 

Agatha sucks on the inside of her cheek. Maybe mad. Perhaps hurt. Likely a bit of both. “I’m trying my best. And I’m well aware that’s never enough for anyone ever, but that’s the truth.”

Rio softens a little. “I know you’re trying. All I was saying was that your impact was not matching your intention. That’s okay — that happens sometimes — but the only way to get better at it is to get feedback.”

Agatha is very used to criticism — nobody ever had a problem telling her exactly everything that was wrong with her — but it was rarely for constructive reasons and never in a kind way. “Okay. Noted. Let’s just…move on.”

“No.” Rio tilts her head. “You’re upset. I know this probably isn’t your favorite thing to hear, but I’m telling you because I care about you and want you to get better at communication.”

“Got it. Thanks.” In a supremely immature move she knows will effectively end the conversation, she looks into Nicky’s bedroom. “Nicky, enough yapping — breakfast’s getting cold!”

Rio gives Agatha a look that sits somewhere between chastisement and disbelief. “Not everyone who corrects you wants to hurt you,” she says, tone something worse than irritated. It’s flat. Disappointed. Resigned. “I’ll be in the bedroom,” she evenly declares, walking into the master and shutting the door behind her.

Agatha absolutely loved to run away from problems and give people the silent treatment, but she very much doesn’t love being on the receiving end of it. “God fucking damn it,” she mutters, shoving her plate away. Suddenly, she's not hungry anymore. 

“What’s wrong, Mama?” Nicky asks as he comes back into the kitchen, hung-up cell phone in hand. 

“Nothing. It’s fine. Everything’s fine. Is Lilia coming on the excursion?”

“She said she would if you paid for her ticket.” 

Agatha rolls her eyes. “I’m pretty sure seniors get free admission, so sure. I’ll let her think that.” 

Nicky frowns. “Where’s Ms. Rio?” She nods toward her bedroom, picking at the napkin. “Are you in a fight?” 

Agatha narrows her eyes. “Why would you assume that?” 

“Because you look like you do when you and Mommy fight.” 

“We’re having a…disagreement,” she says as diplomatically as possible. 

Nicky looks at Rio’s plate. “She didn’t finish eating. She has to finish eating, or else she can’t go to the aquarium,” he states. Agatha doesn’t have the heart to tell him that rule applied only to him, not extending to her sort-of girlfriend she was sort-of mad at. “I’m gonna take it to her,” he decides, picking it up. 

“Nicky, don’t—”

“I’ll finish mine after,” he promises.

Agatha clenches her jaw, but she can’t bring herself to stop him. She was too prideful to face Rio right now. Too prideful and too…scared. That she might let her guard down and say something she’ll regret. Not something cruel but something true — about the kind of person she is. About the kind of things she’s done. About the kind of things she’s feeling.

The kind of things she’s feeling for Rio.

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: Nicky to the rescue.

Note about our summer schedule: Our lives have gotten a bit hectic lately, which means our writing has been a bit slower going, and our backlog of chapters is starting to get low. We love updating every week, but we don’t want to find ourselves in a situation where we’re scrambling and writing something we’re not proud of or leaving you all without updates for long stretches of time. Our goal is to post as consistently as possible, which is why, for July through September, we’ll be switching from weekly updates to updating every other week. (We’ll post a chapter on July 2nd, then July 16th, July 30th, etc.) Depending on how much progress we make this summer, we may go back to weekly posts in October, or we may have to extend this for a bit longer. I’ll make sure to keep you updated!

Thank you all so, so much for your support. The reception of this story has been extremely exciting and, frankly, quite moving. We’re both so grateful for everyone who has taken the time to read and comment. We sincerely apologize that updates will be a little slower for a while (trust me — we love sharing this with you all so much that it bums us out, too), but we hope you understand! Thank you in advance for your patience with us!

Chapter 26: Day 5, Part 5

Chapter Summary

Nicky to the rescue.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio doesn’t register the door opening. She’s lying down and absentmindedly scrolling on her phone, retaining approximately nothing until she hears a little voice say, “Ms. Rio?”

She glances up. “Hey, bud.”

“I brought you the rest of your waffles,” Nicky says, holding out the plate. “I think you have to take more bites if you want to come see the fishes with me.”

“Thank you,” she says, forcing herself to sit up and take it from him. “That was very kind.”

He pushes himself up onto the bed, sitting cross-legged facing her. “My mom says that Mama is a hothead. And a lot of people think that she’s mean because sometimes, she uses her outside voice at them, even when she’s inside.”

Rio tilts her head. God, kids were observant. It was a little frightening, really. She doesn’t let her face betray her as she asks, “What do you think?”

“Mm…” He considers for a moment — deep in concentration, evident by his pinched brows. “I think…I think maybe she just forgets that she doesn’t have to use her outside voice — like sometimes how I forget to be calm around you when you’re feeling icky. Mama spent a lot of time outside when she was a kid like me.”

Rio shudders to think about just how true — how literal — that proclamation might be. Had Agatha’s mother kicked her out, left her to fend for herself on a cold winter’s night? Almost certainly, she had — when she wasn’t locking her in small, dark spaces instead.

It’s too awful to ponder, so Rio tries to push it from her mind as she nods. “I think you’re probably right. You’re very smart, you know that?” His mouth curves into a bashful smile, and he gives her a sheepish shrug. “What do you want to be when you grow up?”

“Mm…” He thinks very hard again. “An animal doctor. Or a singer. Or both.”

“Maybe you could be a vet and sing to your animal patients to keep them calm,” Rio suggests.

“Yeah.” Nicky grins. “Scratchy really likes it when I sing to him. One time, I had to hold him while Mama got a splinter out of his paw.”

“See? You’re already on your way.”

Nicky’s smile fades into a more nervous expression. “Ms. Rio?” he asks, voice uncharacteristically hesitant.

“Hm?”

“Are we gonna be friends forever and ever?”

She should just say ‘yes’ — ease his obvious anxieties — but she can’t bring herself to lie to him. “That’s a complicated question,” she confesses, which seems to confirm his suspicion that this was something to potentially fear.

“Why?” He frowns. “You don’t want to be my friend forever?”

“That’s not it at all,” she reassures him. “I love spending time with you. But there are more factors at play than just what you or I want.”

“Like what my mom wants,” he says, looking down at the blanket.

Rio nods slowly. “That’s one of them.”

“I have one friend at school named Sophie, but she thinks Mama is scary, so she doesn’t like to come over unless I’m at Mom’s house. And my other friend Emily isn’t allowed to talk to me anymore because Mama got into a fight with her mom in the parking lot. She hit the back of our car in the pick-up line, and then they yelled at each other, and the principal had to come out, and they got in trouble, and now Emily isn’t supposed to be my friend.”

Jesus fucking Christ, Agatha, Rio thinks. “That’s…unfortunate,” she admits. “But sometimes, things just need time to blow over. Maybe Sophie and Emily’s mom will come around.”

“Maybe,” he says, clearly lacking confidence in this possibility. He looks back up at her. “Don’t be scared of her, okay, Ms. Rio? Or not talk to her even if you get in a fight.”

“I won’t,” Rio promises, putting out her little finger. “Pinky swear.”

Nicky links his tiny one with hers, seeming to relax a little. “Good. Because Mama likes you. A lot. A lot a lot."

“You think so?” 

“Uh-huh. Like sometimes, she gets all red around you and messes up her words.”

“And how do you feel about that?”

He giggles, covering his mouth with his hand. “It’s funny a little bit.”

The corner of Rio’s mouth quirks into the ghost of a smile. “It is,” she agrees.

“It’s because she has a crush on you,” he loudly whispers, voice conspiratorial.

“I know she does.”

“And you have a crush back.” He giggles again.

“You’re very observant,” Rio muses, amused.

He nods. “I know.”

“Did you finish your food?”

“No.” He shakes his head. “I’m going to, but I wanted to give you yours first. And make sure you weren’t going to leave.”

“I won’t leave,” Rio assures him. “Your mama just said something that hurt my feelings, and I need a little space to process that.”

He frowns a little, brows crinkling. “That’s not how it works.”

Rio blinks. “What do you mean?”

“You put yourself in time-out because Mama hurt you. Mama should be the one in time-out — so she can think about her words and actions,” he recites.

Rio can’t really argue with that logic, so she doesn’t try. “It’s okay,” she lamely replies with an equally lame shrug. “I’m just decompressing at the moment.”

“If I bring my bunny in here so you can eat with him, would that make you feel better?”

Rio reaches out to squeeze his shoulder. “That’s very sweet of you, but I think I’ll be okay. I just needed to step away for a second.”

“But you’re still gonna come to the aquarium, right? Because I really, really, really, really…really want you to come.”

"I’ll be there,” she promises.

He nods, her vow of attendance seeming to relax him even more. “I’m gonna go eat my waffle now,” he declares. “Or else I won’t be able to go.”

“Make sure you also drink plenty of juice and water so you’re hydrated,” Rio finds herself saying. She’s not even sure where it comes from — the maternal suggestion — and she tries not to think about it too hard. It seemed like a whole can of worms she doesn’t currently have the bandwidth to open.

“I want coffee.”

“Well, coffee dehydrates you, which could make you feel gross at the aquarium.”

“Nuh-uh. It makes me want to jump around. Mama let me have it two times even though it made Mom really mad.”

Rio doesn't point out that Agatha had likely let him have it because it made Wanda really mad. “And it dehydrates you,” Rio explains. “It’s also not good for someone who’s chronically sick. I can’t drink it much with my POTS.”

“Oh.” He chews on the inside of his cheek, considering. “Then I’ll abstain with you,” he decides. “Ms. Lilia taught me that word.”

“That’s very sweet of you,” Rio encourages. “And a great word to know.”

“Grown-ups tell me I have a rich vocabulary,” he states — mostly factually, though maybe a little proud, too. He was Agatha’s son, after all. Some arrogance was bound to have rubbed off on him.

“That’s a wonderful skill to have. I’m sure it’ll be very helpful as you work your way through veterinary school.”

He gives her another bashful smile before hopping off the bed to finish his breakfast. 

A few minutes later, Agatha comes into the bedroom, wordlessly sitting on the chair in the corner. She glances over at the plate on the nightstand and, despite still being sort of pissed at Rio, is admittedly pleased to see she’s taken a couple more bites of her waffle. 

There are a few beats of awkward silence, neither wanting to be the first to talk. Agatha crosses her arms and sucks on the inside of her cheek for a moment before, in an uncharacteristic move, caving first. “My six-year-old son just put me in time-out,” she says.

“Did he,” Rio coolly replies.

“Yes. He did.” She looks out at the window — at the waves rolling onto the shore. “If I had ever tried to send my mother to time-out…” She shakes her head, breathes out a humorless laugh. There would have been yelling, definitely. Bruises, probably.

“You aren’t her,” Rio assures her, some gentleness slipping into her tone despite herself.

“Mm,” she hums in tentative agreement. Rio doesn’t say anything else, so after a long, stubborn moment, Agatha sighs. “It’s just the way I talk,” she explains-slash-defends. “I thought you’d been around me long enough by now to realize that.”

“That may be true, but it’s not unheard of that a person would learn how to modulate their tone to match what’s appropriate for the situation.”

“Well, it’s not unheard of that a person struggles with that either, is it?” Agatha snaps. “I mean, you’re the one who accused me of…” She can’t bring herself to say it. She doesn’t know why she can’t bring herself to say it, but she can’t. 

“Being autistic,” Rio finishes for her, which Agatha is both grateful for and irritated by. “There’s nothing wrong with that.”

Agatha purses her lips, shaking her head and looking out the window once more. “Whatever. It doesn’t matter. I’m sorry, okay? I’m sorry. That’s what you want me to say, isn’t it?” It’s a pretty shitty apology — one Agatha knows, deep down, Rio’s right not to accept. Not even acknowledge.

“It’s okay to struggle, Agatha. What’s not okay is acting like every single person is out to get you all the time.” She’s tempted to disagree with that, as most people seem to be out to get her at most times, but for once, she bites her tongue and allows Rio to continue. “What’s not okay is making yourself the victim and being an asshole when someone tells you how they feel.”

“At no point this morning was I trying to be an asshole. Believe it or not, I’ve actually been trying to be really nice, which is why it’s so confusing that we ended up here.” Agatha clenches her jaw, more out of frustration than fury. “At no point this morning have I tried to make myself the victim either. Trust me, I’m well aware I’m not a victim. That I fucking deserve every shitty thing that’s ever happened to me.” That part is factual — not looking for pity.

Rio gives her some anyway, voice softening a bit. “I don't believe that. Nor do I believe you were trying to hurt me. But like I was trying to say earlier, your intention doesn’t outweigh your impact. For example, I may intend to…” She searches for an analogy. “...help someone carry something down a flight of stairs from a place of kindness, but on the way down, I could accidentally trip them — cause them to drop the thing or injure themselves. My intentions never changed, but the tangible impact I’ve made outweighs that.”

Agatha’s quiet for a long beat, considering. “I’ve never thought of it like that, I suppose,” she quietly admits. “Nobody’s ever explained it in that way. Given me an example.”

“Do you get it now? Why I was upset? And how that’s different from being upset with you?”

She nods a little, dropping her gaze from the window down to her lap. “I’m sorry,” she mumbles. “I’m saying that because it’s what you want to hear but also…because…it’s true. I am.” She was fucking terrible at apologies, but the fact she had gotten herself to say a genuine one at all was no small feat.

“Thank you,” Rio says. “I appreciate it.”

Agatha shifts in her seat. It was ironic, the fact she’d come in here to appease Nicky’s time-out badgering, as the whole thing does make her feel rather like a punished child. “So what now? You hurt me back, and we call it even?”

Rio blinks, taken aback. “No? That’s not how that works — like, at all. We just…move on and try to do better.”

She looks back up at her, expression sharp. “Okay, well I don’t fucking know,” she says, defensive to mask the embarrassment. “You can hurt me if you want. I’m a big girl — I can handle it.”

“Well, I don’t want to,” Rio replies, the space between her brows creasing. “I’m not out for revenge because you made a mistake.”

“I hurt you first. It’d be justice or consequence — not revenge.” ‘Justice’ was the word courts liked to hold against her. ‘Consequence’ was her mother’s preference. Her justification for her methods of attempting to keep her in line.

“It would be neither of those things,” Rio argues. “Your consequence is feeling bad for hurting me, and true justice isn’t supposed to cause anyone harm.”

“Oh, fuck.” Agatha rubs a hand over her face. “Please don’t get all lawyer mode on me.”

“That’s not a lawyer thing — it’s just the truth.”

“Okay, fine. Whatever. Are we…good…now, or…?”

Rio slowly nods. “We are.”

“Okay,” she repeats, squirming in the chair once again. “Great. Hunky-dory.”

Rio looks at her for a long moment. “It’s okay to be honest with me, you know. About how uncomfortable this is for you. I’m well aware conflict resolution in your life has not been fruitful or painless.”

Agatha’s throat gets sore, unexpected tears rising up at that. At being seen, maybe. Or hearing someone say it so starkly.  

No, it has not been fruitful. Her mother died as the two were screaming about how much they fucking hated each other, and she and Wanda had one of the nastiest divorces her lawyer had ever seen. There was no closure in that. No growth. No point. 

It certainly has not been painless, either. Conflict ended only after getting the shit beat out of her physically, verbally, legally — sometimes all three at once. And even so, it didn’t really end. Conflict was a constant hum in the background of her life. A thing that Agatha had learned to stoke because then at least she was in control of it. Agatha had made friends with conflict to survive. 

She swallows hard. “No, it’s all right,” she replies, voice hoarse and thick. “As long as we’re good, I’m good.”

Rio’s lips curve into a small frown. “That’s clearly not true,” she gently pushes. “It’s okay to feel what you need to feel, Agatha. I’m not going to judge you.”

“You say that now. Everyone says that at the beginning until they realize my feelings are not palatable things. That they’re loud and violent and ugly.”

“But they’re valid,” Rio says. “Especially with everything you’ve been through. I promise you, bottling them up isn’t helping.”

“Nicky will never see inside that bottle. He can’t.” Agatha shakes her head vehemently, rocking back and forth a bit as she chews on her thumbnail. She hears Lilia’s voice in her head, ‘Feral animal.’ “I don’t…I don’t want you to see it either,” she admits, voice so quiet it’s barely audible — gaze fixed firmly on the wall.

“But I want to see."

She continues shaking her head. “It’s like a shaken-up soda bottle filled with fucking poison. I’m not letting it burst open and contaminate you.”

“I can handle myself,” Rio insists. “I want to be there with you and for you, Agatha.”

“You’ll change your mind,” she says softly. “People always do. I’ve gotten dropped by therapists, Rio. Plural. Ones the state literally assigned to me.”

“I won’t change my mind. Also, if a therapist isn’t qualified to see you, it’s not about you — it’s that they don’t want to do you a disservice. I’m going to look for someone who’s trauma-informed. People who are equipped to handle shit like ours.”

Agatha bristles, baring her teeth as her head snaps over to look at Rio. “Well, I’m not changing my mind about voluntarily seeing a fucking therapist, so don’t bother wasting your time.”

Rio gives her a look, somehow both patient and disapproving of her mini tantrum. “I meant for me.”

“Oh.” A beat as she comes down from her rush of irritation. She feels fucking stupid. Again. “I thought you were going to try and force me to…as a…condition or whatever.”

“I’m not going to force you to see a counselor,” she promises. “I just want you to let me in.”

Agatha’s gaze drops to the floor once more. “My outside is much better than my inside, Rio. Believe me. Much sexier.”

“Not everything has to be sexy. I want to know you — every part.”

“You know what happened when Pandora opened the box, don’t you? You Greek mythology nerd? Bad shit happened.”

“Yes, but it was inevitable. And bad or not, those things are part of being alive. Of human nature and existence.”

Agatha sighs. “You’re completely missing the point.”

“No, I’m not,” Rio argues. “You think you’re too toxic and dangerous for me to know the real you underneath the facade, but you aren’t. You’re not bad. You’re not evil. I want to know you, Agatha.”

She stares at Rio for a long, long moment — the space between her brows pinched. Like she’s speaking a language Agatha is even less familiar with than Spanish. “I don’t know,” she finally responds.

“You don’t know what?”

“I don’t know if I want to do that,” Agatha admits. “I don’t know if I can. I don’t know. About any of it.”

“Well, I believe in you. What part are you having trouble with?”

“I don’t know. Fucking all of it?”

“Elaborate.”

Agatha huffs out a breath. “I like what we have right now. Don’t you?”

“Yes, but I want more. I want a real relationship. What are you so scared of?”

“That you’re going to break my fucking heart, Rio!” she blurts before she knows she’s saying it. She blinks, having startled even herself, her shock intensifying when she feels the bottom of her left eye grow wet. “Fuck,” she whimpers, turning her head and biting her knuckles. “Fuck.”

Rio sighs before stepping out of bed and going to kneel in front of Agatha, her calf be damned. She gently takes the hand that Agatha’s biting in her own. “I can’t promise that whatever we have will last forever because I don’t know,” she admits. “But I can promise I’m going to try my hardest to make it work. That I’ll never hurt you on purpose.”

“Weren’t you the one who just said that intention doesn’t equal impact?” Agatha tries to ask dryly, though the crack in her voice betrays her.

“I know it doesn’t. But fear like that is something you have to surrender to if you’re going to try your hardest to make it work, too.”

She shakes her head. “I always survive,” she whispers. “But I wouldn’t survive that.”

“Yes, you would,” Rio encourages, thumb rubbing soothing circles on her hand. “I need you to try for me.”

There’s a knock on the door then. Lilia, probably. Lilia, hopefully. Agatha never thought she’d think that, but the alternative — the Italian police or something — seemed far worse. “I have to get that,” she says, wiping her eyes and standing from the chair.

“Nicky can answer it.” Rio sighs, managing to push herself up off the floor with a surprising amount of speed to block Agatha’s path. “You can’t avoid this forever, Agatha.”

Agatha glares at her. “I am not letting my six-year-old son answer the fucking hotel door when I'm not 100% certain who is behind it,” she says, voice just as serious. “Move, Rio.”

Rio clenches her jaw before reluctantly stepping aside. “Fine. Keep running.”

Agatha charges a few steps before something makes her stop in the doorway. She balls her hands into fists before letting out a long exhale and turning to face her. “I shed a tear in front of you, Rio,” she points out. “I admitted that I was afraid of something. That is more than most people ever get from me.”

“And still, I would like more,” Rio says simply.

She bites her tongue to keep herself from making some snarky comment about that being greedy. Instead, she scrapes a hand through her hair. “Can we put a pin in this? For now? Please?”

“Details, yes.” Rio nods. “But I need a promise from you that you’re going to try.”

Agatha looks down, toeing the ground. “I wouldn’t be doing any of this if I wasn’t, Rio.”

“You mean it?”

Her eyes flicker up to meet hers. “Yes. For fuck’s sake, yes,” she says, more exasperated than anything. The knocking at the door intensifies. “Don’t be angry,” she finds herself pleading. Another bizarre statement to leave her mouth. She usually didn’t give a fuck. Usually pissed people off on purpose. “Or disappointed or upset or any of that. Just…just be patient with me, okay?”

“I’m none of those things,” Rio promises. “I’m just doing my best.”

“I am, too,” she says sincerely.

“I know.”

She pokes her tongue against the inside of her cheek. “So we’re still good?” she checks. She fucking hates it. How needy she sounds. How insecure. But maybe this is what Rio wants.

“We’re good,” Rio assures her.

Agatha purses her lips and nods as another round of knocks can be heard. She rolls her eyes, turning on her heel. “I’m coming!” she snaps, striding over to the door.

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: A pep talk.

Chapter 27: Day 5, Part 6

Chapter Summary

A pep talk.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha rips the door open, revealing Lilia on the other side. “Someone’s panties are in a wad.”

Lilia lifts her chin. “It’s rude to keep someone waiting after you’ve invited them somewhere.” 

“Oh, I did nothing of the sort — that was all Nicky.” Agatha looks her over. She’s wearing another weirdly patterned muumuu, more chunky jewelry. “Well, come in, then,” she orders, stepping to the side to reluctantly allow her to enter.

“You weren’t supposed to come out until I said,” Nicky says sternly as Agatha shuts the door behind them, pointing at the clock on the microwave. “See how that says 9, 3, 7? I wasn’t going to say until it said 9, 4, 0.”

“What do you mean, Nicky?” Lilia asks, setting her purse on the table.

“She was in time-out because she was mean to Ms. Rio.” 

“I wasn’t actually—" Agatha scoffs. “I was humoring him, obviously,” she explains.

“Mm.” Lilia nods, her expression giving very little away. Agatha hated that — when people were unreadable. It didn’t happen often.

“Look, I said I was sorry,” Agatha says, feeling strangely chastised. Why the fuck she feels the need to defend herself to her six-year-old and some elderly wacko she doesn’t even know, she’s not sure. 

“Did you mean it?” Nicky presses.

“Yes.” She runs a hand over her face. “I meant it.”

Lilia finally snorts a little, which pisses Agatha off to no end. “Are you excited for the aquarium?” she asks, her dumbass bangles clanging together as she turns to Nicky.

“Yes! We’re gonna see catfish, and clownfish, and angelfish, and swordfish, and eels.”

“And dolphins.”

He gasps. “Dolphins,” he whispers.

“Yup.” She nods, grey curls bouncing. “I saw on the pamphlet in the lobby that there are three of them.”

“I’m gonna name them Nicky, Mama, and Ms. Rio,” Nicky declares. 

“Mm,” Agatha hums. “Looks like you didn’t make the cut,” she tells Lilia, more pleased by this than she should be.

“You can be a rainbow fish, Ms. Lilia,” Nicky assures her. “Because of all your colorful outfits.” Agatha wrinkles her nose. Fucking traitor.

Lilia gives him a smile. “Rainbow fish are very pretty.”

“So are you, Ms. Lilia,” he says earnestly. 

Agatha rolls her eyes. “Suck-up,” she accuses under her breath.

“Thank you, son,” Lilia says, ignoring Agatha as per usual. “What are you most excited to see?”

“Mm,” he considers before finally deciding on, “All of them."

“Do you like seahorses?” Lilia asks. “They’re my favorites. I remember yesterday you told me the males carried the offspring, and I thought that was very interesting.”

“Mhm.” He nods vigorously. “They’re also the slowest-moving fish. But that’s okay because of the tortoise and the hare story. You can be slow and steady and still win the race. Except Señor Scratchy would never, ever get beat by a turtle. I like the green ones most. What about you?”

“I’m quite fond of the gold and yellow ones, so green’s cousin, I suppose.”

Nicky tilts his head. “Cousin?”

“That’s the child of your aunt or uncle,” Lilia explains.

“Oh.” He wrinkles his brows. “But I only have one — Uncle P. — and he doesn’t have any kids.”

“And thank god for that,” Agatha mutters.

Lilia once again pays her no mind. “Well, family is more than blood. You can also adopt people you’re close to as your cousins if you’d like.”

Nicky contemplates this for a moment before declaring, very seriously, “Then I’d like to adopt you as my cousin, Ms. Lilia.”

She breathes out a chuckle. “Well, that’s very sweet of you. Thank you.”

Agatha scoffs. “And mathematically impossible. She can be your adoptive great-great cousin.”

Nicky nods earnestly. “I do think she’s great.” 

“No, that’s not—“ Agatha sighs, massaging her temples. “I need an Advil.”

“I’m sure you do,” Lilia smugly muses.

Agatha glares at her. This bitch is enjoying this. Agatha doesn’t want Lilia enjoying anything, but it’s particularly annoying considering it’s at her expense. It must end. Immediately. “I’d ask you to grab me one from my purse, but you tried to rob me last time I requested that favor of you.”  

Nicky frowns. “You shouldn’t steal, Ms. Lilia.” 

“Tell her, Nicky,” Agatha encourages, the corner of her mouth curving into a small smirk. “Maybe she needs a time-out, too.”

Lilia coolly smooths out her kaftan. “Well, perhaps your mother should also hear that lesson. I saw the name on her credit card yesterday, and it wasn’t Agatha Harkness.”

Agatha’s smirk falls, and she sucks her teeth. Well-played, she had to admit. And infuriating. “I think Ms. Lilia should really try wearing her glasses.”

“20/20 vision, darling,” Lilia retorts, raising a brow as if to propose a ceasefire.

Considering Agatha doesn’t particularly want to have to explain Sharon Davis to Nicky, she rolls her eyes. “I’m going to check on Rio.”

From the looks of it, the woman hasn’t found the energy to do much since Agatha left. She’s still wearing her pajamas when she makes it back, zoned out as she stares at her bruised neck in the full-length mirror.

“Hey,” Agatha greets, giving the doorframe a few light taps to alert Rio of her presence. The last thing she wanted to do was surprise her right now. “Lilia’s here.”

“I figured,” Rio muses, only half present. “I’m glad she and Nicky get along.”

Agatha is not actually sure she herself is glad about that, so she doesn’t offer a response. Instead, she asks, “Are you about ready to go? Nicky’s getting antsy, and Lilia’s pissing me off."

“I guess,” she says, gaze firmly fixed on the sickly purple handprints around her throat.

Agatha purses her lips before walking to her closet and fishing out a shirt. “You should wear this,” she tells her, holding out a lavender tank top with a mock turtleneck. “If you want,” she thinks to add in a rare moment of emotional intelligence. “Not, you know…a requirement. Obviously.” Though it isn’t obvious at all, Agatha knows. It’s not even the norm for Rio. “I just…I think you’d look sexy in it,” she says to try and make it better, though she’s probably making it a lot worse. “Or...not sexy. Well, I mean, yes, sexy, but that’s not— I don’t— I…um…I want you to be…comfortable. So. If it might make you comfortable, you may wear it,” she says, somehow veering into overly formal territory.

Rio glances at the shirt, then at Agatha. Back at the shirt. At Agatha again. Instead of verbally responding, she simply wraps her arms around her.

“Oh.” Agatha blinks, buffering for a second before hugging her back. “Okay.” Rio responds by burying her face into her neck. “Okay,” she repeats, softer now. “It’s okay.”

“I just— He never gave me a choice like that,” Rio whimpers. Agatha can feel tears wetting her collarbone. “I always had to do what he said.”

“I figured.” 

“I don’t know how it happened,” Rio insists. “It wasn’t like that at first. And by the time I realized how bad it was, I didn’t see a way out.”

“Boiling frog,” Agatha muses.

Rio sniffles. “What?”

“You don’t know that metaphor? If you put a frog in boiling water, it’ll jump out immediately. But if you put a frog in room temperature water and slowly increase it to boiling, it won’t even realize what’s happening. Will stay there until it’s too late.” Agatha smooths Rio's hair. “I think I’m an anomaly — a frog that jumps out no matter the temperature.”

Rio clutches onto her more tightly. “Don’t jump out this time,” she pleads in a whisper.

Agatha purses her lips. “I’m not,” she promises after a beat. “I may be…drowning a little, but I’m still in the pot.”

She feels Rio relax against her a bit. “Good.”

It didn’t really feel very good, barely treading water. It was so much easier to not be in the pot at all.

There are a few moments of silence before Rio speaks, voice quiet and self-conscious. “People will stare at me."

“Because you’re so magnetic and beautiful, maybe,” Agatha tries.

Rio doesn't take the bait. “No, because there’s a bruise on my neck that even a turtleneck won’t cover.”

“It’ll hide a lot of it, and your calf could’ve happened in a number of ways," Agatha rationalizes. "You’re also well aware I have zero problem with confrontation. I’ll happily cuss and/or knock someone out in the middle of a Sicilian aquarium. Give the fish something interesting to observe for a change.”

“Which I appreciate, but I still hate being stared at.”

Chapter 28: Day 5, Part 7

Chapter Summary

A disastrous reunion.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Why did you major in biology and then go on to do law?”

“Oh.” Rio shrugs. “I don’t know. Because I could.”

What a strange girl. What a strange reason. Agatha robbed convenience stores because she could. Got blackout drunk on stolen vodka because she could. Went to a bar to drink more and fucked multiple women in the bathroom because she could.

“It’s been a while,” Rio continues, “but I remember those behavioral genetics classes well. I always found them interesting.”

“Well, they’re irrelevant in this particular scenario, but you know, gold star, A+, etcetera.”

“They’re very relevant. Your brain and DNA are made up of the exact same things as everyone else's. You are the way you are because of things you had to survive within your environment.”

“Still talking science to me, hot stuff? Is this your way of saying you want to do some professor-student roleplay? Because I could be into that.”

Rio doesn’t take the bait. “No, Agatha. I’m telling you that you aren’t an exception. That you aren’t some special case of fucked up.”

“Accusing me of normality? I’m wounded.” 

Even now, Agatha can’t seem to stop herself. She wants so desperately to be able to stop herself, but somehow, the words keep leaving her mouth anyway.

She doesn’t like that Rio doesn’t immediately say anything back, but she is grateful she doesn’t walk away again. She finds herself…twitching in her chair. A restless, nervous buzz humming through her body. It feels like some strange, hellish combination of alcohol withdrawal and childhood. She crosses her arms over her chest, trying to squeeze herself still. 

Rio sighs. “Look, I’m not going to engage in a conversation that isn’t sincere and genuine. I know humor is your defense mechanism, but you have to stop making jokes and seriously communicate with me.”

“Yeah, I know,” Agatha snaps through gritted teeth — more out of overwhelm than anything. Frustration, yes, but mainly at herself. She sucks in a deep, shaky breath and looks up at the fluorescents on the ceiling. “Can you—” she starts, voice stilted and unnatural. “Will you just—“ She’s trying, she’s trying, she’s trying to express her needs — the real and vulnerable kind — but fighting against every instinct she’s ever acquired is proving hard mentally, emotionally, physically.

“What, Agatha?” Rio prompts, voice gentle but firm. “I need you to tell me.”

“Will you…hold me? Or…hit me?” she awkwardly requests, cheeks burning red at how deeply ashamed the plea makes her feel. “I don’t particularly care which. Just…touch me. Put me back in my body.”

“Okay,” Rio softly agrees, that same pity that Agatha saw in her eyes making its way into her voice now. Or maybe it's compassion. Agatha's not sure. She can't seem to be sure about anything these days. “Okay.” She slides down the bench, closing the distance between them and pulling her in.

Agatha grimaces, sucking air in through her teeth as she turns her head away from Rio — chin resting on her opposite shoulder. Her body’s shivering like she’s outside in the middle of a Salem winter without a coat. (She knows what that’s like.) 

“You chose the first one,” she finally observes. Her voice is impressively even, but it is thick as if there are tears caught in her throat.

“I don’t want to hit you. Even if I am frustrated.”

“Why not?”

“Because that would be wrong, Agatha.” Her tone is patient, as if talking to a child, but somehow, it doesn’t feel condescending.

It also doesn’t really answer Agatha’s question. People wanted to do wrong things all the time. People did do wrong things all the time. Agatha, for instance — all she ever seemed to be able to do was the wrong thing. 

She doesn’t bother pointing this out. The answer, probably, was just that Rio was good. Was the kind of person who wanted to do the right thing and even usually managed to pull it off. 

“Please talk,” Agatha requests, eyes still fixed on the wall opposite Rio — on a faded, peeling jellyfish sticker. “It doesn’t matter what you say. But if you don’t talk, I’ll talk, and everything that comes out of my mouth always makes it all worse.” Always makes you leave.

“I need a little break from talking,” Rio admits, unhooking one arm from Agatha in order to take her phone from her pocket and put on some music. “Here.” 

Agatha’s sure it’s calming for Rio — the whole world quiet except for the music — but it’s fucking agony for her. It’s fucking hell. It’s quiet enough that she can hear her heartbeat, quick and loud. Her breaths, shaky and wet. Her thoughts, the ones that have her mother’s voice. She feels restless and trapped and so like that caged, feral animal Lilia had accused her of being.

It’s three and a half songs before her body can’t bear it. The stress or the shame or whatever the fuck that feeling was swirling in her stomach, spoiling in her gut.  

Rio’s arms are suddenly too tight — too hot — and she untangles herself from them without looking at her, pushing herself off the bench with trembling arms. Her head, she’s suddenly realizing, is fucking pounding. Her head is fucking floating. Her body is lead. Her body is weightless.

Rio breaks from her haze at the sudden movement, shooting her a concerned look. She’s probably either very, very pale or very, very red. She’s not exactly sure which. “Agatha?

Agatha never had a problem mouthing off to her mother, despite the fact that it never really ended well for her. Nor sassing judges despite her lawyer’s advice — her lawyer’s pleas, really — to refrain. But in this moment, Agatha finds the prospect of opening her mouth downright terrifying. Surely, she’s bound to say something insensitive and inappropriate to make Rio walk away again — walk away and never come back. Or perhaps, in this…this fucking state she found herself again, she’d find herself admitting to it all. The awful things she’s done in the past and what she deeply desired for her future despite the fact she doesn’t deserve it. 

What actually happens when she opens her mouth is…possibly a blessing or possibly worse than either, as she doesn’t manage to get a single word out. Instead, Agatha throws up a blueberry waffle in the fucking sensory room of a Sicilian aquarium.

Rio must see it coming, as she manages to kick the small trash can in her direction just in time for it to catch the vast majority of the vomit. She uses one hand to guide Agatha back down to the bench, the other to gather her hair away from her face.

Agatha doesn’t cry, but on the off chance the waterworks do manage to possess her body, she most certainly doesn’t cry in public. Even when Nicky was in the hospital — when it looked like he might not make it all those endless weeks — she waited until she was in the car. 

Agatha cries now, though. Sobs, really — harder than she has since she was a baby. Maybe not even then. Evanora didn’t have much patience for that. Maybe it’s from feeling downright fucking mortified, or maybe it’s from feeling Rio’s hands in her hair — so, so gentle — or maybe it’s some combination of both.

“Shh,” Rio soothes, rubbing her back. It’s clear from the hesitation in her voice — the stiffness in her movements — that she feels out of her depth. It’s clear from the warmth in her voice — the tenderness in her touch — that she’s a natural at it anyway. “It’s okay.”

That makes her cry harder, somehow — something she wasn’t actually convinced was possible. “You shouldn’t—“ she chokes out. “—be doing this.”

“Hush,” Rio murmurs. “I should.”

“No,” she argues, voice strangled but stern and somehow more sure than she’s ever sounded about anything. “You shouldn’t.”

“I should,” Rio replies with equal certainty. “I can. And I will."

“Why? Tell me why. There are eight…billion…people on the planet,” she says, sounding choppy and borderline hysterical. “Why…do you insist on choosing…the worst ones…every fucking time?”

“There’s a difference,” Rio calmly replies, “between the scum of the earth and flawed people who try.”

“And what happens when I try…and I try…and I try…and I’m still the scum of the fucking earth?”

“You’re not, Agatha. But if you feel like you are, then you keep trying. People who want to change usually can.”

‘Usually’ is not always, and Agatha is not ‘usual’ by any definition of the word. 

She pulls away from Rio’s touch, more reluctant than she wants to admit, and turns to face her. She must look an absolute mess — face puffy and splotched, the little mascara she bothered to swipe on running down her cheeks — but it’s necessary. 

“I need to know…why you’re doing this for me. When you were…almost killed yesterday. When you killed yesterday. What do you see, Rio?” she demands. “What do you see? When you look at me? Right now?”

Rio purses her lips, carefully considering her words. “I see someone who’s hurting,” she finally says. “Someone who’s overwhelmed and doesn’t know why she’s being given grace and comfort. I see someone who’s funny. Someone who cares so much about me. Despite her struggle to admit it, I know she cares.” The corner of her mouth twitches into a frown, head tilting in sympathy. “I see someone who hates herself. Someone who thinks she’s irredeemable even though she isn’t.”

Agatha squeezes her eyes shut, unable to look at the sincerity in Rio’s. Unable to look at her as she whimpers. 

It takes a few shuddering, violent breaths before she can get any words out — ask a crucial question. “Do you want me?” she whispers. “Or do you just want to fix me? Do you like me? Or do you just like the idea of what you think I could be?”

“I want you, Agatha,” she assures her. “I like you. I wouldn’t be here if I didn’t.”

That heals something in Agatha. No one had ever wanted her just as she was — not her mother, not her ex, not the world. 

But it breaks something in her, too. Shatters her. 

She lets out another sob and collapses into Rio, silently hoping that she’ll pick up the pieces. Silently trusting her to.

Rio wraps an arm around her, reaching for a tissue with her free hand and wiping the excess vomit off Agatha’s chin. Once that’s done, she wraps the other arm around her, too.

Agatha takes that as an invitation to bury her face into Rio’s chest, tears immediately soaking the shirt she’d let her borrow that morning — no doubt staining it with makeup, too — but Rio doesn’t flinch. She doesn’t move. She doesn’t do anything but stroke her hair with one hand, trace soothing circles on her back with the other.

It’s the most unnatural, uncomfortable, hardest thing Agatha’s ever done — letting herself be held.

It’s the most innate, calming, easiest thing in the world — being in Rio’s arms. 

“This is it,” Agatha quietly notes. “The inside of that bottle I told you about.”

“And that’s okay,” Rio promises. “I’m not running away, am I?”

No, she’s not — even if she definitely should be. No, she’s not — even if she probably will eventually. Right now, she’s not — and right now, that’s enough.

Right now, for the first time in her life, maybe Agatha is enough, too.

Chapter End Notes
