Coming up next time: Nicky has questions. (And he’s not the only one.)

Chapter 30: Day 5, Part 9

Chapter Summary

Nicky has questions. (And he’s not the only one.)

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Time moves strangely in the sensory room. Just as Agatha had no idea how long it was before Rio returned, she has no idea how long she’s in her arms before the door opens again. 

She would hate for a stranger to see her like this. 

She would despise for the stupid waiter kid or stupid Jen or Alice to see her like this. 

But, fuck, she would take any of those options in a heartbeat over who actually opens the door and sees her like this. 

“Ms. Rio! Mama!” Nicky greets excitedly as ever, though the enthusiasm quickly dissipates as he takes in his mom’s condition. The sight of his mother crying is so jarring, so unsettling, so frightening that it makes tears immediately spring to his own eyes. “Mama?”

“Hey, kiddo,” Rio greets. “Everything’s okay. Your mom’s just got a really bad tummy ache."

It’s an admittedly good cover — made even better by the fact it wasn’t a total lie and something Nicky could relate to as someone who was often sick — but it doesn’t completely reassure him. It doesn’t even seem like he completely believes it. He was smart, sometimes inconveniently so, and unluckily for Agatha, he’d inherited her tendency to sniff out bullshit.

But if he senses her bluff, he doesn’t call it, instead yanking his hand from Lilia’s hold and darting across the room. “Mama,” he repeats, throwing his arms around her. 

Agatha adjusts quickly, her son’s well-being, as always, taking immediate priority. She shifts out of Rio’s embrace completely in order to wrap her arms around him. “It’s okay, baby,” she soothes, throat sore from vomiting, from crying, from the whole fucking fiasco. “I’m okay.”

“Nicky,” Rio says, placing a hand on the little boy’s shoulder, “will you stay here while I go get your mom a water bottle?”

“Yes.” He sniffles, clinging to Agatha as tightly as he can. “But not a plastic one. They’re bad for the turtles.”  

“Jesus Christ,” Agatha mumbles under her breath. She never should’ve taken him to that boring-ass environmentalism lecture.

“That might be all they have,” Rio regretfully informs him. “But we’ll recycle it, okay?”

“Okaaaay,” he reluctantly agrees.

Rio nods and silently exits the room, no doubt attempting to regulate her own breathing, her own brain on the walk to the vending machine. Agatha can't help but feel a bit guilty, but she shoves it — along with the rest of her feelings — back into the bottle. Just because she’d let Rio peek inside didn’t mean Nicky was going to do the same. That she would never let happen.

“So,” Agatha awkwardly starts, carding her hand through Nicky’s hair — keeping her eyes fixed on it, too. Looking at Lilia felt…risky considering her sensitive state and how obnoxiously, freakishly well the old bitch seemed to be able to read her. “What did you two get up to? See the seahorses?”

“And we caught the end of the sea lion show,” Lilia confirms. Agatha can feel her eyes studying her intently. “Want to tell your mom about that, son?”

“They balanced balls on their noses. And barked, kinda like a dog. And jumped up and caught fish in the air.” He tilts his chin just enough to look up at Agatha without breaking from her hold. “It was a little sad, because I liked the fish, too, but that’s just the circle of life,” he gravely explains.

“Tell her the special part about where we were sitting,” Lilia encourages.

“Oh, yeah. We sat in the front row, so we saw the trainers get ready. And we got splashed!” 

“Is that why your hair’s wet,” Agatha muses, continuing to run her hand through his locks.

Rio steps back in then, a bottle of water in her hands. “Here you go,” she says as she passes it to Agatha.

“Thank you,” she says as she takes it, arms still around Nicky as she avoids Rio’s eyes as well. The aftermath of her breakdown was too…awkward. Too vulnerable. Like this was the morning after some intense one-night stand but for her emotions instead of sex. 

She curses the way her hands shake as she tries to twist the cap off. Fucking hates herself for not being able to complete such a simple task. She tries not to think of the irony of struggling to open bottles of both the physical and metaphorical sort today and how humiliating both experiences had ultimately proved themselves to be.

Rio sees her battle and wordlessly reaches over to open it.

“Thank you,” Agatha mumbles again, holding it to her lips. 

“Why did the waffle make you sick, Mama?” Nicky asks. “It didn’t make me sick. Or Ms. Rio. And why did you cry? You never, ever cry.”

Agatha takes a deep breath, opening her mouth without quite knowing how she’s going to answer that. But before she’s forced to find out, Rio jumps in again.

“Well, everyone’s body is a little different,” she says. “You know how sometimes you cough, and my heart has some issues? Your mom’s body just had a bad reaction, and there could be a lot of reasons for that.”

“Oh.” He nods against Agatha’s stomach. “I…guess that makes sense.” There’s the smallest undercurrent of skepticism, like deep down he knows this isn’t quite the full story, but it seems to be a good enough answer for now.

Agatha risks eye contact with Rio for a brief moment to mouth, “Thank you,” again. That and ‘I’m sorry,’ two phrases she almost never uttered previously, seem to be the only things leaving her mouth today. Other than vomit, that is.

Rio nods a little, slumping down into one of the beanbag chairs.

Fuck, Agatha is not in any position to take charge and make decisions right now. Nor, it seems, is Rio. Agatha makes eye contact again — this time with, ugh, Lilia — shooting her a look like, ‘Fucking do something, old woman. Can’t you see we need help?’

Lilia breathes out a scoff from her place near the doorway. Her crossed arms seem to say, 'Don't look at me.'

Agatha’s expression turns more desperate but also more pissed off — a pleading snarl. 'Don't make me grovel...not in front of these two...'

She gets a defensive shrug in return. 'I really don't know what you expect me to do, you bossy bitch.'

Agatha rolls her eyes, throwing her head back. Absolutely useless. 

“Nicky, what do you want to do next, hm?” she murmurs. Her six-year-old. Her six-year-old son was going to have to lead here. 

“Can we see the dolphins now?” 

“All right.” Agatha nods, making a move to set him down on the ground. 

“No,” he says, his grip tightening around her neck. “Carry.” 

Agatha bites the inside of her cheek. She was probably not in the state to be carrying a 45-pound child around, but she wasn’t about to deny him. Not when he so clearly needed to be close to her. Not when she so badly needed to be close to him, too. “Okay,” she agrees, knees wobbling the slightest bit as she stands from the bench.

Rio reaches a hand out to steady her, and she feels a jolt run through her at her touch. Just moments ago, she had let herself feel so safe in it, which means it’s infinitely more dangerous now. Rio had dismantled part of her wall. And it was nice in some way — there was more light now, more air coming in — but she was also left exposed. Left vulnerable. 

“You expecting a tip or something?” Agatha mumbles to Lilia as she walks past her holding the door, a relatively stupid dig but a necessary one for her to feel more like herself again.

Lilia’s lack of a sassy retort only serves to make her feel more pitiful. As does the appearance of the stupid fucking waiter kid right outside the doorway again. He does look downright terrified of Agatha, though, which is somewhat comforting.

“Sorry,” he immediately blurts. “Sorry. I didn’t realize you were still—“ His nose wrinkles as he sniffs the air. “Did someone puke in there?” 

“Why?” Agatha snaps. “You gonna have to clean it? You work here, too?”

“Yes,” he surprises her by saying. “I’m…literally wearing the uniform.” He gestures at a navy polo with the name BILLY embroidered in cursive above the aquarium logo and a pair of khaki shorts. 

“Oh. I thought you just dressed like a dork.”

“Sorry for the mess,” Rio apologizes, giving him a tight smile as she ushers Agatha away from the potential conflict.

“I’m not,” Agatha informs him over her shoulder.

Rio shoots Billy a pleading, ‘Please, don’t poke the bear’ look, and he lifts his palms innocently, shaken and confused by Agatha’s general demeanor.

Rio breathes out a sigh of relief as they make it to the dolphin area without any more bloodshed. “I’m going to grab something to drink while you guys watch the show.”

“No.” Nicky shakes his head. “No more plastic. And you have to see them with us. I named one of them after you.”

“He’s right,” Agatha agrees, unable to look at her even as she tries to convey, through those two syllables, ‘Please, don’t leave me. Please, I need you.'

Rio rubs her forehead. “I’ll use a paper cup, Nicky. And I’ll just be five minutes — I’ll make it for the end.”

“You promise you’ll come?” he presses. “In time to see them?” 

Agatha glances at her then, silently asking the same. ‘You’ll promise you’ll come? That this isn’t too much? That I’m not too much?’

“I’ll be there,” she vows. “I just need a second.”

“Go ahead,” Agatha replies, looking away once again. “You don’t need my permission.”

She mostly means it to be reassuring — that she wasn’t going to control her like Thanos used to. That she could go where she wanted, do as she pleased. 

But the slightest bit of hurt creeps its way in — the slightest bit of snark to try and mask it. Rio hadn’t seemed to need this much space before Agatha had admitted to needing her. Before she had cracked the lid of the bottle Rio had begged and begged to see inside. That’s always how it seemed to go.

To her credit, Rio is only gone for about five minutes — three hundred agonizing seconds that tick down slowly as Agatha attempts to pay attention to Nicky’s seemingly endless well of dolphin facts. As soon as she takes her seat, she reaches over and clasps Agatha’s hand in either a subtle act of comfort or a silent plea to receive it. Perhaps a bit of both. 

Agatha glances down at it, then up at Rio’s face, then down at her hand again. Wordlessly, she shifts her fingers so she’s holding it back. 

“You’re breathing funny, Ms. Rio,” Nicky astutely points out from his place on Agatha’s lap, brows pinched in concern. “Do you need my PEP mask?”

“I’ll be alright,” she assures him. “Sometimes, I just feel a bit overwhelmed, but I’m working on getting back to normal.”

“Mama says normal is overrated.”

The ghost of a smile appears on Rio’s face. “It is,” she agrees. “But I’m trying to calm down so I can focus on enjoying all of the animals.”

“Do you know which one of the dolphins is you?” he asks, pointing out at the large tank. Then, before she even has a chance to reply, “Guess.”

“Hm.” Rio narrows her eyes, surveying the three dipping in and out of the water. “I’m not sure.”

“You have to guess,” he reiterates.

Agatha lightly squeezes Rio’s hand with just her pinky. “The one on the left,” she says, catching on.

“Yes!” Nicky squeals, clapping in delight. “How’d you know?!”

“Must've just gotten lucky.” She shrugs.

“You should buy a lottery ticket,” he replies, so casually it catches Agatha off guard and makes her laugh — hard and genuinely for the first time in a while. 

“What, babe?” Agatha asks.

“That’s what Ms. Lilia told me yesterday,” Nicky explains, confused as to what’s funny. “A ladybug landed on me, and she said it was a lucky omen and that I should buy a lottery ticket.”

“Maybe,” Rio hums, mouth twitching into another small smile. “But we aren’t in America right now.”

“Sicily has its own lottery, and anyone of age can play it,” Agatha points out. 

“How do you even know that?”

Nicky quickly deems the grown-up conversation irrelevant, checking out of it and turning to Lilia to inundate her with even more dolphin trivia. Which was fine by Agatha. She was about dolphined out, and she relished the chance to speak to Rio a bit more freely while still keeping him close.

“I could ask you the same about so many topics,” Agatha replies. “But I read about it when I was researching local casinos in case the activities at this place turned out to be boring as shit.”

“Ah.” Rio nods. "I’m not really a gambling person.”

“Or maybe you’re just not very good at it,” Agatha counters. “I’m an exceptional gambler. Blackjack, craps, poker — there’s nothing like the rush of beating a table full of arrogant pricks at poker.”

“Statistically, it’s very hard to be good at gambling without cheating.”

“Oh, I’m sure it is.” Which is exactly why she always did.

Rio rolls her eyes. She knows this, of course. “You’re good at it for a reason.”

Agatha scoffs in faux offense. “I’m not sure what you’re implying, Ms. Vidal. Fortune simply smiles upon me. After all, I won the genetic lottery way back in the womb considering I came out looking like this.” She was cursed as fuck in every other manner, genetically speaking, what with the fact of her mother. But to point that out would be to dilute her argument.

Rio’s small smile grows. “Your hair is very nice,” she agrees. “So is your smile.”

“Oh, you flatter me, dear.” The corner of her own mouth curves into a smirk. “Please, do go on.”

“Maybe later,” Rio says, giving her a gentle nudge. “But I do mean it.”

“My perfect eyes, tits, and ass are impatient and offended to be left out of the conversation." A beat as she lifts her chin. "But thank you.”

It scares her, how easy it is to fall back into this banter with Rio. This rhythm. This…relative peace. It’s reassuring, in a way, that even after she’d fallen apart, they could have this. But it’s dangerous, too. It ran the risk of tempting her to let her guard down again — let it down further than before. She had played with fire, and while it had made her feel warm in the moment, she was bound to get burned. And Agatha Harkness was too smart to get burned.

“Look!” Nicky points at the tank. “Ms. Rio dolphin and Mama dolphin are cuddling."

Rio chuckles a little bit, looking out at the two dolphins swimming beside each other. “Why is that one your mom?”

“Because its skin’s a little purple,” he explains. “And it has marks on its back, too.” 

Ah. There it was. The stark, swift reminder that peace was something Agatha didn’t get — didn’t deserve.

She can’t help but flinch a little, taken aback by the mention of the light scars that line down her spine. Agatha was more than confident in most of her skin, but she couldn’t help but loathe that particular patch of it.

Nicky tilts his chin, looking up at her from his place on her lap. “I saw them when you were in your swimsuit,” he casually informs her, thinking nothing of it. Why would he? Nicky had never suffered at his mothers’ hands like she did. Never knew one could be so cruel. 

“Mm.” Agatha simply nods a little, the nauseous feeling swirling in her gut once more.

“And marks or not,” Rio gently butts in as she takes in Agatha’s nearly paralyzed response, “I know you love your mom a lot.”

“Uh-huh,” he proudly confirms with a grin, face still tilted up. “I do.” 

His smile drops when Agatha doesn’t return it. Doesn’t reassure him that she loves him back like she always does, her gaze distracted and far away. “Mama?” he asks, his post-sensory room concern for her flaring up again tenfold. “Mama, are you sick again? Mama, did— did I say something bad?”

Rio looks between the two, inhaling a hesitant, grounding breath. “Hey, Nicky — can you look at me?” 

He shrinks into himself but turns his face to her as requested. 

“You’re all right. And she’s all right. You didn’t do anything wrong. But those marks you mentioned? They're probably really hard for her to think about.”

“But why?” he asks, voice small. “They’re like stripes on a tiger.”

“Well, because there are bad memories associated with them.”

“Bad memories like how?” 

“Like nothing,” Agatha responds, snapping out of her haze and running a shaky hand through his hair. “Like nothing, baby. Mama just got distracted by the dolphins for a minute.” She shoots Rio a look, equal parts grateful and warning: ‘Thank you, but don’t you dare say another word on this.’

Nicky looks up at her, face panicked but also…betrayed. “You’re lying.”

Agatha’s head jerks back slightly. She’d never seen that look in his eyes before. Never heard that tone in his voice. Most certainly never directed at her. “I’m not lying. I—" 

“Yes, you are. You’re lying.” He tears up, fear and frustration alike bubbling up. “Why are you lying?" 

Agatha blinks. “Nicky—" 

“Why do you lie?!”

A few people turn around to look at them. Agatha tries not to think of the irony. Rio had been so worried people would stare at her, yet here she was, the one on display — more than the fucking dolphins even.

“Why do you lie?!” he repeats, shoving her stomach. 

“Nicky!” she says, more out of shock than chastisement. 

“Why?” The tears stream down his face now — red and pinched — as he continues shoving his tiny hands against her. “Why? Why? Why?” 

“Stop, Nicky,” she practically pleads, pulling him tight against her. “Please, stop," she whispers. Her voice cracks. Her heart cracks with it. 

He struggles in her grasp for a few moments before giving up, his body going lax against her as he cries, face smushed against her shirt. 

“Shh,” she soothes, hugging him close. She feels the urge to fucking wail, too — for the…third time that day? Honestly, she’d lost count at this point. “It’s okay,” she lies again. “It’s okay.”

The moment is interrupted by an unfamiliar voice coming from a face that looks…vaguely more familiar than Agatha would like. She’s seen some of these features on another man’s face before, minus the thick head of brown hair that looked straight out of a boy band. “Rio?” he says.

“Who the hell is that?” Agatha asks Rio under her breath, still rubbing Nicky’s back.

Rio’s eyes go wide, jaw dropping in shock. “Eros,” she says by way of greeting, indirectly answering Agatha’s question in the process. One of them, at least.

“Who the fuck is Eros?”

He speaks before Rio can. “Her brother-in-law.”

Chapter 31: Day 5, Part 10

Chapter Summary

The arrival of Thanos' brother shakes things up in unexpected ways.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Former brother-in-law,” Rio whispers. “Please. Thanos is—” She evidently can’t bring herself to say ‘dead,’ but Eros doesn’t need her to.

“Right.” He grimaces, swiping a hand through his hair. “I only found out…well, hours ago. Still adjusting.”

“Yeah.” Her fingers fidget in her lap. “How— What do you know? I mean, do you— questions? Do you have questions? Should we go talk?”

“We’ll all go talk,” Agatha cuts in, giving Eros a steely glare. 

Eros wrinkles his brow. “Sorry, who the hell are you?” 

“Agatha,” she coldly replies. “Harkness.” 

“Relation to Rio? I thought that’s what we were sharing here.” 

“Her bodyguard,” she snaps. “Against your fucked-up family.” 

She goes to stand and shift Nicky onto Lilia’s lap, but the little boy grips on tight. “No. I’m coming with you.” 

“Nicky, this is a grown-up conversation, sweetheart.” 

“No! No, you can’t leave,” he cries. “You can’t go.” He squeezes her middle even more tightly.

Agatha sighs, torn between the two threats currently facing her: to leave Rio alone with this man she didn't trust or to have her son distrust her even more than he evidently already did.

“I'll be okay,” Rio quietly assures her.

She looks her straight in the eye. “I let you go alone last time,” she reminds her, voice deeply serious and steady apart from the tiny hint of regret that creeps in. Last time, Thanos had left bruises on her neck. Last time, he'd slashed her calf. Last time, she almost didn’t come back. “I will not make that mistake again.”

Rio bites her bottom lip, a combination of relief and guilt pooling in her eyes as she briefly glances at Nicky. “If you’re sure…”

“Oh, I’m extremely fucking positive.” Agatha flicks another venomous glance at Eros before turning her head to whisper in Nicky’s hair. “Baby, why don’t you go back to the room with Ms. Lilia and have a nap?” 

“I don’t—“ He sniffles against her, still clutching on. “—want to nap. I want—“ Another. “—to…to stay with you.” 

“I know, I know. But you’re clearly tired.” And stressed out. And confused. And it’s all my fault. “I bet you I’ll be back by the time you wake up, and we can order ice cream, and we can have a talk, okay? Any scoops, any toppings, any…” She hesitates for a beat before reluctantly using the only piece of leverage she has. “…any questions you want me to answer.” 

Nicky moves his head back just enough to look up at her, eyes red and puffy and narrowed and skeptical. “I want four.” 

She's deeply impressed and annoyed that he's inherited her ruthless negotiation skills. She nods, though half will likely go uneaten. “Okay.”

“And I want whipped cream and sprinkles.” 

She nods, though it will likely make him sick. “Okay.” 

“And I don’t want you to lie.” 

She nods slowly, though the prospect of telling him the truth about her back, about the past, about what was in her bottle and why she was so adamant about keeping it sealed shut is the most awful, painful thing she can think of. “Okay,” she agrees more quietly.

He looks at her for another second before letting out another whimper, burying himself against her once more. 

Agatha purses her lips, risking another pleading glance at Lilia. The woman gives her a stern look in response — one that makes it clear she expects Agatha to make good on her promise — but nods in agreement.

She can’t help but scowl. God, couldn’t the old bat cut her some slack? It was bad enough that Agatha had opened up to her. It was even worse that she had opened up to Rio. Opening up to Nicky — to her sweet, innocent little boy she wanted to protect more than anything, who she wanted to be strong for — was fucking unthinkable. 

It’s certainly unthinkable now, when she had so much else to think about with the Eros of it all.

She plants a lingering kiss on the top of Nicky’s head before taking his face in her hands, leaning forward so their noses are touching. “I love you,” she whispers. “More than anything in this whole wide world.”

His lip trembles. “I’m sorry I yelled. And pushed you. That was mean. I’ll go to timeout. I was— I just—"

“I know.” She thumbs a few tears from his cheeks. “I know. I understand." She understood better than anyone — his temper and his big, big feelings that came uncontrollably exploding out of him. "Just go have a rest with Ms. Lilia for me, okay?” He nods, and she kisses his forehead before setting him down.

“Come on, son,” Lilia says, offering her hand. “You want to hold it while we walk?”

He nods a little, shyly reaching out and taking it. His free hand goes to his mouth, sucking on his thumb for the first time in years.

Agatha sighs — another thing to deal with later — before turning to Rio. “Back to the quiet place?”

“Maybe the food court, considering the vomit of it all.”

“I’m sure the stupid waiter kid has cleaned it up by now, and the smell of Italian aquarium cuisine mixed with the look of this guy’s face might make me do it again.” Agatha nods toward Eros.

“Why'd you hurl the first time?” Eros asks. 

“None of your beeswax.”

Rio rubs a hand over her face. "Then I don’t care.”

Agatha is too on guard to feel guilty about stressing her out. Rio had said he was the nicer of the brothers, but Rio tended to see too much good in people. See good when there was none. Thanos was proof (and maybe so was Agatha). 

“All right,” Agatha says, making an executive decision. “Quiet place it is. More private that way.” She takes Rio’s hand — because she seemed to like it when she did that — and leads the charge as a show of dominance to Eros. 

“We need the room,” she barks to the waiter kid, who is vacuuming the floor when they arrive. 

He looks up, confused and petrified. “Wha—"

She promptly yanks the cord out of the wall. “We need the room. Leave.” 

“But my boss said—“ One seething glare makes him gulp and skedaddle, nearly tripping on the cord in the process.

Agatha slams the door shut behind him before transitioning the glare to Eros once again. “So. Why the fuck are you here?”

“Well,” he starts, voice diplomatic, “my brother is dead.”

“Yeah, no shit, Sherlock — we’ve established that already. But he’d be dead if you were still in whatever hole you crawled out of, too.” 

“The authorities wouldn’t tell us much apart from that. The resort either. Said it was technically still an ‘ongoing investigation.’” 

Agatha scoffs. “Ab-fucking-surd. There’s nothing to investigate.”

“Agatha.” Rio gives her a warning look. “You can play guard dog, but please, let me talk.” 

Agatha lifts her hands innocently before moving one to rest on Rio’s back as she takes the floor.

Rio looks to Eros. “You know how he treated me. Or snippets of it, at least. The control, the verbal abuse…”

“Yes,” he quietly confirms with a small, uncomfortable nod.

“Well, it…went beyond that. Far beyond that. He hit me. He—” She clears her throat, voice softer when she continues. “He did things to me that no human being should have to experience. I finally decided that I was going to leave him, and when I came to get my things, he tried to kill me.” Rio pulls the turtleneck down so her bruised throat is on full display, hand marks clearly visible.

“Shit, Rio,” Eros says, scraping a hand through his hair. “Shit.”

“Yeah.” She lets go of the shirt, the collar concealing the injury again. “He also threw a lamp at me.” She gestures to her bandaged leg, a bit of blood starting to leak through.

“So you fought back,” he reasons. “And you…you…” He can’t seem to bring himself to say it either.

“It was him or me, and he made it clear that if he couldn't have me, he'd make sure no one else could either."

Eros sighs, massaging his temples. “How did we get here? I mean, obviously, he was always kind of an asshole, but I never thought…” He trails off. 

“You people never do,” Agatha can’t help but mumble, unable to bite her tongue entirely.

“‘Kind of an asshole’ is a gross underexaggeration,” Rio corrects, the space between her brows creasing in the first flickers of frustration. “Eros, he beat me — frequently. He raped me the day before, and that morning, he did it again, except that time he drugged me beforehand too as a nasty little cherry on top.”

“I had…I had no idea,” he says softly. “Why didn’t you tell me all this earlier? Why didn’t you make sure someone was there when you told him? Why didn’t—"

“Wrong fucking questions,” Agatha snaps. “Why didn’t you rub your two brain cells together and figure it out?” she interrogates, pointer finger on the hand not resting on Rio’s back harshly poking the middle of his chest. “Why didn’t you make sure to protect her?” Poke. “Why didn’t you hold the ugly fucking thumb accountable?” Poke.

“I— I didn’t know!” he defends. 

“Bullshit. You grew up with the son of a bitch. You witnessed things when you saw them together. You were suspicious, but you were too much of a coward to actually do anything about it.”

Rio’s quiet for a long moment before she speaks again. “You don’t understand what it was like, Eros. Every time he hurt me, he’d gaslight me until I calmed down and forgave him. He isolated me — made me feel crazy. The only reason I got the courage to leave was because of a conversation I had with Agatha.”

He purses his lips, looking from Rio to Agatha and back to Rio again. “I…I believe you,” he says. “I do. I…he was always a bully. As kids, he’d give me wedgies and swirlies and noogies—“ 

“Was he a villain in a John Hughes movie?” Agatha mutters under her breath. 

“—but he’d always manage to get away with it.”

“Typical.” Rio rolls her eyes. “White man privilege.”

“More like 'mom’s favorite' privilege in this case.” Eros grimaces. “Speaking of which…”

Rio fixes her gaze on him again. “What?” she prompts, though it’s hesitant — like she’s not sure she really wants to know.

“My mother is…well…she’s not happy, to put it mildly. That her favorite son is gone.”

She crosses her arms. “Yeah, figures.”

“No, Rio…” he says slowly. “I don’t think you understand. She’s out for blood. Your blood.”

“With what money? Last time I heard, she didn’t get anything in the divorce.”

“With this money.” Eros sighs, pulling out his phone and turning his screen to show her a GoFundMe page titled JUSTICE FOR THANOS 🕊️ that’s already raised $34,025. “She made this yesterday. Got some women from her church group to share it on Facebook. Apparently, one of them has a cousin who’s a semi-big podcaster?” He shakes his head. “It’s not a lot right now — of money or buzz — but it’s only been a day, and it’s likely only going to snowball from here.”

Rio’s nostrils flare, fearful and furious. “Well, how do you suggest we stop it? Can’t you get her to quit?”

He gives her a look. “You’ve met my mother. She doesn’t listen to me. She doesn’t listen to anyone. The only one she ever listened to was…well, my brother.”

“And the dumb fucker is dead,” Rio mumbles, massaging her temples. “Any chance she’d go to a cheap psychic I could bribe to say Thanos is at peace?”

“Lilia would do it for twenty bucks and a pack of smokes,” Agatha offers. 

“No.” Eros shakes her head. “She’s super religious now. She even thinks Harry Potter is satanic.” 

“Harry Potter is satanic,” Agatha counters. “Just not for the reason she thinks.”

“Of course she’s super religious now.” Rio shakes her head.

“Yeah. It’s…not my favorite advancement either,” Eros sympathizes.

“God, now I have to deal with an ultra-religious and racist boy mom.” Rio huffs. “I wish she’d shove a crucifix up her pale ass.”

Agatha blinks at the surprisingly vulgar comment — one that was much more likely to leave her own mouth — but runs a soothing hand up and down Rio’s back. “We will deal with a racist, ultra-religious boy mom,” she corrects. “Lucky for you, I’m well-qualified in this department.” And had just as much to lose from this monster-in-law’s smear campaign. If this bitch contributed to her losing custody… 

“That so?” Eros asks, the question seemingly posed out of genuine curiosity. 

Agatha narrows her eyes at him but answers, “My own mother was a bible-beating bigot who said I acted like a boy," she explains. 

The mere mention of Evanora — the reminder of the conversation she was soon going to need to have with Nicky — makes another wave of nausea crest over her.

Rio leans back into Agatha’s touch, looking at Eros. “How long can you hold her off?”

“I don’t…think I can put that genie back in the bottle,” he regrettably admits. “It’s already out there on the internet. I’m already here at her urging..."

She scoffs. “To do what? Revenge kill me?”

“Over my dead fucking body,” Agatha darkly mutters, a bit ironically. 

“I mean, not literally,” Eros says. “Not physically. But kill your chances at freedom — or, at the very least, any chance at having a life free of harassment again? — that’s…the gist, I’m afraid.”

“Mm, well, she’s going to be sorely disappointed.” Rio raises her chin. “I know what evidence I have against him.”

“That doesn’t…always matter. Especially when it comes to powerful men,” Eros says. “I was old enough to remember my parents’ divorce — the way my dad dragged my mom’s name through the mud, painted her out to be some whore even though he was the one who constantly cheated on her. Sure, the fact that he was loaded and had an airtight prenup helped, but it didn’t do her any favors when it came time for the settlement. Even after that, we had to keep moving because people kept finding our house.”

Agatha bites the inside of her cheek. “I loathe to admit it, but he’s right.”

“A divorce settlement is vastly different from any case where expert witnesses like doctors and forensic psychologists testify about injuries and defensive wounds,” Rio reasons. “There’s very little arguing with biological evidence.”

“A real court might care about that, but the court of public opinion?” Agatha counters. “When there are rabid fucking Facebook moms involved? They don’t tend to care about facts or truth — that’s why they’re so easy to scam.” 

“Easy to what?” Eros asks. 

Agatha waves him off. “I don't have time for your dumb questions.”

Rio covers her face. “I hate all of this,” she grumbles. “It would’ve been easier if he’d just killed me.”

“Hey,” Agatha says sternly, her gaze snapping over to her. “Look at me.” She waits to continue until Rio reluctantly drops her hands and makes eye contact. “Don’t say that. Don’t you ever say that. We are going. To figure. It out. Do you hear me?”

Rio takes a deep breath. “I guess,” she whispers. “I’m just so fucking tired.”

Agatha sighs, taking to tracing soothing circles on her spine. “I know, honey.” 

Eros squints, pointing between them. “So, are you two, like…?” 

Agatha whips her head to face him once again. “Choose your next words very fucking carefully.”

Eros lifts his palms. “No judgment. I roll with the LGBT.” 

“What?” Agatha snaps, disgusted. “Don’t ever say that again. And don’t you dare say anything to your QAnon procreator. She’d have a fucking field day leveraging that.” 

“Wasn’t planning on it. Though I don’t know what the hell I am supposed to report back..."

“Nothing?” Rio proposes, a hint of judgment seeping into her tone. “You’re a grown man.”

“She’s already called five times and sent thirty-one texts asking for updates since I’ve been here. She’s…persistent.” He swallows hard, pulling at his shirt collar. “And a little scary.”

“I repeat,” Rio says dryly, “you’re a grown man.”

“Eh, honestly, I’m not convinced.” Agatha examines the nails on her free hand with performative nonchalance. 

He scoffs. “What’s that supposed to mean?” 

“That I’d call you a little boy, but I don’t want to insult my six-year-old son like that.”

“Please.” Rio takes to rubbing her forehead again. “I can’t take another fight today.”

“Sorry,” Agatha apologizes, half meaning it. Which was still more than she usually meant it.

“Maybe I’ll tell her that I haven’t been able to find you yet,” Eros muses. “Buy me some time. Or I could tell her I did find you and that you were in bad shape — mention your neck and your calf…though, I’m sure she’d probably find a way to spin it or claim you were faking it somehow…”

“It’s up to you,” Rio replies, voice heavy with exhaustion. “I’m so over today."

Agatha sighs. Just because she was over it did not mean it was going to go away. In fact, it was likely to get worse — a lot worse. 

“Say you haven’t found her,” Agatha tells Eros. “She’ll think about it and text you later what, exactly, she wants you to say.” She turns to Rio. “Giving up any kind of control here because you’re overwhelmed is a mistake," she says, voice gentle.

Rio shoots her a desperate look. “I'm trying, Agatha,” she promises. “But I don’t know how much more I can handle right now.”

“Which is why you’re going to take a break and then get back to him,” she asserts. She looks at Eros. “And he isn’t going to say a goddamn thing before you do.”

“I can…reasonably hold her off for a few more hours,” he agrees. “The area’s big enough it wouldn’t be a stretch. Plus, she thinks I’m a little stupid.” 

“Well, broken clock’s right twice a day,” Agatha mumbles. “Why did she send you, anyway? Instead of coming herself?” 

“Oh, she’s terrified of dying in a plane crash.” 

Agatha raises a brow. “But she doesn’t care if you die in a plane crash?” 

Eros shrugs with a small, sad smile. “Pretty much.” 

Agatha can’t help but feel the tiniest bit of tenderness toward him. Evanora, too, would’ve happily stuck her on a doomed aircraft.

Rio gives him a sympathetic look. “I’m sorry. I’m not exactly happy you’re here for…well, obvious reasons, but you deserve better than her.”

“Thanks, Rio,” he says softly. “You…you deserved better than him, too.”

She chews on the inside of her cheek. “I wish I’d been smart enough to realize that years ago.”

Agatha opens her mouth to argue, but Eros cuts her off before she can. “You aced law school," he reminds her. "I don’t think it’s about smart. If it is, the rest of us are screwed.”

“Once again, I have to agree with the floppy-haired bastard,” Agatha says, though there’s a noticeable lack of vitriol in her tone now.

“It still feels like I’m stupid,” Rio admits. “Like I’m having the biggest, meanest joke in the world played on me.”

“Well, I’m not laughing,” Eros promises. “And I’m not…blaming you either. I…I want to help.”

“Then leave her alone,” Agatha answers. Normally, she’d be reluctant to do that — answer on her behalf, especially in a way that could be perceived as isolating her like Thanos so often did — but she’s trying to help her, too. Solve some of her decision paralysis. She looks to Rio, checking that this was okay. “For now, at least. Yeah?”

Rio gives a little nod in response, and Eros purses his lips, considering. “Okay,” he relents after a moment. “Text me later.” 

“She will,” Agatha promises. “I’ll make sure of it.” 

“Maybe we could have breakfast tomorrow or something?” Eros suggests.

“Don’t push your luck. You’re still on the thinnest of ice.” 

“But I haven’t fallen through yet,” he points out. 

A beat. “No,” Agatha admits. “No, I suppose you’re right.”

He rubs the back of his neck. “I’ll see you later, Rio. It was nice to meet you, Agatha.”

Agatha scoffs. “No, it wasn’t.” 

“No,” he agrees, the tiniest ghost of a smile on his face. “I suppose you’re right,” he echoes her words. 

Once he leaves, Agatha turns to Rio. “You ready to get out of this cursed-ass aquarium?”

Rio nods vehemently, letting out a breath of relief at the mere thought. “Please.”

“All right,” she says, shifting the hand on her back to wrap around her for support instead and walking them out of the room. 

The waiter kid’s eyes get big as he nearly runs into them. Third time, he senses, is not the charm today. 

“Don’t worry,” Agatha says gruffly. “We’re leaving.”

He nods, relaxed — something that doesn’t last long when she calls over her shoulder, “And we’re giving you one star on Yelp!”

Agatha shakes her head as she opens the main door, the sunlight mercifully hitting them once again — getting them out of the seemingly warped space where she felt she lived a hundred lives. “Worst fucking aquarium I’ve ever been to.”

Chapter End Notes

Coming up next time: Rio supports Agatha through a tough conversation with Nicky.

Chapter 32: Day 5, Part 11

Chapter Summary

Rio supports Agatha through a tough conversation with Nicky.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The pit in Agatha’s stomach seems to get larger with each slow step she and Rio walk back to the resort. She tells herself she’s taking her time because Rio is under duress and needs some air. She knows, deep down, it’s because she’s delaying the inevitable. 

“I know you’re not a betting woman,” she starts, trying to keep her voice light as she unlocks the door to her room and quietly pushes it open. Nicky is not in any of the common areas, which means he’s probably still napping in his bedroom. Small miracles. “But what are the odds my kid’s forgotten about our little deal?”

“Probably around zero?” Rio admits as they make their way into the master suite.

“Yeah,” she agrees as she shuts the door behind them, unable to keep up the nonchalant facade. “Yeah, you’re probably right.”

“Hey,” Rio says, giving her arm an encouraging squeeze. “You can do it.” She immediately strips the borrowed turtleneck off, breathing an audible sigh of relief as she slips her oversized pajama shirt back on.

“How, Rio?” Agatha asks, breathing out a humorless laugh as she flops back onto the bed, covering her face with her hands. “How am I supposed to do this?”

“You just do, Agatha,” she says gently. “You just tell him."

“But I don’t want to scare him. I don’t want him picturing his mother—" Her voice cracks on the word. She can’t even bring herself to say it now. How the hell was she going to tell her sweet little boy? To tell him of her scars would almost certainly scar him in the process.

“You don’t have to go into the gory details,” Rio reasons. “There’s a balance between sharing every little thing and completely shutting him out from your past.”

Agatha has never been good at balance, living only in extremes. She attempts to clear the emotion from her throat, it only half-working. “He can’t think that I’m weak,” she quietly insists. “He needs to know I’m strong — that I can protect him.”

“Admitting that something happened to you doesn’t make you weak. Does he think I’m weak because of what Thanos did to me? No. Now apply that logic to yourself.”

“It’s not the same. I’m his mom. I’ve spent my entire life shielding him from that — from her.” She purses her lips, looking at Rio. “Knowing will hurt him. And she does not get to hurt him.”

“She won’t, Agatha. She can’t. She’s dead. What will hurt him is you icing him out. You owe him the truth — at least enough of it so he understands.”

She takes a deep breath, pushing herself up so she’s sitting against the headboard. “He is the best thing in my life, Rio. The best thing that’s ever happened to me. And he is kind, and he is pure, and he is good.”

“Yes, and he deserves your honesty.”

“Well, honestly, I’m scared, all right?” she snaps before turning her head toward the window in shame — at admitting that, at letting it explode out of her.

“And that makes sense,” Rio replies, her voice as calm as Agatha’s is heightened. “It’s a valid, normal response, but you need to face that fear.”

Agatha takes another breath — shakier this time — eyes burning as they stare out at the sea. “What if he looks at me differently?” she whispers, so quietly that Rio likely has to strain to hear. She somehow feels much too far away, even though she’s only standing on the other side of the bed. She wants her to come snuggle up against her, to wrap an arm around her belly, to rest her head in the crook of her neck.

But despite their moment at the aquarium, Agatha still doesn’t know how to ask for any of those things, and besides, Rio doesn’t seem keen on giving them to her even if she did.

She runs a hand over her face. “Well, that happens sometimes. But even if it does, I don’t think it’ll be negative. He’ll probably think you’re brave.”

Agatha looks back at her and nods slowly, detecting a bit of impatience. Resentment maybe. God, she feels stupid. She feels so fucking stupid. And more than that, she feels her walls slowly creeping back up.

“You know, if you’re tired of listening to me, Rio, you can just say that,” she says, voice impressively restrained from all the…the feelings she’s feeling. “I get you’re exhausted — and understandably so — but believe it or not, I am actually baring my fucking soul here because I thought that’s what you wanted. I thought that’s what you meant by the whole ‘communication' thing. But if you’d rather I shut up and suck it up, believe me, I am more than happy to comply. Makes it much easier for me.” She slaps her hands down on her legs before swinging them over the bed. “Why don’t you take a nap while I do this, hm?”

It's a shitty, passive-aggressive thing to say, but Rio lets it go. She sighs again, her voice stopping Agatha from leaving the room. “I appreciate that you’re communicating with me — I do. I’m grateful you trust me enough to open up,” she promises. “That said, I am tired. I’m burnt out from doing damage control all day, and the quality of my reassurance isn’t what you deserve. That doesn’t mean I don't still want to listen.”

Any kind of reassurance is more than Agatha’s ever really gotten. More than she’s ever really allowed anyone to give. More than she probably deserves as well. 

“Okay," Agatha says slowly. She crosses her arms protectively over her chest, feeling untethered and unsure. She loathes both. “I don’t— What do you want to do then? I— What do you want me to do?”

“I want you to keep opening up. I want to know you, even the hard, ugly parts. I want you to keep talking so I can listen, but I may not be able to verbally respond. That doesn’t mean I hate you — it just means I don’t have the words.”

Agatha chews on the inside of her cheek, immediately apprehensive at the thought. “I don’t…I don’t think I can do that,” she admits. “It’ll feel too much like the silent treatment. I…” She swallows hard. She might as well practice saying this shit, she supposes, considering Nicky is still up next. “She used to love that punishment, too.” She digs her thumb into her arm in a desperate attempt to ground herself. “Are you— I mean…is it okay? If I don’t want to do that?”

“That’s okay.” Rio nods. “That’s perfectly okay. If you want, you can lie down with me for a while, and we can just be.”

Agatha blinks. Was she capable of that? Of just being? She’s not totally sure. If the brief time she attempted it in the aquarium directly before vomiting was any indication, she wasn’t, though she supposes she could try again. 

She should probably wake Nicky — she did promise him they’d talk right when she got back — but she can’t bring herself to do so just yet. As much as Rio had tried to soothe her anxieties, she knows that this conversation will change things between them in some irrevocable way. She wants to preserve his blissful ignorance on the subject for as long as she possibly can, even if that’s just hours now. Just minutes or seconds, even. 

“All right,” she whispers, lowering herself back onto the mattress and patting the space next to her. “Come on, then. Just be with me.”

Rio does. She snuggles up against her, wraps an arm around her belly, and rests her head in the crook of her neck without Agatha even having to ask.

Agatha doesn’t manage to fall asleep in the next couple of hours, though she doesn’t throw up again either, which she supposes is some kind of bare-minimum progress. The sound of Rio breathing beside her does admittedly lull her into a slightly calmer state.

Eventually, there’s a light knock on the door — one that unmistakably belongs to her son. Rio sits up a bit as Agatha takes a deep breath, buying herself a few more seconds of that sweet ‘before’ until she’s forced to say, “Come in.” 

Nicky slowly pushes the door open, his rabbit clutched in one hand, the other hovering near his mouth. Right. The thumb-sucking had made its return. “Ms. Lilia said she had to leave to meet someone for dinner.” 

Agatha raises a brow, looking at the clock: 4:08. “Early bird special, huh? Checks out.”

“No, not a bird…” He wrinkles his brows, confused. “She said it was with a dashing gentlewoman she met playing shuffleboard.” 

Agatha’s other brow lifts now, too. She hadn’t necessarily pinned the old broad as a fellow fruit. “Huh. Interesting.”

Nicky stares at her blankly, and she takes another deep breath, opening her arms. “Come here, baby.”

Nicky wastes no time padding over, leaping on the bed and nestling into her arms. Agatha shoots Rio a vaguely panicked look as he settles in and hopes to whatever higher power probably wasn’t out there that the few hours of rest had given her a bit more energy. That she would be able to support her through this somehow. It’s terrifying how much she needs her in this moment. How much she seems to need her in general now.

Rio responds by reaching over and rubbing her arm, which gives Agatha the courage to clear her throat and run a hand through Nicky’s hair — the action as much to ground herself as to comfort him. “I told you that you could ask me anything you wanted, so…” 

“Why do you have lines on your back?” he wastes no time asking, the Harkness bluntness winning out. Usually, she’d be thrilled they seemed to be kicking the Maximoff influence’s ass, but now… 

“Well, they’re…scars. Kind of like that little line you have on your chest from when you got surgery as a baby.” She touches her finger to his sternum. 

He tilts his head. “So you got surgery? Are— are you sick?” His eyes well with tears. “Are you gonna die? Like Sienna’s mom from my class? She had cancer.” 

“No, honey — nothing like that.” She was sick, probably. In the head and in the soul. But that’s not what he’s asking. “Someone…someone gave me them — a long time ago — to hurt me.” 

His mouth curves into a deep frown. “But why?” he asks softly, eyes so wide and earnest and innocent. “Why would someone do that?” 

She feels a sob threaten to creep up her throat and desperately swallows it down. She couldn’t answer that, not just because she didn’t want to but because she didn’t know. She didn’t fucking know.

“Because some people aren’t very nice,” Rio jumps in to explain. “That's why being kind is so important. It helps make up for the people who aren’t.”

“Like that scary man you were with at breakfast?” Nicky asks.

Agatha sees Rio clench her jaw and swallow hard. “Mhm.”

Nicky looks back at Agatha. “Did he give you the marks?” 

“No.” She shakes her head. “No, it wasn’t him.” 

“Then who?” 

She closes her eyes for a moment, tilting her head toward the ceiling. God, this was killing her. Telling him about how she got the scars was proving almost as painful as getting them in the first place. Was like reopening the wounds once again. 

“Do you remember what I told you about your grandmother? When you asked why she couldn’t come to grandparents’ day at school?” 

He nods. “You said that she was dead like Mom’s parents, but that I shouldn’t feel sad about her because she was mean anyway.”

“Yes.” She opens her eyes again, forcing herself to look at him. “She did it when I got in trouble. Way, way back when I was still little like you.” 

His eyes pool with confusion and distress in equal measure. “But…you and Mom don’t do that.” 

“No,” Agatha vehemently agrees. “And we never, ever, ever would,” she promises. “You don’t have to worry about that. Not ever, do you understand? No matter what you do, nobody will ever raise a hand or anything else to you." 

He nods a little, relieved by this, though concern is still etched into his features. “Why wouldn’t she just send you to timeout?” he asks, voice small. 

Agatha shrugs a shoulder and gives him a sad smile. “I guess she thought I was really, really bad,” she says quietly.

“But she wasn’t,” Rio firmly cuts in. “Her mom was the one who was really, really bad. Your mom was just a kid — she didn’t deserve it. No one does.”

Nicky nods in fervent agreement, a few tears shaking loose. “You’re not bad, Mama.”

Agatha can’t manage to swallow down this sob, it leaving her throat without her consent. She covers her mouth as if that’ll change anything. 

“You’re not bad,” Nicky says again, shifting so he’s hugging her tight. 

“Okay,” she whispers, carding her fingers through his locks. 

“You’re not,” he insists. 

“Yes, I heard you.” 

“But you don’t believe me.” 

To disagree would be to lie, and that’s how they ended up here in the first place. So she tells him a truth instead. “I want to, honey. I want to."

Rio moves her hand up to Agatha’s shoulder, giving it a comforting squeeze.

Agatha takes another shuddering inhale, giving her a nod of thanks. “Do you have any more questions right now?” she asks Nicky. 

Please say no, please say no, please say—

“Yes.” 

Fuck. 

“All right. What is it?” 

He pulls his head away from her stomach, tilting his chin to look up at her. “How do I make you not hurt anymore?” 

Her heart simultaneously aches and feels like it’s going to burst from her chest. “You want to know a secret, my love?” she whispers. He nods, eyes wide and curious. “You already do. Just by being my baby. Just by being you. Every single day.” She places a kiss on his nose. 

“You promise?” 

“I promise. I don’t want you to worry about me, okay?” She pokes his chest gently. “It’s my job to take care of you — not the other way around.” 

“But someone should take care of you, too, since your mama didn’t.”

“That’s why your mom has other adults in her life who can help,” Rio explains.

“Like you?” Nicky asks.

Rio opens her mouth. Shuts it. Then opens it again. “That’s up to her,” she admits, avoiding eye contact with Agatha. “I can’t make her pick anyone, including me. She has to want that.”

“She wants that,” he assures her before looking back at his mother. “Right, Mama?” 

Agatha purses her lips before giving a small nod, avoiding eye contact as well. “Right,” she quietly confirms.

Rio responds by giving Agatha’s shoulder another squeeze before lying back down.

“You’re going to sleep?” Nicky frowns. 

“She’s had a long day,” Agatha tells him. 

“So did I, but I’m not tired anymore. And I already took a long, long nap just like you said.” 

“You did,” she agrees with a nod. “Tell you what, why don’t the two of us go get some dinner and that ice cream I promised you and let Ms. Rio rest by herself for a bit?” 

“Four scoops and whipped cream and sprinkles?” 

“That is what I agreed to.”

“Okay.” 

Agatha turns to Rio. “What do you want us to bring you back? And, no, I will not take ‘nothing’ for an answer.”

Rio chews on her lip for a moment, ultimately deciding she’s too tired to fight her on the subject. “Pasta? And some garlic bread?”

“You got it,” she promises. Chicken parm, she decides. She’d get her chicken parm on a bed of spaghetti noodles. She’d seemed to enjoy that the other night. 

Agatha stands up and helps lower Nicky to the ground, awkwardly hovering by the bed for a moment before leaning down and planting a light, uncharacteristically domestic kiss on Rio’s cheek. “Back soon,” she vows, turning and walking out the door before she can react.

The sun is setting by the time the two of them return. The first hour is spent at dinner, the second getting ice cream and eating it on the beach, and the third indulging Nicky with a dip in the hotel pool despite the fact that he had not only not waited the recommended 30 minutes after eating to swim but had shoved a truly impressive-slash-ludicrous amount of dessert into his tiny body. 

The fourth hour is spent doing…well, a notably less enjoyable activity — one Rio gets informed of immediately upon their return, Agatha's mouth flattened into a thin, agitated line as she holds her phone out to her. 

“My ex called,” she tells her. “She’s demanding to speak with you.”

Chapter End Notes

Thank you all so much for 50k hits! 🥹🫶 That is, as Kathryn Hahn would say, bananas. We love hearing your thoughts, feelings, predictions, memes, etc. in the comments. 👀

Coming up next time: Wanda. (Who wants to place bets on how reliable of a narrator Agatha has been when it comes to her?)

Chapter 33: Day 5, Part 12

Chapter Summary

Rio and Wanda talk.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Oh.” Rio blinks, a little taken aback. This is…not what she expected, but then again, no part of this vacation had been. No part of her life, really, has been what she anticipated for herself growing up, for better (Agatha) and for far, far worse (Thanos). “Okay.”

“I’m sorry — I tried.” Agatha sighs as Rio takes the phone from her. “Trust me, I tried. The bitch insisted.” 

“I can still hear you!” Wanda yells from the other end of the line. 

Agatha leans forward so her mouth is closer to the receiver. “Good!”

“It’s okay, Agatha,” Rio reassures her, though she’s not entirely sure that it is. She’s startled and woefully unprepared for this conversation, but she can’t handle witnessing another argument right now.

“I’m Wanda,” the woman greets once the phone is to Rio’s ear. “Agatha’s ex-wife. Which I’m sure you’ve figured out, but it felt rude not to say. Could you do me a favor and tell her not to eavesdrop? She’s not going to listen to me if I ask, and I want to have an actual conversation with you without her butting in every two seconds with some snarky commentary.”

She’d really rather not do this alone, but Wanda admittedly does make a decent point — she can’t imagine a world in which this talk is even remotely productive with Agatha involved. Rio gives a little nod, feeling stupid when she realizes Wanda obviously can’t see it, and glances up. “Could you not listen in?”

Agatha immediately opens her mouth to argue, but Rio cuts her off before she can with a firm, “Agatha. Please. I got this.”

Agatha closes her mouth and contemplates for a long moment. “Fine,” she reluctantly relents. “Fine. I’ll be in the living room with Nicky, no doubt being roped into watching some boring nature documentary, if you need me.” She leans in closer to the phone. “You better not act like a psychotic bitch!” she warns. 

“Don’t worry — those are both your specialties!” Wanda yells back. 

“Ginger cunt!” 

“I went blonde, like, two years ago!”

Agatha bares her teeth and hisses before rapidly switching gears to give Rio a sympathetic look and leaving the room. 

“Sorry you had to hear that,” Wanda apologizes. “I’d say I must be making a terrible first impression, but I’m sure Agatha already took care of that — painted quite the picture of me.”

“She…has,” Rio confesses, unable to think of a good reason to come up with a lie that Wanda almost certainly wouldn’t believe anyway. “But I take things like that with a grain of salt.”

“That’s…refreshing,” she admits, a trace of surprise evident in her tone. “Agatha’s a very good talker. She has a talent for making people fall under her spell when she wants to.”

“I’m sure.” And she is. Rio has absolutely no doubt about that. It had happened to her, after all. But it wasn’t that simple. Agatha — she wasn’t that simple. “I feel like I can see through her, though,” she adds.

“Hm,” Wanda hums, clearly skeptical, though she quickly moves on, evidently not wanting to risk detonating that particular bomb of a topic at the moment. “You’re probably wondering how I even know about you.”

“News reports combined with Nicky?” Rio guesses.

“Facebook post, actually,” Wanda corrects. Rio can practically hear the suspicious narrowing of her eyes across the telephone line. “You and Agatha in a blurry photo attached to some fundraiser someone forwarded me. Nicky didn’t say a word until I whipped out my mom voice today and forced it out of him, which I’m really not thrilled about. She shouldn’t be encouraging him to keep secrets from me.”

“I agree with that much,” Rio concedes, “but I’ve been a little preoccupied with almost being murdered.” She can’t help the smallest bit of frustration that creeps out. Had everyone forgotten what she’d been through? Had it not absolved her from being unable to perfectly solve everyone else’s more trivial problems?

Wanda’s tone prickles to match hers as she retorts, “And murdering?” 

It’s not the first time someone had thrown that word around — reacted like that — but it punches Rio in the gut all the same. She wonders if blaming, minimizing comments like that will always sting this badly or if she will eventually grow numb to them like she did with Thanos over the course of all those hellish years. 

Wanda speaks again before she can respond. “I’m sorry.” She sighs. “That was uncalled for.”

Yes, it sure the fuck was. And despite the apology, Rio isn’t ready to let it go that easily. Rio is tired of letting shit go so easily.

“It was also inaccurate,” she points out. “I’m a lawyer, and legally, what I did was acting in self-defense.”

“I’m not arguing that it wasn’t.”

“Really? Because it kind of sounds like that’s exactly what you were doing.”

“No,” Wanda says, and Rio thinks she can detect some genuine shame and remorse in her voice. “Agatha filled me in, and it...seemed like she was being honest for once in her life. So I get why you did it. It must have been horrifying, going through all that. Truly.”

“Oh.” Rio blinks again, caught off guard by Wanda for the second time in the span of five minutes. “Sorry. I’m…getting used to people not believing me.”

“Well, that’s awful.”

That’s putting it pretty fucking mildly, she thinks. “It is,” she says.

Wanda clears her throat. “My son…my son has also been through a lot of awful.”

Rio has a pretty good idea of where this is headed, so she stays quiet, waiting for her to continue.

“Between hospital visits and the divorce, things haven't been…easy for him, you know? He’s endured so much — far more than a child his age should have had to — and the last thing I would want is to introduce more stress and confusion and chaos into his life.”

Yup. There it was.

“I can assure you that’s not my intention,” Rio promises as patiently as she can manage. “I have nothing but empathy for what he’s been through.”

“And I appreciate that.” Wanda pauses, seemingly choosing her words carefully. “But things don’t always go according to plan. All the empathy in the world won’t keep him from being exposed to this — by being affected. Can you understand where I’m coming from?”

Rio can’t help but soften a little at that. Of course, she could understand wanting to protect Nicky. She’d been doing just that since the first time she met him, when he was a scared, lost boy wandering the beach without his mother. 

“I do,” Rio confirms. “But no one has said anything beyond what a six- or seven-year-old should know or comprehend.”

“Six,” Wanda says. “You had it right the first time — he’s only six.” 

It’s undeniably a bit petty, but Rio decides to let it go this time. “Basically, he knows that someone hurt me and that I fought back. That’s all.”

Rio hears Wanda scrape a hand through her hair. “What happens when he starts having nightmares about some monster hurting him? What happens when one of the kids at school gets wind of this fundraiser or sees something on the news and starts asking him questions that aren’t age-appropriate? What happens when he gets called to testify as a witness in your case?”

Rio rubs a hand across her face, choosing not to risk revealing that the first one of her concerns had already come to fruition. “Kids will be kids no matter what,” she says instead. “All I can control is what I tell him, which, again, I can assure you has never crossed any kind of line and never will. As I said, I’m a lawyer, and the chances of him being subpoenaed are low.”

“Low is not the same as impossible, especially in a case this high-profile,” Wanda counters. “And I don’t want him dragged into a media circus that, frankly, feels a bit inevitable.”

Rio sighs, already exhausted by the circle they seemed to be starting to go in. “I don’t have all the answers,” she admits. “I wish I did. I wish more than anything that this weren’t happening. I care about your son, and the last thing I would ever want to do is hurt him."

“Well…I’m glad we can agree on that.” She takes a deep breath. “Look, I’m not dumb enough to try to threaten you and Agatha into ending things. God knows nobody tells Agatha what to do, least of all me.”

Rio forces herself to refrain from breathing a sigh of relief. There was always another shoe somewhere just waiting to drop. “That’s true.”

“Plus, telling her she can’t do something all but guarantees she’s going to. She's fueled by spite.”

“I can tell.”

Wanda’s voice gets that narrowed-eye quality to it again. “But you’re still drawn to her,” she observes.

“Yes,” Rio says simply, once again seeing no reason to deny something fairly obvious.

There’s a long, long beat of silence before Wanda speaks again. “Do you love her?”

There’s an even longer beat before Rio replies. “I don’t know,” she lies. “I think so,” she tries again. Yeah. Yeah, that feels more truthful. That feels more honest than she’s ever been about something, and she’s surprised by just how much it hurts — how raw it makes her feel. “I care about her a lot, but that’s too big a question for me to answer at the moment. To answer so soon.”

It’s a ‘yes’ with more fear and hesitation — more words and technicalities — and they both know it. 

Wanda grows quiet once more before she speaks again. “I loved her, too,” she admits, voice tinged with sadness. With her own exhaustion. “Which is why I need you to promise you’ll be careful. I know she seems very exciting, but you’re very…fragile right now. And I don’t say that to infantilize you — you’re clearly a strong, intelligent woman — I…” She takes a deep breath. “I know what it’s like is all. When Agatha Harkness swoops in when you’re at your most vulnerable and sucks you into her orbit. When she turns your entire world upside down before you even realize it’s happening.”

“I know,” Rio says softly. She knows what that’s like in the most extreme, terrible sense with Thanos — knows the signs now, even if it took nearly dying to develop that hindsight. “I’m sorry things ended so poorly between you.”

“Thanks,” Wanda says, her tone sincere. “You think I’d be used to things falling apart by now — my parents died when I was young, then I miscarried twins with my high school sweetheart before he died, too — but…” She breathes out a small, humorless laugh. “God. Sorry. I don’t know what on earth possessed me to tell you that. This whole situation is…odd.”

“It’s all right — I don’t mind.” And she doesn’t. She’s even a little grateful for the more complete picture Wanda is offering her. The gaps Agatha had left that she’s filling in. Rio has always valued information, found comfort in knowledge and figuring out the rules of people. “I’m sorry you went through all of that.”

“Thanks,” she repeats, voice thicker with emotion now. “I could never…get her to do that with me, you know? Open up? Sometimes, I felt like I caught glimpses of her, but I don’t think I ever saw the whole thing.” Wanda sniffles. “It’s not like I’m so great at it either, but I tried with her. I tried really hard for a really long time.”

“I can imagine,” Rio sympathizes. “She’s a tough nut to crack, not to mention chock-full of self-loathing and bravado.”

“‘Tough nut to smash,’” Wanda quotes. “She insisted that’s what the phrase was — I’m fairly certain just to piss me off. Not even close to the stupidest thing we ever argued about, mind you. I think she enjoyed it,” she bitterly recalls. “Got off on it in some twisted way.” She sighs again before continuing. “And yeah, I know, ‘When you're born in a burning house, you think the whole world is on fire,’ but I tried so many times to hand her a hose, only for her to turn it on full blast and spray me in the face with it. It’s almost like she wanted the flames to consume her.”

“I think part of that is the self-loathing,” Rio reasons. “That doesn’t excuse how she hurt you, but I know people like her. She’s so scared of what it means to heal and make peace with her trauma that she indulges in self-harming behavior — the kind where she yells and screams and pushes people away.”

“I know that. I do,” Wanda responds, the slightest bit defensive. “I was with her for years — I know that better than anyone.” The small edge in her tone dissipates, leaving nothing but sad surrender in its wake. “I just…I had hope that eventually, not everything would end in a fight. That eventually — after bending over backwards time and time again to earn her trust — she would lean into me instead. That eventually, I would be enough for her.”

Perhaps it’s strange, but Rio finds herself feeling some sort of compassion for her girlfriend’s (was Agatha even technically, officially her girlfriend?) ex-wife. Finds herself saying “I’m sorry” and meaning it.

“It is what it is,” Wanda replies with another small sniffle. “Anyway, I just wanted you to know I’m not a monster. I’m a mother, and I would do absolutely anything for my son, including unpleasant things like suing my ex-wife for custody when she’s unable to properly care for him and vetting the random women she allows to sleep next to him without so much as consulting or even informing me.”

The comment hits her in the stomach again, though this time, it’s more from worry than annoyance, her face growing hot with nerves and a smidge of shame. She probably did look like something of a monster from Wanda’s perspective. The first things she learned about Rio, after all, were that she was sneaking around with her ex-wife and son and that she had ended someone’s life. “I’m sorry,” she repeats. “I never meant to hurt anyone.”

Her voice must be dripping with anxiety, as Wanda softens. “Hey,” she says. “It’s okay. My frustration lies with Agatha and her increasingly selfish, irresponsible choices — not with you.” A beat. “Are you okay?” she asks more gently still. "As I said, I know these circumstances are strange and that Agatha is not a particularly easy person, and that's without all the other...complications you're dealing with."

Rio’s not sure what compels her to be so forthcoming, but she finds herself telling the truth again. “I’m so fucking tired,” she confesses, breathing out a humorless laugh. “I don’t think I can do this much longer.”

“Do…what exactly? Be with Agatha? Because if that’s the case, you should cut it off now before you’re in too deep with her. And before Nicky is in too deep with you. I don’t want him getting…attached if you don’t plan on sticking around.”

The burning in her face turns from apprehension to irritation. “For fuck’s sake, no," she snaps. "It’s not about Agatha. It’s not about Nicky. It’s about my fucking life. Agatha would kill me for this, but I just want to die. I just want this all to go away. I think maybe everyone would be better off if I were dead. I know it’d sure as hell be easier for me.”

There’s another long, long beat of silence — long enough for Rio to start catching her breath again after her unexpected rant and grow increasingly mortified for baring her soul to this stranger. One who was already primed to hate her. 

How could she be so fucking stupid? Agatha was terrified that Wanda was going to try to use the situation to take Nicky from her. By spilling the fact that she was suicidal, she’d offered her ammunition on a silver fucking platter. She has the ironic urge to slam her head into the bedpost.

But Wanda surprises her for a third time when she finally speaks again. “Got it,” she says, voice soft. “I apologize. I misunderstood.” 

There’s yet another stretch of quiet, then — longer still — before she continues. “I made…an attempt once,” Wanda admits. It’s clear from her voice that this is a subject she doesn’t talk about much. Doesn’t talk about ever, maybe. “After the miscarriage and my husband…” she trails off before clearing her throat. “So I won’t pretend to know exactly how you feel, but I know how that feels. That emptiness. That loneliness. That…endless nothingness. It’s like being crushed under a mountain.” 

Wanda takes a deep breath. “For what it’s worth — which may not be much considering I don’t really know you, and you don’t really know me — I don’t think anyone would be better off. I already know two people certainly wouldn’t. Nicky seems to adore you, and I’ve…I’ve never heard Agatha talk about someone the way she talked about you.” There’s a bittersweetness to the revelation that makes Rio ache in a way she can’t quite comprehend.

Rio sucks in sharply, tears pricking at her eyes. For once, someone hadn’t told her to stop. Hadn’t berated her for the urge. Had tried to understand. 

“I don’t know if I ever actually could,” Rio admits. “Even outside of Agatha and Nicky, I know my dad would be devastated. I’m just—” She pauses, taking another shaky inhale. “Everything feels so hard. I’m having to relearn how to live because I let some fucker abuse me for almost a decade. Everything hurts.”

“Abuse isn’t something that someone invites or allows,“ Wanda gently points out. “And as someone who’s had to relearn how to live four times — and that’s a conservative estimate — it is hard. And it does hurt. Some days, it might hurt even worse than it does right now,” she confesses. “But you know what? Some days, it’ll hurt a little less. And some rare, fleeting, tiny moments, it won’t even hurt at all. You have to live for those. You have to keep living for those,” she says, voice almost soothing. “You know?”

“I’m scared that he’s broken me,” Rio finds herself whispering.

“He may have broken parts,” Wanda concedes. “But they’re not beyond repair. You can always figure out how to piece yourself back together.”

Rio purses her lips. “I want to try,” she promises. “But like I said, I’m so tired.” A pause. “Does that part get better?”

“In my experience — which I know is not exactly your experience — yes, it does. Eventually, the exhaustion won’t feel so bone-deep and persistent — so all-consuming. But there’s only one way to find out, right?”

“I suppose so,” Rio relents. She’s not quite sold, but maybe she’s getting there. Perhaps she will be able to get there. “Right now, it’s all just so heavy.”

“Listen, why don’t you…take my number?” Wanda suggests, a little awkward but sincere. “Maybe I can help you…learn to carry it. Somehow. If you’d want that. It’d probably be smart for you to have it anyway if you’re going to be spending time with Agatha and Nicky.”

“Yeah. Yeah, okay.” Rio nods despite once again knowing Wanda can’t see. The action is just for her — a motion to help her process all of this. She was still learning how to do that — things for her own sake and no one else’s. “I think that would be…nice.”

“Please use it, all right? If you feel like you want to give up and you don’t feel like you can talk to anyone else...” she trails off again. “Just promise that you’ll use it if you need, okay? I wish…I wish someone had told me the same back then.”

“Thank you,” she responds after a moment. “I…I really appreciate that.”

“Be good to Nicky,” Wanda says, voice serious but not exactly threatening.

“I will.” 

“And Rio?” she adds, tone softening considerably. “Make Agatha be good to you.”

“I will,” she repeats, quieter this time. “I will.”

Chapter End Notes

Shoutout to Reneé Rapp’s “That’s So Funny” for helping me unlock Wanda in this story. 🫡

Coming up next time: Agatha tries to be romantic. (It goes about as well as you’d expect.)

Chapter 34: Day 5, Part 13

Chapter Summary

Agatha tries to be romantic. (It goes about as well as you’d expect.)

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Nicky falls asleep within five minutes of the nature documentary, so he either finds it as dull as Agatha does or is as tired as Rio is. Agatha conveniently decides to take this as a sign from the universe, concocting a plan to eavesdrop as she carries him to bed. Considering Rio and Ginger Bitch took precautions to avoid this, the solution she comes up with is, unfortunately, imperfect. Which is to say she’s standing with her ear to the door like she’s in some ridiculous sitcom. 

Wanda used to love those stupid shows. She still loves those stupid shows, probably, not that Agatha gives a shit. She’d indulged her by watching them with her on occasion, during that sliver of time when they were still something resembling happy together, even though the inane laugh tracks and caring parents and cheerful children pissed Agatha off. The Disney movies Evanora would put on for her on the rare, rare occasion she was in a halfway decent mood — the ones about talking animals and fairy godmothers — seemed to her less far-fetched.

The door’s thickness does not make it easy — or frequently possible — to hear the actual words Rio is saying to Wanda, but she can tell when she’s talking, as well as when she stops. She wants to swing it open the millisecond that happens, but she forces herself to have the smallest bit of restraint. It would frighten Rio, probably — her barging in like that. Plus, it would make her seem anxious about the prospect of her ex-wife and current…Rio having a conversation.

Which she is. Obviously. It sort of makes her want to throw up. Again.

But Agatha had admitted to far too much fear already today — so much so that her body seemed to be literally, physically rejecting that, too. Agatha could pound back round after round of shots like it was nothing, put every drug in the world into her body and be, more or less, fine. But the moment an emotion entered her system? The second she had to, even worse, talk about said feeling? Oh, it made her feel positively terminal.

So Agatha knocks, and Rio responds with a “Hm?” which she takes as an invitation to push the door open. 

“Did she act like an uptight, holier-than-thou, morally superior twat?”

“No.” Rio shakes her head. “She was…” Ever the attorney, she searches for the perfect word. “Respectful.”

“Oh.” Agatha blinks, flooded with surprise and relief and…something else she can’t quite name but that doesn’t feel very pleasant. Feels like a wound, either to her pride or her heart or both. “Well. Good, then.”

“Yeah. She was…kind, actually,” Rio adds. Agatha’s sure it’s meant to reassure her, but it feels like she’s pouring salt in.

“You don’t already like her better than me, do you?” she jokes, hoping the real, underlying insecurity to it is undetectable. Everyone tended to like Wanda better. She had all this natural power over people, and she didn’t even have to work at it. Didn’t even have to try. Barely even used it for anything worthwhile. It all came so easily to her in a way Agatha could never comprehend. It was fascinating and infuriating and intoxicating and fucking bullshit.

“I’m not comparing you two. I see no reason to do that.” And Agatha’s sure this is meant to reassure her, too, but it feels like she’s kneading the salt in further.

Agatha doesn’t want to settle for being on the same level as Wanda. She wants to be better. She wants to be the best. She wants to be… 

She wants to be good. Good enough for Rio to choose her confidently and without hesitation. 

But she doesn’t know how to voice any of that without sounding pathetic or bitter or both. Without making herself sick or accidentally starting another argument or forcing Rio into giving her more undeserved reassurance when she had made it pretty clear she was in no position to do any more of that today. 

So she doesn’t, simply nodding and crossing her arms protectively over her chest. “Good, then,” she repeats.

Rio raises a brow, looking at her for a long, long moment. “I like you, Agatha,” she finally says. “I want you — in ways I don’t like or want her or anybody else.”

Agatha’s sure it’s meant to reassure her, and it does. But it’s also…disconcerting — the way Rio is able to read her.

Then again, Rio had used that power not to hurt her but to help her — to tell her what she needed to hear. That realization sort of makes Agatha want to cry, but that would probably be pathetic, too, and besides, she doesn’t think she has any tears left after today, so she doesn’t do that either. 

Instead, she clears her throat and walks the rest of the way into the room. “You need to eat,” she says, handing her the takeout box of chicken parmesan. “There’s some ice cream in the freezer, too. If you want. That’s optional, but this isn’t — at least half of it.”

Rio takes the box without breaking her gaze, which is intent and lawyerly. “You can’t avoid what I’m saying. Avoidance builds resentment.”
