Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The doctors give Rio the go-ahead for the shark outing with the caveat that she is to be carefully bandaged before submerging her leg and extremely cautious during the whole activity. Which, no shit. Agatha makes sure to thank them with more than a little sarcasm for their brilliant expertise.

She plans to call and reserve a slot a little after lunch while Rio gets ready, but she finds herself phoning someone else first. 

“Lilia,” she greets once she hears the woman pick up.

“Well, if it isn’t my least favorite criminal,” Lilia replies.

“Aww, you’re gonna make me blush. I’d say you’re my least favorite centenarian, but I think you’re the only one I know — not many people are lucky enough to live into their hundreds,” she shoots back. She smirks as she hears the undeniable sound of clinking plates and scraping forks in the background. “How was your dinner date with your ‘dashing gentlewoman’? Are you still on it? Have you been at the restaurant with her all night? Oh, Lilia — you absolute trollop.”

“What do you want?”

She’s half-tempted to press about the mysterious shuffleboard woman, but she doesn’t want Lilia to get the impression she actually cares. (Because she doesn’t. Obviously.) 

Just like she obviously doesn’t actually care about Lilia’s approval when she tells her, “I talked to Nicky last night. About Mommy Dearest. Like I said I would. Just so you know.”

“Oh?” Lilia says, surprise evident even in the single syllable. “Good for you.”

Agatha scoffs, vaguely offended. “You thought I wouldn’t do it.”

“Yes,” she bluntly responds. “You’re a notorious coward in the emotions department.”

“Well, I talked to Rio, too,” she adds. She sounds petulant, which she hates, but she’s telling Lilia how wrong she is, which she loves. “Last night and this morning. About my stupid feelings. So put that in your pipe and smoke it."

“I don't feel ashamed for voicing my opinion of you,” Lilia retorts, tone almost bored. “Especially when it’s right on the money.”

“Um, no? I’m proving how incorrect your perception of me is with a plethora of extremely compelling evidence. Exhibits A, B, and fucking C. Rio would back me — and she’s a lawyer.”

“You sound like a child,” Lilia dryly points out.

“Everyone sounds like a child when you’re ancient,” she snaps back in a rather lame retort. It was difficult to truly rile Lilia up — to engage in a satisfying argument with her — a fact that got under Agatha’s skin in a uniquely irritating way.

“I assume you didn’t call me just to tell me you spoke to your son.”

She…sort of did, though that felt like too complicated a thing to explain.

Or maybe it wasn’t. Maybe it was just your run-of-the-mill raging mommy issues. A subconscious craving to demonstrate to herself that yes, actually, she was capable of not being a total fucking disappointment and yes, actually, she could make someone like that proud.

Maybe it was actually extremely fucking simple to explain, but it was definitely far too mortifying a thing to admit to, so Agatha does what she does best and lies. “Nicky wants to see how you fare in shark-infested waters.”

“No, thank you,” Lilia politely and firmly declines.

“It's not optional."

“I’ll babysit or go to an aquarium all day, but I will not be getting in the water with sharks.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “You’re being a baby. My six-year-old is doing it. So is Rio, and she has a bruised neck and a fucked-up leg.”

“All right,” Lilia replies, unfazed. “If that’s all, I have a spa appointment to get to.”

“You’re really going to break my little boy’s heart?” she asks, laying the guilt on as thick as she can.

“For a deep tissue massage?” Lilia deadpans. “Yes. I’ll see you later.”

“Lilia,” she says, forcing her name out through gritted teeth before she can hang up. God, she was really going to make her say it, wasn’t she? “Please.” Ew. “I…would also…like you to come.” Disgusting.

There’s a long beat of silence. “Oh?” Lilia repeats, voice somehow even more shocked than before.

“Are you calling me a liar?” she snaps. Then, before she can answer, “Don’t answer that. Yes. Okay? Yes.” She needs a buffer. And a babysitter. She wasn't confident she could properly handle both Rio and Nicky's needs on her own, and it’s not like she had a plethora of suitable options.

There’s a slightly shorter pause as she considers. “I’ll come along,” she finally agrees. “But I’m not getting in the water.”

“Afraid you’ll melt?” Agatha quips. “Wicked Witch style?”

“Goodbye, Agatha.”

The call with the shark swimming people takes a little longer than expected. She has to…persuade them to shuffle some other appointments around to accommodate a chronically ill little boy and a woman who had just suffered a horrific accident before they left the next day.

The bathroom door opens at the same time the bedroom one does, Rio and Nicky both stepping into the room. Agatha throws up her hands. “I’m being flanked! I’m being ambushed! You’ll never take me alive!”

Nicky giggles, running in and jumping into her arms. Agatha catches him, dramatically falling back onto the bed.

Rio smiles, though Agatha can sense an undercurrent of apprehension as she glances over at her. “Rio, you want to tell Nicky what we’re doing today?”

She blinks, snapping out of that dissociative daze she often seemed to fall into. “What?”

“What are we doing today, Ms. Rio?” Nicky helps.

“Oh.” She shakes her head a little as if trying to clear it. “Swimming with sharks.”

Nicky gasps and sits up straight, his face lighting up as he looks at his mother to confirm.

Agatha nods, a small smile playing on her own face. His enthusiasm was contagious. “It was Ms. Rio’s idea.”

He leaps off the bed, going to tackle her in a hug now.

Rio lets out a little ‘oof’ as Nicky barrels into her, tensing for a millisecond before wrapping her arms around him. “You’re excited, then?”

“Really, really, really excited." He bounces on the balls of his feet. "I love, love, love sharks.”

“And we are all so, so, so glad,” Agatha playfully ribs.

The corner of Rio’s mouth curves into a tiny smile. “I happen to love sharks, too.”

“Because you’re like me!” Nicky proclaims, stepping back from her embrace to look up at her. “Are we going right now?”

“Food first,” Agatha informs him. “And I have to wrap Ms. Rio’s leg.”

“Can you wrap mine, too?” Nicky asks.

Agatha gives Rio a look like, ‘See? Told you so.’ “Sure. You can be my guinea pig.”

“I want to be a rabbit instead.”

“All right.” Agatha nods. “My test bunny. Hopefully, PETA hasn’t bugged this room, or we’re in a world of trouble.”

“I’ll go clean mine off while you do that,” Rio says, nodding toward the bathroom.

“I’ll help,” Agatha offers as she sits up on the bed, voice casual but leaving no real room to turn her down. 

“And I’ll hold your hand,” Nicky volunteers. “So it’ll hurt less.”

Rio forces her mouth into another smile, though this one doesn’t quite reach her eyes. “That’s sweet of you both, but I’ll be okay.”

Nicky frowns. “Do you want to hold my bunny? Like you did at the hospital?"

Rio shakes her head. “I’m all right. Promise.”

Agatha’s eyes flit between them a few times. “Nicky, why don’t you go get dressed, brush your teeth, call your—“ Ugh, she hates that she was suggesting this. Again. “—mom while I help Ms. Rio.” 

“I already did my teeth,” Nicky insists, eyes drifting to the left. 

Agatha narrows her own in response, reaching forward and grabbing his chin. “Breathe,” she orders. 

He sucks in an inhale through his nose. 

“Out,” she sternly clarifies. “Through your mouth.” 

He reluctantly does so, and Agatha sniffs before wrinkling her nose and letting go of his face. “Liar. Brush.”

“But the toothpaste is yucky,” he whines. 

“Trust me, your breath is yuckier. Go.” 

Nicky’s shoulders slump, but he sulkily heads to his bathroom.

Rio raises her brows, shooting Agatha a questioning look. Agatha’s lift to match. “What?” she asks. “I’m not allowed to want to do some PG-rated doctor-patient roleplay with you?”

Rio drops her gaze to her shuffling feet. “It’s not that,” she quietly admits. “I’m just…still worried about it all.”

Agatha sighs. The teasing was, once again, not working, so the bluntly honest truth would have to do. “Yes, I know. And I’m worried about you. I don’t trust you not to give your calf the same treatment as your neck, and it'd be a shame to have to amputate such a beautiful leg."

“I'm trying, Agatha. I really am."

“I know you’re trying. I’m trying, too — to help you. Aren’t you the one who’s always telling me there’s no shame in accepting it?” She wishes it felt more cathartic, throwing Rio’s own words back in her face, but mostly, she just feels mortifyingly incompetent. She must be doing something wrong for Rio to reject her assistance.

“It’s not that I don’t want to,” Rio swears, risking a glance up at her. “There’s just this…nagging feeling that I don’t deserve your help, and it’s making me push back. But I don’t mean to push you.”

There’s a beat as Agatha searches Rio’s face, finding nothing but sincerity there. So much sincerity, in fact, that it gets to be too much for her now. She looks down at her hands, picking at a hangnail. “I get that,” she quietly confesses. “I mean, obviously, you know firsthand just how much I get that.”

Rio takes a deep breath. “What if we compromise?”

Agatha’s eyes flick back up. “Go on…”

“I’ll wrap my own leg, but you can sit in there with me and make sure it all goes okay.”

Agatha slowly nods, the pieces falling into place. “You don’t want to be touched,” she says. A statement — not a question. “Do you.”

Rio purses her lips. “Not right now.”

That awful, gnawing feeling — the one that told Agatha she was a failure — intensifies tenfold. “Then you can tell me that, Rio,” she vows, undercurrents of desperation and exasperation both simmering under her words. “I need you to know that you can just tell me that, point-blank. I know that I’m pushy and bossy and horny, but I’m never going to do that unless you want me to — whether that means fingering you to your fifth orgasm in a row or just holding your fucking hand."

“Okay,” Rio whispers, biting her lip now. “I’m sorry. I’m just…conditioned to people being upset when I say what I want.”

“I know.” She pinches the bridge of her nose. “But I need you to know that I’m not going to do that. And I really, really need you to stop apologizing for this shit — because that actually does upset me.” She looks at her sternly. “Do not respond to that with another apology.”

Rio sucks in an inhale but miraculously resists the urge to ask forgiveness once more. “Logically, I think I do. But every time I try to advocate for myself, my stomach drops about 10 feet to my ass.”

She squints, scanning her up and down. “Your stomach to your ass is only, like, a foot and a half. You're short."

The comment earns her an eye roll. “It’s called hyperbole. I’m attempting to make a point.”

“I’m aware. I’m attempting to lighten the mood.” Agatha reaches out to take Rio’s hands instinctively, abruptly dropping them back to her sides. “Sorry. No touching.”

“Hand is okay,” Rio permits. “Just nothing else.”

She nods and reaches up again, gently clasping one in her own. “What if you compromise with me now?”

The space between Rio’s brow creases. “How do you mean?”

“What’s the stupidest, silliest, most outrageous word you can think of?”

The line on her forehead deepens. “I’m not sure…”

Agatha sighs. “It’s not a test, Rio. There’s no wrong answer. Just tell me the first thing that comes to your mind. I, for instance, might say ‘flaccid.’"

“Um…” Rio blinks a few times. “Squamous,” she settles on.

“I don’t know what the hell that means.”

“It’s a biology term that has to do with—”

Agatha waves her off. “Doesn’t matter. It’s perfect. Every time you want to say ‘sorry,’ you’re going to say ‘squamous’ instead.”

The crease between her brows grows deeper still. “Why?”

“Because I know you can’t quit serial apologizing cold turkey, but you can replace it with something else. Think of it as a verbal nicotine patch.” Agatha didn't believe in those and wouldn’t give up her beloved cigarettes even if she did, but that was beside the point. “Still scratches enough of that itch while weaning yourself off the habit. The fact that the word is humorous to you should make it feel less serious — lower stakes.”

The look on Rio’s face is vaguely Lady and the Tramp situation-esque, which is really not Agatha’s favorite, but at least she verbally replies with lukewarm agreement in the form of, “I’ll…try, I suppose.”

“If you mess up, you have to say one nice thing about yourself,” she adds. A beat. “And one nice thing about me, just because.”

Rio cringes at the mere thought. “I don’t know about that.”

“Okay, fine — forget the part about me. You can just affirm yourself.”

“Let’s just start with the word thing, okay?”

Agatha shakes her head. "You need to recognize something you like about yourself if you forget to do that, though. I guess saying something you hate about him instead could also work…but there needs to be some kind of productive association to help change the behavior.” 

Rio gives her a skeptical look. “I thought you didn’t believe in therapy.”

She holds up her palms. “Oh, god — I don’t,” she defends. “But I have been forced to go to a few shrinks in my day. And while I think most of what they say is a crock of shit, I do know the power of both vanity and spite.”

Rio’s suspicious expression morphs into something more vulnerable and pleading. “I can’t change everything overnight.”

Agatha huffs out a breath. “Have I not made it clear that I don’t expect you to?” She seemed to be hitting a wall. And while she was doing her damnedest to fucking scale it — to not just knock it over like she normally would — it doesn’t particularly feel like Rio’s eager to throw her any rope to help her up the stupid thing.

Because she doesn’t trust her? Probably, that was at least somewhat true, even if it was unconscious on Rio’s part. And probably, she was smart not to, as loath as Agatha was to admit it.

Had she given Wanda rope on the phone last night? Was she already higher on the wall than her despite only beginning the climb hours ago?

The thought makes her feel inadequate and demoralized enough to continue explaining — to try to salvage a conversation it feels like she’s somehow already tanked despite her greatest efforts. “I’m trying to give you small, actionable steps.”

“I know,” Rio recognizes. “But these are patterns that I’ve spent years of my life adhering to.”

“Right. Yes.” She’s trying so hard not to let any of the frustration — aimed mostly at herself, of course, though Rio almost surely wouldn’t read it that way — seep through. “And I’m trying to help you break them.”

“All the little behavior changes in the world won’t truly fix anything until I actually heal.”

“But the two things go together and are meant to help you heal by—" Shut up, Agatha, a voice in her head stops her — one that sounds dangerously similar to the one she’d heard during her breakdown in the aquarium. Just shut the fuck up and walk away from the wall. What the hell do you know about healing anyway? About helping? About anything like this? You’re only embarrassing yourself here. You’re only making it worse. Like you always do. “Okay,” she relents. “Okay, fine. Let’s just…wrap your leg.”

“I do appreciate what you’re doing.”

Agatha purses her lips, nods her head — any encouragement falling on deaf ears as Rio’s voice is drowned out by the one in her brain. “Okay.”

“And I appreciate how much you care.”

“Good.” 

“I think it’s just…too much pressure right now. I need to take things slower.”

“I get it,” she mumbles. And just like last night, she’s positive that Rio is trying to help her, but it hurts in a way she despises. Agatha was always too fast, too aggressive, too much — and somehow, it all added up to never being enough. 

She desperately needs a distraction — an action to help her pretend that wasn't the case — and takes Rio's hand again, tugging her toward the bathroom. “Leg.”

Chapter End Notes

trickofthelights suggested that this version of Lilia is probably retired mafia, and that's canon to me. That makes the most sense of anything ever. I need you all to know that.

We've done a little outlining, and we're probably looking at four or so more chapters! 🫶

Chapter 37: Day 6, Part 3

Chapter Summary

Agatha tries to prove herself to Rio as crucial plans are made.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The leg wrapping is a fine (albeit quiet) affair, with Agatha still far more in her head than she’d like to be. Her head is not a particularly fun place to live most of the time, which is why she preferred to be in her body — preferred to smoke, to drink, to touch and be touched.

She supervises Rio’s very necessary bandage application before doing Nicky’s frivolous one, too — an activity he enjoys as much as opening birthday gifts and getting extra dessert after dinner. Little weirdo.

Agatha doesn’t have time to do her own, seeing as their shark swimming appointment is soon approaching and she needs to feed Nicky (and Rio, as much as she might resist it) before they go.

It must be peak brunch hour, as the buffet is packed — so packed, in fact, that she spots Eros sharing a table with Jen and Alice near the front, presumably unable to find a free place to sit. (Jen does not look thrilled by this.)

“Well, if it isn’t The Three Musketeers,” Agatha greets as she approaches.

"What?” Jen scowls.

"Three Stooges?" Agatha pitches instead. "Three Amigos? Alice and the Chipmunks?"

"At least she remembered my name this time," Alice mutters under her breath.

“We're not a trio," Jen spits. "I literally don't even know this man.”

Eros stands. “Rio,” he says, voice somehow both frantic and relieved.

“Hi,” she replies, weariness already evident in the single syllable. “What do you need?”

“You never texted me last night — about what you wanted me to tell my mom.” He looks at Agatha. “You said you’d make sure she remembered."

“Oh. Yeah.” Agatha grimaces over-dramatically, performatively sucking in some air through her teeth. “I guess, um…” She rubs the back of her neck. “I guess maybe I lied.”

Jen gives Eros a look. “Rookie move. I could’ve told you she was gonna do that.” 

Eros furrows his brows. “I thought you said you barely knew her.”

“I did,” Jen deadpans. “And I still could’ve told you she was gonna do that.”

Rio sighs, running a hand over her face. “Shut up, Jen.”

Jen puts up her palms. “You people dragged me into this — I was trying to eat my kale salad in peace.”

“Kale salad.” Agatha snorts. “My god, that is so ridiculously on the nose.”

Rio promptly ignores them both. “Eros, you’re a grown man. Why couldn’t you handle that?”

He throws his hands up. “Because she—" He gestures at Agatha. “—told me to wait until you told me what you wanted me to say, remember?”

Nicky tugs on Agatha’s hand. “Mama, what’s he talking about?”

Agatha purses her lips, looking down at him before glancing up at the table once more. “Do you mind watching him for a sec?”

“Um, yes?” Jen replies, looking at her like she’s fucking insane. “Yes, I very much mind. I thought we agreed we weren’t even going to speak again on this trip. Or ever again, for that matter.”

Agatha looks at Alice now — the bigger pushover of the two. “Just for a quick, adults-only sidebar.” She pinches one of Nicky’s cheeks. “How could you say no to this precious little face?”

Before Alice can respond, Rio steps in. “Okay, I don’t have the patience for this again, so here’s what’s going to happen. Agatha, you’re going to find a place to sit with Nicky. Eros, we’re going to talk over there.” She gestures to the back corner of the dining room. “Jen and Alice…” She refocuses her attention on the table. “Well, I don’t actually care what you do.”

“Why am I even part of this?” Jen mumbles. “How do I always somehow become part of this?”

Agatha reaches out to put a hand on Rio’s back before dropping it abruptly. She doesn’t want to be touched. She doesn’t want….Agatha? At all? Maybe?

It’s a horrible thought. And leaving Rio alone with Eros — however cordial he seemed — felt like a horrible idea, what with his inevitable communication to the WASPy Witch of the West.

Fuck, this was bad. Bad enough that she suddenly very much wishes they had already met up with Lilia so she could help.

Fuck, if that thought was crossing her mind, this was really, really bad.

Agatha leans in close to Rio’s ear. “I’m sorry — I’ll behave,” she whispers, hoping that her voice is communicating sincerity without too much pathetic desperation and panic creeping in. “I’ll set Nicky up with his iPad and a pair of those big-ass headphones. Just…please let me come with you.”

“I’ll be okay. He’s not his brother.”

The bar is in the ninth circle of hell, she thinks. “Please,” she says. “I’ll do what my mother always wanted for me and be seen and not heard — not speak unless spoken to — but let me be there for you.”

Rio blinks, turning her head to look at her. “I’m not mad at you,” she assures her. “You know that, right? I’m just trying to problem-solve.”

It’s Agatha’s turn to blink. No. No, she didn’t know that, actually. But she doesn’t really want to admit to that, so she avoids the question entirely, focusing only on the second part of what she’d said.

“I’m trying to do the same,” she promises. “At least let me supervise again, like I did with your leg.”

Rio bites her lip, contemplating. “Nicky can’t overhear any of this.”

“Of course not. They’re noise-cancelling — he won’t be able to hear shit.”

“You’re 100% sure?”

“Let’s just say I used to borrow them to wear around Ginger Bitch to piss her off, and it worked like a charm. At least, I think. I’m no expert lip reader, but it certainly looked like she was yelling curse words at me.” She can’t help but smirk a little at the memory, even despite the seriousness of the situation.

Rio switches to chewing on the inside of her cheek. “Turn him facing away from us, too. He’s very astute, and I don’t want him to pick anything up from our facial expressions.”

It’s highly unnecessary, Rio’s concern about Nicky in this situation, considering Agatha’s protectiveness toward him would have guaranteed all of these precautions anyway. And if anyone else were acting like this, she’d likely be defensive — pissed, even. Nicky was her child, after all, and she was more than capable of taking care of him.

But for some reason, Rio’s fretting makes Agatha soften instead of prickle. Touches something tender inside.

“I will strategically angle him,” she pledges.

“And you’ll keep an eye on him while we talk to make sure he stays there?” Rio checks. “I don’t want him wandering away again. He was so scared when I found him on the beach that day.”

“That was a fluke.” Agatha quirks a brow. “You’re well-acquainted with the fact that I’m a phenomenal multitasker, are you not?”

A small blush creeps into her cheeks, no doubt thinking of when she simultaneously used her tongue and fingers to do some truly mind-blowing things the other day. “Y— yes.”

“Can we—“ Eros speaks up. 

Agatha whips to face him. “The grown-ups are talking,” she snaps. “Patience is a virtue, or so I’ve heard.”

Nicky taps Agatha’s leg, impatiently shuffling. “Mama, I’m hungry.”

Agatha runs a gentle hand through his hair as she looks down at him, demeanor doing a 180 at his interruption. “I know, angel. We’re going.” She glances back up at Rio with a little nod — her silent oath that it’d be okay.

Rio nods, too, taking a deep breath. “Eros, let Agatha set Nicky up with some food, and then we’ll talk.”

“Come on,” Agatha says, jerking her head toward the back of the restaurant, slyly snatching something as she ushers them there. “We’ll sit in that corner.”

“There’s nothing free back there,” Eros says. “Trust me — I’ve checked.”

“And trust me — there will be.” 

Agatha locates the four-top with the most privacy and the easiest looking targets in the form of a Midwestern family. “‘Scuse me,” she says as she approaches, sneakily setting the object she’d lifted onto the table before tapping it a few times. “This table’s booked.”

The father looks up at her. “This one?"

"This very one."

"Are you sure?”

Agatha gestures toward the RESERVED sign she definitely hadn’t just planted here. "Yes, my teeny tiny little lady brain is positive."

“Oh, Harold — she’s right,” his wife says, patting his arm with a blush. “We’re so sorry.”

Agatha gives her a tight smile that communicates that she doesn’t quite forgive them.

“This is such bullshit,” the son grumbles as he picks up his half-empty plate, the daughter shooting a glare at Agatha as she does the same.

Agatha subtly flips them off as they retreat before locating the waiter kid a few tables away. “Hey!” she calls.

He looks over at her before frantically ducking his head and turning away.

Agatha rolls her eyes. “I know you saw me.” She snaps her fingers before pointing to the dirty table. “This needs bussed. Chop, chop.” She drops her bag on the chair before leading the group over to the buffet. 

Agatha makes good on her promise to multitask even in line, simultaneously scooping some eggs and potatoes onto her own plate, making sure that Nicky didn’t get too much pure sugar, and checking that Rio got enough of anything at all.

The waiter kid is still wiping the table off when Agatha returns, and she takes a quick, menacing step toward him — pretending she’s about to lunge. She has no plans to actually do so, but it is fun to watch him flinch.

“That’ll do.” She drops her tray on the table. “Scram.” He very eagerly complies.

Agatha reaches into her bag, rummaging around Nicky’s PEP mask, Goldfish crumbs, and a few loose cigarettes to pull out the iPad. “You want to watch some Dora?”

Nicky’s eyes grow wide. “At a restaurant?”

“Yup.”

His voice grows quiet and vaguely scandalized. “But Mom doesn’t even like it when I eat in front of the TV at home.”

“Well, she’s not here, and I’m not gonna tell her.” Agatha takes the initiative to put the headphones — adorably a little too big for him — over his ears. “Happy last day of vacation.”

“What?!” he yells.

Agatha looks at Rio. “They work,” she confirms.

“Good. Now make sure he’s completely turned away.”

“You’re just stalling at this point,” she accuses in a mumble, though she dutifully bumps the iPad with her elbow while reaching for her coffee, angling it away from the other chairs.

Nick looks up at her, puzzled.

“Sorry, buddy — accident,” she explains.

“Huh?!” he loudly asks, the idea of taking the headphones off not even crossing his mind. Thank god even the smartest kids could be a little dumb sometimes.

Agatha shakes her head as if to say, ‘Nothing,’ and points back at the screen. Nicky takes a forkful of waffle as he does so, syrup dripping down his chin and onto his shirt. Whatever.

“All right,” Agatha says, snatching a piece of bacon off of Eros’ plate.

“Hey. What the—"

“Start figuring this shit out. We have sharks to swim with."

Eros sighs, pressing the heel of his hands into his bloodshot eyes. “Rio, I just need you to tell me what information you want me to relay to my mother. Your—" He wisely decides not to try to label whatever the hell she and Agatha were. “—she—” He settles on instead, nodding toward her. “—said to wait so you could control the narrative with her, and I agree, but she’s been bombarding me nonstop.” His phone buzzes, lighting up with the word MOTHER on the table. “See? It’s been happening all night. Between that and the jet lag, I’ve gotten no sleep.”

There are about a dozen snarky comments sitting on the tip of Agatha’s tongue, but she bites it before any of them can tumble out of her mouth. She’d made a promise to be an observer in this conversation — one that was already proving fucking torturous.

“Okay, then let’s go over our options,” Rio reasons. “There’s the truth — that her son is a monster I had to protect myself from — which she won’t like.”

“Or believe,” Eros mumbles.

“And then there’s a lie that you couldn’t find me. That I’d already left the island.”

“Which is risky. She might spot you in the background of someone’s photo on the resort’s location tag.”

“You think she’s combing through that?” Eros gives Rio a look, and she scowls. “Right,” she mutters. “Of course she is. I wouldn't put anything past her.”

“It might also make it seem like you have something to hide.” 

Rio glowers at him. “Which I don’t.”

“I know. I know.” Eros holds his hands up. “You’re in an impossible situation.”

“Story of my fucking life,” she grumbles, stirring some yogurt around her bowl. “What does she want to hear, huh? What’s going to make her happy?”

“That it was all a tragic mistake?” Eros proposes. “That her son’s still alive?”

“Clearly, that's not happening.”

“As far as consolation prizes go…for me to tell her that you’re a crazed lunatic who’s clearly lying?”

She shoots him another glare. “Well, you aren’t doing that either.”

“No.” He holds up his palms. “No, obviously I’m not going to do that.”

Agatha narrows her eyes, an idea forming in her brain. “But maybe you could tell her you’re a crazed lunatic.”

Eros’ gaze snaps over to her. “What?”

Agatha purses her lips as she looks at Rio, the slightest bit guilty at already breaking her promise to be a silent chaperone about two minutes in. “Permission to speak freely?”

Rio raises a cautious eyebrow. “Motion granted…”

Agatha nods and turns to Eros. “You tell your mother that you found Rio and gave her a piece of your mind. Really laid into her — I’m talking verbal annihilation, maximum intimidation.”

Eros’ eyes widen, horrified. “But I don’t…I don’t want to do that.”

Agatha rolls her own in response. “You wouldn’t actually have to,” she snaps, rather impressed she managed to hold back a far more derogatory comment. “You just say you did. She’d feel smug that her master plan worked — that she managed to get to Rio through you — which might even make her slow down on the online crusade for a beat. And she’d be pleased with you for doing her bidding. Might even let you spearhead some of the threatening, when really, you’d be a double-agent working for us. Plus, wouldn’t it feel good to finally find out what Mommy’s approval feels like?”

Eros squirms in his seat, looking down at the table. “I guess,” he admits.

“The story that she coerced you into bullying an abuse survivor might even help Rio’s situation if there’s any justice in the world,” Agatha points out. “Which there isn’t, but you know — ‘hope’ and ‘optimism’ and whatever the fuck.”

She and Eros both peer over at Rio. “What do you think?” Eros asks.

Rio’s tongue pokes the inside of her cheek as she considers. “It’s probably an okay plan.”

“It’s a brilliant plan,” Agatha mumbles, a little insulted at the mere ‘okay’ label.

“If—” Rio looks at Eros. “—you can pull it off. You’d have to commit. Fully. 120%.”

Eros swallows hard. “What do you mean? What— What, exactly, would I have to do?"

“Construct the ‘rant’ you yelled at me in your head — she might ask for details. And speak with conviction. She’s a nasty bitch, so obviously, don’t egg her on, but you can’t shrivel away.”

“You should practice,” Agatha suggests. “Rio, you’re a lawyer — interrogate him about the fake screaming match.”

Rio raises a brow at him. “Do you need that?”

“I mean...I don’t— I don’t kn—“

“He needs it,” Agatha dryly answers on his behalf.

Rio rubs her temples and lets out a long sigh. “Just get it together, okay?”

He lifts his palms. “I will. I will. I promise.”

“You know what happens if you break that promise?” Agatha threatens.

He winces. “You break me?” 

“Precisely.”

“She’s probably not kidding,” Rio warns.

“Oh, I’m not,” Agatha confirms.

“I know.” He grimaces. “I know that.” He blows out a breath, giving Rio a look — sympathetic and serious. “I can do this.”

“You swear?”

“Yes,” he vows. “You can trust me.”

Rio softens a little. “I believe you,” she assures him. “But do you believe in your ability to do this?”

He nods. “I’m going to figure it out. It’s the least I could do.”

“Correct,” Agatha agrees. “Very good job at recognizing your bare minimum contribution.”

“And you won’t fold under pressure, right?” Rio checks. “If she asks for specifics?”

“I won’t let you down.” He places a gentle hand over hers. “I’ll rehearse everything I’m going to say — every potential question she might ask — a hundred times. I’ll even run it through ChatGPT to check if there are any holes in my story,” he says earnestly.

“ChatGP—“ Agatha puts her hands over her face. “Oh fuck, we’re doomed. We’re fucking doomed.”

A few people turn to give her odd looks.

“What?” she snaps at them, putting her hands up. “We are! Wake up and look at the state of the world right now!”

“No AI,” Rio firmly insists. “Call me if you have to.”

He lifts his palms again. “Okay, okay. You…call me if you have to, too. If you need anything. I know I’m probably fucking up, but…I really am trying. I really do care.”

Rio gives him a soft, bittersweet smile. “I know."

“Good.” He nods.

There's a beat of not altogether uncomfortable silence as Agatha looks down at her phone to check the time. “We should get going. The sharks aren’t going to swim with themselves.”

Eros’ brows wrinkle. “I’m…pretty sure they—"

Agatha cuts him off by stealing the last piece of bacon off his plate, popping it in her mouth before scooting her chair out. “Ta-ta for now.” 

Rio’s plate is still fuller than Agatha would like, but to her credit, she does grab a slice of pineapple to take to-go.

Agatha rewards this by carding a hand through her hair. “Good girl,” she praises with a purr, taking advantage of the fact that Nicky still couldn’t hear them — and that Eros most certainly could.

His face turns red. “I’m gonna—“ He gets up too fast, losing his balance and slamming his hip on the table. “—ow. Go now.”

Rio rolls her eyes as he leaves, though she does melt back into Agatha’s touch. “You didn’t have to torture him.”

Agatha scoffs, continuing to stroke her locks. “That was light hazing at most.”

“Which still isn’t great.”

She pouts. “I thought I showed remarkable restraint.”

“You did,” Rio admits, tilting her chin back to peer up at her. “But honey gets you far more flies than vinegar.”

“Good thing I don’t like flies, then,” Agatha quips, grabbing a piece of waffle off Nicky’s plate and giving him a nudge. “You ready to go?”

He looks up at her from the iPad. “What?!” he yells.

Agatha lifts one of the headphones off his ear. “I said, ‘Are you ready to go?’”

“Oh!” He perks up. “Yes!”

Agatha lets the headphone fall back into position. “Wonderful.”

“Huh?!”

Agatha rubs a hand over her face, already mapping out how she could steal a mimosa on the way out of the restaurant.

Agatha when Nicky interrupts her vs. Agatha when Eros interrupts her.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 38: Day 6, Part 4

Chapter Summary

The morning catches up to Agatha as she encounters the most intimidating shark of all.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Ms. Lilia!” Nicky greets as he spies the woman waiting outside the shark swimming headquarters, looking a bit silly as he runs over to her with his heavily and unnecessarily bandaged leg.

Lilia is unfazed. “Hello, young man. How are you this morning?”

“Happy!” He throws his arms around her. “We’re gonna swim with sharkies!”

“Well, Ms. Lilia isn’t,” Agatha tells him as she and Rio approach more slowly.

“You’re not?” Nicky’s mouth drops into a frown, tilting his head back to peer up at her. “How come?”

“Because she’s chickenshit,” Agatha mutters under her breath.

“Because I have old, brittle bones,” Lilia explains, shooting Agatha a disapproving look. “I’ll still come out on the boat with you, all right?”

"Okay," he replies, satisfied enough by the compromise. He looks back at Agatha in concern as they make their way into the building. “Are your bones too old and brittle, too, Mama?”

Agatha scoffs, offended. “I’m half her age, Nicky. My bones are youthful and exceptionally strong.” It was true enough. She’d only broken her arm once as a child, though with the way Evanora handled her, it probably should have been a lot more. She leaves this part out. The conversation about the scars the previous night had been plenty.

The stupid waiter kid is working the check-in desk, because of course he is. He grimaces as he spies Agatha.

“Do you have a twin or something?” Agatha asks him.

He blinks in surprise at the question. “Y— yes, actually,” he tells her. “But we’re fraternal. And Tommy doesn’t work here.”

“So you just work everywhere, then.”

“Kind of? I’m a floater. I go where they need me.”

Agatha taps the desk impatiently. “Well, I need you to check us in. Four for the boat ride, three for the actual excursion.” 

He purses his lips and types on the computer, wincing as he pulls up their booking. “Yeah. Um. So. About that…” 

“About what?” Agatha snaps. “I called and made a reservation. They said it was handled.”

“It is!” he reassures her. “But, uh…there were only two slots available.”

Agatha’s nostrils flare. “Why didn’t they tell me this on the phone?”

“The notes said they tried? But that you hung up before they could get it all out.” 

Oh. Right. Probably true.

Agatha sighs, running a hand over her face before turning to Rio. “Will you be okay to go with him?”

Rio freezes, a hint of panic flickering in her eyes. “I mean, I suppose, but I don’t have to if that’s a problem.”

“Don’t be ridiculous — it’s your dream.”

“It’s okay,” Rio quickly assures her. “I don’t want to overstep or do something wrong. I'm—” She abruptly cuts herself off. “Squamous,” she mumbles.

Agatha blinks in confusion before her brain catches up, the corner of her mouth quirking into a small, approving smile. She leans forward to place a light, encouraging kiss on her jaw before whispering in her ear, “Flaccid, baby. Flaccid. As long as you make sure he doesn’t drown or get eaten, I promise I'll drown in your cunt later and let you eat mine whenever you want.”

Agatha can practically feel the sudden heat radiating off Rio’s blushing cheeks. “Just hold me for a second?” she quietly asks.

She wordlessly wraps her arms around her. “You’re allowed to say no to me touching you,” Agatha reminds her. “But I’m never going to say no to the privilege."

Rio sinks into her embrace, her muscles relaxing at the contact. “It’ll be okay?”

“You supervising Nicky in the shark water? Yes, without a doubt. Me being trapped with the old kook on the boat for an hour? To be determined.”

Rio nods. “Tighter?” she requests.

“Only if you do the same,” Agatha negotiates, though she obliges. “‘I’m clinging on with everything I have,’ remember?”

“I’m trying,” Rio promises, fingertips pressing harder into Agatha’s back in compliance. “I really am.”

“I’m about to give that phrase the ’squamous’ treatment,” she playfully threatens, holding onto her for another moment before giving her a squeeze and pulling away with an embarrassing amount of reluctance. “You don’t have to keep saying that, okay? Just keep doing it." She reaches up, cupping Rio's still lightly flushed face. "Now go cross some shit off your bucket list." 

The boat ride out into the ocean is uneventful, save for the fact that the safety precautions the instructors drone on and on about are entirely too long. ‘Don’t antagonize the sharks.’ Fucking duh. (Never mind the fact that Agatha probably would if she were allowed in the water. Besides the point.)

No, Agatha was stuck next to a different kind of shark in the form of Lilia as Nicky and Rio tread water below.

“You know, the sharks would probably relish biting you,” the older woman dryly muses, a cigarette in hand.

“Projecting, Lilia?” Agatha retorts. “Is this your way of saying you’re desperate for a taste of me?”

Lilia wrinkles her nose in disgust that looks insultingly sincere. “Absolutely not. I just meant that your pervasive antagonistic energy would be enough to make them mad on principle.”

“Give me more credit — my pervasive antagonistic energy would be enough to make the most pure and patient of saints mad, too.”

Lilia gives her a look. “That’s not a badge of honor.”

“To you, maybe.”

“To 99% of the world, dear.”

“Guess I’m part of the 1%. A special little snowflake.”

Lilia shakes her head, taking another drag. “Whatever helps you sleep at night.”

“I sleep just fine,” Agatha proclaims, more defensiveness than she planned creeping into her voice. It’s half true, she justifies to herself, crossing her arms over her chest. She sleeps amazingly when she’s holding Rio. When she’s thinking about Rio, on the other hand — when all of the doubt, the worry that she won’t be able to hold onto Rio seeps in — that’s when she tosses and turns.

“Sure,” Lilia skeptically replies, blowing out a long trail of smoke.

“I do,” she snaps, plucking the cigarette from her hand. “You can’t do that on here. Didn’t you hear the safety guides?” she asks before taking a puff. She makes a face. “Ugh, I forgot you smoked Kols.”

“They’re not paying a damn bit of attention to us,” Lilia notes. She either doesn’t want to fight Agatha for it back, doesn’t want to share saliva with her, or some combination of the two, as she fishes a fresh one out from the container in her purse.

“Well, luckily, it sounds like you already got plenty of attention from your shuffleboard woman last night, hm?” Agatha side-eyes her.

Lilia shrugs, nonchalant as they come. Super irritating. Agatha was really hoping to make her squirm at least a little. “Sure.”

“Oh, come on.” She rolls her eyes. “You’re really gonna hold out on me?”

She shrugs again. “I don’t know why you’re so interested in my sex life.”

“Well, you either tell me about your sweet, sweet lovin’, or I stare out at the sea with my thoughts for the next—“ She looks down at her watch. “—52 minutes.”

“Okay,” Lilia replies, clearly choosing the latter option.

“Does she not actually exist?” Agatha presses. Anything not to be alone with the anxieties that had been stewing since that morning. That were rising to the surface as Rio and Nicky went under it. “Is that why you won’t give me the deets? Is it a ‘my girlfriend goes to another school’ situation? Because that would be pathetic — and I would mercilessly make fun of you — but after, I might also give you some tips on how to land a not-imaginary woman if you groveled a little and asked very, very ni—”

“Can you just shut the fuck up?” Lilia cuts her off with a glare. “You’re the only one interested in what you have to say.”

That stings more than it should — a fact she’s sure shows on her face the millisecond before she manages to school it back into her nonchalant mask.

Normally, she wouldn’t give a shit. Normally, it’d egg her on even more. Normally, it’d make her feel big and powerful instead of very, very small in every sense of that word.

But nothing about this vacation had been remotely normal.

Lilia wasn’t Rio or Nicky — Lilia wasn’t even close — but she wasn’t…nobody, either. Not anymore. For some mysterious, infuriating reason.

Plus, it compounded every fear she’d felt with Rio. She had been trying to bond, in her own weird, fucked up way. Had been trying to show interest in Lilia’s life under the guise of the snippy banter that the foundation their short, strangely intense relationship had been built upon.

“Geez, I was just trying to make conversation,” she mumbles.

Lilia raises her chin, straightens her posture against the bench. “Well, a conversation about my sex life is not one I want to have.”

“Got it. You made that crystal fucking clear,” she responds, taking another puff of the stolen cigarette as she looks out at the ocean. The big, stupid ocean keeping her from storming away from stupid Lilia and her own stupid feelings. “So sorry for disrupting your prudish peace.”

“We can talk about something. Just not that.”

“It’s fine. I don’t need your charity.”

Lilia looks over at her. “What’s got you so puffed up?”

“That’s not a conversation I want to have,” she snarks back, though using Lilia’s own words against her feels...hollow, somehow. Doesn’t give her the satisfaction she’d hoped.

“All right.” Lilia nods, proceeding to pull out her phone.

Agatha clenches her jaw, unable to decide if she’s more upset or relieved that Lilia hadn’t pushed for once. After a few agonizing moments of silence, she glances down at Lilia’s screen, raising a brow as she sees her playing Tetris. “Took you more for an online poker person.”

“There’s no internet out here.”

She rolls her eyes. “A poker app that doesn’t require service, then.”

“Eh, not as fun.”

“And that is?” Agatha presses, trying to drag the conversation out by any means necessary. “Stacking things into neat little rows — that’s your definition of a good time?”

“Mm.” Lilia shrugs a shoulder, eyes staying glued to the phone.

Agatha runs her tongue over her teeth. “Well, it’s not mine. Patiently building things up? That shit’s not fun for me.”

“I’m shocked,” Lilia deadpans. 

Agatha briefly glances over at Rio and Nicky in the water before her gaze drops to the bottom of the boat. “That shit’s not possible for me,” she mutters.

Lilia pauses her game in order to look up at her. “I disagree," she says, tone growing more sincere. “You just have to put the work in.”

“I’ve been putting the work in — I’ve been clocking triple fucking overtime,” she barks, though there’s a small croak of hurt in the midst of the frustration. “I’m still coming up short. I’m still doing it wrong. I’m still…" She struggles to even get the word out. "Failing.”

“It’s not a quick thing,” Lilia reasons. “You have to mess up a couple of times to get it right. It’s part of the whole process. And mistakes are just that — mistakes.”

“I can’t afford to make them. Not with her. The stakes…” Agatha shakes her head. “They’re way too high.”

“Well, you’re going to have to, or it’ll all culminate in something that’s not ideal.”

“Things are already not ideal, Lilia,” she snaps, looking over at her with a glare. “They’re already so far from ideal. She apologizes for every single thing, and she’s too afraid to let me touch her, and she opens up more to my fucking ex she met on the phone last night than she does me, and the worst part — the worst fucking part — is I can’t even really blame her for any of it,” she rambles, voice cracking. “Fuck.” She frantically swipes at a tear that’s fallen down her cheek. “Motherfucking fuck.”

Lilia sighs, softening a little. “She’s traumatized, Agatha. It’s just the way her nervous system is wired right now. Did she ever actually say she was afraid of you?”

“She doesn’t have to say it — I can see it in her eyes. In her body language when she flinches away from me. The fact is, I’m doing what you told me to do in your hotel room. I'm giving her my best and then some, and it’s still not good enough. She can still do better.”

“She flinches because she’s used to being hit,” Lilia rationalizes. “It’s not personal.”

“I’m used to being hit, too,” she bluntly retorts. “It’s always at least a little bit personal.”

“To you, maybe. Don’t project that onto Rio.”

“I know you don’t like me, you know,” Agatha accuses, swiping another stupid tear away. The timing of it is a total coincidence, of course, and not because a little part of her wishes Lilia did. “I know you see me as an annoying little gnat that doesn’t matter — that can’t affect you. So how do I know you’re not projecting that onto Rio when you claim there’s no way her reaction could have anything to do with me, huh?”

“I don’t dislike you,” she argues. A beat. “I don’t necessarily…like you either,” she confesses, “but I don’t dislike you, Agatha. My saying that you should read things as neutral until you have explicit confirmation that it’s not isn’t projecting. She and I both know you don’t want to hurt her.”

“Don’t you get it? She’d never give me explicit confirmation because she doesn’t want to hurt me for some mysterious fucking reason!”

“You’re not hearing me,” Lilia says, voice aggravatingly calm. “If you’re that concerned, have an adult conversation with her.”

“No, you aren’t hearing me,” she hisses. “We have conversed. We’ve conversed about this topic to death. She may say I’m what she wants — she might even believe it right now — but I know.” Agatha puts a hand to her chest, face contorting in pain. “I know who I am in here,” she continues in a whisper. “I’m not capable of loving her the way she needs, and I’m not—“ Her breath hitches. “—I’m not deserving of the love she has to give. That’s not a projection — it’s just a fucking fact.”

Lilia shakes her head. “That’s simply not true. She chose you, Agatha.”

“Yeah, well, she chose him, too, once upon a time." She sniffles, swiping the snot with her sleeve. "And she’s told me she gets stuck in patterns easily. Maybe she jumped out of the frying pan with him and straight into the fire with me.”

“I think you’re a lot of things, but an abuser is not one of them.”

“Like what?” she challenges. “Name the things, Lilia. I’d love to hear them.”

“A human, albeit a prideful one,” she lists. “A stubborn broad. A person with a weird simultaneous superiority and inferiority complex.”

“Great. That’s covered. What else you got, hm?” Agatha curves her fingers, motioning for her to bring it on. “Don’t hold back. It’s our last day here.”

Lilia sighs, pinching the bridge of her nose. “Why are you like this?”

“Because I’d rather you just call me an evil bitch, or a trashy whore, or a terrible mother and get it over with already,” she spits, though there’s an undercurrent of wounded defeat. 

She shifts her gaze away, clenching her jaw as she stares straight ahead. “It’s what you think. It’s what everybody thinks. And don’t lecture me about projection again — if I were to list everyone who’s said those things about me, we’d be here all day.”

She doesn't care. Not really. Not usually. She's trained herself not to care — to use the words as gasoline on the fire within her. But that doesn't stop her from getting burned on occasion.

“I don’t think you’re those things,” Lilia says, her voice achingly sincere and something close to soothing. “I think you’re doing everything you can to hide a world of hurt. I think you’re trying your best to be good for her.”

Agatha's quiet for a long, long moment, not daring to look over at the woman. “You really think I can?” she asks, voice taking on that vulnerable and vaguely childlike quality again. Something about that phrase…it shook those walls she’d built up so high. “You think I can be good?”

“I know you can.”

The simple affirmation — the mere belief — hits Agatha hard, touching somewhere deep and crumbling a layer of brick or two.

She clears her throat, attempting to rid it of the emotion that rises up. “I don’t know where the fuck you call home back in the States, but Nicky is going to want you to visit.” I do, too. “You’re old as shit, so he’s obviously latched onto you as a pathetic excuse for a grandmother figure.” You’re not pathetic, and I’ve gotten attached as well. “I hope you have airline points saved up or, at the very least, a car that gets decent gas mileage. If you don’t, I guess I’ll have to deal with your incompetence and figure it out myself, as per usual.” Steal, commit fraud, engage in various illegal activities. “For his sake.” And mine. “Okay?” Please, Lilia. Please.

Lilia quirks a brow. “Where do you all live?”

“Jersey. Snobby little suburb called Westview.”

She nods. “I’m up in Brooklyn.”

An hour and a half away. What are the odds? What are the fucking odds?

“Hm,” Agatha hums as nonchalantly as she can. “Not too far. That’s lucky for you.”

She hopes the way she reaches into her bag, pulls out a cigarette, and wordlessly hands it to Lilia to pay her back for the one she stole communicates the fact that she feels a little lucky, too.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 39: Day 6, Part 5

Chapter Summary

Big feelings are felt, and big confessions are made.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Nicky talks Agatha’s ear off about the shark swimming, proclaiming, no fewer than a dozen times, that “he and Ms. Rio looked so silly in the big goggles” and that “one of the sharks winked at him” and that this is “the best day of his life.”

It gives Agatha a chip on her shoulder — one that will surely grow even bigger when he inevitably relays these declarations on the phone to Wanda. The best day of his life, and Agatha was the sole mom responsible. 

Lilia offers to babysit Nicky so she and Rio can have one last romantic evening together — admittedly very thoughtful, even if it is likely mostly for Rio’s sake, as she had flat-out admitted she didn’t particularly like Agatha. (Though the way she gives her a little smile and wink makes her suspicious that she might be growing on her the smallest bit.)

Which is how Agatha finds herself across from Rio at the resort restaurant — the same table they’d first had dinner at a few days ago, ironically enough, though things had changed dramatically and irrevocably since then. 

“So,” Agatha says as she picks up her menu. “I’ve heard Nicky’s recollection of events — approximately one thousand times — but how was it for you? Did you have as much fun diving into the shark-infested ocean as you did dipping into the lady pond with me?” She quirks a brow, the corner of her mouth rising to match in a little smirk.

Rio either doesn’t pick up on the innuendo or chooses to ignore it. Both would be equally on brand for her. “It was really great, actually,” she says, and Agatha can tell she means it. She seems to be breathing a little easier — her whole demeanor lighter. Freer. “I know it’s probably odd, but I thought they were cute.”

“Definitely odd,” she agrees, “but not all that surprising coming from you, considering you think I’m cute, too.”

“You are.” Rio shrugs. “We mostly saw blues and great whites, though we also got a glimpse of a couple of blacktip reefs. The guide said that was special — apparently, they’re pretty rare for the area.”

“Blacktip…” Agatha purses her lips. “I’m tempted to make a dick joke right now, but you’re being so wholesome, it’d feel wrong.”

She makes a face. “Please don’t. It’s an animal.”

Agatha scoffs. “Just because I have a dirty mind doesn’t mean I’m into bestiality. Jesus, Rio.”

“You’re the one threatening to make sex jokes about it.”

“If anything, I’m making a joke about the perv of a scientist who named the poor thing.”

“It’s not pervy — it’s descriptive,” Rio defends. “Their dorsal fins have a black tip.”

“You’re such a nerd.” Agatha rolls her eyes affectionately before looking at her menu again. “Think I might eat like a shark tonight and order the fish. What about you?”

“I’m…not sure. Pesto chicken sounds okay, I guess.”

“We’re not settling for 'okay' on your last night at a luxury fucking resort. What sounds amazing? I don’t care if it’s not on the menu — the chef can figure it out.”

Rio stares down at her options for another long moment, chewing on the inside of her cheek. “I’m not sure,” she repeats, though the pitch of her voice heightens ever so slightly, and her gaze drifts to the left.

Agatha rolls her eyes again. “Unlike me, you’re not a very good liar.”

“I’m not lying,” she mumbles.

“You are,” she presses. “Tell me what you want, without thinking about price or calories.”

Another long beat passes. “Lobster,” she finally mumbles.

Agatha doesn’t even blink. “With which two sides?”

“I don’t need sides.”

“Yes, you do — you’ve basically been working out all day. Double working out, between the swimming and wrangling a feral six-year-old. Plus, they’re included with the entrée. So, I’ll ask again: with which two sides?”

A few more seconds of silence. “Mashed potatoes,” she says quietly. “And the broccoli cheddar soup.” She cringes as if the ghost of Thanos will materialize at any moment to berate her for her selections.

“Good girl,” Agatha praises, plucking the menu from her hand. “We’ll cross the dessert bridge when we come to it.”

“Dessert?” she repeats, anxiety simmering under the word.

Agatha scoffs. “Obviously, dessert. I was thinking something a little more grown-up than the ice cream Nicky’s been living off of. Tiramisu, perhaps. Or cannolis. Hell, maybe both — when in Sicily — but as I said, we haven’t gotten to that bridge yet.” She waves her hand. “So what are you adding to your bucket list? Since you crossed pornographically named sharks off?”

Rio shrugs. “I wasn’t really going to add anything.”

“Well, you should — it’d be a shame to run out of shit to live for.” It’s a joke, but it also…kind of isn’t. “What else do you have left on it, then?”

“I guess I’ve always sort of wanted to get into gardening? Maybe even grow my own weed.”

“Used to do that in high school. Very lucrative. Happy to give you pointers. But I’m going to need you to dream bigger than one of my teenage hobbies.” 

“I don’t have anything else right now.”

“I don’t believe that. The only way you survive years locked in a tower is dreaming about what you’re going to do when you bust out of it."

“My career is what kept me going,” Rio counters. “Not dreams about the future.”

“You’re every capitalist overlord’s fantasy.”

She frowns, a flicker of hurt crossing her features. “I love my job. It gives me purpose.”

Agatha softens a little. “I know, honey — I was mostly just giving you a hard time.” She swirls some water around in her glass and desperately wishes the waiter had already brought the bottle of white wine she’d ordered. “I…even understand,” she adds, a little crumb of vulnerability to make up for the fact she’d accidentally upset her. “To an extent. I think.”

“How so?”

“Nicky,” she says simply. Quietly.

“Nicky…what?”

“Is what kept me going when...” She shakes her head a little, eyes still fixed on the water glass. “Maybe it doesn’t count. It was still a dream about the future — it’s just that the future I was dreaming about was his.”

Agatha sees Rio tilt her head out of the corner of her eye. “What do you mean?”

She takes a deep inhale, blows it out slowly through her mouth as if it’s cigarette smoke. “He was sick as a baby. He's still sick, but he was really sick back then. I…pretty much wanted to die,” she admits, clearing her throat. She’d never said that aloud — never allowed herself to name a feeling so weak and contrary to her brand of fighting at any cost, of surviving by any means necessary. “But I couldn’t. It was my job to stay alive to make sure he did, too.” She downs the water in one large swig. “I knew, from the moment he was born, that one second without him would be infinitely more painful than all those years with her combined.”

“That makes sense,” Rio gently replies. “I’m glad that you’re both still here.”

She gives her a nod and shifts in her seat. She hadn’t expected it — to be quite that open. To confess to something she never had before, and without it being forced out of her. It was jarring. Disorienting, even. She looks left and right — anywhere other than at Rio. “Where’s the waiter with that fucking wine?” she mutters.

Rio purses her lips, her pointer tracing the lid of her water glass. “My job allows me to help survivors — give them hope. It made me feel good, giving people a chance at a better life, even if I couldn’t have one myself.”

There’s a strong temptation to simply rehash the argument they’d had at the beginning of the trip — the one about the stupidity of having hope, of trying to be helpful, of not looking out for yourself first and foremost. It would fit Agatha’s pattern and be much more comfortable, familiar territory than engaging with the topic on any meaningful level.

It would also — at least partially — be a lie. (It had always at least partially been a lie, though Rio is the first one who’d ever been able to get her to admit that, too, even to herself.)

“It’s how I feel about being a mother,” she softly muses, bringing her water glass to her lips again.

She flushes in embarrassment, dropping the bone-dry glass back onto the table and sliding it away. 

“But I’m glad you have that,” Rio adds. “It’s tangible — something that you can hold onto.”

Agatha shakes her head. “It isn’t, though. Not really. As hard as I try to hang onto him, he still slips away. Long days when my ex has custody. Surgeries I can’t be in the room for. Even just the fact he’s getting older — doesn’t want me or need me the way he used to."

“Then use him as motivation to be better.”

“That’s what I’ve been doing,” she says, the defensiveness flaring up more. “That’s what I’ve been doing with you, too.”

Oh. Oh, fuck. Definitely hadn't meant to let that part slip.

Thank god the stupid waiter kid finally chooses that moment to approach the table with their bottle of wine. “Took you long enough,” Agatha mumbles, taking a swig as soon as the waiter pours her a glass and ordering food for both of them. “I’m going to need you to elaborate,” Rio says once the server leaves.

“Elaborate on what?”

She gives her a look. “Agatha…”

She finishes the rest of her glass before reaching for the wine bottle again. “Lilia told me that I should try to be better for you. For some reason I still can’t fathom, I took the old bat’s advice.”

“Why me?”

Agatha blinks, the bottle freezing halfway to her glass. “What the fuck do you mean, ‘Why you’?”

“Exactly what I said.”

“Is it not obvious by now that I— I—“ She chokes on the word, as if it’s too large to force out. 

Rio raises a brow. “That you what?” 

“Love you,” she blurts, shoving the word from her mouth — setting the damn genie free from its lamp — before she can think too hard about it. She scoffs. “You think I get drunk off of one measly bottle of wine? Don’t insult me.”

“You’re missing my point. I want to have a serious conversation without alcohol.”

“Fine.” She sighs, pulling a cigarette out of her bag. She catches a glimpse of Rio’s disapproving expression as she goes to light it. “What?” she asks. “You gotta give me something here.”

“No, I don’t. I want you to be sober when we speak about this.”

She chews on the inside of her cheek, cigarette still unlit between her fingers. She’d normally tell whoever requested that to fuck right off, but she seemed incapable of saying that to Rio’s face. “Does that include nicotine, or can I smoke this?”

“Includes nicotine.”

She rolls her eyes, though she flicks the lighter shut and drops it and the cigarette onto the table, sitting back in her seat and crossing her arms. She feels vaguely like she’s back in high school, having been called to the principal’s office. “And I need you to say it before I can promise,” she retorts. “I just leapt off a cliff, Rio," she adds more quietly. "It’s not fair to ask me to do anything more until you jump, too.”

“I just got out of an abusive relationship where my love was weaponized,” Rio reminds her. “I need to know that won’t happen again.”

“It won’t,” she vows. “But I grew up around a woman with no love for me at all. I need to know that won’t happen again, either.”

“We wouldn’t have gotten to this juncture if that were the case.”

“I still need to hear the actual words from your mouth.”

Rio rubs her face with a sigh. “Agatha, I wouldn’t be here if I didn’t. I can give you that, but I need you to give me some safety here.”

“Well, I can’t do that,” she admits, blunt but not unkind. “There’s nothing safe about this, sweetheart — for either of us. It’s the most dangerous thing in the world, these matters of the fucking heart."

Fuck, she wishes that wine wasn't so far away. That she could reach for the cigarette next to her.

"But I’m willing to risk it," she continues. "I’m willing to risk everything in the world for you because I love you. I love you. I. Love. You.” Her voice cracks, an unexpected slip of fragility in the middle of the firm declaration. “And I need you to look. Me in. The eye. And say it back.”

Rio purses her lips, staring at her for a long, long moment. “I love you,” she says, voice just as quiet. “I love you, too.”

She’d begged for it — demanded it, really — but now that Rio had said it, she doesn’t know quite what to do with it. How to process it. It's like the sun shining directly on her after she'd been holed up in a cave for years: overwhelming in its brightness, in the heat it makes her feel all over. She nods, squirming a little as her gaze drops down to the tablecloth. “Good,” she awkwardly says. “Thank you.”

“But now I need to know that you’ll try,” Rio presses. “That this is serious for you.”

Agatha blows out a frustrated breath as tears burn in her eyes. “I’m doing everything I can to show you that I am and that it is.” But it’s not enough, the little voice says. You’re not enough, and you never will be. 

She forces herself to look up at Rio, both more intense and vulnerable than she’s ever been with her. Maybe than she’s ever been period. “I’m giving you everything that I have. I need you to decide if you’re going to take it — if you’re going to choose all of it, and all of me, and all the shit that entails.”

She purses her lips. As much as she might not want to, it wouldn’t be right, not giving her an out. “If you’re going to leave it, I’d understand," she says more softly. "I wouldn’t fault you. Any more time spent basking in the sun of Rio's existence, and she would not be able to figure out how to live without its warmth again. “I won’t recover.”

Rio softens a little at that. “I want to take it. I want you — all of you.”

Maybe Agatha, in all her selfishness, is allowing Rio to make the biggest mistake in her mistake-filled life. Agatha can’t quite bring herself to care at this moment. Agatha can’t do anything except work against her very nature — perhaps fate itself — to try and make it the right choice.

“Then you got me,” she whispers. She places her hand halfway across the table, palm up — an invitation. “All of me.”

Instead of holding her hand, Rio begins to play with Agatha’s fingers — an even more intimate action, somehow. She was letting her guard down, quietly taking what she needed without fear of judgment. “Could we get the cheesecake for dessert?” she quietly asks.

Agatha’s mouth curves into a smile. There’s a strange feeling stirring in her chest. Pride, maybe. Or that hope thing Rio had mentioned. “Sure, honey. Whatever you want.”

The tender moment is interrupted by a few Italian cops — the same ones who questioned Rio — approaching their table. “Signoras? We need to speak with you.”

Chapter 40: Day 6, Part 6

Chapter Summary

It's all over.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio straightens her posture as she looks at the cops. “Okay.” She gives them a small nod. “Sure.”

“Make it quick,” Agatha snaps, covering up for the fact that she’s internally far less cool and collected about the sudden police presence than Rio seems to be, considering her own experience with the law. She’s tempted to get up and bolt — it would be just her luck, getting arrested for fraud or identity theft or one of the other dozen crimes she hadn’t been caught for yet right now — but Rio’s still holding onto her fingers, and she can’t bear to take that small comfort from her.

“We’ve been continuing our investigation — going over the case with a fine-tooth comb,” one of them says.

“So your job,” Agatha says. “You’ve been doing your job. Do you want a gold star? Or maybe a cookie? Shall we throw a parade? Create a holiday in your honor? Considering how useless most of you are, I suppose I do understand why you think this warrants a special congratulations, but—“

“The evidence overwhelmingly points to self-defense, just as you said,” he tells Rio. “That’s what we’re ruling in our official report. We wanted to personally let you know the case is now closed.”

Rio closes her eyes, breathing out a deep sigh of relief. “Thank you for telling me.”

“Of course.” He nods. “We hope you enjoyed Sicily otherwise. That you’ll visit again soon.”

“What are you, the fucking tourism board?” Agatha asks, dismissing them with the wave of her hand. “You can go.”

She should be relieved, too, but it feels too…easy. Goodness and truth didn’t ever just prevail like that. (Did they?) You didn’t get anywhere without some lying and cheating. (Did you?) The other shoe always dropped. (Didn’t it?)

Rio settles back into her chair, taking her hand with her. Agatha misses its absence immediately — the softness. The warmth. The safe grounding of her touch. Had she always secretly craved that so much? “This is good,” she muses.

“Mm,” Agatha mumbles in something she hopes sounds like agreement.

“I feel a little better now.”

“Let’s just hope Floppy Boy Band Hair-os doesn’t fuck things up on the monster-in-law front.”

“Former,” Rio corrects. “Please. I don’t want to be associated with her in the present tense.”

“Right. You have quite the track record with those, don’t you? Between his and mine. Of course, mine had the good sense to die. And we’re not, you know, married. Obviously.” Agatha awkwardly clears her throat, reaching across the table. “Can I have the wine back now?”

She hands it over with a half-warning look. “Don’t drink the whole thing.”

“Oh, you want a sip?” Agatha asks facetiously, cocking a brow as she takes it. She knows Rio just wants her coherent, but she just wants to have a little fun in the midst of all this seriousness. She seductively curves her pointer. “Lean forward and open your mouth.”

Rio furrows her brows, looking down at her cup. “But my glass is still full.”

She sighs, having Lady and the Tramp flashbacks. “I thought it would be sexy to see you do,” she explains — bluntly, both because she had no shame and because that’s the only thing that worked on Rio. “And sort of romantic, hand-feeding you grapes like they did for royalty in Ancient Greece.”

“Oh.” Rio’s cheeks grow pink. “I’m sorry.”

She raises a brow. “What was that? I could’ve sworn I just heard a ‘sorry’ come out of your mouth, but I know that can’t be right considering that word isn’t in your vocabulary anymore.”

Rio shakes her head, fiddling with the napkin on her lap. “Well, I was dumb, so I ruined something.”

“No, your autism popped out, so you misunderstood,” Agatha corrects. “I think I’ll survive without the frat party activity of pouring alcohol down your throat.”

She takes her bottom lip between her teeth. “You sure I didn’t mess up?”

“Have you ever seen me hold back on telling someone when they messed up, Rio?” Agatha deadpans.

“I guess not,” she mutters.

“Exactly.”

Rio’s silent for a moment before relenting. “Squamous,” she amends under her breath.

“There you go,” Agatha says, rewarding her by leaning down to kiss her hand and topping up her glass. “I love it when you talk dirty to me.”

Rio takes her first sip, a pleased little sound escaping her throat.

“Good, right?”

“Very.” 

“I told you, I don’t drink that cheap shit.” Agatha pours another hearty glass and takes a sip of her own — much larger than Rio’s, more like a swig, really. She needs it. She needs far more than it, honestly, to broach the topic she’s desperately put off multiple times for multiple days, but she doesn’t want Rio to go snatching the bottle away from her again.  

“So,” she starts. “Tomorrow.”

Rio must hear the trepidation in her voice, as she narrows her eyes and proactively reaches across the table to snag the wine anyway.

“Hey!” Agatha protests, attempting, in vain, to snatch it back.

Rio promptly ignores her, setting it near the edge of her side of the table. “What about it?”

Agatha lets out a frustrated sigh. “Well, we fly back to the United States of Assholes.” She squirms in her seat, still — for some reason — trying to skirt around the increasingly large elephant in the room. “Lilia lives in Brooklyn, too, you know. Maybe she'll be on the same flight as you. Are you going into JFK or LaGuardia?”

“Newark, actually.”

“Newark,” she repeats. She hadn’t been expecting that. Again, what are the odds? What are the fucking odds? “I guess that means you’ll be on the same one as me.”

“Oh,” Rio says, her expression annoyingly unreadable. “That’s lucky.”

On the one hand, it certainly was very lucky indeed. On the other hand, it was almost…too lucky. So lucky that it wrapped around to being something of a curse. There were no excuses now to chicken out.

“You said your dad was picking you up at the airport?” Agatha asks.

“Yeah,” Rio slowly replies. “Last he told me.”

“Do you…” She clears her throat. Fuck, she couldn’t do this. But she had to do this. Was she seriously doing this? “You think he’d have room in his car for one more?” She shakes her head. “Maybe you don’t know. Maybe he doesn’t even know if he’s planning to rent it when he gets there. Though I can’t imagine there are a lot of sexy two-seater convertibles at the airport’s Enterprise, nor do I think your father would get one for the two of you."

Rio’s brows furrow in confusion. “Yeah, there’s…probably an extra seat…”

“To be clear, I…meant I’d be going to Brooklyn with you. Not trying to hitch a ride back to Westview. That would be...psychotic." And something she would, admittedly, absolutely do.

She blinks. “You’d want to go there with me?”

Agatha shrugs, swirling the last few drops of wine around in her glass, rationing them for when she really, really needed more liquid courage. “Six hands are better than four, right? For packing? Plus, that way, we can go through and separate all of the ugly shit your undearly departed picked out that needs to be burned in a fire from the good shit I want you to move into my place.”

Rio chews on her lip for a few seconds. “I am a little excited to find clothes I actually like,” she admits.

“I’m sure you’ll look even more beautiful in them. Though I’m even more sure that my favorite look on you is always going to be in nothing at all.”

A blush creeps into Rio’s cheeks as she looks down at the perfectly ironed tablecloth. “Will you go shopping with me? Help me narrow down all the options?” The thought of that — the newfound autonomy — clearly overwhelms her more than she’d like to admit.

“Don’t have to ask me twice,” Agatha flippantly agrees. “Especially if that invitation includes entry into the fitting room with you. Lost my virginity in one of those, you know. “You’re just noticing this?”

“Well, it’s obvious now.”

“Oh, yeah?” Agatha rests her chin in her hand, batting her lashes. “What else has become oh-so-clear about me this week?”

“That you care,” Rio says, casual yet confident and without missing a beat.

“Hm.” Her gaze drops down her wine glass, the straightforward sincerity of the statement almost too much to bear. “And here I thought I was being subtle.”

“You’re bad at that.”

She scoffs, offended enough to look back up at her. “Am not.”

“Are too,” Rio insists, the corner of her mouth curving into a small, mischievous smile.

She places a hand over her heart, faux-wounded. “Why do you want to hurt me so?”

“It’s not my fault you can’t be discreet.”

“There a reason you glossed over my invitation to participate in the time-honored lesbian tradition of U-hauling with me, then?” she asks, deciding now is the time to take her last emergency drink of wine. “Seeing as how it must’ve been pretty overt?”

Rio bites the inside of her cheek. “It’s not that I’m against it,” she explains, voice quiet. “I just don’t want to rush.”

“You’re the one who kept asking to come stay with me,” Agatha points out. “I thought the idea of doing it on a more permanent basis would make you happy.”

“It does,” she promises. “I’m just…scared.”

Agatha taps her nails against the side of her empty glass. “Me too,” she forces herself to confess.

“I wish I could find a way not to be.”

“Mm,” Agatha hums again. She sure as hell wishes the same. Being scared was one of her least-favorite feelings, right next to being wrong. (Thankfully, the latter didn't happen often.) “On the bright side, you’ve already done the hardest part — of leaving him. The rest should be a cake walk in comparison. Cheesecake walk, since you like that better.”

The ghost of a smile appears on her face, which Agatha takes as a win, considering her humor often fell flat with her. “I know. It just feels…weird. I haven’t been this free in years, you know?”

“Well, my sham court-ordered therapists were always going on and on about the benefits of maintaining structure and routine. Nicky needs driven to school at the ass-crack of dawn every morning I have him.” A beat. “If, you know, you did move in.” Another. “And you’d be interested in that.” 

“I have work early,” Rio reminds her. “And it’ll be a pretty long commute into the city from Westview.”

“Right. Duh.” She shakes her head, the heat of embarrassment creeping into her cheeks. Nice going, Agatha — in trying to give her a reason to get out of bed, you’d minimized her job. She relaxes a little at that. “Even better, honestly. Those stupid worksheets are only going to get harder, and I barely got my diploma.”

Rio gives her a look. “You know I don’t like it when you do that.” 

“Do what? It’s a fact. I think my GPA was 1.8 on a good day.”

“Yeah, but you could’ve graduated with honors if you’d put your mind to it. If you actually did the homework and showed up to take the tests. You’re naturally curious and a quick learner, so if you’d had any kind of support at home…”

Agatha scoffs. “What are you, my guidance counselor?”

She holds her gaze, expression serious. “Just a person who sees that you’re a lot more intelligent than you give yourself credit for.”

“Not true — I know I’m brilliant.”

“You know you’re street-smart. I know you’re more than that.”

Agatha purses her lips, staring longingly at the bottle of wine Rio is hoarding across the table. 

Luckily, Rio changes the subject. “Maybe we could do a weekly movie night, too?”

“Considering you’ve seen absolutely nothing and understand approximately zero of my references, we can even bump it up to twice a week if you’d like.”

“I watch stuff,” Rio defends. “Just…stuff I’m interested in.”

“Well, let’s see if we can’t get you interested in some of the classics.” Agatha immediately wrinkles her nose. “God, I sound like my ex. That’s disgusting.” She motions for Rio to hand her the wine bottle. “Please, I need something to get that awful taste out of my mouth.”

“I know. Because the characters in those usually have more fucked-up lives than you. You also can’t stand rom-coms and find reality TV annoying,” she recites, nearly verbatim from their conversation from the previous morning. Rio shifts in her seat, glancing down at the table once more. “I didn’t know if you would. Nothing against you — just, you know…used to being ignored.”

“Well, you’d better get used to me paying attention.” She reaches across the table, lifting her chin so she has no choice but to look at her. “You can’t hide from me, sweetheart.”

The corner of Agatha’s mouth curves into a small, affectionate smirk. “Yes, dear,” she confirms. “Or you can kiss me if you’d rather — makes no difference to me.”

“Mm.” She narrows her eyes. “You know, I think you’d better do it again — much, much slower — so I can be 100% sure.”
