Agatha moans into it, the noise turning to a groan as she feels her phone vibrate. She reluctantly pulls back and rips it from her pocket, glancing at the screen.

“Ginger Bitch,” she notes before flashing Rio an apologetic look. “Usually, I’d ignore it, but I have to ask her if she’ll pick Nicky up from the airport tomorrow.” She accepts the call and holds it to her ear, annoyance immediately overtaking her features once more. “What?”

“You seriously can’t even give me a ‘hi’?” Wanda asks, equally irritated. “It’s literally fewer letters.”

“Same number of syllables, though.”

“Whatever.” 

“Same word with two extra syllables added on,” Agatha obnoxiously points out.

“Do you want to hear the good news I have or not?”

“Ohh, can I guess?” Agatha asks, proceeding to do so without waiting for an answer. “You’re moving to Mars? You have two months to live? You—“

“Talked to Thanos’ mother.”

Wanda scoffs. “Wow, you sure picked a convenient time to start giving a shit about manners. Let me talk to her, or I'll call her myself and not tell you anything. I was doing you a courtesy by looping you in." She shifts into an (in Agatha's opinion, terrible) impression of her voice. "'Thank you, Wanda.' You're welcome, Agatha."

"Eat shit," Agatha says, though she does comply by putting the phone on speaker and placing it in the middle of the table.

“Hi, Rio. See how easy that greeting was, Agatha? Maybe she can teach you later.”

“Oh, if you think that’s impressive, you’d be amazed at the other things her tongue can do in all kinds of places,” Agatha retorts.

“Well, if one of those places is down your throat, she’s doing me a favor, considering that's the only way you ever shut up,” Wanda says sweetly.

“Hey, you.” Agatha flags down their waiter, who, lucky for her (and very unlucky for him), happens to be walking past their table.

“Y— yes?” he asks. “Is there a problem?”

“Yeah, take this back to the kitchen.” Agatha gestures to the phone. “I don’t recall ordering an appetizer of self-righteous cunt.”

“Agatha,” Rio scolds.

“Uh…” His eyes widen and dart between Agatha and Rio, the rest of his body frozen for a few beats. “I’m gonna go check on your food,” he announces before scurrying away.

“As I was saying, Rio,” Wanda continues, ignoring Agatha’s childish antics, “I talked to Thanos’ mother. Well, technically, I talked to some guy named Eros first?”

Rio fixes Agatha with a warning glare as she replies, “Uh-huh. That’s his brother.”

“Right. Well, I saw him in the Facebook comments of that post someone forwarded me about you. He was agreeing with some really offensive things.”

“Huh.” Agatha nods, vaguely impressed. “Honestly, I didn’t think he had it in him.”

“It was disgusting,” Wanda continues. “I don’t know what came over me — I’m usually not so rash — but I messaged him saying he was a hateful, ignorant son of a bitch who didn’t know the truth from his bony ass.”

“Yeah, yeah — on your side. I cracked him in about two minutes, and I got him to give me his mom’s phone number in five.”

“Then what happened?” Rio prompts, biting her thumbnail.

“I gave her a call. We had a very…productive conversation,” she diplomatically replies.

Agatha rolls her eyes. “I refuse to grovel for details from you, Red—” she says, undoubtedly irritated, though the old, almost fond nickname slips out with it for the first time in years. Damn Rio for making her so soft. Damn Wanda for being so good to Rio. 

“Once again, I’ve been blonde for years,” Wanda mumbles. 

Agatha promptly ignores her. “—but Rio deserves to know what went down.”

“Please,” Rio quietly pleads. 

There’s a beat before Wanda sighs. “We have a few mutual acquaintances — that’s how the post got sent to me in the first place. I know for a fact that a few of them have some pretty damning evidence that she’s talked badly behind the backs of everyone in her powerful little circle. She’s already lost everything once — became a social pariah after her divorce — and she did not want to risk it happening again, which is highly likely if proof of her nasty gossip habit were to ever get leaked.”

“So you blackmailed her,” Agatha infers. 

“I simply told her that this was not the right way to grieve and hinted that it would be wise for her to stop spreading lies about the innocent woman her son relentlessly tormented. Oh, and to donate the money she raised for Thanos’ GoFundMe to the local domestic violence shelter.”

“She said a lot of things,” Wanda vaguely admits. “The conversation wasn’t particularly short, and she wasn’t particularly thrilled about any of it, but eventually, we...reached an understanding. She’s taken the posts down, called off the cavalry, and promised to write a check totaling just shy of $40,000 by morning. Let’s just say I can be very…persuasive when I want to be.”

Rio takes a deep inhale. “Holy fucking shit,” she whispers. 

Holy fucking shit indeed. Sweet relief and bitter insecurity flood through Agatha in equal measure as this all sinks in. The best possible outcome had been achieved by the worst possible person. Life sure had a twisted sense of humor.

Rio clears her throat and grips Agatha’s hand — clinging on with everything she has, just as she promised. Giving Agatha the safe, grounding warmth of her touch that she hadn’t even admitted that she needed. Maybe it means something that their fingers lock together like two pieces of Nicky’s half-finished jigsaw puzzle spread out across the coffee table.

“Is this for real?” Rio asks, somehow even quieter than before.

“I wouldn’t lie about this,” Wanda vows.

“She wouldn’t,” Agatha agrees, voice softer now, too. Wanda was too good to do anything like that. Wanda was too good at everything. Too good, period. 

She squeezes Rio’s hand and tries so very hard to swallow her pride — swallow the anxiety that there were now very likely two shoes dangling over her head (weren’t there? Surely, there had to be) — as she looks in her eyes and gives her a half-forced smile. “I think it’s really over, honey.”

Rio slowly nods, her brain clearly attempting to process all of this. To begin to figure out what ‘over’ looks like, what ‘over’ means for her. She sucks in a shaky breath, tears — of relief? Of overwhelm? Of apprehension? Or maybe some combination of all three — forming in her eyes. “Th— thank you.”

Agatha reaches up to cup her cheek, lightly brushing a tear away with her thumb.

“It’s all thanks to Agatha, really,” Wanda surprises her by saying. “Eros told me she came up with that plan, and I wouldn’t have done all of this had she not spoken so highly of you on the phone last night.”

Now that is a blatant lie. All Wanda did was help everyone all the time. How did Agatha always somehow fall for these bleeding hearts?

“Oh, stop being modest, Red — it doesn’t suit you at all,” Agatha snarks — she was always so nauseatingly humble, so gratingly gracious — though there’s an undercurrent of sincere gratitude peeking through at her passing the credit along. At painting Agatha as some kind of hero. At making her look…well…good, too.

Good.

She’s still not sure that’s something she can be. 

But despite everything (her fear, her pessimism, and her better judgment), she thinks perhaps it’s something she’ll allow herself to feel right now, staring at the woman she loves — the woman who loves her in return — on their last night at this luxury Sicilian resort.

Chapter End Notes

We posted the first chapter of this story on the first day of the year, so it feels pretty poetic to post the penultimate one on the very last day! 🥹

Coming up next time: Everything comes full circle.

Chapter 41: Day 7

Chapter Summary

Everything comes full circle.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

There’s a strange sense of déjà vu the next morning as Agatha, Rio, and Nicky check out of their room, trudge through the resort property, and board the same boat that had brought them all there in the first place.

Once the stupid waiter kid (Billy, Agatha had finally bothered to learn as he handed her a glass of champagne for the ride back) and the rest of the staff wave them off as they depart the dock, Agatha scans everyone on board. Yes, the trip had changed her — probably changed her far more than she even realizes yet, than she will ever let herself admit — but old habits died hard.

Jen glares at her from the bench she’s sitting on, while Alice gives her a small smile. Agatha had written them off at the beginning of the trip as irrelevant, irritating, and self-involved, and she’d been pretty spot-on in her assessment, if she did say so herself. She’d pat herself on the back if both of her hands weren’t currently occupied, but holding an outrageously expensive drink and touching an outrageously beautiful woman both took priority.

Lilia has her head buried in virtual Tetris, looking up only when Nicky pokes her in the arm to spout off Sicily facts — something that happens rather frequently. Better her than Agatha, especially since Lilia spouts just as many right back at him. They matched each other’s extremely boring trivia-loving freak. She’d been…half-right about the old bat. She is kooky and ridiculous, though she’s not quite as stupid as Agatha had initially thought. Not quite as useless.

And then there was Rio. Instead of Thanos’ possessive palm on her leg this time around, it’s Agatha’s own hand that’s resting on her knee. She’d been…well, she’d been all wrong about her. And while that was bad for her ego, it had turned out to be pretty damn good for everything else, so she supposed she’d take the tradeoff.

“You really meant it?” Rio asks, interrupting Agatha’s mental end-of-trip evaluations. “That you’ll come help me pack up?” Her voice grows quieter. “That you want me to move in?”

“For the—” She counts in her head the number of occasions that question had already been posed between the previous night and that morning. It would have been five, but Agatha had cut her off with a kiss at breakfast. “—four and halfth time? Yes. I meant it. Wanda’s picking Nicky up at the airport — it’s all set.”

“Do you think she’ll like Shelly?” Nicky asks, taking out a shell he’d found on the beach from his pocket — the souvenir he’d decided to gift his mom with. Despite establishing a dynamic that resembled something in the ballpark of civility at the end of their phone call last night, Agatha sure as hell wasn’t spending money on Wanda, even with Sharon Davis’ credit card.

“For the eighth time, yes. I’m sure she will.”

Rio smiles at him. “Say hi to her for me, Nicky.”

“I will!” He grins.

“Do not say hi to her for me, Nicky,” Agatha half-teases, which really is an improvement considering that, at the beginning of this trip, there would have been no trace of joking in that statement at all.

“So,” Rio says, deftly changing the subject. “Will I finally get to meet the famous Señor Scratchy?”

“Oh, you and Scratchy will get well-acquainted,” Agatha confirms. “He sleeps with me every night, so you’ll have to fight him for the left side of the bed.”

“He’s a rabbit. How much room does he need?”

“He’s chunky.” Nicky giggles.

“Yes, because you sneak him food when you think I’m not looking,” Agatha says. She tickles his stomach, which turns the giggles into squeals of laughter. “He’s the king of the house — absolutely spoiled rotten.”

“I’m not surprised, from what I’ve heard,” Rio affectionately admits. “He’s…friendly, right? Like, you think he’ll like me?”

“He’s easily bribed. Give him a carrot to gnaw on, and you’ll have his endless devotion.”

“Good to know.”

“Mm,” she hums in agreement. “Any more rabbit-related questions or concerns?”

Rio shrugs a shoulder, taking her bottom lip between her teeth. “Not necessarily.”

“Non-rabbit-related questions or concerns, then.” The hand resting on Rio’s knee travels up to rub at her inner thigh — not high enough to raise eyebrows or scar Nicky, but high enough to bloom goosebumps on Rio's skin. "You have those?”

She swallows hard, though whether it’s from being turned on by Agatha’s touch, being apprehensive at sharing her response, or some combination of the two isn’t clear. “I think I’m still just scared,” she confesses as Nicky turns to blab something to Lilia. “Not of anything tangible — just…the future, I guess.”

Agatha nods, sucking in an inhale. She could do this. She could help. She was capable of making things better instead of worse, despite all prior evidence to the contrary. Lilia believed that, and so did Rio, so maybe she could, too. “You know the best way to eat an elephant?"

Rio tilts her head, brows furrowing. “What do you mean?”

“Just a dumb proverb about approaching big tasks — big things like the future.” She waves her glass of champagne, expertly managing to spill nary a drop. “You try to eat the elephant too fast, you get sick, especially if you go in famished. You’re the biology major — you must know what refeeding syndrome is.”

That’s what Agatha had done. What she’d suffered from. There had been this whole world, this whole feast, on the other side of her mother. And considering Evanora had starved her of nutrients — of support, of care, of love — the minute she could break away from her, she’d gorged herself on freedom. On drugs, on alcohol, on meaningless sex to try and feel fed. (She never did.)

Rio, on the other hand, was clearly terrified to taste it at all. Scared to pick up a fork and knife and get to work.

“But you do have to eat it,” Agatha says more gently. “You have to eat, Rio.” She means this in a metaphorical elephant sense and a very literal one, too. “And the best way to consume it is taking it one—“ She kisses Rio's jaw. “—bite—“ She nips at her bottom lip. “—at a time.” She finishes with a long, lingering kiss on her lips before pressing their foreheads together. “Just one bite at a time. That’s all,” she whispers.

Rio sinks into the touch — as easy for her, it seems, as breathing. “I don’t know where to start.”

“Start here. With me.”

“How?”

“Just be here. Be here. Now. Not dwelling on what’s happened. Not worrying about what might.”

She sounds like a hypocrite, giving her advice she doesn't live her own jaded, cynical life by. (Impulsivity, after all, was not the same as living in the moment. As being present.) And while Agatha doesn’t particularly have a problem with her own hypocrisy, she intends to practice what she’s preaching this time.

This wasn’t real life, of course — the two of them on this boat. This was a vacation, was fantasy, was paradise. Things would be infinitely more difficult when they both woke up without the sound of waves hitting the shore outside their window, without the smell of a freshly prepared breakfast buffet wafting its way through the door.

No, this wasn’t reality.

But fuck it. Agatha had spent a large percentage of her life living a nightmare, so she’d let herself exist in a dream for once, at least until the wheels touched down at Newark.

Rio takes a deep breath. “You really think I can do this?”

“You really think I’d be wasting a second of my precious time with you if I didn’t?”

Rio rolls her eyes, reluctantly mumbling out, “I suppose not.”

“Then there you have it.” Agatha pulls away and squares her shoulders, satisfied and a bit smug. 

She downs the rest of her champagne, catching movement in the water out of the corner of her eye as she gives her empty glass to an attendant. “Look.” She points into the distance. “A shark. Seems like a good omen. Maybe not for the people in Jaws — another movie I’m sure you haven’t seen — but for you, considering you’re such a fin-atic, pun absolutely intended.”

“Corny,” Rio accuses, though the corner of her mouth lifts into a small, amused smile. It was addictive, really — eliciting that response. Agatha had tried a lot of drugs in her day, but nothing made her feel higher than that little grin.

Rio rests her chin on Agatha’s shoulder, peering out at the sea. “I hope it wasn’t actually a dolphin you saw. They’re evil.”

“Oh, yeah?” Agatha snorts. “So just like me, then.” A beat. Rio doesn’t like that, she remembers — the self-deprecating jokes about the kind of person she was, even if she was still pretty convinced it was true. “Sorry,” mutters. She shakes her head. “I mean— Flaccid. Squamous. Whatever.”

Rio gives her a little nod of approval. “They’re more like…him,” she softly muses. “They’re literally nicknamed the ‘rapists of the sea.’”

“Ah.” She awkwardly purses her lips, not quite knowing what to say. 

It’s a blessing and a curse, then, that they’re distracted by the boat hitting a large wave, violently jerking everyone onboard. “Shit,” she mutters, narrowly grabbing Nicky to steady him before they’re slammed by another one. “Do you even have a fucking captain’s license?!” she yells to the front.

“Sorry, ma’am!” the man yells back. “Choppy waters!”

“I think I’m gonna be sick,” Jen whimpers, clutching onto the bench as Alice rubs her back.

“Do us all a favor and aim overboard,” Agatha tells her.

Jen shoots nauseous daggers at her, though Agatha is too busy to notice, having refocused her attention on Nicky. “You okay, baby?” she asks as she runs a hand through his hair, eyes scanning him for any sign of fear or injury.

“I’m okay.” 

“You sure?”

He nods. “It felt fun. Like when you drive really, really fast over that pothole in our neighborhood, even though Mom hates it when you do that.”

“Oka— Shit,” she says again as they jolt once more, causing something to fly out of Rio’s pocket. Agatha miraculously manages to catch it, clasping it tightly in her hand.

She waits a few moments until the rocking calms and Nicky goes back to giving Lilia advice on where she should stack her next Tetris squares before daring to open it again. “You nearly lost your—“ she says as she uncurls her fingers, revealing a giant, familiar diamond. “—wedding ring…”

“Oh.” Rio crosses her arms over her chest, self-conscious. “I was planning on burying it,” she murmurs.

Agatha holds it up between her fingers, examining it more closely. “Could probably pawn it for a pretty penny,” she muses before seeing the look on Rio’s face. “Or…” she proposes. “You could just throw it into the ocean now and wash your hands of it. It'd be very dramatic and Titanic of you — yes, I know you haven't seen that either.”

“I’ve seen part of it,” Rio defensively mumbles. “I didn’t like it.” She tilts her head in consideration. “Do you think I should?”

She narrowly resists the urge to say, ‘Absolutely the fuck yes.’ It should be solely her choice. It had to be. “I think you should if you want to.”

Rio chews on the inside of her cheek, pondering for a few more beats. “I think I’d rather bury it.”

“Okay.” She nods, attempting to keep any disappointment from her tone. Why hang onto it for even one more second if she wasn’t ready for a completely fresh start? Ready to move on — move on with Agatha?

Usually, she would leave it at that, let the unasked question linger and insecurity nag at her for all eternity, but fuck, she was trying to turn over a new leaf, wasn’t she? So as much as it terrifies and humiliates her, she swallows hard and says, as diplomatically as possible, “May I ask why?”

“I don’t know.” Rio squints, searching for the words. “It’s something about returning it to the earth.”

“Is the sea not part of the earth?”

“Technically. But the ocean is an abyss — it’s not the same as mud and bugs.”

Agatha runs her tongue over her teeth. That made some semblance of sense, she supposed. It was about the ritual. About having control.

“So what I’m hearing is you like things dirty,” she says, quirking a teasing brow. Perhaps she was relying on old crutches again — jokes and sex to lighten the mood — but it feels different somehow. And from the way Rio responds with an undeniably fond eye-roll, she clearly doesn’t mind.

Encouraged, Agatha leans forward to whisper in her ear. “Well, in that case, you’re in luck. I can be positively filthy.”

“Oh, I’m well aware of your capabilities.”

Agatha scoffs. “Honey, you ain’t seen nothing yet.”

“Plenty to look forward to then, it seems,” Rio quips, turning her head to look at her, though her eyes shine with the kind of sincerity that always threatens to take Agatha’s breath away. They seem to say, ‘I’m looking forward to everything with you.’

Agatha’s smirk fades into something softer — more genuine. “Why don’t you let me hold onto this, okay?” she asks, nodding at the ring still in her hand. Let me help you carry it — the whole load of your past. Trust me to handle it with care.

Rio gives her a small nod. “You’re not gonna…leave me, right?” she quietly checks.

“Well, you’re moving into my house, so…the logistics of that would be pretty complicated,” Agatha says as she slips the ring into her pocket.

She gives her a look. “You know what I mean.”

It’s absolutely absurd — the mere thought of Agatha leaving Rio instead of the other way around. Still, she appeases her. “I’m not going anywhere,” she promises her more gently. Then, before she can inevitably get too embarrassed and talk herself out of it, “You?"

She shakes her head. “Still clinging on with everything I have,” she vows, mouth twitching into a small, reassuring smile.

For some reason, Agatha believes her. She believes her with everything she has.

She puts an arm around Nicky’s shoulders and pulls him close, turns her hand palm-up on Rio’s leg so she can take it, play with it, do whatever she wants to do with Agatha. Agatha — independent Agatha who never gave up a single ounce of control a week ago — is game for it all.

Because Agatha — insatiable Agatha — has never felt so full. So content. So…at peace.

Disneyland. Chuck E. Cheese. Sky Zone. All cesspools crawling with pee and screaming children but all places Agatha was prepared to brave for Nicky when she’d asked him where he wanted to go during their (too-short, unfair, single) week of summer vacation together. 

Sicily. He’d picked Sicily.

And thank god for that.

Chapter End Notes

Thank you, thank you, thank you for all of your support on this story. I think I speak for both of us when I say we’ve never had a reception quite this big, warm, and moving. If you’ve connected with any of these characters or themes, we hope you found some comfort in knowing that you’re not alone. The process of writing and sharing this with all of you has been so rewarding (and, at times, even therapeutic), and we’re going to miss this version of these characters so much. That said, they’ve wormed their way deep into our hearts, so who knows? Maybe it won’t be goodbye forever! Thank you again for sticking with us on this journey for over a year! We would absolutely love to hear what you thought. Until next time. ❤️
